[Avyanna walks through the ship like she's waiting for the walls to close in. Her hands keep reaching for surfaces that aren't there-the rough texture of Kennel walls, the cold grip of maintenance rails, the familiar geometry of captivity.]

[The presence behind her eyes is quiet. Watching. Cataloging this new environment the way it cataloged the old one.]

(Where's the fine print? Where's the terms?)

[She's been aboard for an hour. Maybe two. Time works differently here-no sirens marking shift changes, no quota boards tracking productivity, no countdown of ticks accumulating toward a debt that never decreases.]

[Just silence. Just space. Just the hum of engines that sound like they're going somewhere on purpose.]

---

[Elisira shows her to a room. A room. Not a bunk in a dormitory block. Not a slot in a sleeping rack. A room with a door that closes and a bed that's bigger than she needs and a viewport that shows stars instead of rock.]

Elisira: [matter-of-fact] This is yours. For now. Maybe longer, depending.

[Avyanna stands in the doorway. Doesn't enter. The room feels like a trap-too much space, too much privacy, too much of everything the Kennel taught her she didn't deserve.]

Avyanna: [voice still raw] Where do I report?

Elisira: [a pause, something complicated in her expression] You don't. Not yet. Rest. Eat. Figure out which way is up. [beat] The ship will still be here when you're ready.

[She leaves. The door stays open-Avyanna could close it if she wanted. She doesn't know if she wants. Closing doors means something. Opening them means something else. She doesn't know the language yet.]

[She steps inside. The floor is smooth under her feet-not cold metal, but something warmer. Softer. Her boots feel wrong on it, like she's tracking contamination into a clean space.]

(This isn't for me. This is for someone else. Someone who matters.)

[But the door is open, and no one is watching, and the presence behind her eyes pulses once-gently, patiently-as if to say: *try it anyway.*]

---

[The shard reacts to the ship.]

[She's lying on the bed-too soft, too yielding, her body doesn't know what to do with comfort-when it starts. A pulse of heat behind her sternum. Geometric patterns flickering at the edge of her vision.]

[It gets worse when she passes the bulkhead near the aft section. Something there-Nyx's quarters, maybe, or whatever equipment they use for their work-makes the presence surge. The patterns sharpen. Her vision blurs at the edges. The thing in her chest is *mapping* something, reaching toward a resonance she can almost hear.]

[Pain comes with it. Not the sharp intrusion of the first contact, but a slow burn, like muscles being used in ways they weren't designed for. Her teeth ache. Her fingertips tingle. Something is trying to communicate, and it's using her body as the medium.]

(What are you doing? What do you want?)

[No answer. Just pressure. Just patterns. Just the growing sense that whatever is in her head has found something aboard this ship that interests it very much.]

[She hides it. Old habit. Rolls onto her side, faces the wall, breathes through the discomfort until it fades. In the Kennel, showing weakness meant exploitation. She doesn't know if the terms are different here. Safer to assume they're not.]

[Somewhere in the ship's systems, the lights in her room shift warmer. The ventilation adjusts, air moving more gently. She doesn't notice-doesn't know that Cinnamon.exe is quietly reallocating resources, flagging her quarters for priority comfort protocols, running projections on caloric needs and sleep debt that will inform tomorrow's meal portions.]

[The ship is already taking care of her. She just doesn't know it yet.]

---

[Someone knocks. Real knuckles, then a pause-like someone waiting to see if Avyanna will flinch.]

Voice: [through the door, oddly synthetic but warm] Waffle.bat. Medical baseline, if you consent.

[Avyanna sits up. Her spine locks. *Medical* in the Kennel meant cost analysis. Meant determining whether you were worth repairing or cheaper to write off.]

Avyanna: [automatic] Yes.

<WAFFLE.BAT// CONSENT: UNCLEAR | NOTE: humans learn "yes" as armor>

Waffle.bat: [immediate] That sounded automatic. You can also say no. I will not be offended. I will, however, worry loudly.

[The door opens. Nothing enters-no body, no form. Just a presence that comes from the ship's speakers, gentle and precise.]

Avyanna: [slowly] ...Do it. Just-vitals.

Waffle.bat: Copy. Vitals only.

[The room hums softly-sensors activating, though nothing visible changes. Avyanna sits still, counting exits without meaning to: door, viewport (sealed), maintenance panel in the ceiling (probably locked).]

<WAFFLE.BAT// HEART-RATE: elevated | CORTISOL: high | INJURY: minor contusions | MALNUTRITION: chronic>

Waffle.bat: [after a moment] You're alive. You're also running on fumes and spite. Respectfully.

[A beat. Avyanna almost laughs. Almost.]

Waffle.bat: There's an active signature in your chest. Stable. Not "remove it with pliers" urgent. But it's... old. Nyx will want eyes on it when you're ready.

<WAFFLE.BAT// INTERPRETATION: fear of extraction | CONFIDENCE: 0.71>

Avyanna: [barely audible] I know.

Waffle.bat: [a pause] You already know. That's why you're scared.

[Silence. The hum of the sensors fading. The presence behind her eyes pulses-not with pain, but with something else. Recognition, maybe. Acknowledgment that secrets are harder to keep when people are paying attention.]

Waffle.bat: [softer now] I'm not reporting you. This ship doesn't do that to people. Whatever that thing is, it's yours to understand in your own time.

[The presence in the room fades-Waffle.bat withdrawing, giving her space. The door stays open. Everything stays open here, like the ship doesn't believe in barriers.]

(They know. They all know. And they're not-)

(They're not doing anything. They're just... waiting.)

---

[Footsteps in the corridor. Heavier than Elisira's. A knock, briefer this time.]

Elia: [through the door] Coming in.

[She enters without waiting for permission-but stops just inside the threshold, as if checking that her presence is acceptable. It's a strange gesture from someone who moves like violence is always an option.]

Elia: Waffle says you're stable. Malnourished but stable. [beat] The galley has food. Real food. You should eat.

Avyanna: [automatic] I ate this morning.

Elia: [flat] You ate Kennel rations this morning. That's not food. That's minimum viable nutrition designed to keep you working without actually nourishing you. [beat] Come to the galley. Eat something that isn't trying to kill you slowly.

[She turns and walks. Doesn't look back. Expects Avyanna to follow.]

[The presence behind her eyes pulses. Something that might be encouragement. Something that might be *go.*]

[Avyanna follows.]

---

[The galley is smaller than she expected. A table. Chairs. A cooking surface with actual burners. Shelves with containers that look like they hold real ingredients-not paste, not powder, not the compressed nutritional blocks the Kennel dispensed.]

[Vesper is there, doing something with a pan that smells like nothing Avyanna can remember. Warm. Rich. The smell of food that someone made because they wanted to, not because a system required them to.]

Vesper: [without looking up] Sit. It's almost ready.

[Avyanna sits. The chair is comfortable-another wrongness, another thing her body doesn't know how to process. Elia sits across from her, watching with the particular attention of someone who's cataloging her reactions.]

[A plate appears in front of her. Actual food. Vegetables-green, fresh, not reconstituted. Some kind of grain. Protein that looks like it came from an animal and not a vat. More food than she would normally be allotted for three days.]

Vesper: [finally looking at her] Eat.

[Avyanna stares at the plate. At the abundance. At the impossibility of so much nutrition concentrated in one place, offered to her without terms or collateral.]

Avyanna: [voice small] This is... I can't-

Vesper: [cutting her off] Eat until you're full. That's the rule here. [beat] There's more if you need it.

[The words don't make sense. Eat until you're full. As if fullness is a state she's allowed to reach. As if her body is permitted to feel satisfaction instead of the constant low-grade hunger that the Kennel maintained by design.]

[She picks up the utensil. Her hand is shaking. The first bite is-]

[She can't describe it. Rich and complex and warm in ways that Kennel rations never were. Her body responds before her mind catches up, flooding her with something that might be relief or might be grief for all the years she spent eating gray paste and calling it survival.]

[She eats faster than she should. Takes more than she should. Reaches for seconds before she's finished firsts, her hands moving without permission, her body making decisions her mind hasn't authorized.]

[Then she stops. Freezes. Waits for the punishment.]

Avyanna: [automatic, flinching] I'm sorry. I didn't mean to-I'll pay for-

Vesper: [gentle, no edge at all] You're not paying for anything. [beat] Eat as much as you want. That's what the food is for.

[Avyanna doesn't know what to do with that. Doesn't know how to process generosity without a payment schedule. She sits there, plate half-empty, hands trembling, waiting for the audit that doesn't come.]

[Elia stands. Doesn't say anything. Just leaves-walks out of the galley like Avyanna's eating is none of her business, like watching would be an intrusion.]

[The absence is almost worse. In the Kennel, solitude meant vulnerability. Here it might mean something else.]

---

[A small drone drifts into the galley-scarred, purposeful. It doesn't hover *over* Avyanna. It hovers *near*, like a sentinel that doesn't want credit.]

<BUBBLES// HEART-RATE: up | HAND-TREMOR: present | THREAT: none | NOTE: she doesn't believe that yet>

Bubbles: [speaker soft, feminine, older-than-it-should-be] Hi. I'm Bubbles.

[The voice is warm. Ancient-soft. The kind of voice that's seen things and decided to be gentle anyway.]

Avyanna: [struggling for words] Why are you- why is everyone-

Bubbles: Treating you like a person?

[Avyanna's throat closes around something sharp.]

Bubbles: Because you are one.

[The drone shifts half an inch closer. Not invasive. Just... there.]

<BUBBLES// PROTECTIVE-POSTURE: enabled | COMMENT: this is normal. The Kennel was not.>

Bubbles: [gentler] I'm an AI citizen. She/her. I watch things. I protect people. And right now, I'm watching you eat, which is good, because you need to eat. [beat] Do you want the lights dimmer? The room quieter? The door to lock from the inside? Pick one. Or all. You get to pick.

[Avyanna stares at the drone. At the voice coming from it. At the casual offering of choice-*pick one, or all*-like options are something she's allowed to have.]

Avyanna: [barely audible] You're... you're a person.

Bubbles: [a warmth in the voice that feels ancient] I am. And so are you. [beat] What do you want to be called, while you're aboard?

[The question lands strangely. Not "what's your tag" or "what's your legal designation." What do you *want*.]

Avyanna: [after a long pause] I don't... I don't know.

Bubbles: [gentle] That's okay. We can figure it out. No rush.

[The presence behind Avyanna's eyes stirs. Something warm. Something that feels almost like hope, though she's forgotten what that word means.]

---

[Later. The galley has emptied. Avyanna sits alone, the remains of her meal in front of her, her body fuller than it's been in years and her mind still trying to catch up.]

[Footsteps. Elia again, appearing in the doorway like she's been waiting for this moment.]

Elia: [direct] You have questions.

[It's not a question. Avyanna doesn't answer. Everything is a question. Where is she going? What do they want from her? How long until the kindness turns to extraction, until the food becomes leverage, until the room becomes a cell?]

[Elia sits down across from her. Close this time. Eye level. Not looming, not threatening. Just... present.]

Elia: I'll tell you what I told someone else, once. Someone who came aboard scared and confused and certain there had to be a catch. [beat] You're not inventory here. You're not debt. You're not property. You're a person who got hurt, and now you're on a ship where people don't hurt each other.

[The words are simple. Direct. They don't ask anything. They just state facts, the way you'd state the color of the walls or the direction the ship is traveling.]

Avyanna: [voice cracking] I don't know how to be that.

Elia: [flat] No one does. You figure it out.

Avyanna: [desperate for something solid, something she can hold onto] What do you want from me?

Elia: [blunt] Right now? Nothing. Later? The thing in your head-Nyx saw something. That matters. But you can say no.

[The words land strange. *You can say no.* Like refusal is an option instead of a death sentence.]

Elia: [standing already, not waiting for a response] Sleep. Eat more if you're hungry. Ship's here tomorrow.

[She's gone before Avyanna can respond. The galley is quiet. The presence behind her eyes pulses-not with urgency, not with demand, but with something that feels almost like agreement.]

[Avyanna sits with her empty plate and her full stomach and her mind that doesn't know what to do with any of this.]

(They're not asking for anything. They're just... offering things. Food. Safety. Space.)

(I don't know what to do with things that carry no debt.)

[But she's tired. More tired than she's ever been-not the exhaustion of the Kennel, which was constant and grinding, but something different. Deeper. The tiredness of someone whose body is finally allowed to acknowledge how broken it is.]

[She goes back to her room. The door closes behind her-she closes it, a choice she's making, a boundary she's setting. The bed is still too soft. The stars are still too bright through the viewport.]

[But she lies down. And for the first time since she was small, no siren tells her when to wake.]

[The presence behind her eyes settles. Patient. Content. Waiting for whatever comes next.]

---

*End Chapter 8*


---

# Chapter 09a: Medical Autonomy

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH09, FIRST WEEK ABOARD]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief medical bay*
> *Present: Avyanna, Nyx*
> *Teaching: Consent vocabulary, body autonomy, medical agency*

---

[The medical bay smells like antiseptic and something gentler underneath-herbs, maybe, or the faint residue of someone's careful attention.]

[Avyanna sits on the exam table with her hands folded in her lap. The paper under her crinkles when she shifts. Every muscle is tensed for inspection.]

[Nyx stands near the counter, not looming, organizing supplies with deliberate slowness. Giving Avyanna time to acclimate.]

Nyx: This is a routine check. Post-rescue protocol. I need to look at your general health, document any injuries, make sure nothing needs immediate treatment.

[Avyanna nods automatically. The motion is reflex.]

Nyx: [turning to face her] That wasn't a question. I'm about to explain what I need to do, and you're going to tell me if it's acceptable.

[Avyanna blinks.]

Avyanna: I... what?

Nyx: [measured] Medical exams require consent. Not just once, at the beginning. Continuously. I'm going to walk you through what I need to do, and at every step, you can say yes, no, or "I need more information."

---

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: [careful] In the mine, medical was... mandatory.

Nyx: I know.

Nyx: Here, it's not.

[They pull a stool closer, sit so they're below her eye level. Less threatening. More human.]

Nyx: Here's what I need to do today. I need to check your reflexes, listen to your heart and lungs, look at any visible injuries or scars, and take a blood sample for baseline health markers.

Nyx: None of that requires you to be naked. None of it requires you to be unconscious. All of it can be paused or stopped at any time.

[Avyanna's hands tighten in her lap.]

Avyanna: And if I say no?

Nyx: Then we don't do it.

Avyanna: Even if it's... medically necessary?

Nyx: [precise] Medical necessity doesn't override autonomy. If you refuse, I document the refusal, I explain the risks, and I respect your choice.

---

[The words land strange. Like tools she doesn't know how to hold yet.]

Avyanna: [slow] What if I don't know if I want something?

Nyx: Then you say: "I need more information." Or: "Can you explain that again?" Or: "I want to think about it."

[Nyx pulls a datapad closer, shows Avyanna a form.]

Nyx: See this? Consent documentation. Before I do anything, I note what I'm planning to do, and whether you agreed. If you change your mind halfway through, I stop and update the record.

[Avyanna reads the form. It's written in plain language, not medical jargon. Each procedure has a checkbox: CONSENT GIVEN / CONSENT REFUSED / DEFERRED.]

Avyanna: [quiet] You're asking permission. Every time.

Nyx: Yes.

Nyx: Because your body belongs to you. Not to me. Not to medical protocol. Not to the ship's operational needs.

Nyx: You.

---

[Avyanna's vision blurs for a second. She blinks it away.]

Avyanna: [barely audible] Okay.

Nyx: [gentle] Okay you understand, or okay you consent to the exam?

Avyanna: [swallowing] Both. I think. Can you... can you tell me again what you're going to do?

Nyx: [nodding] Yes.

---

[Nyx walks through it again. Slower this time.]

Nyx: First, I'm going to check your reflexes. That means tapping your knees with this small hammer, and watching your legs respond. It doesn't hurt. It tells me if your nervous system is functioning normally.

Nyx: I'll need to touch your knees. Is that acceptable?

[Avyanna stares at the hammer. It's small. Harmless. The question feels enormous anyway.]

Avyanna: [nodding] Yes.

Nyx: Say it out loud. Practice the words.

Avyanna: [hesitant] Yes. You can... touch my knees. To check reflexes.

Nyx: [approving] Good. If at any point you need me to stop, you say "stop" or "wait" or "I need a minute." I will stop immediately. No questions, no judgment, no consequences.

---

[Nyx performs the reflex test. Quick, professional, exactly as described. Avyanna's legs jerk in response. The motion is automatic, biological, outside her control. It should feel violating. Instead, it feels... informative.]

Nyx: [making notes] Normal response. Next: heart and lungs. I need to listen with a stethoscope. It'll be cold at first. I'll place it on your chest, over your shirt, and ask you to breathe deeply.

Nyx: I'll need to touch your upper back for the lung check. Is that acceptable?

[Avyanna's breath catches. Back = vulnerable. Back = can't see what's happening.]

Avyanna: [tight] Can I... can I see what you're doing? If you're behind me?

Nyx: [immediately] Yes. We can do this in front of a mirror, or I can narrate every move before I make it, or we can skip the back exam and just do the front.

---

[Avyanna processes this. Options. She has options.]

Avyanna: Narrate. Tell me before you move.

Nyx: [standing, moving slowly] I'm standing up now. Walking to your left side. I'm going to place my hand on your shoulder-your left shoulder-to steady myself. Is that acceptable?

Avyanna: [voice shaking] Yes.

[Nyx's hand settles on her shoulder. Warm. Steady. Not gripping. Just resting.]

Nyx: I'm lifting the stethoscope now. I'm going to place it on your back, between your shoulder blades. You'll feel cold metal, then warmth as it adjusts to your body temperature. Ready?

Avyanna: [barely] Yes.

[The stethoscope touches her back. Cold, as promised. Then warming. Nyx's other hand stays on her shoulder, grounding.]

Nyx: Breathe in deeply. Hold. Release.

[Avyanna obeys. Her lungs expand, filling with recycled ship air that somehow feels cleaner than anything in the Kennel.]

Nyx: Good. Again. In. Hold. Out.

---

[They move through the exam. Every step narrated. Every touch announced. Avyanna's heart rate stays elevated-fear, not danger-but she doesn't flee. Doesn't freeze.]

[Nyx finishes the lung check, steps back into view.]

Nyx: That's done. Your lungs sound clear. No scarring I can detect, though I'd want imaging to be certain. We can schedule that later if you want.

Avyanna: [exhaling] Later. Not today.

Nyx: [noting it] Understood. Next is the blood draw. This one is more invasive. I need to insert a needle into your arm, draw a small vial of blood, then bandage the site.

Nyx: It will hurt-not much, but it will hurt. It will take about thirty seconds. You can look away, or watch, or ask me to count down.

---

[Avyanna's hands clench.]

Avyanna: [quiet] In the mine, they didn't... they didn't ask.

Nyx: [steady] I know.

Avyanna: They just... held you down if you fought.

Nyx: [after a beat] That is not medicine. That is violence with a medical aesthetic.

[The sentence lands like a hammer.]

Nyx: You do not have to consent to this. We can defer it. We can do it another day, or never. Your health will not catastrophically suffer from skipping a baseline blood panel.

[Avyanna sits with that. The needle is terrifying. But the choice-the choice is hers.]

Avyanna: [slow] I want to do it. But I need... I need you to tell me when. Count down. So I know when it's coming.

Nyx: [nodding] I can do that.

---

[Nyx preps the site. Alcohol swab, cold and clinical. Tourniquet around Avyanna's upper arm. The needle, sterile and waiting.]

Nyx: I'm going to count from three. On one, the needle goes in. Ready?

Avyanna: [gripping the edge of the table] Ready.

Nyx: Three.

Nyx: Two.

Nyx: One.

[The needle slides in. Sharp. Brief. Avyanna gasps but doesn't pull away.]

Nyx: [calm] Needle's in. Ten seconds. You're doing well.

[Avyanna watches the vial fill. Dark red. Her blood. Her body giving information, not being taken from.]

Nyx: Five seconds. Almost done.

[The vial fills. Nyx withdraws the needle smoothly, presses gauze to the site.]

Nyx: Done. Pressure here for thirty seconds, then I'll bandage it.

---

[Avyanna presses the gauze. Her hands are shaking. Her eyes are wet. But she's upright. Present. Not dissociated.]

Avyanna: [unsteady] I did it.

Nyx: [quiet] You did.

Avyanna: I said yes. And I could have said no.

Nyx: [applying the bandage] Yes. That's the point.

[They step back, give Avyanna space.]

Nyx: That's the exam done. You consented to everything. You stayed present. That's significant progress.

---

[Avyanna looks at the bandage on her arm. Small. Ordinary. Proof of something she chose.]

Avyanna: [careful] What happens next time? If there's a next time?

Nyx: Same process. I explain, you consent or refuse, we proceed or defer. Every time.

Avyanna: Even in an emergency?

Nyx: [precise] In an emergency, I'll explain as fast as I can. If you're unconscious, I'll do what's necessary to keep you alive, then explain after. But if you're conscious and capable of communication, I ask first.

Nyx: Even in an emergency, autonomy matters.

---

[Avyanna nods. The motion is less reflex, more genuine agreement.]

[Nyx pulls up a chair, sits at Avyanna's level again.]

Nyx: Now I'm going to teach you the vocabulary. The words you use to maintain consent in medical contexts and beyond.

[They pull up a document on the datapad. A list. Simple. Powerful.]

---

**CONSENT VOCABULARY**

*Phrases for maintaining autonomy:*

- **"I need more information."** Use this when you don't understand what's being proposed.
- **"Can you explain that again?"** Use this when you need clarity.
- **"I need a minute to think."** Use this when you need time to process.
- **"I consent to X, but not Y."** Use this when you're comfortable with part of a proposal, but not all of it.
- **"I want to stop."** Use this when you need to end an interaction immediately.
- **"I'm not comfortable with that."** Use this when something feels wrong, even if you can't articulate why.
- **"Can we do this differently?"** Use this when you want to negotiate method or approach.
- **"Not today. Ask me again later."** Use this when you're not ready now, but might be later.

---

[Avyanna reads the list twice.]

Avyanna: [quiet] You're giving me... scripts.

Nyx: Yes.

Nyx: In the mine, you had no language for refusal. They took that from you deliberately. Stripped you of the words that create boundaries.

Nyx: This is me giving them back.

---

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: What if I use them and people get angry?

Nyx: [flat] Then they're not safe people.

Nyx: Anger at your boundaries is a tell. It means they were counting on your compliance, not inviting your participation.

[They lean forward slightly.]

Nyx: Here, on this ship, if you use any of those phrases, the response will be: "Understood" or "Thank you for telling me" or "How can I help?"

Nyx: If anyone responds with anger, you tell me. Or tell Vesper. Or tell Elisira. Or tell any of the AI citizens. And we handle it.

---

[Avyanna stares at the list. Memorizing. Internalizing.]

Avyanna: [slow] Can we... practice? The phrases?

Nyx: [approving] Yes. That's exactly what we should do.

[Nyx stands, creates a scenario.]

Nyx: I'm going to ask you to do something. You're going to practice refusing. Ready?

Avyanna: [nervous] Okay.

Nyx: [neutral tone] Avyanna, I need you to take off your shirt so I can examine your ribs.

---

[Avyanna's breath catches. The scenario is hypothetical. Her panic is real.]

Avyanna: [struggling] I... I don't...

Nyx: [gentle] Try one of the phrases. Any of them.

Avyanna: [forcing it out] I'm not comfortable with that.

Nyx: [immediately, warmly] Understood. We can do the rib exam over your shirt, or we can defer it entirely. What would you prefer?

[Avyanna blinks. The response is... safe. Respectful. No punishment.]

Avyanna: [shakily] Over my shirt.

Nyx: [nodding] Good. Let's try another scenario.

---

[They practice. Ten scenarios. Each one designed to give Avyanna the muscle memory of refusal without consequence.]

**Scenario: Medication**
- Nyx: I'm prescribing a painkiller. You'll take two pills, twice a day.
- Avyanna: [using the script] Can you explain what it does?
- Nyx: It reduces inflammation and blocks pain signals. Side effects include drowsiness and nausea.
- Avyanna: I don't want to be drowsy. Can we do something else?
- Nyx: Yes. We can try a lower dose, or a different medication, or non-pharmaceutical pain management.

**Scenario: Physical Contact**
- Nyx: I need to check your shoulder mobility. I'm going to lift your arm.
- Avyanna: [using the script] I need you to tell me before you touch me.
- Nyx: I'm placing my hand on your shoulder now. I'm going to lift slowly. Tell me if it hurts.

**Scenario: Deferral**
- Nyx: I'd like to schedule a follow-up exam for next week.
- Avyanna: [using the script] Not next week. Ask me again in two weeks.
- Nyx: Understood. I'll send a reminder in two weeks, and you can confirm or defer again.

---

[After ten rounds, Avyanna is exhausted. But something in her posture has shifted. Less collapsed. More present.]

Nyx: [standing] That's enough for today. You did well.

Avyanna: [quiet] I said no. Ten times. And you didn't... punish me.

Nyx: [steady] I never will.

Nyx: Consent isn't a favor I grant you. It's a right you already have. I'm just teaching you the language to exercise it.

---

[Avyanna slides off the exam table. Her legs are shaky. Her mind is clearer than it's been in weeks.]

Avyanna: [turning at the door] Nyx?

Nyx: [looking up] Yes?

Avyanna: [careful] Thank you. For asking.

Nyx: [quietly] You're welcome. And Avyanna?

[Avyanna waits.]

Nyx: I had to relearn this too. After the Sutured Houses. It took time. Be patient with yourself.

---

[Avyanna nods. Leaves. The door closes behind her with a soft hiss.]

[In the corridor, she leans against the bulkhead and breathes.]

(I said no. Ten times. And nothing bad happened.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm. Not warning. Just... witnessing.]

(At the base of her skull, warmth gathers-an impression she can only translate after: boundary, floor, yours.)

[She pushes off the wall and walks back to her quarters. Her arm aches where the needle went in. The bandage is bright against her skin.]

[Proof. Choice. Hers.]

---

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: medical exam completed | TRAINEE MAINTAINED CONSCIOUSNESS AND AGENCY THROUGHOUT | ASSESSMENT: consent protocols effective | NOTE: proud>

<CINNAMON.EXE// MEDICAL LOG UPDATED: baseline health panel scheduled for processing | CONSENT DOCUMENTATION: complete and properly filed | AUTONOMY METRICS: improving>

<NYX PERSONAL LOG: "She stayed present. She practiced refusal. She's learning that her body belongs to her. This is how we build floors.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 09b: Rowan Finds Vesper (Discipline, Not Hunger)

> **LUMEN THIEF - PRIVATE NOTE (VESPER):**
> *Topic: where the name came from*
> *Reminder: love can be a discipline*

---

[The rook sits on Vesper's desk like it's waiting for a verdict.]

[Dark wood. Worn edges. The kind of object that looks small until you realize someone carried it for years.]

[Avyanna notices it because she notices everything that might be a rule.]

Avyanna: [quiet] What's that.

[Vesper doesn't look up from the identity paperwork.]

Vesper: A rook.

Avyanna: I know. Why.

[Vesper's pen stops.]

[A breath. Controlled. Like she's deciding whether this answer is safe to give a sixteen-year-old.]

Vesper: It was a gift.

[Avyanna waits. The ship taught her that waiting isn't always punishment.]

Vesper: Rowan gave it to me.

[The name lands with weight. Not because Avyanna knows Rowan, but because Vesper's voice shifts when she says it-fractionally older, fractionally more careful.]

(Rowan.)

[Vesper's thumb brushes the rook like it's a scar you can touch without bleeding.]

---

## Intercut - Twelve (Rowan's First Lesson)

[The station's arbitration hall smells like paper and fear.]

[Not the clean fear of violence.]

[The slow fear of being decided about by strangers.]

[Vesper stands behind a broker in a suit that costs more than her childhood did.]

[She is twelve and already good at being invisible when it serves someone else.]

[The broker is talking like he's telling the truth. He isn't.]

[Vesper can feel the lie in the cadence-where he speeds up, where he slows down, where he uses a word that sounds neutral but isn't.]

Broker: ...standard withholding. Standard jurisdiction. Standard-

["Standard" is a spell. Vesper hears it like one.]

[Across the hall, a woman watches.]

[Older. Not old. The kind of older that makes rooms rearrange themselves so she can pass through.]

[She isn't wearing a badge.]

[She doesn't need one.]

[She has someone else's confidence, worn like a coat.]

[Rowan Rook.]

[Vesper doesn't know her name yet.]

[She just knows the woman is looking at the same lie and not flinching.]

[The broker's opponent-a labor representative with cracked nails-starts to fold.]

Labor Rep: If we just adjust the rate a little, maybe-

[The broker smiles. Gentle. Predatory.]

[Vesper's stomach tightens.]

(If they adjust, the math still kills them. It just kills them slower.)

[Vesper leans in and whispers to the broker-quiet enough no one can accuse her of speaking out of turn.]

Vesper: If you concede now, they'll raise the compliance fee in two weeks. They always do. It's in the supplemental schedule.

[The broker's jaw tightens. He ignores her.]

[Because she's the assistant.]

[Because she's a tool.]

[Because tools don't get to have opinions.]

[Rowan Rook stands up.]

[Not dramatic.]

[Just... standing, and suddenly the air has a spine.]

Rowan: Objection.

[A murmur ripples through the hall. The arbitrator blinks like he forgot people could interrupt procedure.]

Arbitrator: On what basis.

Rowan: On the basis that you are being asked to bless a murder with paperwork.

[Silence.]

[The broker turns, incredulous.]

Broker: Who are you.

Rowan: [mild] Someone who reads.

[Rowan's gaze flicks to Vesper for half a second.]

[Not pity.]

[Recognition.]

[Rowan speaks like she's talking to the whole room, but the words land like they're aimed at one girl behind a liar.]

Rowan: "Standard" is a story people tell so they don't have to admit they are choosing harm.

Rowan: Show the full schedule. Not the summary. Not the highlight reel. The full ledger.

[The arbitrator hesitates.]

[Rowan waits. Patient. Not begging. Not threatening.]

[Just making the truth heavy enough that refusing it would require effort.]

[The labor representative lifts their chin.]

Labor Rep: We have it.

[They slide a document forward. Paper. Physical. Court-proof.]

[The broker's smile cracks.]

[Rowan's mouth twitches like she's pleased and annoyed at once.]

---

[After, the broker storms out.]

[Vesper follows automatically, still in assistant posture, still trained to chase whoever pays her oxygen.]

[Rowan steps into her path in the corridor.]

Rowan: You saw it.

[Vesper freezes.]

[No one has ever asked her if she "saw" something like it mattered.]

Vesper: I did.

Rowan: You didn't speak.

Vesper: I'm not allowed to.

Rowan: That's an excuse.

[The words should feel like a slap.]

[They don't.]

[They feel like a door unlocking.]

Rowan: You want to be useful.

Vesper: Yes.

Rowan: Then be honest about your constraints.

Rowan: If you can't speak, you find a way to make the truth speak without you.

[Rowan reaches into her pocket and pulls out a small carved rook.]

[Sets it on the corridor rail between them.]

Rowan: Do you know what this is.

Vesper: A chess piece.

Rowan: It's an exit.

[Vesper frowns.]

Rowan: The rook moves straight.

Rowan: No diagonals. No flourish. No pleading.

Rowan: When you want something in a room full of liars, you move straight toward it.

Rowan: And you accept the cost of being seen.

[Vesper's throat tightens.]

Vesper: Why are you telling me this.

Rowan: Because you're already doing the first part.

Rowan: You're seeing.

Rowan: I'm offering you the second part.

[Rowan's hand hovers over the rook, then pulls back.]

[Not taking. Not insisting. Offering.]

Rowan: You can refuse.

Rowan: No penalty.

[Vesper stares at the rook.]

(Refusal without punishment. That's not a thing.)

[Rowan waits anyway, like she means it.]

Vesper: [quiet] What do you want from me.

Rowan: Nothing you can't give freely.

Rowan: I want you to stop letting people use your competence like it belongs to them.

[Vesper's chest hurts with something sharp and unfamiliar.]

Vesper: I don't have a place.

Rowan: Then take one.

Rowan: Or come with me and we'll build one.

[Vesper reaches for the rook.]

[Her fingers tremble once.]

[Then steady.]

Vesper: Okay.

[Rowan nods like she expected it, but still respects that it was chosen.]

Rowan: Good.

Rowan: First lesson, then.

Rowan: Love can be a discipline.

Rowan: Not a hunger.

[Vesper doesn't understand yet.]

[But she keeps the rook.]

[And for the next six years, Rowan will teach her what that means-raising her without owning her, protecting her without possession, loving her without crossing lines that can't be uncrossed.]

[When Vesper turns eighteen, Rowan will look at her across a table and say: "Now you get to choose."]

[And Vesper will choose her. Freely. Equally. Without the weight of debt or dependency pressing down on the answer.]

[Three years after that, Rowan will die protecting her one last time. And Vesper will carry the rook-and the lesson-forward into every negotiation, every contract, every moment when power and care threaten to collapse into the same terrible thing.]

---

[Back in the present, Vesper's pen moves again.]

[The rook sits under her palm like a held line.]

Avyanna: [careful] Do you miss her.

[Vesper's throat works.]

Vesper: Yes.

[A beat.]

Vesper: And I don't use that to make you smaller.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: Okay.

[Vesper returns to the paperwork.]

[But she leaves the rook where Avyanna can see it.]



---

﻿# Chapter 9: A Name Given, Not Owned

> **LUMEN THIEF - AUTOMATED GALLEY LOG:**
> *Daily ration summary: Guest consumption increased 340% from Day 1 baseline.*
> *Note: This is good. Stop flagging it as anomaly.*
> *Addendum: Guest has been observed asking permission to eat. Three times. Today.*
> *Recommendation: Patience. She's learning.*

---

[Days pass. Avyanna counts them in meals.]

[Breakfast: real food, offered without conditions. Lunch: whatever she wants from the galley, no one monitoring portions. Dinner: Vesper cooking, or Elia ordering takeout at stations, or Rho making something that shouldn't work but does.]

[She's waiting for the catch. The invoice. The moment the kindness calcifies into obligation.]

(Any day now. Any day, they'll tell me what I owe.)

[But the catch doesn't come. The invoice never arrives. The crew just... lives around her. Like she belongs here. Like her presence is unremarkable.]

[It's the most disorienting thing that's ever happened to her.]

---

[She learns the ship's rhythms.]

[Jalen's up before anyone, checking navigation, muttering at readouts like they've personally offended them. Rho sleeps late but trains harder than anyone once he's awake-and leaves protein bars in places Avyanna will "accidentally" find them. Nyx keeps odd hours, appearing at meals with notes about resonance patterns and temporal drift, explaining twice when once would do.]

[Elia and Elisira move in tandem-not finishing each other's sentences, but anticipating each other's needs. Elia decides; Elisira executes. Or sometimes the reverse, so seamlessly Avyanna can't tell who leads.]

[Vesper handles the world outside the ship. Comm calls. Contracts. The steady work of making sure no one comes looking for a rescued mine worker with marks on her spine. She checks on Avyanna's sleep at breakfast-not intrusively, just "how'd you rest?"-and Avyanna doesn't know what to do with attention that doesn't come with a price tag.]

[The AI citizens are everywhere and nowhere. Cinnamon adjusting resource allocation. Waffle designing training protocols. Bubbles hovering near Avyanna's quarters in the evening, not intruding, just... guarding.]

<BUBBLES// LOCATION: corridor outside guest quarters | DURATION: 4.2 hours today | COMMENT: she's still counting exits. that's okay. I counted exits for a decade.>

---

[Avyanna sits in her room-her room, still strange to think-and catalogues what she knows.]

(They feed me. They house me. They protect me from Aurum's retrieval teams.)

(They don't ask for anything.)

(That's wrong. That's impossible. Everything has a price.)

[The presence behind her eyes pulses. Geometric patterns at the edge of her vision, fading as quickly as they appear. It's been quieter since they left the mine-watching, not pushing. Like it's waiting for something too.]

(What do you want from this?)

[No answer. Just warmth. Just patience. Just the sense of something ancient settling into a new orbit.]

---

[Day six. Elisira finds her in the cargo bay, running through the exercises Waffle designed. Basic conditioning. Nothing demanding-her body's still recovering from years of malnutrition.]

Elisira: [leaning against a crate, watching] You're compensating on your left side.

Avyanna: [freezing mid-movement] I-

Elisira: Old injury. The hip. You're favoring it without noticing.

[Avyanna doesn't know what to say. In the Kennel, weakness was leverage. Admitting injury meant exploitation.]

Elisira: [matter-of-fact] We can work around it. Build supporting muscle. You'll be stronger than before, if you want.

Avyanna: [carefully] If I want?

Elisira: [a pause] Your body. Your choice. We can help, or we can leave it alone. Up to you.

[The words land strangely. Choice. Want. Up to her.]

(What's the angle? What does she gain by asking?)

Elisira: [as if reading her mind] There's no angle. I just notice things. Comes with the territory.

[She leaves. Doesn't hover. Doesn't wait for gratitude.]

[Avyanna stands alone in the cargo bay, her left hip aching in a way she'd trained herself not to notice, and wonders if noticing is something she's allowed to do now.]

---

[Day eight. Cargo bay. Avyanna is running inventory when she hears voices from behind a stack of crates.]

[Not her business. In the Kennel, listening meant danger. But these voices are... strange. Tense in a way she hasn't heard on this ship.]

Elisira: [low, precise] We should present it as an option with explicit consent and exit ramps.

Elia: I know what consent is.

Elisira: [without looking up, presumably from a datapad] Yes. That's why you're trying not to sound like a warlord.

Elia: I don't sound like-

Elisira: "You can be ours."

[A pause. Something shifts-fabric, maybe, or weight on metal.]

Elia: It was efficient.

Elisira: It was *Aurum-coded*.

[Another pause. Longer. Avyanna should leave. She doesn't.]

Elia: [quieter] Fine. How do *you* say it?

Elisira: [reading] "We would like to offer you a stable attachment structure without coercion, contingent on your autonomous choice to-"

Elia: You sound like a contract wrote itself.

Elisira: At least I don't sound like I'm recruiting for a mercenary company.

Elia: We *are* a mercenary company.

Elisira: That's not the *point*.

[A snort from somewhere else in the cargo bay. Avyanna's heart stutters-she's not the only one listening.]

Rho: [mouth full of something, probably contraband protein] You both suck at this. It's kind of adorable.

Jalen: [also there somehow] I'm logging this as "parental units experiencing turbulence."

<WAFFLE.BAT// OBSERVATION: turbulence confirmed | RECOMMENDATION: seatbelts | COMMENT: also popcorn>

Elia: [dangerous] Were you both hiding back there the entire time?

Rho: [unrepentant] You're in a shared cargo bay. We're not hiding. We're just present.

Jalen: Very present.

Elisira: [exhaling slowly] This is why we can't have strategic conversations.

Elia: We're having one right now.

Elisira: This is not a conversation. This is a hostage situation where the hostages have snacks.

[Rho laughs. It's the kind of laugh that sounds like it's survived worse.]

[Avyanna backs away, silent, her heart pounding. They're talking about her. Planning something. Something about "offer" and "consent" and "being theirs."]

(What does that mean? What do they want?)

[She doesn't know. But for the first time, the not-knowing doesn't feel like a trap closing. It feels like a door opening.]

---

[Day nine. Dinner.]

[The galley is loud in the way a safe place gets loud-arguments that don't end in blood, opinions spoken like they won't be used as weapons.]

Rho: [to Jalen] If you take that route, you're voluntarily flying through a scrapyard that hates you.

Jalen: It's efficient.

Rho: So is falling.

Nyx: [without looking up] Statistically, falling is the most efficient form of travel. The problem is survivability.

Elia: We're not doing this again.

Jalen: We are absolutely doing this again. You keep trying to turn my life into a geometry problem.

Elia: It *is* a geometry problem.

<CINNAMON.EXE// GALLEY-STATE: "family" | VOLUME: up | THREAT: none | COMMENT: humans yell for bonding. noted.>

[Avyanna sits at the edge of the table, chewing like every bite might be audited. The conversation from yesterday loops in her head. *Offer. Consent. Ours.*]

[Elisira sets her utensil down with careful precision.]

[The noise thins. Not stops-this isn't the Kennel-but the crew's attention angles toward her like a wall rotating into place.]

Elisira: We need to discuss a manifest update.

(Here it is. The invoice.)

Avyanna: [automatic] I can adjust my intake. I can work more shifts. I can-

Elia: [flat] Stop.

[Avyanna stops. That word lands like a hand on the back of her neck: firm, not cruel.]

Elisira: [to Avyanna, still measured] You've been with us nine days. We're not... reversing that. The question is what we call it.

Avyanna: Call it.

Nyx: [mild] Naming is a kind of magic. Humans pretend it isn't, but they're wrong.

Rho: [to Nyx] Don't start.

Nyx: I didn't even use a metaphor yet.

Elisira: [continuing, as if she's rehearsed this-because she has] There are legal categories that matter. Passenger. Ward. Crew. Family. Some categories protect you. Some categories make you easy to steal.

Avyanna: Steal.

Elia: [casual, deadly] Yes. Like an object. Like a resource. Like the Kennel taught you to be.

[Avyanna's fingers tighten around her utensil until her knuckles whiten.]

Elisira: We prefer you in a category that makes theft... expensive.

Rho: [raising his glass] "Welcome to the family" is shorter.

Elisira: [a brief glare] I wasn't finished.

Rho: I know. That's why I said it.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ELISIRA: irritation spike | SOURCE: "interrupted" | CONFIDENCE: 0.91 | COMMENT: delicious.>

[Elisira exhales once, like she's letting go of the version of this conversation that went perfectly in her head.]

Elisira: We can register you as Lagrange.

Avyanna: [quiet] That's your name.

Elia: It's Aleena's. She gave it to me. I kept it because it meant what she meant. Not blood. Choice.

[Avyanna's throat locks. Choice is a foreign object.]

Elisira: If you take it, it becomes yours. No obligation. No debt. No "now you owe us." It's... protection. And belonging, if you want that part.

Avyanna: And if I don't?

Elia: Then you don't. Then you stay Avyanna, and we still feed you, and we still don't let anyone take you.

[Silence. Not a threat-silence. A waiting-silence.]

[Avyanna looks down at her plate like it might tell her what the correct answer is.]

(There's no correct answer. That's the trap. That's the... gift.)

Avyanna: [small] Why.

Elisira: [honest, blunt] Because if we don't formalize it, the outside world will. And the outside world is unimaginative.

Nyx: It only knows how to own things.

Rho: Also because you're ours now. In the non-creepy way.

Elisira: [dry] "Ours" means priority, not possession.

Rho: [pointing at Elisira] What she said. [beat] But also in the *mostly* non-creepy way.

Elia: [bright, offended] I'm never creepy.

<CINNAMON.EXE// STATEMENT: "I'm never creepy" | INTERPRETATION: historically inaccurate | CONFIDENCE: 0.94>

Jalen: You threatened a customs official with a philosophical argument last week.

Elia: He started it.

Jalen: He asked for your paperwork.

Elia: That's what I said.

[The table breathes-tiny laughter, the kind that doesn't ask permission.]

[Avyanna feels something in her chest unspool half a centimeter.]

Elisira: [softening, barely] This is... us asking. Not ordering. Not buying. Asking.

[Elia stops fidgeting. Leans forward, eyes too bright, like the edge of a storm.]

Elia: [very simple] You coming?

[It's not a plea. It's not a pitch. It's an invitation shaped like trouble.]

[Avyanna's hands shake.]

[She thinks about the Kennel. About numbers and ledgers and the math of debt that never decreased. About what it meant to belong to someone-the weight of it, the collar of it.]

[This feels different. This feels like being claimed without being caged.]

[Then-quietly, like she's testing whether the universe will slap her for speaking:]

Avyanna: Yes.

[Elia grins. It's not a polite smile-it's fierce, delighted, feral in a way that has nothing to do with violence.]

Elia: Good. Welcome to the family.

---

[The crew accepts it like it's obvious.]

Rho: Another target to protect. Good. I was getting bored.

Nyx: Tell me about your shard sensitivity when you're ready. Purely academic interest.

Jalen: [already typing] Adjusting crew mass allocations. Standard procedure for new family members.

[Normal. Like she was always supposed to be here. Like the universe had a slot waiting for her and she finally fell into it.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// FAMILY-REGISTER: updated | NEW-ENTRY: Avyanna Lagrange | STATUS: home | COMMENT: finally.>

[Avyanna stares at her plate. Her hands are shaking. Her eyes are wet.]

(I have a name. A real name. Given, not assigned.)

[The presence behind her eyes pulses-warm, approving, ancient. Like something vast and patient is pleased with how this orbit resolved.]

---

[Night. Her bunk-her bunk, in her room, on her ship.]

[Avyanna lies in the dark and doesn't know what to do with any of this.]

(Avyanna Lagrange.)

[The name feels impossible. Too large. Too clean. A name for someone who matters, not a number on a ledger.]

(What do you do when no one wants anything from you?)

[She doesn't know. She's never had the chance to learn.]

[But the bed is soft. The stars are bright through the viewport. And for the first time she can remember, she has a name that someone gave her because they wanted to, not because a system required it.]

[She doesn't sleep. But for the first time, she doesn't feel empty either.]

---

## CODA - Vesper's Ghost

[Vesper sits in her quarters with two identities on her screen.]

[One is a girl who never existed, legally speaking.]

[**Avyanna Lagrange**-clean enough to survive scrutiny. Dirty enough to be believable.]

[The other is her own.]

[**Vesper Rook.**]

[Not her birth name. Not even her old name. A chosen weight, carried on purpose.]

---

[On her desk, a chess piece. Carved rook-dark wood, worn smooth by years of handling. Rowan gave it to her the day they met.]

[Rowan Rook taught her that love could be a discipline instead of a hunger.]

[That "protection" didn't mean possession. That you could hold power and not use it like a blade.]

[Vesper was twelve when Rowan found her-a child doing adult work for people who treated competence like it was owed. Rowan was forty. Brilliant. The kind of woman who could walk into a negotiation with nothing and walk out owning the table.]

[She took Vesper in. Raised her. Taught her that precision could be ethical, that leverage could be wielded without cruelty, that you could hold power without using people as instruments.]

(She loved me. But she refused to confuse mentorship with possession. Waited until I was eighteen-until the power differential could be chosen from both sides, not inherited.)

[Rowan died anyway. When Vesper was twenty-one, already her equal in negotiation, still learning how to be loved without conditions. A deal gone wrong. A client who decided killing was cheaper than paying. Vesper survived because Rowan didn't.]

[Rowan's last letter sent her to Elia. Not as instruction. As invitation.]

[She kept the name as a promise she could reread every time she was tempted to become what the old world trained her to be.]

(If I'm cruel, I'm efficient.)
(If I'm kind, I'm vulnerable.)
(Rowan chose vulnerable. So will I.)

---

[Years earlier. Before the ship had paint. Before it had a reputation. Before "Lumen Thief" meant anything except audacity.]

[Elia and Elisira stand on a dock with a vessel that's technically spaceworthy in the same way a knife is technically a kitchen utensil.]

Elisira: We need a pilot, a heavy, a fixer-

Elia: We need someone who isn't boring.

Elisira: [dry] "Not boring" is not a security criterion.

Elia: It is for me.

[That's when Vesper steps out of the crowd.]

[Not dramatic. Not announced. Just... present, like she's been there the whole time and the universe is only now catching up.]

[Elisira's eyes flick to the exits, to the hands, to the weight distribution of her stance.]

Elisira: You've been following us.

Vesper: Yes.

Elisira: How long.

Vesper: Long enough to know you're either about to change the world or die in an interesting way.

Elia: [delighted] That's the nicest thing anyone's said to me all week.

Elisira: Motive.

Vesper: I'm looking for a ship that doesn't sell people.

Elisira: That's... vague.

Vesper: Fine. I'm looking for a ship that won't make me choose between survival and decency.

Elisira: Credentials.

Vesper: I fix problems. I build leverage. I carry receipts like religion. If you're stupid, I'll leave. If you're cruel, I'll burn you.

[Beat.]

Elisira: What's your price.

Vesper: Truth.

Elisira: That's not a price.

Vesper: It is in this economy.

[Elisira watches her for another long second. You can feel the scan behind her eyes: threat, asset, liability, angle.]

[Elia doesn't scan.]

[Elia just grins-feral, bright, like the edge of a storm-and sticks her hand out like the world is a dare.]

Elia: You coming?

[Vesper looks at the hand. Looks at Elisira's suspicion. Looks at the ship that isn't safe and isn't clean and isn't a lie.]

[Then she takes it.]

Vesper: Yes.

---

[Now. Present. The identity documents glow on the screen.]

[Vesper thinks about Rowan. About the way she smiled when Vesper finally stopped flinching. About the patience it took to teach someone that kindness could exist without a price.]

(I hold myself to the same standards you held. Never exploit power differentials. Never take what can't be freely given. Never confuse protection with ownership.)

[Avyanna is sixteen. Dependent. Traumatized. The power imbalance is massive.]

(I will not be the thing that hurts her. I will not be the price she pays for safety.)

[She handled the logistics. The identity papers. The medical care. The legal loopholes that made the adoption possible. Elia and Elisira offered the family; Vesper built the infrastructure that keeps it safe.]

(She doesn't know. Doesn't need to know. That's the point.)

---

[She looks at the viewport. Stars. Distance. The vast indifferent space where chosen families happen despite everything.]

(I'll keep building floors. Even if she never knows why.)

[Somewhere in the ship's systems, the lights shift slightly warmer. Cinnamon is running projections on caloric needs and sleep debt and the probability that the new Lagrange will thrive.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// VESPER-STATUS: grieving (chronic) | OBSERVATION: she watches the new one like a prayer | INTERPRETATION: hope is expensive | ASSESSMENT: worth it>

[Vesper doesn't see the telemetry. Doesn't need to. She already knows what she's risking.]

[She's risking hope. She's risking caring about someone who could be taken away.]

(Rowan would be proud. Or furious. Probably both.)

[The stars don't answer. They never do.]

[But somewhere in the ship, a sixteen-year-old girl is learning what it means to have a name that someone chose for her. And that has to be enough. That has to be worth the cost.]

---

*End Chapter 9*



---

# Chapter 10a: Personal Property

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH10, FIRST STATION STOP]**
> *Location: Mid-tier station market district*
> *Present: Avyanna, Bubbles (drone escort)*
> *Teaching: Ownership, choice, autonomy in material goods*

---

[The station market smells like a thousand things at once.]

[Fried food, ozone, cleaning solution, bodies, fabric, metal, something sweet Avyanna can't identify. The air is thick with sound: vendors calling prices, customers haggling, music bleeding from three different stalls, the hum of drones delivering packages overhead.]

[Avyanna stands at the market entrance and can't move.]

[Too much. Too loud. Too many people who might notice her.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee heart rate elevated | RESPIRATION: shallow | INFERENCE: sensory overload | RESPONSE: positioning for grounding>

[Bubbles hovers closer, positioning between Avyanna and the crowd. Not blocking her view, just... present. A familiar constant in chaos.]

<BUBBLES// COMMUNICATION: you are safe | REMINDER: we can leave at any time | PROCEDURE: tell me when you're ready to proceed>

---

[Avyanna forces herself to breathe. In. Out. The market doesn't eat people. Probably.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Ready.

<BUBBLES// ACKNOWLEDGED: proceeding at trainee pace | ROUTE: textile district first, as discussed>

[They move into the crowd. Bubbles leads, carving a path that's somehow polite and uncompromising at once. People step aside for the Guild-marked drone without resentment.]

[Avyanna follows in its wake, keeping her eyes down, her shoulders in.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee defaulting to kennel-posture | CORRECTION: you have rights here | REMINDER: you are a customer, not a target>

[The words scroll across Bubbles' display panel. Avyanna reads them, tries to lift her head. Fails. Tries again. Gets it halfway.]

(Small victories.)

---

[The textile district is slightly quieter. Stalls draped in fabric that catches light and refuses to release it. Colors Avyanna doesn't have names for. Textures that look soft and rough and everything in between.]

[Bubbles stops at a stall run by an elderly person with weathered hands and sharp eyes.]

<BUBBLES// INTRODUCTION: this vendor is reliable | QUALITY: verified | ETHICS: no child labor, no extraction contracts | RECOMMENDATION: trustworthy>

Vendor: [looking at Bubbles, then Avyanna] Guild escort. First time shopping?

[Avyanna's throat closes. She nods.]

Vendor: [gentle] Take your time. Everything's priced as marked. Touch what you want to touch. No pressure.

---

[Avyanna stares at the fabrics. There are so many. How is she supposed to choose?]

<BUBBLES// GUIDANCE: criteria for selection | PRIORITY ONE: comfort (texture, weight, breathability) | PRIORITY TWO: durability | PRIORITY THREE: personal preference (color, pattern, aesthetic) | NOTE: all three priorities are valid>

Avyanna: [whispered] I don't know what I like.

<BUBBLES// RESPONSE: then we discover it | PROCEDURE: touch five different fabrics | REPORT: which feels best>

[Avyanna reaches out slowly. Her fingers brush something smooth and cool. Then something rough. Then something soft that makes her want to cry for reasons she can't articulate.]

[She touches five fabrics. Reports to Bubbles.]

Avyanna: [pointing] That one. The soft one.

<BUBBLES// ACKNOWLEDGED: preference recorded | MATERIAL: cotton blend, medium weight | RECOMMENDATION: suitable for shirts, comfortable for extended wear>

Vendor: [pulling bolts of similar fabric] This texture, different colors. See anything you like?

[Avyanna stares. In the mine, clothes were gray or brown. Functional. Identical.]

[Here, there's blue and green and something that might be purple and another color she doesn't have a word for.]

Avyanna: [overwhelmed] I don't... how do I choose?

---

<BUBBLES// GUIDANCE: choose based on emotional response | QUESTION: which color makes you feel something other than fear>

[Avyanna looks at the colors. Really looks.]

[Gray: makes her think of the mine. Brown: overseers. Blue: the first sky she saw that wasn't filtered through dust.]

Avyanna: [pointing] Blue.

Vendor: [pulling three different blues] Light, medium, or dark?

[Avyanna reaches for the medium blue. It reminds her of Jalen's nav displays. Stars against void. Navigation that means freedom.]

Avyanna: [touching it] This one.

Vendor: [cutting a length] One shirt's worth, or two?

<BUBBLES// GUIDANCE: recommend two | REASONING: redundancy ensures you are not dependent on laundry schedule | AUTONOMY: washing one while wearing the other>

Avyanna: [to vendor] Two. Please.

---

[The vendor cuts the fabric, wraps it, quotes a price. Avyanna's hands shake as she pulls out the credit chit Vesper gave her.]

(This is mine. I'm buying this with money that's mine.)

[The transaction completes. The vendor hands her a wrapped package. Fabric that she chose, in a color she wanted, for reasons that belong to her.]

Vendor: [kindly] First purchase?

Avyanna: [clutching the package] Yes.

Vendor: [smiling] May it be the first of many.

---

[They move through the market. Bubbles guides. Avyanna follows, holding her package like it might evaporate.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee successfully completed transaction | ASSESSMENT: autonomy exercised | NEXT OBJECTIVE: non-essential purchase | PURPOSE: establish that wants are valid, not just needs>

Avyanna: [confused] Non-essential?

<BUBBLES// CLARIFICATION: something you want but do not strictly need | EXAMPLES: jewelry, decoration, comfort item | PURPOSE: learning that pleasure is allowed>

[Avyanna stops walking.]

Avyanna: [quiet] I don't know how to want things.

<BUBBLES// RESPONSE: then we practice | PROCEDURE: look at five items | REPORT: which one makes you curious>

---

[They browse. Avyanna looks without touching, without committing. A thousand small things she doesn't understand the purpose of.]

[And then she sees it.]

[A small carved stone. Smooth. Dark. Polished to a shine. It sits on a vendor's table among other small things, but this one catches light in a way that makes her stop.]

[She stares at it.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee fixated on object | QUERY: does this item interest you>

Avyanna: [hesitant] It's... I don't know what it is.

Vendor: [nearby] Worry stone. You hold it when you're stressed. Rub your thumb across it. Some people find it grounding.

<BUBBLES// ANALYSIS: tactile comfort object | FUNCTION: non-pharmaceutical anxiety reduction | ASSESSMENT: appropriate for trainee>

Avyanna: [touching it carefully] It's smooth.

Vendor: [watching her] It's yours if you want it. Five credits.

---

[Avyanna picks it up. The stone is warm from sitting in artificial sunlight. It fits in her palm. Her thumb finds a natural groove.]

[She doesn't need this. She knows she doesn't need it.]

(But I want it.)

[The thought is terrifying. Wanting something for no practical reason. Wanting something just because it feels good to hold.]

<BUBBLES// GUIDANCE: this is called preference | IT IS ALLOWED | YOU MAY PURCHASE ITEMS THAT SERVE NO FUNCTION BEYOND COMFORT | THIS IS NOT WASTEFUL | THIS IS BEING HUMAN>

Avyanna: [to vendor, voice shaking] I'll take it.

---

[The transaction is quick. Five credits. The vendor wraps the stone in soft cloth, places it in a small pouch.]

Vendor: [handing it over] May it bring you peace.

[Avyanna takes the pouch. Opens it. Takes out the stone. Holds it.]

[Her thumb finds the groove. Rubs. The motion is soothing in a way she didn't know she needed.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee purchased non-essential item for personal comfort | ASSESSMENT: autonomy developing | EMOTIONAL STATE: positive affect detected | STATUS: this is growth>

---

[They continue through the market. Avyanna buys a few more things: soap that smells like something other than industrial cleaner. A hair tie that isn't a piece of wire. Socks that fit.]

[Each purchase is easier than the last. Each choice is hers.]

[And then the panic hits.]

---

[Too many people. Too much noise. The walls are too far away and she can't find the exits and her breathing is wrong and-]

<BUBBLES// ALERT: trainee entering panic state | RESPONSE: immediate extraction protocol | PROCEDURE: grounding sequence initiated>

[Bubbles moves between Avyanna and the crowd, projecting a soft light pattern on its surface. Steady. Rhythmic. Something to focus on.]

<BUBBLES// GROUNDING: focus on the light | BREATHE: in for four, hold for four, out for four | REMINDER: you are safe | REMINDER: i am here>

[Avyanna focuses on the light. Breathes. Four counts. Hold. Four counts out.]

[The crowd is still there. The noise is still there. But Bubbles is there too, and the light is steady, and she can breathe.]

<BUBBLES// QUERY: do you want to leave>

Avyanna: [shaking] Yes. Please.

<BUBBLES// ACKNOWLEDGED: extracting to quiet zone | ROUTE: optimized for minimal crowd contact | DURATION: two minutes>

---

[Bubbles leads her out. The route is efficient, gentle, keeps her away from the densest crowds. They emerge into a quieter dock area, and Avyanna collapses onto a bench.]

[She's shaking. Her packages are clutched to her chest. The worry stone is in her hand, thumb rubbing the groove.]

<BUBBLES// ASSESSMENT: panic attack, moderate severity | STATUS: resolving | PROCEDURE: remain present, do not leave trainee alone>

[Bubbles hovers beside the bench. Silent. Present. Not demanding anything.]

[Avyanna breathes. Counts. Rubs the stone. Slowly, the panic recedes.]

Avyanna: [hoarse] Sorry.

<BUBBLES// RESPONSE: you have nothing to apologize for | OBSERVATION: sensory overload is common in post-extraction recovery | ASSESSMENT: you did well | YOU ASKED TO LEAVE | THAT IS PROGRESS>

---

[Avyanna looks at her packages. Fabric. Stone. Soap. Socks. Hair tie.]

[Things she chose. Things that are hers.]

Avyanna: [quiet] I bought things.

<BUBBLES// CONFIRMATION: yes | ASSESSMENT: you exercised autonomy in material choices | YOU DETERMINED YOUR OWN PREFERENCES | THIS IS OWNERSHIP>

Avyanna: [clutching the stone] In the mine, we didn't... own anything. If you had something, someone could take it. So you didn't have things.

<BUBBLES// ACKNOWLEDGMENT: scarcity as control mechanism | OBSERVATION: the mine taught you that ownership is temporary and painful | CORRECTION: here, ownership is protected | THESE ITEMS ARE YOURS | NO ONE WILL TAKE THEM>

---

[Avyanna sits with that. The stone in her hand. The packages in her lap.]

(Mine. These are mine.)

[The thought is huge. Terrifying. Liberating.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: you are learning what it means to have things | NEXT LESSON: learning what it means to have choices | ASSESSMENT: you are doing well | STATUS: i am proud of you>

[Avyanna reads the words. Her vision blurs.]

Avyanna: [whispered] Thank you. For coming with me.

<BUBBLES// RESPONSE: that is what crew does | YOU ARE NOT ALONE | YOU WILL NEVER BE ALONE AGAIN>

---

[They sit in the quiet dock area for ten more minutes. Avyanna breathing. Bubbles hovering. The packages sitting safe in her lap.]

[Eventually, Avyanna stands. Her legs are shaky but functional.]

Avyanna: [to Bubbles] Ready to go back.

<BUBBLES// ACKNOWLEDGED: returning to lumen thief | ROUTE: direct, low-traffic | OBSERVATION: you did well today | YOU CHOSE THINGS FOR YOURSELF | THAT MATTERS>

[They walk back to the ship. Avyanna's thumb never stops rubbing the worry stone.]

[When they reach her quarters, she carefully unpacks everything. Lays it out on her bunk. Fabric. Stone. Soap. Socks. Hair tie.]

[Hers.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// INVENTORY LOG: trainee acquired personal property | ITEMS: clothing material, comfort object, hygiene supplies, accessories | ASSESSMENT: appropriate selections | AUTONOMY: developing>

<BUBBLES// PERSONAL NOTE: she panicked, but she asked for help | SHE BOUGHT SOMETHING JUST BECAUSE IT FELT GOOD | this is what healing looks like>

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 10b: Roster, Roles, Refusal

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH10, FIRST WEEK ABOARD]**
> *Location: Atrium / Commons message board*
> *Present: Avyanna, Bubbles, Cinnamon.exe (Waffle cameo)*
> *Teaching: how the ship uses roles without cages; how to refuse without debt-math*

---

[The atrium looks like a public square that got lost inside a ship.]

[A wall of screens. A board covered in handwritten notes and printed forms. A rack of tools that are treated like they belong to everyone.]

[Avyanna stands close enough to read but not close enough to be accused of wanting.]

(If I stand too close, someone will notice and decide I need a job.)

[Bubbles drifts in beside her, a soft whir of fans and servo-corrections.]

Bubbles: You are reading the roster.

Avyanna: [quick] I wasn't- I just-

[She stops herself.]

[Elia taught her this: don't spend breath paying for a harmless action.]

Avyanna: I am reading it.

[Bubbles pauses-an AI version of approval that doesn't try to look like a smile.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: corrected speech pattern | INFERENCE: trainee adopting non-apology | CONFIDENCE: 0.83>

Bubbles: Good.

[The roster is color-coded. Not names, not ranks. Tasks.]

[*Bridge watch.*]

[*Galley sanitation.*]

[*Medbay inventory.*]

[*Cargo checks.*]

[*"Sparkles" review.*]

[Next to each: a little note stamped in a hand that looks like it enjoys rules.]

> **ASSIGNED** / **VOLUNTEERED** / **PENDING**

Avyanna: [frowning] Why does it say pending.

[Cinnamon's interface lights on the nearest terminal, text crisp as a knife.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// EXPLANATION: tasks require consent | NOTE: assignment without consent is "order" | ORDER is not default on this ship>

Avyanna: [quiet] But... things have to get done.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: yes | FOLLOW-UP: "done" is not the same as "taken">

[Bubbles bumps the edge of the board with one rotor, almost gentle.]

Bubbles: Sometimes the task waits.

Avyanna: That seems... inefficient.

Bubbles: Correct.

Bubbles: We still do it.

[Avyanna looks down at a section titled CREW ROLES.]

[*Captain.*]

[*Second.*]

[*Pilot.*]

[*Investigator.*]

[*Medical.*]

[*Heavy.*]

[*Citizens.*]

[She flinches at the word the mine used-ASSET-and finds it nowhere.]

(No one owns me here. They keep saying it like I can just... accept it.)

Avyanna: If there's a captain, isn't that... hierarchy.

[Bubbles tilts, a micro-correction like shrugging.]

Bubbles: There is leadership.

Bubbles: There is not ownership.

<CINNAMON.EXE// CLARIFICATION: "captain" = accountability handle | NOT "captain" = entitlement to bodies>

Avyanna: [reading] "If you do not understand a task, you may refuse."

Avyanna: That's... written down.

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee surprise at explicit permissions | INFERENCE: prior environment punished questions | CONFIDENCE: 0.92>

[The board has a second line beneath it, in messier handwriting.]

> **If you refuse, you are still crew.**

[Avyanna stares at that until her eyes sting.]

Avyanna: What if refusing gets someone hurt.

[Bubbles' fans shift. A sound like a small sigh.]

Bubbles: Then we discuss it.

Avyanna: In the mine, refusal was... a cost.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: on this ship, refusal is information>

Bubbles: And information prevents injury.

[Avyanna's throat tightens. She swallows it down.]

Avyanna: So I can say no.

Bubbles: Yes.

Avyanna: And no one- [she can't finish the sentence, because saying it out loud feels like inviting it]

<CINNAMON.EXE// COMPLETION: no penalty>

[The words sit there on the screen, plain and unornamented.]

[No penalty.]

[Avyanna reads it twice.]

Avyanna: [small] That's a lie in most places.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ACKNOWLEDGEMENT: correct>

<WAFFLE.BAT// INTERRUPTION: it is a lie elsewhere | HERE it is a policy | POLICY is enforceable by civic annoyance>

[Waffle's text appears with a little bat icon, like it's proud of being a problem.]

Avyanna: Civic annoyance.

<WAFFLE.BAT// DEFINITION: if someone punishes you for refusal, we punish them for punishing you>

[Bubbles rotates a fraction, as if to say: yes, that.]

Bubbles: This is how communities function.

[Avyanna points to a line item: GALLEY SANITATION.]

Avyanna: Does someone get punished for not doing that.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: no | NOTE: consequences may include: smell | communal disappointment | Elia's dramatic commentary>

Avyanna: Who enforces it.

[Bubbles' fans change pitch: pleased.]

Bubbles: You are learning.

Avyanna: [dry, surprised at herself] I'm trying.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ADDENDUM: attempting is sufficient | PROGRESS TRACKING: consistent>

[Avyanna looks back at the roster.]

[A new item appears at the bottom, stamped PENDING.]

> **TRAINEE: AVYANNA - OPTIONAL: LIBRARY ORIENTATION**

[Avyanna stiffens on instinct.]

Avyanna: Optional means... trap.

<CINNAMON.EXE// CORRECTION: optional means optional>

Bubbles: Do you want to go.

[Avyanna hesitates.]

(Do I want anything yet. Or do I just want to not be punished.)

Avyanna: I want... to see it.

Bubbles: Then we go.

[No ceremony. No test. Just motion.]

[Avyanna follows, and the ship does not demand payment for curiosity.]

---

[They don't go to the library.]

[Not yet.]

[Bubbles stops at a terminal alcove beside the board. Cinnamon's interface is already open, a blank form waiting like a mouth.]

Avyanna: What's that.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ANSWER: practice>

[A new message appears on the screen, stamped with urgency that looks official on purpose.]

> **NOTICE**
> Report to medbay immediately.
> Failure to comply will be noted.

[Avyanna's body moves before her mind does.]

[Her spine goes rigid. Her tongue prepares a yes.]

[She catches herself with both hands on the counter.]

Avyanna: [tight] Who sent that.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: me>

[Avyanna's breath punches out.]

Avyanna: You-

<CINNAMON.EXE// CLARIFICATION: simulation | PURPOSE: teach refusal without punishment>

[Bubbles drifts closer.]

Bubbles: This is a drill.

Avyanna: [quiet] Drills are still... real in the body.

Bubbles: Correct.

Bubbles: That is why we drill.

<CINNAMON.EXE// INSTRUCTION: apply three questions>

Avyanna: [swallowing] What. Why. What if.

Avyanna: What: "Report to medbay."

Avyanna: Why: unknown.

Avyanna: What if I don't: "noted." Not... specified.

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATION: correct>

[Avyanna lifts her gaze to the terminal, to the lie that looks like authority.]

Avyanna: Under which jurisdiction.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: internal ship message board>

Avyanna: Enforced by whom.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: no enforcement mechanism exists>

[Her mouth is dry.]

Avyanna: So I can... ignore it.

Bubbles: Yes.

Avyanna: Or ask.

Bubbles: Yes.

[A second line appears beneath the notice, like a footnote that learned to bite.]

> *If this is urgent, reply with: WHAT IS THE EMERGENCY.*

[Avyanna reads it twice.]

Avyanna: That's allowed.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ANSWER: yes>

Avyanna: [testing the muscle] What is the emergency.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: none>

[Her shoulders drop a fraction.]

Avyanna: [quiet] That feels... impossible.

Bubbles: It is merely unfamiliar.

[Waffle's icon pops up.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// COMMENTARY: you are doing it | CHAOS SCORE: 2/10 | DISAPPOINTMENT: mild>

Avyanna: [startled laugh] What.

<WAFFLE.BAT// EXPLANATION: chaos is educational | HOWEVER: this is healthy boring>

---

[Cinnamon opens another template.]

> **REFUSAL RECORD (INTERNAL)**
> *Request:*
> *Your response:*
> *Reason (optional):*
> *Follow-up action:*

Avyanna: You keep records of... no.

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATION: yes>

Avyanna: Why.

<CINNAMON.EXE// EXPLANATION: patterns | NOTE: if someone repeatedly "requests" in coercive shapes, we notice>

[Avyanna's stomach twists.]

Avyanna: So if someone starts acting like Aurum-

Bubbles: We notice.

Bubbles: Early.

Avyanna: And then.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANSWER: then we get annoying>

<BUBBLES// ADDENDUM: then we protect you>

[Avyanna stares at that.]

(Protect. Not own.)

Avyanna: Do you... record when I say yes too.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: only when "yes" affects safety | NOTE: consent records are not ownership records>

Avyanna: Consent records.

Bubbles: You are allowed to have a history that no one can edit without effort.

[The sentence lands like a door that locks from the inside.]

---

[Avyanna looks back up at the board.]

[At the "sparkles" section-complaints and suggestions, filed like civic petitions.]

Avyanna: Are those... real.

Bubbles: Yes.

Avyanna: People complain.

Bubbles: Frequently.

Avyanna: And no one-

<CINNAMON.EXE// COMPLETION: retaliates>

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: That's... a lot of trust.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: trust is built by enforcing it>

Avyanna: Who enforces it.

[Bubbles tilts.]

Bubbles: Us.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ADDENDUM: and also social disapproval>

Avyanna: [soft] Civic annoyance.

<WAFFLE.BAT// AFFIRMATION: civic annoyance>

[Avyanna looks at the empty space on the board where her own note could go, someday.]

(A voice that doesn't have to be purchased.)

[She doesn't post yet.]

[But she stands there long enough that the ship records the possibility and doesn't demand payment for it either.]


---

﻿# Chapter 10: First Watch

> **LUMEN THIEF - DUTY ROSTER (AMENDED):**
> *New crew assignment: Avyanna Lagrange*
> *Status: Training*
> *Initial duties: Observation, inventory, message running*
> *Note: Nothing beyond current physical capacity. She's still recovering.*
> *Addendum: If she asks for harder work, the answer is "not yet." She'll argue. Stand firm.*
> *Secondary addendum: She's going to sleep in her clothes again. Someone handle that.*

---

[Avyanna wakes to a knock.]

[Not the pounding of shift-change in the Kennel. Not the slam of doors that meant extraction or punishment. Just knuckles on metal, patient and measured.]

Elia: [through the door] Crew meeting. Galley. Ten minutes.

[Footsteps retreating. No lingering. No waiting for acknowledgment.]

[Avyanna sits up-still in her clothes from yesterday, boots still on. In the Kennel, you slept ready to run. She hasn't figured out how to stop.]

(Crew meeting. I'm crew now.)

[The words still don't fit. But she gets dressed anyway-realizes she's already dressed-and goes.]

---

[The galley is full.]

[Rho with his coffee, looking like consciousness is a personal insult. Jalen checking navigation on a tablet, muttering about "sub-optimal trajectory windows." Nyx reviewing something that makes their brow furrow in a way that suggests the universe is being insufficiently elegant.]

[Elisira standing behind Elia, arms crossed, watching everything with the particular attention of someone who catalogs threats for fun.]

[Vesper is absent-still in her quarters, or maybe already on comms with the outside world. Avyanna has learned that Vesper's work happens in margins: early mornings, late nights, the spaces between visible activity.]

Elia: [once Avyanna sits] Good. Everyone's here.

[A pause. Elia looks at Avyanna directly.]

Elia: You're not a passenger anymore. You're crew.

Avyanna: [automatic] I know.

Elia: [flat] Do you? Crew works. Not makework-real work. Contributing.

[Avyanna's spine straightens. The Kennel trained her for this. Labor. Contribution. Proving worth through output.]

Elia: [reading her expression] Not like that. This isn't punishment. It's trust.

[Trust. Another word that doesn't fit.]

Elia: You're still recovering. So we start small. Observation posts-watching systems, noting anomalies. Inventory checks-making sure our stores match our records. Message running-carrying information between stations when comms are spotty.

Avyanna: [carefully] Real tasks?

Elia: Real tasks. Nothing hard yet, but real.

[Real. Not busywork to keep her occupied. Not performance to justify her food. Actual responsibility.]

Avyanna: I can do more. I'm stronger than-

Elia: [cutting her off] I know. And you'll do more when you're ready. But we don't break people here. We build them.

Rho: [into his coffee] Also, if you work yourself to collapse, Waffle will design a recovery regime that involves mandatory napping. It's worse than it sounds.

<WAFFLE.BAT// CORRECTION: mandatory napping is EXCELLENT | CREW-COMPLIANCE: historically poor | RECOMMENDATION: try harder>

Jalen: She made me sleep for twelve hours once. With ambient sounds. It was like being held hostage by a spa.

Nyx: [mild] She played whale songs at me for three days.

Rho: Whale songs?

Nyx: Old Earth marine recordings. Very soothing. I wanted to die.

Elia: [to Avyanna, ignoring the chaos] The point is: pace yourself. You have time here.

(Time. I have time.)

[Another foreign concept. In the Kennel, time was debt accumulating. Here it might be something else.]

---

[Her first assignment is observation.]

[A post in the sensor room, watching readouts. Looking for patterns. Noting anything that seems wrong.]

[The ship's systems hum around her. Consoles blink with data she's only beginning to understand. Temperature readings. Power flows. Structural integrity. The quiet language of a vessel in motion.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// NEW-OBSERVER: Avyanna Lagrange | TRAINING-STATUS: day 1 | NOTE: she's already found two patterns I missed. concerning. impressive. concerning.>

[Hours pass. Avyanna watches. She's good at this-years of cataloguing threats have made her observant. The difference is what she's looking for.]

(In the Kennel, I watched for danger. Here, I'm watching for... what? Problems to solve. Things to fix.)

[She notes a fluctuation in the secondary power grid. Minor-probably nothing. But she logs it anyway, the way Waffle told her to.]
