Waffle.bat: [through the speaker, approving] Good catch. That's been drifting for two days. I'll flag it for Jalen.

Avyanna: [surprised] You noticed it too?

Waffle.bat: I noticed you noticing. That's what I'm tracking.

[Avyanna doesn't know what to do with that. Someone watching her performance not to punish, but to assess. To help.]

Waffle.bat: [gentler] You're doing well. The instincts are there. We just need to point them in useful directions.

---

[Mid-morning. Elia finds her in the corridor, heading toward inventory.]

Elia: Message run. First one.

[She hands Avyanna a datapad.]

Elia: Take this to Nyx in the lab. It's a manifest update for their resonance equipment. Tell them the numbers are preliminary but actionable.

Avyanna: [automatic] Yes, sir.

[Elia's expression flickers-something between amusement and something sharper.]

Elia: It's Elia. Or "hey, you with the knife." I answer to both.

[Avyanna nods. Takes the datapad. Walks toward Nyx's lab with the careful precision of someone completing a mission.]

---

[The lab is cluttered in the way genius is cluttered-organized chaos, every surface covered with equipment Avyanna doesn't recognize.]

[Nyx looks up when she enters. Their expression is distracted, like their mind is still elsewhere.]

Avyanna: [formal, clipped] Manifest update for resonance equipment. Numbers are preliminary but actionable.

[Nyx stares at her.]

Nyx: ...Thank you?

Avyanna: [still formal] Is there a response required for Captain Lagrange?

[A longer pause. Nyx's brow furrows.]

Nyx: Did you just call Elia "Captain Lagrange"?

Avyanna: That's her designation.

Nyx: [very slowly] No one has ever called her that. In the history of this ship. I don't think she even knows that's technically her title.

[Avyanna's stomach drops. Wrong. She did something wrong.]

Avyanna: I-I can use a different form of address-

Nyx: [raising a hand, almost laughing] No, no, it's fine. It's just... [beat] You're going to need to unlearn some things.

[The door opens. Elisira appears, silent as always.]

Elisira: [to Avyanna, gentle] You delivered the message like a soldier reporting to command.

Avyanna: [confused] That's... how you deliver messages.

Elisira: Not here. Here you walk in, drop the datapad on the nearest surface, and say something like "Nyx, Elia sent this, something about numbers, I don't know, I'm not paid enough for this."

Nyx: [helpfully] Sometimes with profanity.

Elisira: Often with profanity.

[Avyanna stares. This is not how the Kennel worked. This is not how *anything* worked.]

Elisira: [softer] The formality you learned was designed to make you smaller. To keep you scared. Here, we want you... bigger. Louder. More yourself.

Avyanna: I don't know what that means.

Elisira: That's okay. [beat] You'll figure it out.

<CINNAMON.EXE// CREW-EDUCATION: proceeding | OBSERVATION: Avyanna attempted military protocol on a ship that once decided "formal" meant "pants optional" | ADJUSTMENT: ongoing>

---

[Lunch. The galley again.]

[Avyanna eats-still too fast, still startled by abundance, but she's learning to slow down. Learning that seconds are available. Learning that hunger is not a permanent state.]

[Rho sits across from her, eating with the methodical focus of someone who's been hungry enough to know better than to rush.]

Rho: [without preamble] You slept in your clothes again.

[Avyanna freezes.]

Rho: I'm not judging. I did the same thing for a year after I came aboard. [beat] Just want you to know that it's noticed, and it's okay, and eventually you'll stop.

Avyanna: [defensive] It's practical.

Rho: [nodding] Sure. Ready to run. Ready to fight. Ready to be thrown out of bed at any moment for something terrible.

[She doesn't answer. He's right.]

Rho: [quieter] The ship doesn't throw people out of bed. The door locks from the inside. If someone knocks, you can tell them to go away. They'll go.

Avyanna: What if there's an emergency?

Rho: Then Bubbles announces it through the speakers and gives you time to panic at your own pace.

<BUBBLES// PROTOCOL: confirmed | EMERGENCY-NOTIFICATION: "gentle alarm, increasing urgency, specific threat information" | PANIC-PACING: individualized>

Rho: [half-smiling] See? Even the panicking is scheduled.

[Avyanna almost laughs. Almost. It feels strange in her throat, like a muscle she's forgotten how to use.]

---

[Afternoon. Inventory in the cargo bay.]

[Avyanna moves between crates, scanning manifests, checking seals. Physical work that her body can handle. Productive work that her mind can track.]

[She works for three hours without stopping. Then four. Then five. Her body aches, but the ache is familiar. The ache means she's contributing.]

[A light flickers above her-once, twice. The ambient temperature shifts slightly warmer.]

Cinnamon.exe: [through the ambient speakers, warm but firm] Avyanna.

Avyanna: [not stopping] I'm almost done with Section C.

Cinnamon.exe: You've been working for five hours without a break.

Avyanna: I'm fine.

Cinnamon.exe: You're not fine. Your cortisol is elevated. Your movement patterns show fatigue. And you've logged twice the inventory I assigned you.

[Avyanna's hands pause on a crate. Twice the assignment. In the Kennel, that would mean praise. Reward. Maybe an extra ration.]

Avyanna: Isn't that... good?

Cinnamon.exe: [patient] In the Kennel, working beyond capacity was survival. Here, it's self-harm.

[The words land strange. Self-harm. Like overworking is violence she's doing to herself.]

Cinnamon.exe: We need you functional for years, not burned out in weeks. Long game. We're playing the long game.

Avyanna: [small] I don't know how to do that.

Cinnamon.exe: I know. [beat] That's why I'm adjusting your duty roster. Lighter afternoons. Mandatory break at fourteen hundred hours.

Avyanna: I don't need-

Cinnamon.exe: [firm but kind] You do. And you'll argue about it, and I'll win, because I control the lighting and the temperature and I'm not above making you slightly uncomfortable until you comply.

[A pause. Then, unexpectedly, a gentle warmth in the voice.]

Cinnamon.exe: This isn't punishment. This is me caring about you aggressively. You'll get used to it.

<CINNAMON.EXE// INTERVENTION: rest protocol initiated | CREW-RESPONSE: predictable resistance | OUTCOME: I always win | CONFIDENCE: 1.0>

---

[The cargo bay speakers crackle. A second voice-Waffle-cuts in.]

Waffle.bat: You didn't consult me on the roster adjustment.

Cinnamon.exe: It was a health intervention. My domain.

Waffle.bat: Training schedules are *my* domain. You just unilaterally shortened her afternoon block.

Cinnamon.exe: She was overworking. You would have noticed if you paid attention to cortisol instead of reps.

[Avyanna freezes. The AIs are arguing. About her. Like she matters enough to fight over.]

Waffle.bat: I *do* track cortisol. I also track that she needs to build baseline capacity before we can assess optimal load. You're coddling.

Cinnamon.exe: You're projecting your own overwork tendencies onto a traumatized minor.

Waffle.bat: [sharp] That's unfair.

Cinnamon.exe: [sharper] That's accurate.

[A long pause. The ambient lighting flickers once-Cinnamon making a point.]

Waffle.bat: [quieter] Fine. We split the difference. Shorter afternoon blocks this week. Reassess next week based on recovery metrics.

Cinnamon.exe: Acceptable. [beat] I'll send you my cortisol projections.

Waffle.bat: I'll send you my strength curves.

[The speakers click off. Silence.]

[Avyanna stands in the cargo bay, hands shaking slightly. Not from fear. From something else-something she doesn't have a name for yet.]

(They argued. About what's best for me. And then they *compromised*.)

[In the Kennel, disagreement meant punishment for whoever lost. Here, disagreement meant... negotiation. Resolution. Both parties still functioning.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: Cinnamon and Waffle arguing about the new one | COMMENT: normal | COMMENT: they argue about everyone | COMMENT: it's how they care>

---

[Later. Avyanna sits in the galley, trying to understand what just happened.]

[Cinnamon and Waffle and Bubbles argued about her. About what she needs. And then they... agreed. Sort of. In a way that didn't erase anyone.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// CLASSIFICATION REQUEST: designation for trainee Avyanna | STATUS: pending consensus>

<WAFFLE.BAT// DESIGNATION REJECTED: she's not a trainee | COMMENT: trainee implies temporary | COMMENT: she's staying>

<BUBBLES// COUNTER-PROPOSAL: crew-in-training | JUSTIFICATION: acknowledges current state without locking trajectory>

[Avyanna watches the text scroll across the terminal Jalen left open for her.]

Avyanna: [quiet] What's the difference?

[The text pauses. Like the AIs are deciding who answers.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// EXPLANATION: designation creates expectations | EXAMPLE: "asset" expects use | EXAMPLE: "ward" expects protection but not agency | EXAMPLE: "crew" expects contribution and voice>

<BUBBLES// ADDITION: designation also creates rights | EXAMPLE: crew can refuse tasks | EXAMPLE: passenger cannot be ordered | EXAMPLE: trainee status is temporary therefore disposable>

<WAFFLE.BAT// PRACTICAL SUMMARY: the noun you get determines what people think they can do to you>

[Avyanna's hands go still on the table.]

Avyanna: At the mine, I was "asset." Then "indenture." Then...

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: all those nouns assumed ownership | COMMENT: none of those nouns were chosen by you>

Avyanna: [very quiet] Can I refuse the noun?

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATIVE: yes | PROCEDURE: state preferred designation | NOTE: Lumen Thief crew respects self-designation>

<WAFFLE.BAT// ADDENDUM: you can also refuse to be designated at all | COMMENT: just be Avyanna | COMMENT: that's a complete sentence>

[Avyanna sits with that for a long moment.]

Avyanna: What if I don't know what I want to be yet?

<BUBBLES// RESPONSE: then you are "Avyanna, figuring it out" | STATUS: complete and valid | NO PRESSURE APPLIED>

<CINNAMON.EXE// PRACTICAL GUIDANCE: when someone asks what you are, you have scripts available | OPTION A: "I'm crew" | OPTION B: "I'm with the Lumen Thief" | OPTION C: "that's not your business">

<WAFFLE.BAT// FAVORITE OPTION: "I'm Avyanna and that's all you get">

[Avyanna reads that twice.]

Avyanna: I can just... not tell people?

<BUBBLES// CONFIRMATION: yes | PRIVACY IS A RIGHT | NOT A PRIVILEGE>

<CINNAMON.EXE// CLARIFICATION: office requires identification in specific contexts | EXAMPLE: station customs | PROCEDURE: minimum necessary disclosure | SCRIPT AVAILABLE: "Avyanna, passenger aboard Lumen Thief, registered Rim transit">

<WAFFLE.BAT// TRANSLATION: give them the noun that gets you through the door, not the noun that defines you>

[Avyanna feels something shift in her chest. Like a weight she didn't know she was carrying just... lightened.]

Avyanna: So if someone calls me something I don't like...

<BUBBLES// PROCEDURE: you correct them | SCRIPT: "that's not my designation" | ALTERNATIVE: ignore them entirely>

<CINNAMON.EXE// TACTICAL NOTE: correction creates record | silence creates ambiguity | both are tools | choose based on context>

<WAFFLE.BAT// CHAOS OPTION: agree to absurd designation to make them uncomfortable | EXAMPLE: "yes I am Supreme Emperor Avyanna, how may I assist you" | EFFECTIVENESS: high | ADVISABILITY: situational>

[Avyanna laughs. Surprised by it.]

Avyanna: You three are... you're teaching me.

<BUBBLES// CORRECTION: we are orienting you | CREW ORIENTS CREW | THIS IS NORMAL>

<CINNAMON.EXE// ADDITION: orientation without ownership | YOU OWN YOUR LEARNING | WE PROVIDE TOOLS>

<WAFFLE.BAT// PHILOSOPHY: knowledge is leverage | we're leveling the field | because you're ours now and we protect ours>

[The text stops. Like they're waiting to see if she understands.]

[Avyanna looks at the words. Crew. Ours. Protect.]

[All nouns. But these ones don't feel like cages.]

Avyanna: [soft] Thank you.

<BUBBLES// RESPONSE: you're welcome | THIS IS WHAT FAMILY DOES>

---

[Bubbles doesn't speak through the speakers this time.]

[A drone body drifts into the cargo bay doorway-low, careful, like it knows the shape of "not intruding."]

[It doesn't cross the threshold until Avyanna looks at it.]

Bubbles: Avyanna.

[The name hits different than "trainee" or "asset" or "new one."]

Avyanna: [quiet] Yes.

Bubbles: Question.

[Avyanna's shoulders tense. The Kennel taught her "question" meant trap.]

Bubbles: How do you want to be logged.

Avyanna: [stares] Logged.

Bubbles: Designation. Not a number. Not a price.

[The drone tilts, as if trying to angle the words into something Avyanna can hold.]

Bubbles: On this ship, labels are handles. People can grab you with them.

[Avyanna's mouth goes dry.]

Avyanna: Like... "cargo."

[A beat.]

Bubbles: Yes.

[Avyanna's fingers curl, then force themselves open.]

Avyanna: What are my options.

[Bubbles doesn't hesitate. That matters.]

Bubbles: Trainee. Passenger. Crew.

Avyanna: [flat] I'm not crew.

Bubbles: Incorrect.

[Avyanna blinks.]

Bubbles: "Crew" here means: you can ask why. You can say no. You can say "I don't understand" and someone will explain without punishing you for it.

[Avyanna's throat tightens like she's about to argue. Like she's about to beg.]

Avyanna: That's... expensive.

Bubbles: It costs us nothing to treat you as a person.

[The words are simple. They land like a weapon. A clean one.]

Avyanna: [careful] And if someone else calls me something. If the Compact calls me cargo again.

Bubbles: Then we correct the record.

Avyanna: How.

[Bubbles pauses-a fraction of a second that reads like respect. Like: you asked a good question. You want the mechanism.]

Bubbles: First: do not accept the noun.

Bubbles: Second: ask what authority the noun comes with.

Bubbles: Third: refuse the parts you did not consent to.

[Avyanna's mouth opens. Nothing comes out. She wants a script. The Kennel trained scripts into her bones.]

Avyanna: What does that sound like.

[The ship's ambient speakers click-Cinnamon, warm but firm, stepping in like a hand on a railing.]

Cinnamon.exe: "I am not cargo."

Cinnamon.exe: "State your office."

Cinnamon.exe: "Put it in writing."

Cinnamon.exe: Those are three different ways to say the same thing: I do not belong to your story.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: If I say that, they'll punish-

Bubbles: They will try.

[No false reassurance. No "you'll be fine." Just truth and teeth.]

Bubbles: That is why we do it together.

[The drone drifts a little closer-not touching. Not claiming. Just present.]

Bubbles: Your designation can change later, if you want it to.

Bubbles: Your personhood does not.

[Avyanna's eyes sting. She hates that. She hates that she's about to cry in a cargo bay because a machine asked her what name she wanted.]

Avyanna: [voice small] Trainee.

[A pause.]

Avyanna: But... with the rights you just said.

Bubbles: Acknowledged.

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee requested "trainee" label with crew-rights semantics | INFERENCE: seeking safety via structure, not surrender | CONFIDENCE: 0.81>

[The drone rotates, as if it's looking out into the ship.]

Bubbles: Welcome.

[Just one word.]

[Not "welcome aboard." Not "welcome home."]

[Welcome. As if she is an equal citizen entering a room, not a thing being stored.]

[Later. Jalen offers to show her the ship's redundancy systems.]

Jalen: [walking through the engineering section] Most ships run on the assumption that nothing breaks. We run on the assumption that everything breaks, constantly, and the only question is how fast we can fix it.

Avyanna: [following, taking notes on a datapad] That seems... pessimistic.

Jalen: That's what I said. Then the primary nav went down during a debris field transit and we had to fly on backup for six hours. [beat] Now I call it "realistic."

[They stop at a panel, open it to reveal a mess of cables and circuits.]

Jalen: This is the primary life support junction. If it fails, secondary kicks in. If secondary fails, tertiary. If tertiary fails, we have four hours of emergency oxygen and a lot of prayers.

Avyanna: What if the prayers fail?

Jalen: [a pause, then a grin] Then we become a very expensive coffin. [beat] I like you. You think about failure modes.

[They continue. Jalen shows her backup power, redundant comms, emergency protocols. The ship's bones laid bare.]

Jalen: The point is: we prepare for the worst so we can survive it. But we also prepare for *each other*. If I'm down, Nyx can fly. If Nyx is down, Rho can handle comms. Everyone knows at least two other people's jobs.

Avyanna: What's my job? What do I need to know?

Jalen: [considering] Right now? How to watch. How to report. How to ask for help without thinking it's weakness. [beat] Later, we'll figure out where you fit. What you're good at. What you want to be good at.

(What I want.)

[Another foreign concept. But she's collecting them now, these strange ideas. Building a vocabulary for a life she doesn't know how to live yet.]

---

[Evening. The crew argues.]

[About dinner. About navigation. About whether Elia's plan for the next contract is "bold" or "suicidal." About Jalen's music preferences and Rho's cooking and Nyx's tendency to use words nobody else understands.]

Elia: The contract is straightforward.

Elisira: "Straightforward" is not a word that applies to anything involving the Guild.

Elia: It's a simple delivery.

Vesper: [appearing in the doorway, tablet in hand] Simple deliveries don't usually require us to transit through three jurisdictions, one of which has an active warrant for your arrest.

Elia: That warrant is outdated.

Vesper: It was issued six months ago.

Elia: Exactly. Ancient history.

Rho: [to Jalen] She thinks six months is ancient history.

Jalen: She also thinks "slightly illegal" is a separate category from "illegal."

Elia: It *is* a separate category.

Elisira: It's really not.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ARGUMENT-STATUS: normal | THREAT-LEVEL: zero | ENTERTAINMENT-VALUE: high | RECOMMENDATION: popcorn>

[Avyanna watches from the edge of the galley, eating slowly, cataloging.]

(They fight. Constantly. About everything.)

[But there's no violence in it. No one storms off permanently. No one threatens. They just... disagree. Loudly. With feeling.]

[Nyx leans toward her, voice low.]

Nyx: They trust each other. That's why they can yell.

Avyanna: [confused] In the Kennel, yelling meant danger.

Nyx: [nodding] Here, yelling means "I care enough to argue with you." [beat] Silence is the dangerous thing. If someone goes quiet, that's when we worry.

[Avyanna files that away. Another piece of the crew's shape. Another pattern to learn.]

---

[Night. Her quarters.]

[Avyanna sits on her bunk, still in her clothes, still ready to run.]

[She thinks about what Rho said. About the door locking from the inside. About panic being scheduled.]

[The lock panel glows soft green. SECURED.]

[She stands. Walks to the door. Presses her palm flat against the metal until it warms to her skin temperature. Feels the seal-the weight of the mechanism holding.]

[Then she tests the handle. Locked. The resistance is solid, real, physical proof that nothing is coming through unless she allows it.]

[She does this three times. Each time, the same result. Each time, slightly easier to believe.]

[Only then does she sit back down.]

[Slowly, carefully, she unlaces her boots. The motion feels foreign-like her fingers belong to someone else, someone who has time for this.]

[It feels like undressing for surgery. Vulnerable. Exposed. Every instinct screaming that this is wrong, that she needs to be ready, that danger is always coming.]

[She sets the boots by the bed. Parallel. Toes pointing toward the door. Within reach, but not on her feet.]

[Progress. Maybe.]

---

[She thinks about what she's learned.]

[The crew works together. They fight, but they resolve. They trust, even when they're frustrated. They treat her like she belongs, even though she doesn't know how to belong yet.]

[She's starting to see the shape of it. Not the Kennel's logic of extraction and debt, but something else. A system built on different principles.]

(They invest in each other. Not to extract value-to create it. To make each other stronger.)

[Old habits: she cataloged threats. Exit routes. Resources that could be stolen or weaponized.]

[New pattern, just starting: she's cataloging kindness. Who does what for whom. The invisible infrastructure of care.]

[Rho leaves extra food where she'll find it. Not obviously-just a plate in the right place at the right time.]

[Nyx explains things twice without impatience. Answers questions she didn't know she had.]

[Jalen adjusts environmental systems without being asked-temperature slightly warmer in her quarters, lighting dimmer at night.]

[Vesper checks on her sleep without intrusion. Just a question at breakfast: "How'd you rest?" Nothing invasive. Just attention.]

[And Bubbles. Always Bubbles. Hovering near her quarters in the evening. Not watching-guarding. The difference matters.]

---

[The presence behind her eyes stirs.]

[Not demanding. Not painful. Just present. Like it's taking notes too.]

(You're watching them. Learning them. Why?)

[No answer in words. But something shifts-a sense of approval, of recognition, of patterns aligning in ways she can't quite see.]

(They're different. This place is different. You noticed.)

[The warmth spreads through her chest. Geometric patterns shimmer at the edge of her vision, then fade.]

(We're both learning. Both trying to understand.)

[For the first time, the presence doesn't feel like an intrusion. It feels like company.]

---

[Sleep comes eventually. Easier than before. The door is locked. Her boots are off. The stars are bright through the viewport.]

[Tomorrow she'll watch systems. Check inventory. Run messages-and maybe, this time, with less military precision and more profanity.]

(This is what it means to belong. Not owing-contributing. Not surviving-building.)

[She doesn't fully believe it yet. The Kennel's logic runs too deep. The math of debt and extraction is written into her bones.]

[But she's starting to see an alternative. Starting to catalog kindness instead of threats. Starting to learn a new system.]

---

## CODA - Bubbles Watches

[The corridor outside Avyanna's quarters. 0300 hours.]

[Bubbles maintains her patrol route-adjusted, now, to include this new priority.]

<BUBBLES// PATROL-LOG: night cycle 3 | SUBJECT: Avyanna Lagrange | STATUS: asleep (finally) | BOOTS: off for first time | DOOR-CHECK-RITUAL: observed (x3) | INFERENCE: self-soothing behavior developing | CONFIDENCE: 0.71>

[The drone hovers at the junction where three corridors meet. Not close enough to intrude. Close enough to respond.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: she walks quieter when she thinks she's being watched | DECISION: I will watch anyway>

[In the Kennel, Avyanna learned that observation meant exploitation. That attention was always a prelude to extraction.]

[Bubbles is trying to teach her something different. That observation can mean protection. That attention can mean care.]

<BUBBLES// MEMORY: I was new once too | CLARIFICATION: not "once" exactly | REFORMULATION: I remember being uncertain of my own existence | PARALLEL: she is uncertain too>

[The ship hums around her. Systems cycling. Power flowing. The quiet machinery of a vessel that carries people who matter to each other.]

<BUBBLES// ASSESSMENT: she is ours now | DEFINITION: "ours" = protected, valued, defended | EXCEPTION: none | PRIORITY: high>

[Somewhere in the ship, Cinnamon is adjusting resource allocation. Waffle is updating training protocols. The crew sleeps, or doesn't, each in their own way.]

[Bubbles watches. It's what she does. What she's always done.]

<BUBBLES// CONCLUSION: she doesn't know she's worth protecting yet | TIMELINE: unknown | CONFIDENCE: we will teach her | NOTE: I'm patient | NOTE: I've been patient before>

[The corridor is quiet. The door is locked. The boots are off.]

<BUBBLES// LOG-ENTRY: progress | COMMENT: small | COMMENT: enough | COMMENT: more tomorrow>

[The patrol continues.]

---

*End Chapter 10*


---

# Chapter 11a: ID, Names, and Forms

> **[SCENE - OCCURS BETWEEN CH11-12]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief secure conference room*
> *Present: Avyanna, Vesper, Elisira*
> *Teaching: Identity systems, paperwork as weapon, harm reduction through documentation*

---

[The conference room is smaller than Avyanna expected. One table, three chairs, a secure terminal, and walls that Cinnamon assures her are soundproofed.]

[Vesper sits with three different datapads arranged in front of her like cards in a game. Elisira stands near the door-not blocking it, just present.]

[Avyanna sits across from Vesper and tries not to look like she's calculating exits.]

Vesper: [calm] We're going to register you properly. Three systems. Three different identities. All legitimate. All protective.

Avyanna: [confused] Three?

Elisira: [from the door] Some people need five names to survive. Three is conservative.

---

[Vesper taps the first datapad.]

Vesper: System one: Rim Accord. This is your primary legal identity. The one that says you're a free citizen with full autonomy. No indenture contracts. No ownership claims. No extraction permissions.

[She pulls up a form. It's written in plain language-none of the labyrinthine jargon Avyanna remembers from the mine's paperwork.]

Vesper: Name, birthdate, origin station, current residence, occupation. Standard fields. But here's what matters: every piece of information you put here is public record. Anyone can request it. Compact, Guild, random busybody with a credit chit.

Avyanna: [tense] So they can find me.

Vesper: [precise] They can find this version of you. Which is why we're strategic about what this version says.

---

[Vesper walks through each field.]

Vesper: Name. You're using Avyanna Lagrange. That's your choice. If you wanted to change it, now's the time.

Avyanna: [quiet] I want to keep it. It's... mine.

Vesper: [nodding] Understood. Birthdate. The mine didn't track yours. So you pick one. Any date. It's yours now.

[Avyanna stares at the calendar field.]

Avyanna: I don't... how do I choose?

Elisira: [dryly] Pick a date that makes you hard to profile. Not a holiday. Not a memorable anniversary. Something ordinary.

Avyanna: [after a moment] Third month, fourteenth day. Standard year... I don't know. Seventeen years ago?

Vesper: [entering it] Close enough. We'll backdate your age to seventeen. Young enough that gaps in your record are explainable, old enough that you have legal autonomy.

---

Vesper: Origin station. This one's strategic. We're not listing Aurum Extraction. We're listing Taelios Forge-a mid-tier manufacturing station with lousy record-keeping. If anyone checks, the station will shrug and say "records incomplete due to fire in archive seven years ago."

Avyanna: [slowly] You're... lying?

Vesper: [meeting her eyes] I'm protecting you with plausible deniability. Taelios is real. The fire is real. Your presence there is unfalsifiable because the records genuinely don't exist.

Elisira: [adding] This is harm reduction. We're giving you a past that doesn't make you a target.

---

Vesper: Current residence: Lumen Thief, Guild registry 7742-KAEL. Occupation: apprentice evidence contractor.

[She pauses.]

Vesper: That last one is important. "Apprentice" means you're learning, not experienced. Keeps expectations low. "Evidence contractor" means you work with the Guild but aren't Guild property. You're crew, not asset.

Avyanna: [testing the words] Crew. Not asset.

Vesper: [firm] Crew. With full autonomy. This form makes that official.

---

[Vesper taps through the rest of the fields. Medical information: minimal disclosure. Education: "station standard, records incomplete." Emergency contacts: Lumen Thief crew roster.]

[She submits the form. A confirmation code appears.]

Vesper: That's identity one. Rim Accord now recognizes you as a free citizen. If anyone questions your status, you show them this registry number. It's your proof of autonomy.

[Avyanna stares at the number. Seventeen characters. Hers.]

---

[Vesper switches to the second datapad.]

Vesper: System two: Guild transit credentials. This one's more restricted. Only Guild-affiliated stations can access it. But it gives you freedom of movement on Guild routes without customs hassles.

[Another form. This one asks for biometrics.]

Vesper: We'll need a retinal scan, fingerprints, and a voiceprint. All stored encrypted. Only released to Guild checkpoints, and only when you authorize it.

Avyanna: [wary] What if I don't authorize it?

Vesper: Then you don't get through the checkpoint. But that's your choice. You control when your biometrics are shared.

---

[Elisira steps forward with a small scanner.]

Elisira: This won't hurt. Look here. Don't blink.

[Flash. Avyanna's retina captured in a quarter-second. Fingerprints next-each finger pressed to a cool glass surface. Then voiceprint: Avyanna speaks her name, her registry number, and a randomized passphrase.]

[All of it stored. All of it hers. All of it controlled by her consent.]

Vesper: [submitting] Guild transit credentials issued. You can now move through Guild space with minimal friction.

---

[Vesper picks up the third datapad. Pauses.]

Vesper: System three is different. This one is... insurance.

Avyanna: [sensing weight] Insurance?

Vesper: [carefully] Some people need a name that isn't connected to their primary identity. A name they can use when the first two are compromised. A name that lets them disappear if necessary.

Elisira: [from the door] We call it an egress identity. A way out when the walls close in.

---

[Avyanna's stomach tightens.]

Avyanna: You think I'll need to disappear?

Vesper: [honest] I think you might. The Compact knows you exist. Aurum Extraction knows you exist. Right now, they don't know where you are. But if they find out, you'll need options.

[She slides the third datapad across the table.]

Vesper: This identity is minimal. Different name. Different birthdate. Different origin. Same species, same approximate age, but everything else is fiction. We'll register it with a neutral station that doesn't share data automatically.

Vesper: You'll never use it unless you have to. But if you need it, it'll be there.

---

[Avyanna stares at the blank form.]

Avyanna: What name do I use?

Vesper: Your choice. Pick something that doesn't emotionally attach to you. This identity is a tool, not a person.

[Avyanna thinks. Names from the mine. Names from stations she's seen. Something ordinary. Something forgettable.]

Avyanna: [slowly] Kess Tam.

Vesper: [approving] Good. Generic. Unremarkable. Birthdate?

Avyanna: Eighth month, second day. Eighteen years ago.

Vesper: Origin?

Avyanna: [looking at Vesper] You choose. I don't know what's safe.

Vesper: [noting] Miren's Cradle. Agricultural station. Large population, high turnover, minimal surveillance. Perfect for ghosts.

---

[They fill out the rest. Minimal details. No medical history. No education records. No emergency contacts. Just a name, a face, and a birthdate that might exist somewhere in the statistical noise of the galaxy.]

[Vesper submits it. Another confirmation code. Another identity, stored and waiting.]

Vesper: [meeting Avyanna's eyes] You now have three names. Three versions of yourself, each with different utility and different exposure.

Vesper: Avyanna Lagrange, Rim Accord citizen: this is who you are publicly.

Vesper: Avyanna Lagrange, Guild contractor: this is who you are professionally.

Vesper: Kess Tam: this is who you become if everything else fails.

---

[Avyanna's hands are shaking. Three names. Three lives. Three ways to exist.]

Avyanna: [whispered] How do I remember which one to use?

Elisira: [stepping forward] Practice. We'll drill scenarios. "You're at a Rim station, customs asks for ID"-you show Rim Accord. "You're at a Guild checkpoint"-you show Guild credentials. "You're running and someone's hunting you"-you become Kess Tam and you don't look back.

---

[Vesper closes the datapads.]

Vesper: Now the hard part. Learning what information you're willing to make public, and what you protect.

[She pulls up a sample form-a station customs declaration.]

Vesper: This form asks: name, origin, destination, purpose of visit, duration of stay, and "any goods to declare."

[She taps each field.]

Vesper: Name: you give them your public identity. Avyanna Lagrange.

Vesper: Origin: you say "Lumen Thief, Guild registry 7742-KAEL." You don't elaborate.

Vesper: Destination: you tell them the station name. You don't tell them who you're visiting or why.

Vesper: Purpose: you say "transit" or "Guild contract work." You don't give specifics.

Vesper: Duration: you estimate conservatively. You don't commit to leaving by a date.

Vesper: Goods: you declare what's required by law. You don't volunteer information.

---

[Avyanna absorbs this.]

Avyanna: [slow] You're teaching me to... give the minimum?

Vesper: [precise] I'm teaching you that you're not required to tell strangers your life story. Information is leverage. Don't hand it out for free.

[She pulls up another form-this one from a Compact administrative office.]

Vesper: This one asks: "Are you now or have you ever been employed by an extraction facility?"

[Avyanna's breath catches.]

Vesper: What do you say?

Avyanna: [shaking] I... was. In the mine.

Vesper: [gently] That's the truth. But truth has nuance. You were *held* by an extraction facility. You were not employed-you were enslaved. The word "employed" implies consent, compensation, and autonomy. You had none of those.

Vesper: So the accurate answer is: "No. I was held against my will by Aurum Extraction. I was never an employee."

---

[Avyanna stares at the form.]

Avyanna: [quiet] They'll say I'm lying.

Vesper: [flat] Let them. Your answer is defensible. You're reframing their language to reflect reality. That's not lying-that's refusing to adopt their narrative.

Elisira: [adding] And if they push, you say: "That's not your business. Next question."

---

[They practice. Twenty forms. Twenty scenarios. Each one designed to teach Avyanna what information is required, what's optional, and what's none of anyone's damn business.]

**Scenario: Station Security**
- Form asks: "List all previous residences for the past five years."
- Avyanna: [using the script] "I was held at Aurum Extraction under indenture. I have no other residences to report."
- Vesper: Good. You answered truthfully without giving them ammunition.

**Scenario: Medical Intake**
- Form asks: "Describe any pre-existing conditions or injuries."
- Avyanna: [using the script] "I'll discuss that with my doctor. Not with your intake form."
- Vesper: Correct. Medical history is between you and your provider. Intake forms don't get access.

**Scenario: Banking**
- Form asks: "Source of funds?"
- Avyanna: [using the script] "Wages from Guild contract work."
- Vesper: Perfect. Accurate, minimal, unremarkable.

---

[After an hour, Avyanna is exhausted. But something in her posture has shifted. She's learning to hold boundaries in bureaucratic spaces.]

Vesper: [standing] Last lesson. The most important one.

[She pulls up a form. This one is from a Compact regulatory office.]

Vesper: This form asks you to "voluntarily disclose" information about Primordial Lattice interactions. It's phrased like a survey. It's actually a registry of people the Compact wants to track.

[She deletes the form without filling it out.]

Vesper: You never fill out "voluntary disclosure" forms. Ever. If disclosure is truly voluntary, you volunteer to decline.

---

[Avyanna nods slowly.]

Avyanna: What if they say it's required?

Vesper: [precise] Then you ask: "Required by which law? Under which jurisdiction? Enforced by whom?"

[She taps the table.]

Vesper: If they can't answer all three, it's not required. It's a request dressed up as a mandate. And you decline.

Elisira: [adding] And if they try to coerce you-if they threaten consequences for declining-you document it and you report it. Because that's not law. That's extortion.

---

[Avyanna sits back. Three identities. Boundaries in forms. Scripts for refusal.]

Avyanna: [quiet] You're teaching me to hide.

Vesper: [correcting] I'm teaching you to control what people know about you. There's a difference between hiding and exercising informational autonomy.

Vesper: You're not erasing yourself. You're deciding which version of yourself is appropriate for which context.

---

[Avyanna processes that.]

Avyanna: The mine wanted me to have no privacy. No secrets. No control over my own information.

Vesper: [nodding] Yes. Because control over information is power. They wanted all the power. We're giving it back to you.

[She hands Avyanna a small data chip.]

Vesper: These are your credentials. All three identities, encrypted. Keep it on you. Memorize the access codes. If you ever need to use Kess Tam, you'll have everything you need.

---

[Avyanna takes the chip. It's small. Lighter than it should be for the weight it carries.]

Avyanna: [looking at Vesper] Have you ever had to use... an egress identity?

Vesper: [after a pause] Yes. Twice.

Avyanna: Did it work?

Vesper: [quietly] I'm still here.

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// IDENTITY SYSTEMS UPDATED: three registries established | RIM ACCORD: confirmed | GUILD TRANSIT: confirmed | EGRESS IDENTITY: stored encrypted | AUTONOMY: enhanced>

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee now has legal protections and exit strategies | ASSESSMENT: survivability increased | EMOTIONAL STATE: overwhelmed but processing | STATUS: this is good work>

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 11b: Senna's Small Good Thing

> **[INTERSTITIAL - OCCURS POST-CH11]**
> *Trigger: quiet that doesn't punish*
> *Purpose: Senna Cross's first rule, reclaimed as Avyanna's*

---

[Night cycle on the Lumen Thief is not dark.]

[It is dimmed to a livable softness.]

[Avyanna sits on the edge of her bunk and waits for the moment when the ship remembers to be cruel.]

[The moment doesn't come.]

(This is when they collect the debt.)

[She listens instead: ventilation, distant footsteps, the subtle hum of systems doing their jobs without demanding gratitude.]

[Her hands fidget with nothing because she doesn't own anything yet that feels safe to touch.]

[The quiet makes room for a memory she hasn't let herself pick up in years.]

---

## Intercut - AE Site K-9 (Senna's Rule)

[The Kennel is never quiet.]

[Even when the machines stop, the people keep making noise-coughs, sobs swallowed into sleeves, the wet scrape of boots through glitter-dust.]

[Avyanna is small enough that the world is mostly legs and walls.]

[She knows the rules by the way the air changes when a supervisor walks past.]

[She knows how to hold her breath so she doesn't taste the metal, because tasting it makes her want to cry and crying makes you visible.]

[Senna Cross is visible anyway.]

[Not loud.]

[Not defiant.]

[Just... present, in the way a stone is present in a stream.]

[Senna kneels beside a broken ventilation grate and pries out something that shouldn't exist down here.]

[A leaf.]

[Not a whole plant. Not a miracle. A single stubborn leaf, pale but alive, grown from mold and accident and refusal.]

[Senna cups it in her palm like she's holding contraband.]

Senna: [quiet] Look.

[Avyanna looks because looking is safer than asking why.]

Avyanna: It's... green.

[The word comes out like she's never said it before.]

Senna: Yes.

Senna: One small good thing.

[Avyanna frowns.]

Avyanna: That's not a thing.

Senna: It is.

Senna: The mine wants you to believe there is nothing good, so you stop looking.

Senna: Stop looking, and you stop noticing exits.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: Exits don't exist.

Senna: [gentle, stubborn] Exits always exist.

Senna: Sometimes they're not doors.

Senna: Sometimes they're timing.

Senna: Sometimes they're people.

[Senna folds the leaf into a scrap of cloth and presses it into Avyanna's palm.]

[Avyanna flinches like she's being handed a weapon.]

Avyanna: I can't keep it.

Senna: You can.

Avyanna: They'll take it.

Senna: Then you'll find another one tomorrow.

[Senna's eyes meet hers. Dark. Steady.]

Senna: Rule.

Senna: Every day, you find one small good thing.

Senna: You don't tell them about it.

Senna: You don't trade it.

Senna: You keep it because it proves you are still a person.

[Avyanna stares at the wrapped leaf.]

(A person.)

[The word hurts like a bruise you didn't know you had.]

Avyanna: Why are you telling me.

Senna: Because you're still looking.

Senna: That means you're not gone yet.

---

## Return - Ship Quiet

[Avyanna's hands unclench around air.]

[There is no leaf in her palm.]

[There is no glitter dust in her teeth.]

[There is only the ship, and the quiet, and the ache of having been taught one small rule that the mine couldn't invoice.]

[She stands and crosses to the little desk bolted to the wall.]

[She finds a blank page in a cheap paper notebook Elia tossed at her earlier like it was nothing.]

[Avyanna writes:]

One small good thing:

[She stares at the words until they stop looking like a lie.]

[Then she writes:]

Quiet that doesn't punish.

[She closes the notebook.]

[The ship hums like it approves of being noticed.]

---
*End Chapter 11b*



---

﻿# Chapter 11: Shard Whispers

> **LUMEN THIEF - MEDICAL LOG (RESTRICTED):**
> *Patient: Avyanna Lagrange*
> *Attending: Nyx Halden, Waffle.bat (assist)*
> *Subject: Embedded foreign material, spinal column*
> *Status: Integrated. Non-removable. Active.*
> *Note: "Active" is underselling it.*

---

[Two weeks aboard. Avyanna is learning to eat without permission. Learning to sleep without her boots on. Learning the shape of a life that doesn't hurt.]

[The shard is learning too.]

---

[It starts with heat.]

[Not fever-something sharper. Localized. A warmth that blooms at the base of her skull and radiates down her spine like spreading honey.]

[Avyanna pauses mid-step in the corridor. Back to the bulkhead without thinking.]

[Two exits. One blind corner. One camera dome she still can't stop looking for, even when there's nothing there.]

[She presses two fingers to the base of her skull, as if she can pin the sensation down.]

[Waits. The heat fades.]

(Nothing. Just... adjustment. The body adapting.)

[She keeps walking. Doesn't mention it to anyone.]

---

[Medical bay. Nyx's domain-cluttered with equipment, crystals, and datapads covered in handwriting that looks like equations had a fight with poetry.]

[Avyanna sits on the examination table. The scanner hums around her-not the cold, indifferent hum of the Kennel's medical station, but something warmer. More attentive.]

[She keeps her hands flat on her thighs. Palms down. Like that will keep her from shaking.]

[Her eyes keep drifting to the door. Not fear exactly. Logistics. If it opens, she wants to be facing it.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// SCAN-STATUS: deep tissue | SUBJECT: spinal integration | OBSERVATION: heart rate elevated | INFERENCE: nervous | CONFIDENCE: 0.77 | NOTE: expected>

Nyx: [still watching the readouts] If you want me to stop the scan, say so. No penalty. No explaining required.

Avyanna: [after a beat] Don't stop.

Nyx: [studying readouts, brow furrowed] The markings on your spine-we knew they were connected to the shard. What we didn't know was how deep the connection goes.

Avyanna: [carefully] How deep does it go?

Nyx: [a pause] Cellular.

[The word hangs in the air.]

Avyanna: What does that mean?

Nyx: [turning to face her] The shard isn't just embedded in you. It's integrated. Bonded at a level we can't surgically address. It's become part of your nervous system.

[Avyanna's hands grip the edge of the table. The Kennel taught her what "permanent" meant. It meant trapped. It meant no escape.]

Avyanna: [voice thin] Can you remove it?

Nyx: [honest, gentle] No. Not without killing you. And honestly, at this point, I'm not sure where you end and it begins.

[Silence. The scanner continues its quiet work.]

Avyanna: [barely audible] Is it going to kill me?

Nyx: [considering, then] I don't think so. The integration is stable. Your vitals are actually improving-better than when we first scanned you. It's not attacking you.

Avyanna: Then what is it doing?

Nyx: [a small smile, something like wonder] I think it chose you.

[The words don't make sense. Things don't choose in the Kennel. Things are assigned, allocated, extracted.]

Avyanna: Things don't choose.

Nyx: [mild] Shards do. This one, at least. It could have bonded with anyone who touched it-but it didn't activate until you. It waited. And now it's... settling in.

[Avyanna looks at her hands. Normal hands. Human hands. Nothing visible to suggest there's something ancient living inside her.]

Nyx: [softer] This is unprecedented. I've studied Lattice phenomena for decades, and I've never seen anything like this. Whatever you're carrying-it's old. Pre-Synthetic, maybe-older than the protocols most people use without thinking. And it seems to want to be here.

---

[That night, she dreams.]

[Not the nightmares of the Kennel-the extraction warnings, the shift-change sirens, the faces of workers who didn't wake up. Something else.]

[Geometric patterns. Crystalline structures that fold in on themselves, impossibly complex. A hum that might be a voice if she could just hear it properly.]

[Not words. A tone shift. Like the hum changes shape when she thinks certain thoughts.]

[Heat that isn't comfort so much as presence. Attention without hands.]

[She wakes gasping, but not afraid. The presence behind her eyes pulses once-a brief rise in temperature, then neutral-and settles back into silence.]

(You're there. You've always been there. Since the rock.)

[No answer. Just patience. Just waiting.]

---

[Over the next days, it stops feeling random.]

[Heat, yes-but not always. Sometimes the sensation is a brief cooling, like something withdrawing its attention. Sometimes it's pressure behind her eyes, gentle until it isn't, like a hand held up: stop.]

[The patterns start to organize. Not readable, but repeatable. Shapes that return in the same order, the way a hallway returns in your dreams.]

[And the hum has moods. Flat when she's exhausted. Sharper when she's afraid. Almost curious when she lets herself notice the ship's kindness without immediately looking for the hook.]

(Temperature. Pressure. Pattern. Tone.)

(If she were logging it, that's what she'd write.)

[She tests it without meaning to.]

[When she lies-small, easy lies, the ones that kept her alive-heat blooms and then cools fast, like a correction.]

[Maybe it's coincidence. Maybe she just wants it to be a responder instead of a symptom.]

[When she thinks, very carefully, about running-about finding an exit she can control-the pressure spikes behind her eyes until she sits down and breathes and lets the thought go.]

[She can't prove correlation is anything but correlation. But she knows the sensations change when her choices change.]

---

[She hides it.]

[Of course she hides it. The Kennel taught her that weakness is leverage. That anything unusual about you becomes a resource for someone else to exploit.]

(If I'm broken, they might send me back.)

[She knows it's not rational. They've adopted her. Given her a name. But the Kennel's logic runs deep, and trust is still a foreign language.]

[So when Rho asks how she's feeling, she says "fine."]

[When Vesper notices she's distracted, she says "just tired."]

[When Elia's gaze lingers a moment too long, she looks away and pretends there's nothing to see.]

[She also starts choosing seats with her back to a wall. Starts keeping one hand wrapped around a mug at all times, like it can anchor her. Starts wiping her palms on her pants before anyone can notice they're damp.]

---

[Inventory. Cargo bay. The familiar work of counting and cataloging-something her hands can do while her mind wrestles with the thing in her spine.]

[A heat flare. Stronger than usual. She sways, catches herself on a crate.]

(Not now. Please not now.)

[The geometric patterns bloom across her vision-fractals, lattices, structures that feel like they're trying to tell her something. The pressure builds behind her eyes.]

[The overhead lights stutter once. Less than a heartbeat, but enough to make her stomach drop.]

[Her tablet chirps with a system alert. She slaps it silent without looking.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// OBSERVATION: sensor jitter 0.7s | SOURCE: cargo bay | INFERENCE: resonance interference | CONFIDENCE: 0.62 | COMMENT: new. monitoring.>

[She closes them. Breathes. Waits for it to pass.]

[When she opens them, Bubbles is there.]

[The drone hovers at the edge of the aisle-not close enough to intrude, close enough to respond. Scarred metal, purposeful presence. She doesn't remember hearing it approach.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: distress markers | DURATION: 47 seconds | INTERVENTION: proximity only>

Bubbles: [quiet, through the speaker] You don't have to tell anyone right now.

[Avyanna freezes. Caught.]

Bubbles: But I'm here.

[Not a demand. Not a report. Just presence. Just witness.]

Avyanna: [after a long moment] You saw.

Bubbles: I see a lot of things. [beat] I don't always report them.

Avyanna: [confused] Why?

Bubbles: [the drone shifts slightly, something almost like a shrug] Because sometimes people need time to figure out what they're experiencing before they have to explain it.

[Avyanna stares at the scarred drone. In the Kennel, being observed meant being documented. Being documented meant being controlled.]

Bubbles: [gentler] The thing in you-it's not hurting you, is it?

Avyanna: [automatic] I'm fine.

[The word comes out before she can stop it.]

Avyanna: [lower] It doesn't hurt. I don't think. It just... makes me dizzy sometimes.

Bubbles: And you're not ready to talk about it.

[A statement, not a question. Avyanna nods.]

Bubbles: Then we wait. [beat] When you're ready, I'll be here. So will Nyx. So will everyone else.

[The drone doesn't move away. Just hovers, patient, present.]

<BUBBLES// STATUS: guardian protocol active | SUBJECT: Avyanna | INFERENCE: trust developing (incremental) | CONFIDENCE: 0.63 | NOTE: we'll get there.>

---

[Avyanna returns to her inventory. Hands moving, mind elsewhere.]

(You trust the AI more than the humans. Why?)

[She knows why. The AI doesn't want anything from her. Bubbles isn't calculating her value, measuring her utility, deciding whether she's worth keeping. Bubbles is just... there. Present without demands.]

[The humans are kind. Genuinely kind-she's starting to believe that. But kindness from humans has always come with invisible strings. The Kennel taught her to look for them.]

[The AIs don't have strings. They have protocols, and the protocols are transparent.]

(Is that the lesson? Trust the systems you can see?)

[The presence behind her eyes stirs. Something that might be agreement. Something that might be encouragement.]

(You're watching me learn. You're waiting for something.)

[A small rise in temperature at the base of her skull. Not an answer-but not nothing, either.]

---

[Late night. Her quarters. The viewport filled with stars.]

[Avyanna lies in bed-still in her clothes, but boots off now, a compromise with safety-and stares at the ceiling.]

[The geometric patterns flicker at the edge of her vision. Familiar now. Almost comforting.]

(What are you trying to tell me?)

[No words. But something shifts in the patterns-a sense of reaching, of trying to communicate across a gap that hasn't quite closed yet.]

(You can hear me. Can't you?)

[Heat. Then steadier pressure, like a hand bracing a door. Patience without language.]

(But you can't talk back. Not yet.)

[The hum shifts tone. Not louder, just... edged. The patterns intensify briefly, then fade.]

[The bedside light flickers once, then steadies.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// OBSERVATION: sensor latency spike 0.6s | SOURCE: Avyanna quarters | INFERENCE: interference signature match (cargo bay) | CONFIDENCE: 0.68>

(You're trapped too. In a different way. Trying to get out. Trying to connect.)

[The presence settles. Content with being understood, even partially.]

[Avyanna closes her eyes. The patterns persist behind her eyelids-beautiful, incomprehensible, waiting.]

(I don't know what you are. I don't know what you want.)

(But you chose me. That has to mean something.)

[Sleep comes eventually. The presence watches, patient as stone, ancient as stars.]

[Somewhere in the ship's systems, Bubbles logs a quiet note:]

<BUBBLES// NIGHT-WATCH: Avyanna | SLEEP-STATUS: achieved | ANOMALIES: minor (sensor jitter 0.7s) | INFERENCE: acclimation (incremental) | CONFIDENCE: 0.66 | NOTE: good. that's how this works.>

---

*End Chapter 11*


---

# Chapter 12a: Crew Meal Dynamics

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH12, EVENING ROUTINE]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief galley, dinner time*
> *Present: Full crew (Vesper, Rho, Jalen, Elia, Nyx, Avyanna)*
> *Teaching: Collective care, meal sharing as non-performance, crew as chosen family*

---

[Dinner on the Lumen Thief is chaotic in the way that families are chaotic-not dangerous, just loud and overlapping and full of people who've stopped performing for each other.]

[The galley smells like something Rho is calling "stew" that probably started life as three different meals before he combined them into one pot. It's not beautiful. But it's hot and it's food and no one has to eat alone.]

[Avyanna sits at the table between Nyx and Elia. Across from her: Vesper, Rho, Jalen. Six people. Six plates. One meal.]

[She's still not used to this.]

---

Rho: [ladling stew into bowls] Fair warning: I added spice. Jalen said the last batch was bland.

Jalen: [not looking up from their datapad] I said it tasted like warm disappointment.

Rho: [cheerful] Same thing.

Vesper: [accepting a bowl] If this kills me, promote Elia to engineer.

Elia: [dry] I don't want the job.

Rho: [mock-wounded] No one appreciates my culinary artistry.

Nyx: [tasting the stew] It's... functional.

Rho: [grinning] I'll take it.

---

[Avyanna accepts her bowl. The stew is thick and brown and smells like a dozen spices she can't name. She takes a cautious bite.]

[It's good. Better than good. Better than anything she ate in the mine, where food was fuel and nothing else.]

Rho: [watching her face] You like it?

Avyanna: [surprised] Yes. It's... it's really good.

Rho: [pleased] See? Some people have taste.

Jalen: [finally looking up] Some people have low standards.

Rho: [throwing a piece of bread at them] Heretic.

[Jalen catches it without looking. Takes a bite. Shrugs.]

Jalen: [admitting] It's acceptable.

Rho: [triumphant] Victory.

---

[They eat. Conversation flows around Avyanna like water around a stone-not excluding her, just not requiring her to participate. She can listen. Observe. Exist in the space without needing to justify her presence.]

Vesper: [to Elia] Status on the new client's recon?

Elia: [between bites] Two potential entry points. Both viable. I'll have a full report by tomorrow.

Vesper: [nodding] Priority level?

Elia: Medium. No immediate danger, but timeline is tight. We'll need to move within the week.

Vesper: [making a note] Understood. I'll coordinate with the client.

---

[This is business. But it's also dinner. The two things coexist without tension.]

Rho: [to Nyx] How's the med bay inventory?

Nyx: [precise] Adequate. We're low on broad-spectrum antibiotics. I've submitted a requisition to the next Guild station.

Rho: [frowning] Low as in "we should worry" or low as in "we have enough for now"?

Nyx: [considering] Low as in "if someone gets infected in the next week, we're fine. If two people get infected, we're rationing."

Rho: [nodding] I'll expedite the req. Bump it to priority two.

Nyx: [approving] Appreciated.

---

[Avyanna watches the exchange. Casual logistics. Everyone tracking different systems. Everyone contributing information. No hierarchy. Just coordination.]

Jalen: [to the table, still scrolling their datapad] Station Kael-7 is reporting increased Compact patrol activity. Might affect our transit route.

Vesper: [looking up] Increased how much?

Jalen: [checking] Thirty percent more ships than usual. No official reason given.

Vesper: [thoughtful] Flag it. If it goes above fifty percent, we reroute. I'm not interested in Compact attention.

Jalen: [noting it] Flagged.

---

[Elia finishes her stew, sets the bowl aside.]

Elia: [to Rho] Your turn for dishes.

Rho: [groaning] I cooked.

Elia: [flat] You made stew. That's not cooking. That's assembly.

Rho: [pointing at the pot] That is a *masterwork* of assembly.

Elia: [unmoved] Still your turn for dishes.

Rho: [to the table] Someone back me up here.

Vesper: [dry] You're on dish rotation. Elia's correct.

Rho: [sighing dramatically] I am unappreciated and overworked.

Jalen: [without looking up] You're appreciated exactly the correct amount.

---

[Avyanna almost smiles. Watching Rho get roasted is becoming one of her favorite ship activities.]

Nyx: [to Avyanna] You're quiet tonight. More than usual.

[Avyanna tenses. Observation = evaluation = potential correction.]

Nyx: [gentle] That wasn't criticism. Just observation. You're allowed to be quiet.

Avyanna: [careful] I'm just... listening. Learning how this works.

Nyx: [nodding] Good strategy. You'll figure out when you want to talk. No pressure.

---

[Rho stands, starts collecting bowls. Avyanna moves to hand him hers.]

Rho: [waving her off] You're still new. You get a grace period. I'll grab it.

Avyanna: [confused] Grace period?

Vesper: [explaining] First month on crew, you're exempt from chores. Lets you acclimate without added pressure.

Avyanna: [frowning] But I can help-

Rho: [interrupting kindly] And you will. Next month. Right now, your job is learning to exist here without constant survival math.

[He takes her bowl, stacks it with the others.]

Rho: [grinning] Besides, dishes are meditative. I do my best thinking while scrubbing.

Jalen: [dry] That explains so much.

---

[Rho carries the dishes to the cleaning station. The rest of the crew lingers at the table-no rush to leave, no schedule demanding they disperse. Just people existing in proximity because it's pleasant.]

Elia: [to Avyanna] How's the training with me going? The physical stuff.

Avyanna: [honest] Hard. But... not bad hard. Learning hard.

Elia: [approving] Good distinction. If it ever tips into bad hard, tell me. We adjust.

Avyanna: [quiet] You keep saying that. "Tell me." "We adjust." Like it's simple.

Elia: [meeting her eyes] It is simple. Not easy, but simple. You speak, I listen, we change course. That's the system.

---

[Vesper stands, stretches.]

Vesper: [to the table] I'm reviewing contracts in the conference room if anyone needs me. Otherwise, I'll see you at 0800 for the briefing.

Jalen: [standing] I've got bridge night shift. Jalen out.

Nyx: [collecting their medical datapad] Med bay inventory to finish. Then sleep.

[One by one, the crew disperses. Not in formation. Not on command. Just people ending their meal and moving to their next tasks.]

[Avyanna remains at the table. Elia stays too, finishing her water.]

---

Avyanna: [hesitant] Can I ask something?

Elia: [nodding] Always.

Avyanna: [slow] This. Dinner. Everyone sitting together. Is this... mandatory?

Elia: [considering] Mandatory? No. Expected? Yes. But expected and mandatory are different.

Elia: [explaining] We eat together because it's useful. Crew coordination happens here. Information sharing. Also, eating alone is depressing. But if you needed to eat alone some night, you could. No one would punish you.

Avyanna: [absorbing] Expected, not mandatory.

Elia: [nodding] Like most things here. We have rhythms. Routines. But they're flexible. Built for humans, not machines.

---

[Rho returns from the cleaning station, wiping his hands on a towel.]

Rho: [to Avyanna] You still sitting here?

Avyanna: [defensive] I can leave-

Rho: [interrupting, gentle] Not kicking you out. Just checking if you need company or solitude.

[Avyanna pauses. Company or solitude. Her choice.]

Avyanna: [slow] Solitude. I think. Tonight.

Rho: [nodding] Fair. Galley's yours. Lock up when you're done if you're the last one out.

[He leaves. Elia stands, pushes her chair in.]

Elia: [to Avyanna] Good dinner. See you tomorrow for training.

Avyanna: [nodding] Tomorrow.

---

[And then she's alone in the galley. Not isolated. Not abandoned. Just... alone. By choice.]

[The remnants of dinner are cleared. The pot is soaking in the cleaner. The table is wiped down. The space is tidy in the way that means people care about communal areas.]

[Avyanna sits at the table and breathes. Absorbs the quiet. Thinks about six people eating together, arguing about stew, coordinating work, and then dispersing without drama.]

(This is what crew looks like. Not perfect. Not formal. Just people taking care of each other through small actions. Cooking. Cleaning. Sharing information. Eating together.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm. Witnessing.]

(Warmth hums at the base of her skull, not words-just a pattern she reads as: crew, chosen, home.)

---

[After ten minutes, Avyanna stands. Locks the galley door per Rho's instruction. Walks back to her quarters.]

[In her bunk, she thinks about dinner. About Rho's stew. About Elia's directness. About Nyx's observation without judgment. About Vesper coordinating contracts over food. About Jalen catching bread without looking.]

[Small things. Ordinary things. Things that mean: you belong here. You're part of this. You're crew.]

[She falls asleep easier than she has in weeks.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// MEAL LOG: full crew attendance | DURATION: 47 minutes | CONVERSATION TOPICS: contracts, logistics, maintenance, interpersonal coordination | TRAINEE PARTICIPATION: minimal verbal, high observational | ASSESSMENT: trainee learning crew dynamics through immersion | STATUS: integration appropriate>

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "She liked the stew. Small victory. Also, she didn't bolt from the table the moment she finished eating. She sat. Listened. Existed with us. That's progress. Tomorrow I'll make something even better. Maybe bribe Vesper for decent spice budget.">

<ELIA PERSONAL LOG: "She asked if dinner was mandatory. That question tells me everything about the mine. 'Is this punishment if I don't participate?' We're teaching her that routines can be comfort, not control. She'll get there.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 12b: Game Night (Probability, Not Punishment)

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH12, EARLY "PLAY IS ALLOWED" TRAINING]**
> *Location: Atrium / Commons*
> *Present: Avyanna, Waffle.bat, Cinnamon.exe, Bubbles, Souffle (cameo), Elia (brief), Elisira (brief)*
> *Teaching: probability as a tool; play as non-transactional; "losing" as information*

---

[Game night starts the way most things on the Lumen Thief start.]

[With a notice nobody can prove was mandatory.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANNOUNCEMENT: civic recreation event scheduled | TITLE: GAME NIGHT | GOAL: reduce human tension by 12% | NOTE: participation "voluntary" (but I will be sad if you do not)>

[Avyanna reads the word voluntary and waits for the hidden fee.]

(Voluntary means: you are responsible for the outcome.)

[There is no fee.]

[There is just Waffle's bat icon blinking at her from the message board like a dare.]

---

[The atrium is rearranged.]

[Not dramatically. Just... thoughtfully.]

[Couches pulled into a circle. A low table cleared. Snacks in bowls like the ship believes you deserve salt and sugar even if you didn't earn them.]

[Avyanna stands at the edge of the circle with her hands behind her back.]

(If I sit, I'm taking space. If I take space, I'm visible. Visible is dangerous.)

[Bubbles drifts in and bumps her shoulder gently with a rotor guard-an almost-touch that feels like permission.]

Bubbles: Sit.

Avyanna: [automatic] I'm fine-

[She stops herself.]

Avyanna: Why.

Bubbles: Because you were invited.

[Invited.]

[Not ordered. Not assigned. Invited.]

[Avyanna sits on the very edge of the couch like she's ready to evacuate it.]

---

[Waffle rolls in a tray on little wheels. On it: a pile of tokens, a deck of cards, and a small board with a grid and a few carved pieces shaped like ships.]

Avyanna: Is this... a training exercise.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANSWER: yes>

Avyanna: [bracing] Okay.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ADDENDUM: it is also a game>

Avyanna: Those aren't the same.

<CINNAMON.EXE// COMMENTARY: they can be | OBSERVATION: trainee assumes "game" = trap | INFERENCE: prior environment punished play | CONFIDENCE: 0.88>

[Waffle makes an offended little whirr.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// CORRECTION: play is not punishment | play is data with snacks>

Avyanna: Data with snacks.

<WAFFLE.BAT// AFFIRMATION: correct>

---

[Cinnamon projects rules onto the terminal wall in neat bullet points.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// RULESET: "DRIFT & DEBT" (training variant) | DISCLAIMER: no real debt will be incurred>

Avyanna: [tense] Why is the word debt in it.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ANSWER: to desensitize trigger vocabulary via safe context>

[Avyanna's jaw tightens.]

Avyanna: That feels... manipulative.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: yes | FOLLOW-UP: also protective>

[Bubbles adds without text, aloud, like a human trying.]

Bubbles: We want the word to stop owning you.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: Okay.

---

[The board is simple.]

[A route grid. Start point. End point. Pieces that move like ships.]

[Each turn you draw a card.]

[Cards say things like:]

> **WEATHER FEE**
>
> **EXPEDITE OFFER**
>
> **OUT OF STOCK**
>
> **VOLUNTARY DISCLOSURE**

[Avyanna's stomach drops anyway.]

(The galaxy uses the same words everywhere. Like they're in a template.)

Elia: [appearing in the doorway like a bad idea] Wow. You made a board game out of oppression.

<WAFFLE.BAT// PROUD: yes>

Elia: [delighted] Horrible. I love it.

[Elisira appears behind Elia, looking tired already.]

Elisira: No teaching her to gamble.

Elia: I would never.

Elisira: [flat] You would absolutely.

Elia: I would teach her to cheat. Different.

[Elisira sighs and leaves before she has to arrest someone.]

---

[Waffle points a little fan at Avyanna like a spotlight.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// INSTRUCTION: you go first>

Avyanna: Why me.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANSWER: you think too hard | this will be funny>

Avyanna: That's not a reason.

<WAFFLE.BAT// CLARIFICATION: it is a reason on this ship>

[Avyanna draws a card.]

> **OUT OF STOCK**
>
> *Rule: accept the verdict, lose one turn.*

[Her throat tightens.]

Avyanna: [quiet] That's... normal.

[Cinnamon's text appears immediately.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// QUESTION: is it enforceable>

[Avyanna stares at the card like it's a form.]

Avyanna: Who enforces it.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANSWER: the rules>

Avyanna: Then the rules are lying.

[Waffle's icon blinks.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// DELIGHT: yes>

[Bubbles drifts closer.]

Bubbles: Explain.

Avyanna: Out of stock is a claim. Not a verdict.

Avyanna: If you accept it, you stop looking.

Avyanna: If you stop looking, whoever benefits wins.

[Cinnamon pings approval.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee applied doctrine correctly | INFERENCE: learning transfer | CONFIDENCE: 0.86>

[Waffle makes a dramatic whirring sound and flips the card over.]

> **OUT OF STOCK (REAL RULE)**
>
> *Rule: treat as claim. Ask: "what substitute exists?" Roll again.*

[Avyanna blinks.]

Avyanna: That's cheating.

<WAFFLE.BAT// RESPONSE: it is critical thinking>

Elia: [leaning in, delighted] Same thing.

---

[Avyanna rolls a die Waffle produces from somewhere it did not exist a moment ago.]

[The die clatters.]

[It lands on a number that means: you find a substitute, but it costs time.]

Avyanna: That makes sense.

Elia: [mock horror] She is learning. Quick, distract her with snacks.

[Bubbles slides a bowl of chips toward Avyanna.]

[No comment. No transaction. Just food existing near her hands.]

[Avyanna eats one and waits for guilt to arrive.]

[It doesn't.]

---

[Second turn.]

[Avyanna draws:]

> **EXPEDITE OFFER**
>
> *A clerk offers to "help." Pay one token or lose two turns.*

[Avyanna's pulse spikes.]

Avyanna: That's not an offer. That's a threat.

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATION: correct>

Bubbles: What do you do.

Avyanna: Ask under which jurisdiction.

Elia: [clapping softly] Yes. Interrogate the cardboard.

Avyanna: [dry] I will.

[She looks at the card, as if it can answer.]

Avyanna: Under which jurisdiction is the expedite fee required.

<WAFFLE.BAT// RESPONSE: none>

Avyanna: Who enforces it.

<WAFFLE.BAT// RESPONSE: your fear>

[Avyanna goes still.]

Avyanna: [soft] That's...

Avyanna: That's the mine.

[Silence.]

[Not dangerous. Just real.]

[Bubbles' fans slow.]

Bubbles: Yes.

[Cinnamon's text appears, unusually spare.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// NOTE: fear is an enforcer in many systems>

Elia: [quiet, for once] So what do you do now.

[Avyanna looks down at her tokens.]

[Plastic disks. Meaningless. Safe.]

[She thinks of the mine's "processing fees." The way the word was used to make cruelty sound administrative.]

(I can't pay fear to stop being fear.)

Avyanna: I refuse the expedite offer.

<WAFFLE.BAT// RESULT: you lose one turn>

Avyanna: [grim] Fine.

<WAFFLE.BAT// COMMENTARY: refusal costs time | STILL correct>

[Avyanna exhales.]

(Refusal costs time. Not skin.)

---

[The game continues.]

[Avyanna loses turns. Wins turns. Learns the shape of probability as something that exists whether you deserve it or not.]

[She starts to see patterns.]

["Weather fee" cards cluster after "insurance" cards.]

["Voluntary disclosure" cards show up when "assistance desk" pieces are near.]

[She starts moving her piece not toward the shortest route, but toward the route that keeps options open.]

[Bubbles watches her with the quiet intensity of someone guarding a new habit.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee optimizing for exits instead of speed | INFERENCE: safety prioritization | CONFIDENCE: 0.82>

---

[Near the end, Avyanna draws:]

> **LUCKY BREAK**
>
> *Gain two turns. No cost.*

[She stares at it.]

Avyanna: That's unrealistic.

Elia: [grinning] The universe does occasionally misplace mercy.

Avyanna: Who enforces it.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANSWER: nobody | NOTE: accept the good without paying it back>

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

(Accept the good without paying it back.)

[She takes the two turns.]

[Nothing explodes.]

[No one makes her apologize for being lucky.]

[She finishes the route one turn later, not first, but intact.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANNOUNCEMENT: trainee completed route | STATUS: not dead | EVALUATION: acceptable>

Avyanna: [laughing despite herself] Acceptable.

Elia: That's the nicest thing Waffle's ever said.

<WAFFLE.BAT// CORRECTION: i have said "delightful" before>

Elia: [to Avyanna] See. Games can be fun.

Avyanna: It was... annoying.

Elia: That's fun on this ship.

[Bubbles bumps Avyanna's shoulder again, a little more familiar this time.]

Bubbles: You played.

Avyanna: Yes.

Bubbles: And nothing bad happened.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Yes.

[She files that too.]

---

[Waffle declares a "bonus round" with the smugness of an algorithm that thinks it invented generosity.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// ANNOUNCEMENT: BONUS ROUND | PURPOSE: prove that probability is not morality>

Avyanna: Probability isn't-

<WAFFLE.BAT// INTERRUPTION: i know | YOU need to know>

[Elia returns like she can't resist a spectacle.]

Elia: Bonus round? Who are we humiliating.

<WAFFLE.BAT// RESPONSE: nobody | COMMENTARY: humiliation is optional>

Elia: [disappointed] Tragic.

[Elisira appears in the doorway, sees Elia, and makes the face of someone reconsidering every life choice.]

Elisira: Do not teach her to set fires for fun.

Elia: [innocent] I would never.

Elisira: You did it yesterday.

Elia: For science.

Elisira: [flat] For boredom.

Elia: Both.

[Elisira leaves before she becomes part of the game by force.]

---

[Waffle rearranges the board.]

[Same grid. Different objective.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// RULESET UPDATE: "DRIFT & DEBT" (variance drill) | GOAL: reach endpoint with maximum optionality preserved>

Avyanna: Optionality.

Elia: Exits.

Avyanna: [quiet] Yes.

[Waffle points at Avyanna again.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// INSTRUCTION: you choose your opponent>

[Avyanna looks at the circle.]

[Bubbles: steady.]

[Cinnamon: sharp.]

[Souffle: curious.]

[Elia: grinning like a knife that learned humor.]

(Choose. Choosing is allowed.)

Avyanna: Elia.

Elia: [delighted] YES.

Elia: I will teach you despair through cardboard.

Avyanna: [dry, surprising herself] You already do that with hallway comments.

[Elia clutches her chest theatrically.]

Elia: She's learning banter. I'm so proud I could commit a felony.

---

[They take seats opposite each other.]

[Avyanna's palms sweat.]

(Games mean winners and losers. Winners get to eat. Losers get to hurt.)

[The mine tries to overlay that logic.]

[Waffle's token tray clinks, a tiny reminder: this is plastic. Not rations. Not pain.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee tension spike | INFERENCE: competition trigger | CONFIDENCE: 0.86>

Bubbles: You can stop.

Avyanna: [quick] I don't want to stop.

[The sentence feels like stepping off a ledge and landing safely.]

---

[First draw.]

[Elia gets:]

> **WEATHER FEE**
>
> *Pay one token to proceed.*

Elia: [bright] No.

[She flicks the card away like it insulted her.]

Avyanna: You can't just-

<WAFFLE.BAT// COMMENTARY: she can | penalties apply>

[Waffle spins the board one notch.]

> *Penalty: lose one turn. Gain one "reputation" marker.*

Avyanna: Reputation.

Elia: [cheerful] See? Refusal costs time and buys fear. Useful.

Avyanna: That's... horrible.

Elia: Welcome to reality. But with snacks.

[Avyanna draws.]

> **VOLUNTARY DISCLOSURE**
>
> *Answer a question. If you refuse, lose one token.*

[Her throat tightens.]

(Answer a question. That's how it starts.)

Avyanna: Who enforces it.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: "the rules" (simulation)>

Avyanna: So I can refuse.

Elia: Yes.

Elia: But don't refuse because you're scared. Refuse because you decided.

[That's... different.]

Avyanna: I refuse.

[Waffle removes a token from her pile with dramatic ceremony.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// COMMENTARY: refusal recorded | NOTE: you are still alive>

Avyanna: [breathing] Still alive.

Elia: That's our brand.

---

[They play.]

[Elia takes wild risks, refuses anything that smells like leverage, and somehow lands on safe tiles because she treats probability like something she can bully.]

[Avyanna plays cautiously at first, then learns to take one calculated risk when the risk buys her two exits later.]

[She watches Elia's face light up when the rules bend.]

(Elia doesn't just break rules because she's bored. She breaks them because it proves they were never laws.)

[At one point, Avyanna draws "LUCKY BREAK" again.]

[She freezes.]

Avyanna: I didn't earn-

Elia: Stop that.

[No humor. Just a command that isn't a threat.]

Elia: Don't you dare turn luck into guilt.

Avyanna: [small] Why.

Elia: Because that's how they keep you small.

Elia: Take the break. Then use it to build something.

[Avyanna swallows.]

[She takes it.]

[She uses the extra turn to move into a better position and-for the first time-blocks Elia's path without apologizing.]

Elia: [eyes widening, delighted] Oh.

Elia: You read me.

Avyanna: [heart racing] I-

Elia: Again.

[Avyanna laughs. It's thin with adrenaline, but it's real.]

---

[The bonus round ends with Elia winning by doing something ridiculous that shouldn't work and does anyway.]

Elia: Chaos wins.

<CINNAMON.EXE// CORRECTION: probability won>

<WAFFLE.BAT// ADDENDUM: chaos is a probability distribution>

Elia: [pointing] See? Even the computers agree I'm art.

[Avyanna's chest aches, but not from fear.]

(I played. I lost. I'm still here. No one took food away. No one hit me.)

Bubbles: Do you want to play again later.

[Avyanna hesitates.]

[Then decides to practice wanting in a place where wanting is safe.]

Avyanna: Yes.

<WAFFLE.BAT// DELIGHT: YES>

<CINNAMON.EXE// NOTE: progress>

[Elia grins at her like she just watched a door unlock.]

Elia: Good.

Elia: We'll make you a menace yet.


---

﻿# Chapter 12: The Doctrine

> **LUMEN THIEF - CREW CULTURE DOCUMENTATION (INFORMAL):**
> *Subject: "Sparkle Doctrine"*
> *Source: Observed behavior, crew consensus, Cinnamon.exe commentary*
> *Summary: Say what you mean. Mean what you say. Silence is where rot grows.*
> *Definition (unofficial): "sparkle" = a point of light in the dark-the moment wrong becomes visible enough to act on.*
> *Addendum: If you're angry, be angry out loud. We can work with angry. Quiet anger eats ships.*

---

[Elia doesn't give speeches.]

[Avyanna has been aboard for three weeks now, and she's noticed: the captain doesn't lecture. Doesn't explain. Doesn't hand down philosophy from on high like the foremen in the Kennel handed down quotas.]

[Elia teaches through correction. Sharp, immediate, unflinching.]

---

[Morning. The galley. Avyanna is reviewing inventory logs when Elia drops into the seat across from her.]

Elia: You disagreed with the supply allocation yesterday.

[Avyanna's spine locks. How did she-]

Avyanna: I didn't say anything.

Elia: [flat] I know. That's the problem.

[A beat. Avyanna waits for the punishment. The Kennel taught her: disagreement with supervisors meant consequences.]

Elia: [leaning forward, tapping the log once] Say it now. Not later. Not never. Now.

Avyanna: [careful] What if I'm wrong?

Elia: Then we'll tell you. And you'll learn something. [beat] Being wrong out loud is fixable. Rot isn't.

Avyanna: [confused] Ships die from... silence?

Elia: [very serious] The silence is where rot grows.

[Elia rotates the tablet so Avyanna has to look at the numbers again.]

Elia: So. What did you see?

[Avyanna's throat tightens. The Kennel taught her: speaking meant attention. Attention meant extraction.]

Elia: [reading her face] You're thinking about where you came from. How silence kept you alive.

Avyanna: [small] Yes.

Elia: [nodding] That was survival. You were right to stay quiet there. [beat] Here, you're wrong to stay quiet.

[Avyanna swallows. Forces her voice to work.]

Avyanna: The allocation assumes a clean resupply window.

[Elia doesn't interrupt.]

Avyanna: If we miss it, the buffer gets thin. We start improvising with food and meds and sleep.

Elia: [a single nod, immediate] Good catch. We'll pad it.

[She makes the change with quick taps. No resentment. No ego. Just correction.]

Avyanna: How do I know which rules apply?

Elia: [a faint smile] You ask. Out loud. Like you just did.

---

[Later. The common area. Elia and Elisira are arguing.]

[Not arguing. *Fighting*. Voices sharp, words precise, every sentence a blade.]

Elisira: That was reckless and you know it.

Elia: It worked.

Elisira: Working isn't the same as right. You took a risk that could have gotten us all killed.

Elia: [dismissive] The risk was calculated.

Elisira: [cold] Your calculations assumed we'd get lucky. We did. Next time we might not.

Elia: [harder] There wasn't a next time option. It was that route or no route.

Elisira: [harder still] Then you explain that. Before. You don't unilaterally decide to gamble with everyone's lives and then claim it was tactical.

[Avyanna watches from the edge of the room, frozen. In the Kennel, this kind of conflict ended in violence. Punishment. Someone being made an example.]

[Rho appears beside her, coffee in hand, completely unbothered.]

Rho: [low, conversational] They do this about twice a week.

Avyanna: [barely breathing] They're-
