Rho: Arguing. Yes. Loudly. [beat] They'll be fine by dinner.

[Avyanna stares at him. How can he be calm? How can anyone be calm when two people that dangerous are at each other's throats?]

[Elia's voice cuts through:]

Elia: Fine. You're right. I should have explained the math before I made the call. I was impatient.

[A pause. Elisira exhales.]

Elisira: And I should have pushed harder in the moment instead of letting it fester. We're both wrong.

Elia: [extending a hand] Agreed.

[Elisira takes it. Brief. Formal. Done.]

[Elisira's jaw stays tight anyway. Her fingers hold Elia's hand one beat too long, then let go like it's a decision.]

[Elia's grin flashes too bright, then she exhales through her nose and looks away.]

Rho: [into his coffee, almost inaudible] Progress.

[Then Elia glances at Avyanna-catches her staring-and her expression softens into something almost amused.]

Elia: Lesson learned?

Avyanna: [struggling to process] You just... argued. And then stopped. And you're not-

Elia: Angry? Hurt? Plotting revenge?

[Avyanna doesn't answer, but her face says yes.]

Elia: [walking over] The anger was real. The disagreement was real. But we said it out loud, dealt with it, and now it's done. [beat] If we'd stayed quiet, we'd still be angry. For days. Weeks. Until it poisoned something else.

Elisira: [joining them] The Doctrine isn't about not having feelings. It's about not letting feelings become rot.

Elia: Quiet anger eats ships. We don't feed it. [beat] We said what needed saying. Now we eat dinner.

---

[Dinner. The galley is loud again-Jalen complaining about a nav calculation, Nyx explaining something incomprehensible, Rho making a point about protein storage that somehow involves explosives.]

[Elia and Elisira sit next to each other. Easy. Close.]

[Elisira's knee bounces under the table for three beats before she forces it still. Elia laughs a little too bright at something Jalen says, then reins it in like she's putting a blade away.]

[Avyanna watches them, cataloging.]

(They fought. Really fought. And now they're... fine.)

[The presence behind her eyes pulses-something that might be curiosity, or recognition.]

(Is that what trust looks like? Being able to fight and still stay?)

---

[After dinner. Vesper finds Avyanna in the observation deck, staring at stars.]

Vesper: You have an opinion.

[Avyanna starts. She didn't hear Vesper approach.]

Avyanna: What?

Vesper: [sitting down beside her] About the contract Elia was discussing. The route through Sovereign space. You think it's a mistake.

[Avyanna's throat tightens. She did think that. She noticed the risk numbers, ran them in her head, concluded the margins were too thin. But she didn't say anything.]

Vesper: [patient] I saw you do the math. You're good at math.

Avyanna: [defensive] I don't know enough about-

Vesper: [cutting her off] Try again. Out loud this time.

[A long pause. The stars turn slowly beyond the viewport.]

Avyanna: [very quiet] The fuel margins are too thin. If anything goes wrong-weather, delays, unexpected costs-we're stranded.

[Vesper nods. Doesn't interrupt.]

Avyanna: [gaining confidence] And the route passes through two jurisdictions that have reciprocal reporting. If one flags us, both do. The risk compounds.

[Another pause.]

Vesper: [mild] Those are good points.

Avyanna: [surprised] They are?

Vesper: They're exactly the points I was going to raise at the planning meeting tomorrow. [beat] You saw them too. You just didn't say.

[Avyanna looks at her hands. The old shame-the Kennel shame of being noticed, being visible, being worth targeting.]

Vesper: [gentler] That's how we work. You see a problem, you say it. Even if you're new. Even if you're scared. Even if you think someone else already noticed.

Avyanna: What if I'm wrong?

Vesper: [shrugging] Then we explain why. And you learn. [beat] Being wrong out loud is better than being right in silence. Silence doesn't help anyone.

[Avyanna processes this. The logic is backwards from everything the Kennel taught her. Wrong is vulnerability. Vulnerability is death.]

[But she's not in the Kennel anymore.]

Vesper: [standing, offering a hand] Come to the planning meeting tomorrow. Bring your math.

[Avyanna takes the hand. Stands.]

Avyanna: [small] Okay.

Vesper: [a real smile] Good. That's how we work.

---

[Next day. Planning meeting. The galley again.]

[Avyanna sits with her math on the table like it's contraband.]

[Vesper sits beside her like a witness.]

Vesper: [to Elia] She saw the margins.

[Elia looks at Avyanna. Not patient. Not indulgent. Expectant.]

Avyanna: [quiet, forcing it out] The fuel margins are too thin. If anything goes wrong, we're stranded.

Jalen: [from the counter, without looking up] She's right.

Elisira: [already scrolling] And the jurisdiction overlap she flagged? Real. Reciprocal reporting.

[Elia exhales once. Decision made.]

Elia: Fine. We take the longer route. Floors, not thrones.

[Avyanna waits for the punishment that never comes.]

Vesper: [to her, low] See? Still alive.

---

[Later. A comm call. Elia negotiating with a contact-a potential cargo client.]

[Avyanna is doing inventory nearby. Close enough to hear.]

Contact: [through the speaker, businesslike] Your AIs can run the manifest verification. They follow orders, right?

[Silence. The air feels colder.]

Elia: [very calm, very cold] Say that again.

Contact: [oblivious] I'm just saying, if your AIs handle the verification, we can-

Elia: [cutting him off] They don't follow orders. They make choices.

Contact: [confused] They're programs. They-

Elia: They're crew. Full crew. Equal crew. They argue with me, they disagree with me, and they have the right to refuse any task they find objectionable.

Contact: [sputtering] That's not how AIs-

Elia: That's exactly how AIs work on this ship. [beat] If you can't accept that, we don't work together. Find someone else.

[A long pause.]

Contact: [backing down] I didn't mean to-

Elia: [flat] Yes you did. You just didn't expect pushback. [beat] Are we clear?

Contact: [subdued] We're clear.

[The call ends. Elia turns and catches Avyanna watching.]

Elia: [matter-of-fact] Questions?

Avyanna: [slowly] You almost lost that contract.

Elia: Yes.

Avyanna: Over... what he said about the AIs.

Elia: Yes.

Avyanna: [struggling to understand] They're worth more than the contract?

Elia: [very simple] They're not "worth more." They're not on a ledger. They're people. You don't trade people for cargo deals.

[Avyanna thinks about the Kennel. About being on a ledger. About her value being calculated and extracted.]

Elia: [softer] I know that's hard to understand. Where you came from, everything was on a ledger. Everyone had a price.

Avyanna: [nodding]

Elia: Here, some things aren't for sale. The AIs' personhood isn't for sale. Your safety isn't for sale. The crew's trust in each other isn't for sale. [beat] Some principles cost contracts. We pay that price.

<CINNAMON.EXE// CONTRACT-STATUS: withdrawn | VALUE: 12,000 credits | PRINCIPLE VALUE: incalculable | INFERENCE: correct trade | CONFIDENCE: 0.92>

---

[Night. Avyanna lies in her bunk, thinking.]

(Say it out loud.)

[The doctrine is simple. Deceptively simple. But implementing it requires something she doesn't have: trust that honesty won't be weaponized against her.]

(They're teaching me to speak. Not just words-real speech. The kind that risks something.)

[The presence behind her eyes stirs. Something that might be approval.]

(You like this. You like that I'm learning to be louder.)

[Heat climbs at the base of her skull. The geometric patterns flicker briefly-brighter than usual, more insistent.]

(Are you waiting for me to speak to you too? Is that what this is?)

[No answer. But the heat holds, steady, and Avyanna thinks maybe she's getting closer to something important.]

---

## CODA - Jalen's Flight

[The cockpit. 0300 hours. Stars streaming past the viewport like rain on a window.]

[Jalen flies.]

[Not because they need to-the ship could autopilot through this stretch of empty space. But flying is how Jalen thinks. Flying is how Jalen stays sane.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// PILOT-STATUS: Jalen | REASON FOR MANUAL: "processing" | OBSERVATION: they do this when the new ones arrive>

---

[Jalen was born on a rim station called Kettering's Rest. A waypoint colony, nothing special-except that it was home.]

[When the route collapsed, Kettering's Rest was cut off. The transit lanes that connected it to the rest of civilization just... stopped working. Lattice failure, they said later. Static zone expansion. Technical language for "your world is gone and no one's coming to help."]

[Jalen got out. They were offworld when it happened-a supply run, routine, boring. They watched from the cockpit of a cargo shuttle as the route sealed behind them.]

[Their family didn't get out.]

[Parents. Siblings. The whole network of cousins and aunts and childhood friends who made Kettering's Rest mean something. All of them trapped on the wrong side of a collapsed lane, slowly starving as supplies dwindled and no help came.]

(I've never been back. The route reopened three years later-before Elia, before the Lumen Thief. By then, there was no one left to visit.)

---

[Jalen has been running ever since.]

[Not literally-they stopped running and started *flying*. Better to be the one who controls the escape route. Better to never be trapped on the wrong side again.]

[They flew for cargo companies, for smugglers, for anyone who paid. Never stayed long. Never got attached. Attachment meant loss, and loss meant Kettering's Rest all over again.]

[Then Elia Lagrange showed up.]

---

[It was a job. Simple extraction, tight timeline, the kind of flight that separated good pilots from dead ones. Jalen flew it perfectly-threading through debris fields, outrunning pursuit, landing the crew safely when every calculation said they should have died.]

[Afterward, Elia found them in the hangar. Just stood there, watching, while Jalen checked systems they'd already checked twice.]

Elia: [simple] You coming?

[No interview. No negotiation. No explanation of terms or benefits or expectations. Just a question shaped like an invitation.]

Jalen: [suspicious] Coming where?

Elia: [shrugging] Wherever. We go a lot of places. We need a pilot who doesn't die.

Jalen: [flat] I don't do attachments.

Elia: [a faint smile] Neither do we. We just do loyalty. Different thing.

[Jalen had said no. Of course they'd said no. Attachment was death, and loyalty was just attachment with a fancier name.]

[A month later, they said yes.]

---

[Now. The cockpit. Jalen adjusts a thruster alignment that was already perfect.]

(Elia made me responsible for people again. Not by ordering-by trusting.)

[That trust is violent when you're used to being disposable. When your whole survival strategy is built around never mattering enough to anyone that losing you would hurt them.]

(She trusts me to keep them alive. All of them. That trust weighs more than any debt I've ever carried.)

---

[They've been watching Avyanna adjust.]

[The way she flinches at loud noises. The way she calculates the cost of every meal. The way she's slowly, painfully learning that kindness here isn't a trap.]

(I remember that. The adjustment period. When you can't believe the floor is solid because every floor you've ever stood on had trapdoors.)

[Jalen checks the nav display. Clean route ahead. Nothing to dodge, nothing to outrun. Just empty space and distant stars.]

(She's going to be okay. She's learning faster than I did. She has the whole crew watching out for her, and Bubbles practically adopted her, and that thing in her spine seems like it's on her side.)

[A small adjustment to their flight path. Smoother now. Gentler.]

(I'm going to fly extra smooth tonight. For the new one. So she knows the ship is steady. So she knows someone's at the helm who won't let her fall.)

[The stars stream past. Jalen flies. And somewhere below, in a bunk that's becoming slowly less foreign, Avyanna Lagrange sleeps-learning, bit by bit, what it means to be held.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: Jalen flying manual again | DURATION: 3.2 hours | REASON: "thinking about family" | INFERENCE: healthy coping | CONFIDENCE: 0.81 | COMMENT: they're softer than they pretend. most of us are.>

---

*End Chapter 12*


---

﻿# Chapter 13a: Starmap Hobby

> **[MICRO-SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH13, LIKELY SHIP'S EVENING]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief navigation alcove*
> *Present: Jalen, Avyanna*
> *Teaching: Constellation naming, pattern recognition, early shard-sense hints*

---

[Evening cycle. The Lumen Thief's navigation alcove is dim except for the star display-holographic projections overlaid on real-time sensor feeds. Jalen sits at the console, updating route calculations. Avyanna hovers near the doorway, uncertain whether she's intruding.]

Jalen: [not looking up] You can come in.

Avyanna: [stepping forward] I didn't want to interrupt.

Jalen: Navigation doesn't mind witnesses. Sit.

[She settles onto the jump seat beside the console. The star display rotates slowly-hundreds of labeled points, trade routes marked in faint lines, hazard zones shaded in warning colors.]

[The shard at the base of her skull pulses. Gentle. Curious.]

---

Avyanna: Earlier, when we were calibrating sensors... I said I didn't know the constellation names.

Jalen: [glancing at her] Most people don't. Not the real ones, anyway.

Avyanna: Real ones?

Jalen: [gesturing at the display] Every culture names the stars. Compact names, Guild names, local names. Sometimes the same cluster has six different designations depending on who's claiming it.

[They tap a control. The labels shift-same stars, different text.]

Jalen: See? One set is pure sector code. One set is corridor shorthand. One set is whatever the locals decided was worth remembering.

Avyanna: [leaning forward] Why so many names?

Jalen: Because names aren't just labels. They're claims. "I named this, therefore I know it, therefore it's mine."

---

[Avyanna studies the display. The shard pulses again-still gentle, but insistent. Like it's trying to show her something.]

Avyanna: [hesitant] Can you teach me? Not the politics. Just... I want handles. Ways to remember where things are.

Jalen: [considering her] Most people learn navigation for work. You asking because you're curious?

Avyanna: [quiet] In the mine, I never saw the stars. Didn't know there were this many. Didn't know they had names, or that names could be... complicated.

[She touches the edge of the display. Her fingers pass through a projected cluster.]

Avyanna: I want to understand the map. Even if the map lies sometimes.

Jalen: [after a beat] That's a good reason.

---

[They adjust the display. Zoom out. The galactic arm spreads before them-a sweep of light and void.]

Jalen: Start with navigation-practical handles. The ones that matter for orientation, not ownership.

[They point to a bright cluster near the center of the display.]

Jalen: Four stars in a rough square. No matter where you are in this arm, if you can find that shape, you can get your bearings: coreward, rimward, up, down.

Avyanna: [committing it to memory] Square. Coreward.

Jalen: Good. Now this one-

[They highlight another formation. Three stars in a tight triangle, with a dimmer fourth trailing behind.]

Jalen: Triangle and a tail. It points relative to the plane. Helps you orient vertical when sensors are compromised.

---

[They work through the practical constellations. Jalen is patient, methodical. Avyanna listens, focused, absorbing the patterns.]

[The shard continues to pulse. And then, as Jalen highlights a particular cluster near the edge of the display, something shifts.]

[The stars feel different. Not visually-she's still seeing the same holographic projection. But underneath the image, there's a... texture. A sense of presence. The cluster feels warm, somehow. Active. Like something is paying attention to it.]

Avyanna: [blinking] That one feels-

[She stops. Tries to articulate what she just perceived. Fails.]

Avyanna: [frustrated] Never mind. It's nothing.

Jalen: [sharp] Don't do that. If you noticed something, say it. Navigation is pattern recognition. Weird patterns are data.

---

[Avyanna hesitates. Then tries again.]

Avyanna: That cluster. The one you just highlighted. It feels... different. Not bad different. Just-

[She touches the base of her skull, where the shard sits.]

Avyanna: It feels like something's there. Not a ship. Not a station. Something else.

Jalen: [leaning back, studying her] Different how? Temperature? Pressure? Visual?

Avyanna: [struggling] None of those. It's like... like the difference between a room with people in it and a room that's empty. You can't see them, but you know.

[Jalen pulls up sensor data for that cluster. Scans it. Frowns.]

Jalen: Nothing on sensors. No anomalies. Standard stellar activity.

[They look at Avyanna. Thoughtful.]

Jalen: But you're not looking at sensors, are you?

Avyanna: [uncertain] I don't know what I'm looking at.

---

Jalen: [making a note on their tablet] Tell me when it happens again. If you feel something the sensors don't show, I want to know.

Avyanna: [defensive] I'm not making it up-

Jalen: [cutting her off] I know. But perception is subjective, and subjective data is still data. If you're sensing something I can't, that's worth tracking.

[They adjust the display again. Rotate through different star fields.]

Jalen: Look at these. Tell me if any of them feel "different."

---

[Avyanna focuses. The shard hums, cooperating now. It's interested in this game.]

[Most of the stars feel neutral. Background. Ordinary.]

[But one cluster-a dense formation near a nebula-has that same presence. That same sense of occupied attention.]

Avyanna: [pointing] That one.

[Jalen checks the coordinates. Makes another note.]

Jalen: Heavy Primordial signature. Low overlay clutter.

[They look at Avyanna with something like approval.]

Jalen: You're sensing Lattice topology. The shard's giving you perceptual texture that standard sensors don't pick up.

Avyanna: [slow] Is that... normal? For shard carriers?

Jalen: [dry] I don't know. You're the first one I've met.

---

[They continue the lesson. Jalen teaches her the navigation-practical constellations. Avyanna learns the names, commits the patterns to memory.]

[But underneath the lesson, she's learning something else: the shard isn't just communicating with her. It's changing how she perceives reality. Giving her information that doesn't fit into visual, auditory, or tactile categories.]

[The galaxy has texture now. Presence. Topology.]

[And she doesn't know yet if that's a gift or a warning.]

---

[Later, when Avyanna leaves the alcove, Jalen writes a note in their personal log:]

> *Trainee reports perceptual anomalies correlated with heavy Primordial signatures. Consistent with Nyx's stated shard characteristics, but timeline unclear. Worth monitoring. Flagging for Nyx.*

[And then, in smaller text beneath:]

> *She asked good questions. Wanted handles, not propaganda. Noticed when names were claims.*
>
> *Reminds me of someone. In a good way.*

---

*End Micro-Scene*



---

# Chapter 13b: Coffee Ritual

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH13, EARLY MORNING]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief galley*
> *Present: Avyanna, Rho, Jalen*
> *Purpose: Domestic routine, belonging without performance*

---

[0530 ship time. The galley is dim except for the work lights over the counter.]

[Avyanna wakes early because she still doesn't know how to sleep past dawn. The mine taught her that sleeping late meant missing rations. The Lumen Thief has no such rule, but her body doesn't believe it yet.]

[She enters the galley expecting it to be empty.]

[It's not.]

---

[Rho stands at the counter with his back to the door, doing something that involves the coffee maker, cursing, and what sounds like percussive maintenance.]

[Jalen sits at the table with a datapad, not looking up, radiating the particular stillness of someone who's been awake for hours and plans to stay that way.]

[Avyanna freezes in the doorway.]

Rho: [not turning around] Come in or don't. Door's open either way.

[Avyanna steps in. The door hisses closed behind her.]

---

[Rho is making coffee. Badly. The machine hisses and spits like it's personally offended.]

Rho: [to the machine] I know you don't like me. The feeling is mutual. But we're doing this anyway.

[The machine gurgles. Something that might be coffee drips into a carafe.]

Jalen: [still not looking up] You're going to break it again.

Rho: [cheerful] It's already broken. I'm just negotiating with the corpse.

---

[Avyanna hovers near the table. Uncertain. The mine had schedules. Mealtimes. Assigned seats. She doesn't know the rules here.]

Jalen: [finally glancing up] Sit. Or stand. Or leave. All acceptable.

[The words are permission. Avyanna sits.]

[Jalen returns to their datapad. Avyanna watches Rho wage war with the coffee maker.]

Rho: [to the machine] Yes. I know. You want the good beans. You're getting station-grade swill. Cope.

[The machine makes a noise like dying hydraulics.]

---

[Eventually, Rho wins. He pours three cups of something that looks like coffee and probably contains caffeine. Maybe.]

[He sets one in front of Jalen. One in front of Avyanna. Keeps the third for himself.]

Rho: [sitting] Fair warning: it's terrible.

Jalen: [taking a sip without looking] Always is.

Avyanna: [staring at her cup] I don't... I've never had coffee.

Rho: [grinning] Then you don't know what you're missing. Which means this won't disappoint you.

---

[Avyanna picks up the cup. It's warm. The smell is bitter and sharp and foreign.]

[She takes a cautious sip.]

[It tastes like burnt dirt and regret.]

[She swallows anyway because wasting food-wasting anything-feels like a crime.]

Rho: [watching her face] You hate it.

Avyanna: [lying] It's fine.

Rho: [laughing] You're a terrible liar. It's okay to hate it. Half the crew hates my coffee. The other half is lying.

Jalen: [dryly] I don't hate it. I'm just dead inside.

---

[Avyanna sets the cup down carefully.]

Avyanna: [hesitant] Do you... have tea?

Rho: [standing immediately] Yes. Why didn't you say so?

Avyanna: [confused] I thought... I thought I had to drink what you made.

[Rho pauses. Looks at her. Something in his expression shifts-recognition of an old wound.]

Rho: [carefully] You don't. You can drink whatever you want. Or nothing. Your call.

---

[He pulls out a different container. Tea bags in six different varieties. Sets them in front of her.]

Rho: Pick one. Or don't. I'm not your supervisor.

[Avyanna stares at the options. In the mine, you got what you got. Here, she has six choices and no idea how to choose.]

Jalen: [without looking up] Green tea's mild. Black tea's strong. Herbal tea isn't actually tea but people call it that anyway.

Avyanna: [pointing] Green. Please.

Rho: [making it] Good choice. Least likely to taste like dirt.

---

[He makes the tea. Sets it in front of her. This time, when she sips, it's... better. Still strange. But better.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Thank you.

Rho: [sitting back down] Don't thank me. Just... drink what you like. That's how it works here.

[They sit in silence. Rho drinks his terrible coffee with evident satisfaction. Jalen reads their datapad. Avyanna holds her tea and tries to understand what's happening.]

---

[This isn't... anything. It's not a meeting. Not a lesson. Not a task.]

[It's just three people in a room at 0530, drinking things, existing near each other.]

[No one is performing. No one is proving anything.]

Avyanna: [carefully] Do you do this every morning?

Rho: [nodding] Most mornings. Jalen's always up early. I'm always up early. We collide in the galley and pretend we're not hiding from our own thoughts.

Jalen: [finally looking up] I'm not hiding. I'm working.

Rho: [to Avyanna] They're hiding.

Jalen: [returning to their datapad] This conversation is beneath me.

---

[Avyanna almost smiles. The motion feels strange on her face.]

[She takes another sip of tea. It's warmer now. Less foreign.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Can I... come back tomorrow?

Rho: [surprised] You don't need permission. Galley's open. Coffee's terrible. Tea's mediocre. We'll be here.

Jalen: [adding] Same time. Same silence. Same existential dread.

Rho: [throwing a napkin at him] You're a ray of sunshine.

Jalen: [catching it without looking] I know.

---

[They fall back into silence. Comfortable. Unforced.]

[Avyanna drinks her tea. Rho reads something on his datapad and mutters about supply costs. Jalen's stylus moves across their screen, plotting something that probably involves math Avyanna doesn't understand yet.]

[No one demands anything. No one expects anything.]

[She's just... here. And that's allowed.]

---

[At 0600, Jalen stands.]

Jalen: [to Rho] Shift change in thirty. Don't forget the gyro calibration.

Rho: [saluting lazily] Aye aye, navigator.

[Jalen nods to Avyanna.]

Jalen: [to her] See you at 0530 tomorrow. Or don't. Either way.

[They leave. The door hisses shut behind them.]

---

[Rho refills his coffee. Doesn't offer Avyanna more tea. She's still working on the first cup.]

Rho: [after a moment] In the mine, you didn't get to choose what you drank, did you.

Avyanna: [shaking her head] No. You got water. Or the stuff they called juice. It wasn't juice.

Rho: [grimacing] Yeah. I've tasted extraction-grade "juice." It's a war crime.

[Rho sets down his own mug. Deliberate.]

Rho: Here, you get to choose. Every time. Coffee, tea, water, that terrible synthetic fruit drink Elia likes. Whatever. It's yours to decide.

---

[Avyanna looks at her tea.]

Avyanna: [quiet] I don't know how to... have preferences.

Rho: [leaning back] Then you practice. You try green tea. Tomorrow you try black tea. Next week you try herbal. Eventually you figure out what you like.

Rho: And if you never figure it out? If you just keep drinking whatever's available? That's fine too. Preferences aren't mandatory. They're just... allowed.

---

[Avyanna absorbs this. Preferences as optional. Choice as practice, not test.]

Avyanna: [hesitant] What if I choose wrong?

Rho: [snorting] It's tea, kid. Not surgery. Worst case, you don't like it and you try something else tomorrow.

[He stands, rinses his cup, sets it in the cleaning rack.]

Rho: [turning back] The mine taught you that every choice has consequences, right? That choosing wrong means punishment?

Avyanna: [barely audible] Yes.

Rho: [nodding] Yeah. Thought so.

[He sits back down. Looks at her directly.]

Rho: Here's the thing. Choosing the wrong tea isn't a mistake. It's information. "I don't like black tea" is useful data. It narrows your options. Makes future choices easier.

Rho: The mine wanted you to be terrified of choosing. Because terrified people don't ask for things. They just take what they're given and call it mercy.

---

[Avyanna's hands tighten around her cup.]

Avyanna: [shaking] They said... they said we were lucky. To have rations at all.

Rho: [flat] They lied.

Rho: You weren't lucky. You were exploited. There's a difference.

[His voice drops. Not softer. Heavier.]

Rho: And here, you get to choose your own damn tea. Because that's what people do. They have preferences. They express them. They change their minds. And nobody punishes them for it.

---

[Avyanna sits with that. The tea is cooling in her hands. The galley is quiet except for the ship's ambient hum.]

[She finishes the tea. Sets the cup down.]

Avyanna: [standing] I should... I should go. Let you work.

Rho: [waving her off] I'm not working. I'm procrastinating. You're fine.

[But he doesn't stop her from leaving.]

[Avyanna reaches the door. Pauses.]

Avyanna: [not turning around] Same time tomorrow?

Rho: [grinning] Same time. Same terrible coffee. Same slightly-better tea.

---

[Avyanna leaves. The door hisses shut behind her.]

[In the corridor, she leans against the bulkhead and breathes.]

(I chose tea. I didn't like the coffee. I said so. And nothing bad happened.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm. Quiet. Content.]

(The warmth at the base of her skull steadies, a wordless reassurance she translates anyway: choice, yours, safe.)

[She pushes off the wall and heads back to her quarters.]

[Tomorrow, she'll try black tea. Just to see.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee participated in crew morning ritual | DURATION: 30 minutes | SOCIAL ENGAGEMENT: appropriate | AUTONOMY EXERCISED: preference expressed without fear | ASSESSMENT: integration progressing>

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "She asked if she could come back tomorrow. Like she needed permission to exist in a space. Fucking mine. Fucking extraction economy. Tomorrow I'm making better tea.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 13c: Asking for What You Need

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH13, FIRST WEEK TRAINING]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief cargo bay (converted training space)*
> *Present: Avyanna, Elia*
> *Teaching: Physical consent, requesting breaks without shame, combat as communication*

---

[The cargo bay is mostly empty today. Elia has cleared a practice area-padded mats on the deck, water bottles against the bulkhead, the overhead lights dimmed to something less industrial.]

[Avyanna stands at the edge of the mats in clothes Rho found for her: soft pants that don't restrict movement, a shirt that doesn't chafe. Her feet are bare because Elia said shoes would teach her bad habits.]

[Elia stretches nearby. Methodical. Like they're inventorying their own joints.]

Elia: [not looking at her] You know why we're doing this?

Avyanna: [uncertain] Self-defense?

Elia: [standing] No. Agency practice.

---

[Avyanna blinks.]

Avyanna: I don't... understand.

Elia: [walking onto the mats] In the mine, your body wasn't yours. Someone told you where to stand, how to move, when to stop. You obeyed or you got hurt.

Elia: Here, we're teaching your body that it belongs to you again. That you can say "stop" in the middle of a physical interaction and the other person will stop.

[They hold out a hand.]

Elia: We're not sparring today. We're practicing the part that comes before sparring. The part where you learn to speak while moving.

---

[Avyanna steps onto the mats. The surface is softer than she expected. Forgiving.]

Elia: [calm] First rule. You can stop this at any time. "Stop," "wait," "I need a break"-any of those words ends the session immediately. No explanation required. No consequences.

Avyanna: [swallowing] Okay.

Elia: Say it. Practice the words.

Avyanna: [forcing it out] Stop. Wait. I need a break.

Elia: [nodding] Good. Now we test it.

---

[Elia demonstrates a basic stance. Feet shoulder-width apart, knees soft, hands up but not clenched.]

Elia: Mirror me.

[Avyanna copies the stance. Her body remembers how to follow instructions.]

Elia: [watching] Your shoulders are up by your ears. That's tension, not readiness. Drop them.

[Avyanna tries. Fails. Her shoulders are locked.]

Elia: [stepping closer] I'm going to touch your shoulders to show you where they should be. Is that acceptable?

[The question lands strange. Permission before touch.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Yes.

---

[Elia places their hands on her shoulders. Not gripping. Just resting. Warm through the fabric of her shirt.]

Elia: Breathe in. When you exhale, let your shoulders drop with the breath.

[Avyanna inhales. Holds. Exhales. Her shoulders drop half an inch.]

Elia: [removing their hands] Better. Your body's learning. Let's move.

[They walk through basic footwork. Step forward. Step back. Lateral movement. Nothing complicated. Just bodies in space, learning new patterns.]

[After five minutes, Avyanna's breathing is labored.]

---

Elia: [stopping] You're tired.

Avyanna: [defensive] I'm fine.

Elia: [flat] That's not what I asked. I said you're tired. Your breath says so. Your legs say so. I'm giving you information, not judgment.

[Avyanna's hands clench.]

Avyanna: [tight] I can keep going.

Elia: [precise] I know you can. The mine taught you to push past exhaustion until your body broke. That's not strength. That's survival mode.

Elia: Here, you get to stop before you break.

---

[Avyanna stares at the mats. Breathing hard. Ashamed of her own limits.]

Elia: [gentler] I'm going to ask you a question. You're going to answer honestly, and nothing bad will happen. Ready?

Avyanna: [barely] Yes.

Elia: Do you need a break?

[The question is a trap. It has to be a trap. Needing things is weakness. Weakness gets you hurt.]

Avyanna: [shaking] I don't... I don't know how to answer that.

Elia: [sitting on the mat] Then let's practice.

---

[Elia pats the mat beside them. Avyanna sits. Her legs are grateful.]

Elia: The mine taught you that your needs are irrelevant. That you exist to produce, not to feel or rest or ask for things.

Elia: That's extraction logic. We're unlearning it.

[They pull out a water bottle, take a drink, pass it to Avyanna.]

Elia: Drink. Your body needs water. That's not weakness. That's biology.

[Avyanna takes the bottle. Drinks. The water is cold and clean and tastes like it was never filtered through desperation.]

---

Elia: Here's the new rule. During training-during any physical work-you're required to speak up when you need something.

Avyanna: [frowning] Required?

Elia: [nodding] Required. Water, break, slower pace, clarification, stop entirely. Whatever your body or mind needs, you say it out loud.

Elia: If you don't, I end the session. Because I'm not interested in training someone who's dissociated or in pain. That's not training. That's cruelty with a pedagogical mask.

---

[Avyanna processes that. Speaking up is mandatory. Silence is the failure state.]

Avyanna: [slow] You're... flipping it. In the mine, asking for things was the mistake. Here, not asking is the mistake.

Elia: [approving] Exactly. You're not being graded on endurance. You're being graded on communication.

[They stand, offer a hand.]

Elia: Let's try again. We'll do footwork for two minutes. If at any point you need something-anything-you say so. Understood?

Avyanna: [taking their hand, standing] Understood.

---

[They resume. Step forward. Step back. Lateral movement. Avyanna's legs are shaking now. She can feel the edge of her endurance approaching.]

[She says nothing.]

[Elia stops.]

Elia: [calm] You just hit your limit and didn't say anything. That's strike one.

Avyanna: [startled] I... I can keep going.

Elia: [precise] That's not the point. The point is learning to recognize and name your limits before they become injuries.

[They walk to the water bottles, hand her one.]

Elia: We're going to practice requesting a break. Ready?

Avyanna: [confused] How do you practice asking for a break?

Elia: By asking for one. Right now. Say the words.

---

[Avyanna's throat closes. The words are stuck behind shame.]

Avyanna: [shaking] I need a break.

Elia: [immediately sitting] Granted. We'll sit for three minutes, drink water, and resume when you're ready.

[They sit. Avyanna's legs tremble with relief. She hates herself for being weak. She hates that Elia can see it.]

Elia: [not looking at her] You're not weak for needing rest. You're human for needing rest.

Avyanna: [whispered] How did you know what I was thinking?

Elia: [dry] Because I've trained a lot of people who came from places that taught them survival first, living second. You all have the same look when you admit you're tired.

---

[They drink water in silence. The cargo bay hums around them. Ship sounds. Not mine sounds.]

Elia: [after a minute] In the Wandering Market, I learned to fight by watching people who wanted to hurt me. I got good at reading intent, predicting violence, moving before the blow landed.

Elia: But I never learned to ask for help. Or rest. Or slower pace. I thought needing anything was the same as losing.

[Avyanna looks at them. Elia's face is neutral, but their hands are tight around the water bottle.]

Elia: Took me two years on this ship to learn that asking for things isn't surrender. It's strategy.

Elia: [meeting her eyes] I'm teaching you what I had to learn the hard way.

---

[Avyanna's vision blurs. She blinks it away.]

Avyanna: [careful] What happens if I ask for too many breaks?

Elia: [flat] Doesn't exist.

Elia: You take the breaks you need. If that's one break per session or ten breaks, it doesn't matter. Training adapts to you. You don't break yourself to fit training.

[They stand, stretch.]

Elia: [offering a hand] Ready to continue? Or do you need more time?

Avyanna: [taking the hand] Ready.

---

[They resume. This time, Elia adds light contact drills. Push against my hand. Pull back when I push. Read the pressure and respond.]

[Avyanna focuses. Her body is tired but not broken. She can feel the difference now-tired is before the edge. Broken is after.]

[After ninety seconds, she needs water.]

[She hesitates. Fails to speak.]

Elia: [stopping] Strike two. You need something and you're not saying it.

Avyanna: [frustrated] How do you know?

Elia: [tapping their temple] You're licking your lips. Your swallows are dry. You need water. So ask for it.

---

[Avyanna forces the words out.]

Avyanna: [halting] Can I have water?

Elia: [immediate] Yes. Always.

[They walk to the bottles together. Drink. Elia doesn't make it feel like failure.]

Elia: [casual] Good. You asked. That's progress.

Avyanna: [bitter] I should have asked sooner.

Elia: [correcting] You asked. That's the victory. Sooner comes with practice.

[They cap the bottles, return to the mats.]

Elia: Last drill. This one's harder.

---

[Elia demonstrates a basic block. Arm up, deflect incoming force.]

Elia: I'm going to push toward you-slow, controlled. You're going to block. If I'm moving too fast, you say "slower." If you need me to demonstrate again, you say "show me." If you need to stop, you say "stop."

Elia: Three requests minimum. I'm not letting you finish this drill until you've asked for something three times.

[Avyanna blinks.]

Avyanna: You're... requiring me to ask?

Elia: [nodding] Forcing the muscle memory. Your body needs to learn that speaking up is safe and expected.

---

[They begin. Elia moves toward her. Avyanna blocks. The contact is light, informative.]

[Elia speeds up slightly.]

[Avyanna's block is late.]

Elia: [pausing] Too fast?

Avyanna: [hesitant] ...Yes. Slower. Please.

Elia: [immediately slowing] Good. That's one.

[They continue. This time Avyanna's blocks connect properly. She can read the movement, anticipate the angle.]

[Elia adds a variation-pushing from a different direction.]

[Avyanna stumbles, confused.]

---

Avyanna: [frustrated] I don't understand what you just did.

Elia: [stopping] Then ask me to show you.

[Avyanna's pride fights her survival instinct. Survival wins.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Can you show me? Slower?

Elia: [demonstrating in slow motion] I'm coming from your left now, not center. Same block, different angle. Like this.

[They demonstrate three times. Avyanna watches. Learns.]

Elia: [approving] That's two. One more request and we're done.

---

[They resume. Avyanna blocks successfully now. She's reading Elia's body, predicting movement. It feels almost like partnering, not fighting.]

[And then she hits the wall. Exhaustion. Real exhaustion, not just tired.]

[She needs to stop. But they said three requests. She's used two. One more and the drill ends.]

[She could ask for water. Or demonstration. Something smaller than stop.]

[But her body is screaming stop.]

---

Elia: [watching her face] You're calculating.

Avyanna: [shaking] I need... I need to stop. But you said three requests and I've only-

Elia: [interrupting, firm] Stop is valid. Stop is always valid. That's your third. We're done.

[Avyanna nearly collapses. Elia steadies her, guides her to sit.]

Elia: [kneeling beside her] You just did something hard. You recognized your limit and named it. That's the whole lesson.

---

[Avyanna's hands are shaking. She wraps them around her knees.]

Avyanna: [hoarse] I thought... I thought saying stop would mean I failed.

Elia: [gentle] Saying stop means you passed. The test is communication, not endurance.

[They hand her water. She drinks. Her throat is raw.]

Elia: [after a moment] Tomorrow, we'll do this again. Same drills, same rules. And the day after, and the day after that. Until asking for what you need feels less like confession and more like breathing.

Avyanna: [quiet] How long does that take?

Elia: [standing, offering a hand] Depends on the person. For me? About six months.

[Avyanna takes the hand. Lets Elia pull her to her feet.]

Elia: [meeting her eyes] But you've got a crew who's patient. And a ship that doesn't count survival as productivity. So you've got time.

---

[Avyanna nods. Her legs are unsteady but functional.]

[Elia cleans up the training space-water bottles stowed, mats folded. Casual domesticity after intensity.]

Elia: [not looking at her] You did well today.

Avyanna: [surprised] I could barely finish.

Elia: [turning] You asked for what you needed three times. You stopped when you hit your limit. You stayed present instead of dissociating.

Elia: That's not barely finishing. That's acing the curriculum.

---

[Avyanna leaves the cargo bay. In the corridor, she leans against the bulkhead and breathes.]

(I said stop. I said slower. I asked for water. And Elia didn't punish me. Didn't even judge me.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm. Attentive.]

(A low, warm pressure at the base of her skull: speak. Safe. Yours.)

[She pushes off the wall and walks back to her quarters. Her muscles ache. It's the good ache-the kind that means use, not damage.]

[Tomorrow, she'll ask for breaks again. And again. Until her body believes it's allowed.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// TRAINING LOG: session one completed | DURATION: 42 minutes | AUTONOMY EXERCISES: three verbal requests recorded | ASSESSMENT: trainee learning to name limits before reaching them | PROGRESS: significant>

<ELIA PERSONAL LOG: "She tried to push past her limit and I stopped her. She looked at me like I'd just revealed magic. This is what we're fighting-the reflex that says endurance is virtue. Tomorrow we do it again. And again. Until she stops counting her needs as failures.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 13d: Choosing Rest (Not Productivity)

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH13d, RECOVERY DAY]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief, Avyanna's quarters and common areas*
> *Present: Avyanna, various crew interactions*
> *Purpose: Learning that rest is valid, productivity is not mandatory, recovery is work*

---

[Avyanna wakes up exhausted. Not the usual exhaustion from nightmares or insomnia. A deeper exhaustion. The kind that settles into bones and says: you cannot function today.]

[She lies in her bunk and calculates. She has training with Elia scheduled. She should help Rho with maintenance tasks. She could practice navigation exercises with Jalen. She should be useful. Should be productive. Should be earning her place.]

[Her body says: no.]

[The conflict is paralyzing. Need to work versus cannot work. Obligation versus capacity. The mine's voice in her head saying weakness is unacceptable versus her body shutting down.]

[She doesn't move for twenty minutes. Just lies there, trapped between should and can't.]

---

[A knock at her door. Soft. Not demanding.]

Nyx: [from the corridor] Avyanna? You missed breakfast. Are you okay?

[Avyanna's throat tightens. Missed breakfast = noticed = evaluation = judgment = consequences.]

Avyanna: [hoarse] I'm fine.

Nyx: [pause] That didn't sound convincing. I'm coming in.

[The door opens. Nyx enters with a medical scanner and the particular calm that means they're in diagnostic mode.]

Nyx: [sitting in the desk chair] What's wrong?

Avyanna: [not looking at them] Nothing. I'm just tired.

Nyx: [running the scanner] Tired as in "didn't sleep well" or tired as in "complete exhaustion"?

Avyanna: [quiet] The second one.

---

[Nyx reads the scanner results.]

Nyx: [measured] Your cortisol levels are elevated. You're showing signs of systemic fatigue. Not sick. Just... depleted.

[They put the scanner away.]

Nyx: [to Avyanna] Have you been pushing yourself hard this week?

Avyanna: [defensive] I'm training. That's my job.

Nyx: [correcting] Your job is learning. Learning requires rest. You can't pour from an empty cup.

Avyanna: [frustrated] I have training scheduled. I should get up. I should-

Nyx: [interrupting, firm] You should rest. That's what your body is telling you. And your body is correct.

---

[Avyanna stares at the ceiling.]

Avyanna: [shaking] If I don't train today, I'll fall behind. If I fall behind, I'm useless. If I'm useless-

Nyx: [interrupting again, gentler] If you push through exhaustion, you'll injure yourself or make mistakes. Then you'll be unable to train for weeks, not just one day.

[They lean forward.]

Nyx: [precise] Rest is not laziness. Rest is maintenance. Your body is a system that requires downtime to repair and consolidate learning. Training while exhausted is like running a ship with failing engines-you might move, but you'll cause damage that costs more than you gain.

---

[Avyanna processes that. Rest as maintenance. Not failure.]

Avyanna: [quiet] What do I tell Elia? She's expecting me.

Nyx: [standing] I'll tell Elia. You don't have to justify exhaustion.

[They pull out their datapad. Type a message. Send it.]

Nyx: [showing her the screen] "Avyanna is taking a recovery day. Systemic fatigue. Training postponed to when she's functional. -Nyx."

Nyx: [to Avyanna] Done. Elia will understand. Everyone on this crew has taken recovery days. It's expected, not exceptional.

---

[Elia's response comes back immediately: "Understood. Tell her to actually rest. -Elia"]

Nyx: [reading it to Avyanna] Elia says actually rest. Not pretend-rest while worrying about being productive.

Avyanna: [uncertain] What does actually resting look like?

Nyx: [considering] No obligations. No tasks. No forcing yourself to be useful. You sleep, eat, do low-effort activities that bring comfort. You give your system permission to recover.

Avyanna: [frustrated] I don't know how to do that. I don't know how to just... be useless for a day.

Nyx: [flat] You're not useless. You're recovering. There's a difference.

---

[Nyx pulls out a small bottle from their medical kit.]

Nyx: [handing it to her] Magnesium supplement. Helps with sleep quality and muscle recovery. Take one now. Drink water. Try to sleep more.

[They stand at the door.]

Nyx: [before leaving] If you need anything-food, company, medical check-in-use ship comms. Someone will respond. That's what crew does.

[They leave. Avyanna is alone with the supplement bottle and permission to rest and no idea how to actually do it.]

---

[She takes the supplement. Drinks water. Lies back down.]

[Her brain screams at her to get up. To be productive. To earn her place. To prove she's not weak.]

[Her body says: no. Sleep. Recover.]

[The conflict is exhausting. She's exhausted from being exhausted.]

[Eventually, she sleeps. Not peaceful sleep. But sleep. Her body taking what it needs despite her brain's protests.]

---

[She wakes three hours later. Still tired. But less hollowed-out. The edges of the exhaustion have softened.]

[She sits up. Her quarters feel small and quiet. Not isolating. Just... still.]

[She could stay here. Stay in bed all day. But the walls are closing in. She needs space. People. But not obligations.]

[She pulls on comfortable clothes. Leaves her quarters.]

---

[The common room is empty except for Rho, who's stretched out on the couch reading something on a datapad. He looks up when she enters.]

Rho: [calm] Hey. Nyx said you're on recovery day.

Avyanna: [hovering in the doorway] Yeah. I don't really know what to do with myself.

Rho: [patting the other end of the couch] Sit. Exist. No pressure.

[She sits. Rho returns to his reading. Doesn't demand conversation. Doesn't expect entertainment. Just... shares space.]

[After ten minutes of silence, Rho speaks.]

Rho: [not looking up] You know what I do on recovery days?

Avyanna: [quiet] What?

Rho: [gesturing at his datapad] I read trash fiction. The kind with terrible plots and improbable physics and characters who make deeply stupid decisions. It requires zero brain power. It's comforting in its predictability.

[He grins at her.]

Rho: [adding] Currently reading a space romance where the engineer falls in love with a sentient asteroid. It's magnificently bad.

---

[Avyanna almost smiles.]

Avyanna: [tentative] Do you have... other trash fiction? That I could read?

Rho: [immediately pulling up a list] I have an entire collection. Genre preferences?

Avyanna: [uncertain] I don't know. Something that won't make me think too hard.

Rho: [sending her three titles] Try these. If you hate them, try others. The point isn't literary merit. The point is pleasant distraction.

[Avyanna downloads one. Opens it. Starts reading.]

[The prose is clunky. The plot is ridiculous. The characters are one-dimensional. It's perfect. It requires nothing from her except basic reading comprehension and a tolerance for absurdity.]

[They sit on opposite ends of the couch. Reading. Existing in proximity. Not performing. Not producing. Just... resting in company.]

---

[An hour later, Jalen enters. Sees them. Raises an eyebrow.]

Jalen: [to Avyanna] Recovery day?

Avyanna: [nodding] Yeah.

Jalen: [getting water from the galley] Good. Pushing through exhaustion is how people make catastrophic mistakes.

[They sit in the chair across from them.]

Jalen: [to no one in particular] I once tried to navigate a jump while running on two hours of sleep and four cups of coffee. Miscalculated the trajectory by point-three degrees. Doesn't sound like much, but at jump speeds, that's a forty-thousand-kilometer deviation.

Jalen: [dry] Vesper was not pleased. Made me take a mandatory rest day. I was furious. Until I slept for fourteen hours and woke up realizing how dangerously impaired I'd been.

---

[Avyanna looks at them.]

Avyanna: [careful] You made a mistake and Vesper didn't punish you?

Jalen: [correcting] Vesper mandated rest. That's not punishment. That's operational safety. I was a liability. Rest fixed the liability.

Jalen: [meeting her eyes] Exhaustion isn't a moral failing. It's a state. States can be changed. That's what recovery days are for.

[They return to their datapad. The three of them sit in the common room. Reading, thinking, existing without obligation.]

[Avyanna's brain is quieter now. The guilt is still there-shouldn't be resting, should be working-but it's muffled. Manageable.]

---

[Around midday, Nyx returns with food. Hands Avyanna a plate without asking if she's hungry.]

Nyx: [matter-of-fact] Eat. Your body needs fuel to recover.

[The food is simple. Protein, carbs, vegetables. Not fancy. Just functional nutrition.]

[Avyanna eats. Realizes she's actually hungry. That her body has needs beyond work. That meeting those needs is allowed.]

Nyx: [sitting beside her] How are you feeling?

Avyanna: [honest] Still tired. Less exhausted. Guilty.

Nyx: [nodding] The guilt is the mine's logic. It'll fade as you practice resting without punishment.

Avyanna: [quiet] How long does that take?

Nyx: [considering] Depends. Months, usually. You're retraining your nervous system to accept that rest is safe. That you're allowed to have limits. That you won't be discarded for being human.

---

[Avyanna finishes eating. Nyx takes the plate.]

Nyx: [before leaving] You're doing well. Taking a recovery day when you need it is maturity, not weakness. Remember that.

[They leave. Avyanna sits with Rho and Jalen. Returns to her trash fiction. Lets her brain float in the ridiculous plot about sentient asteroids and improbable romance.]

[Evening comes. She's still tired. But the exhaustion is less sharp. More like normal tired, less like existential depletion.]

[She returns to her quarters. Her plant is there. Alive. Thriving despite her taking a day off from everything.]

(I rested. I did nothing productive. The crew didn't abandon me. The ship didn't fall apart. I'm still here. Still crew.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm.]

(The hum at the base of her skull softens, as if agreeing with the concept: rest is valid; rest is safe.)

---

[She sleeps that night. Real sleep. Deep sleep. Recovery sleep.]

[Tomorrow, she'll train with Elia again. She'll be functional. Rested. Better.]

[But today, she rested. And that was enough.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// RECOVERY DAY LOG: trainee exhibited systemic fatigue | NYX PRESCRIBED REST | TRAINEE COMPLIED | CREW SUPPORTED WITHOUT JUDGMENT | OUTCOME: trainee rested for 11.4 hours, consumed adequate nutrition, engaged in low-effort social contact | ASSESSMENT: appropriate recovery protocol>

<NYX PERSONAL LOG: "Systemic exhaustion. She's been pushing herself too hard. Typical post-trauma pattern-compensating for perceived inadequacy by overworking. Prescribed rest. She struggled to accept it. But she rested. That's progress. She's learning that she's allowed to have limits.">

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "She took a recovery day. Sat with me. Read trash fiction. Didn't apologize for existing without being useful. That's growth. She's learning that crew isn't transactional. That she's valued even when she's not producing. That matters.">

<ELIA MESSAGE TO NYX: "Thanks for canceling training. She's been pushing hard. Needed the break. Let me know when she's ready to resume. No rush.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 13e: Water Is Not a Test

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH13d, EARLY REST PRACTICE]**
> *Location: Crew quarters washroom / laundry nook*
> *Present: Avyanna, Bubbles, Cinnamon.exe*
> *Teaching: comfort is not a quota; care is not a reward*

---

[The washroom is too clean.]

[Not sterile-lived clean. The kind of clean that means someone uses this space and then puts it back the way they want to find it.]

[Avyanna stands in the doorway with her hands in fists, staring at the shower control panel.]

[A dial with temperature ranges. A toggle for pressure. A little display that says WATER AVAILABLE.]

(Available for who. For how long.)

[Bubbles hovers behind her, not pushing her in.]

Bubbles: You have not bathed.

Avyanna: [too fast] I have.

[Bubbles waits.]

[Avyanna hears herself and corrects the lie without being asked.]

Avyanna: I rinsed.

Avyanna: Once.

Bubbles: That is not bathing.

Avyanna: It was enough.

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: deflection language | INFERENCE: scarcity conditioning | CONFIDENCE: 0.89>

[Avyanna stares at the dial.]

[She can feel the mine on her skin like a second uniform: dust that never leaves, sweat that dries wrong, the memory of water that came with eyes on you.]

(If you take too long, someone yells. If you take too much, someone takes it back.)

[Cinnamon's terminal in the corner wakes, as if it has been listening and decides it is time to be useful.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// STATUS: water rationing not active | NOTE: no metering policy for hygiene | POLICY: "take what you need">

Avyanna: [hoarse] Nothing is unmetered.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: correct in hostile systems | NOTE: this ship is not hostile to hygiene>

Avyanna: That doesn't mean it's safe.

[Bubbles rotates toward her, fans quieting.]

Bubbles: You are safe enough to be clean.

[The sentence lands like a hand offered.]

[Avyanna doesn't take it. Not yet.]

Avyanna: If I use too much, does it... affect the ship.

[Cinnamon answers without pity, which is the only way Avyanna can hear it.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// ANSWER: negligible impact | CONTEXT: hygiene is operational requirement | FOLLOW-UP: infections cost more water>

Avyanna: [a small laugh that isn't humor] Everything is operational.

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATION: yes>

Bubbles: We like you operational.

Avyanna: [quiet] I'm not a machine.

[Bubbles' fans change pitch-annoyed in defense of her.]

Bubbles: Correct.

Bubbles: You are a person.

[Avyanna swallows.]

[She reaches for the dial and stops.]

[Her hand hovers over warmth like it's a trap door.]

(Warm water means vulnerability. Warm water means someone can hurt you because you're soft.)

Avyanna: [barely] How long.

Bubbles: How long what.

Avyanna: How long until I'm... done.

[Silence. Listening, not judging.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee framing hygiene as timed task | INFERENCE: prior punishment context | CONFIDENCE: 0.91>

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: there is no "until" | SUGGESTION: bathe until body reports "better">

Avyanna: My body lies.

[Bubbles drifts closer, just enough that Avyanna can hear the tiny corrective hum.]

Bubbles: Your body is a witness.

Bubbles: It is scared. It is still a witness.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: That's not fair.

Bubbles: No.

Bubbles: The mine was not fair.

[Avyanna turns the dial one notch toward warm.]

[Water hisses through the pipes like the ship clearing its throat.]

[She flinches at the sound.]

[Bubbles does not comment.]

[The first spray hits her palm-hot enough to make her jerk back.]

Avyanna: Ow.

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: temperature overshoot | ACTION: reduce to safe threshold>

[The water shifts to a steady warmth, like someone smoothing a blanket.]

Avyanna: [suspicious] You adjusted it.

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATION: yes | NOTE: you are allowed to be comfortable>

[Avyanna stares at the display again.]

[WATER AVAILABLE.]

[It doesn't tick down.]

(It doesn't tick down.)

[Her shoulders drop by a millimeter.]

[She steps in.]

[The water hits her hair, her scalp, her neck. Heat spreads under skin that has been cold for too long.]

[For a second, the mine tries to rise-showers as a line, as a punishment, as a place where eyes measured you for weakness.]

[Avyanna's lungs seize.]

[She turns her face into the spray and forces breath through the moment.]

[In. Out.]

[In.]

[Bubbles speaks from outside the curtain, not entering without permission.]

Bubbles: Do you want company.

Avyanna: [immediate] No.

[Then-because she is learning honesty is a floor, not a threat-]

Avyanna: Thank you.

Bubbles: You are welcome.

[Cinnamon's text appears on the terminal, simple.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// REMINDER: you may take two towels>

Avyanna: [startled] Two.

<CINNAMON.EXE// CLARIFICATION: yes | NOTE: drying quickly reduces chill response>

[She laughs again, quieter.]

Avyanna: Who decided that.

<CINNAMON.EXE// ANSWER: me>

Avyanna: [muttering] Of course.

[She washes. Slowly.]

[Soap that smells like something alive-not mine disinfectant, not chemical fear.]

[When she finally turns the water off, she stands still for a moment, waiting for the other shoe.]

[No alarm.]

[No banging on the door.]

[No shouted quota.]

[Just the ship humming like it has always been this kind.]

[Avyanna steps out wrapped in a towel that is too soft to trust.]

[Bubbles offers another without making it a question that costs anything.]

[Avyanna takes it.]

[Her hands tremble once.]

(I'm clean. And nothing bad happened.)

[She doesn't know what to do with that.]

[So she does the only thing she knows how to do with new evidence.]

[She files it.]

---

[The laundry nook is adjacent, like the ship assumes hygiene includes clothing and isn't making you ask permission twice.]

[A row of baskets. A machine that looks too expensive to waste on ordinary fabric. Shelves of detergent in small bottles, each labeled with a scent name that feels like a luxury someone bothered to catalog.]

[Avyanna stands in front of them as if choosing wrong will be punished.]

(In the mine, you got whatever chemical soap they issued. It stripped skin. It didn't count as cruelty because it was "standard.")

[Bubbles hovers at the doorway again, refusing to enter without being invited.]

Bubbles: Laundry is next.

Avyanna: [stiff] I can do it.

Bubbles: Yes.

Bubbles: Do you want help.

[Avyanna's throat tightens at the question. Help always meant debt.]

Avyanna: No.

[Then-]

Avyanna: Maybe... explain the machine.

[Bubbles' fans shift: approval without fanfare.]

Bubbles: Yes.

---

[The machine has a simple interface.]

[*Load.*]

[*Select cycle.*]

[*Select temperature.*]

[*Start.*]

[No cost display. No countdown. No warning about "overuse."]

Avyanna: [quiet] It doesn't track.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: it tracks for maintenance only | NOTE: not for punishment>

[Avyanna pulls her clothes from the hamper.]

[Crew-issue fabric, already softening from regular washing.]

[She hesitates at the pile, suddenly aware of how much she owns.]

(Mine brain: hoard. Keep. Don't waste. Don't take what you can't defend.)

[She starts sorting like she's trying to prove she deserves it.]

[Bubbles doesn't let her spiral quietly.]

Bubbles: You are permitted to wash all of it.

Avyanna: [defensive] I wasn't-

Bubbles: You were.

[Avyanna freezes.]

Avyanna: [small] If I wash it all, I'll have nothing to wear.

<CINNAMON.EXE// SUGGESTION: use spare linens | NOTE: crew-issue basics exist in supply locker | POLICY: you may take them>

Avyanna: Supply locker.

(The mine would never let you take from supply without "approval." Approval meant debt.)

Bubbles: We can get you two sets of basics.

Avyanna: Two.

Bubbles: Two.

[Bubbles pauses.]

Bubbles: You can have more later.

[Avyanna's chest tightens.]

Avyanna: [rough] I don't know how to...

Bubbles: Want.

[The word is gentle and brutal.]

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: I don't know how to want without paying.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: practice>

---

[Avyanna stares at the detergent shelf again.]

Avyanna: What do I pick.

<CINNAMON.EXE// QUESTION: what do you prefer>

[Prefer.]

[The word feels like a trick question.]

[Avyanna picks up one bottle, reads the label.]

> *Citrus.*

[She puts it down.]

[Picks up another.]

> *Lavender.*

[Her throat tightens unexpectedly.]

(The mine smelled like metal and sweat and disinfectant. Lavender smells like a place where no one dies for production.)

Avyanna: [quiet] This one.

[No alarm. No correction. No laughter.]

Bubbles: Acknowledged.

<CINNAMON.EXE// NOTE: preference logged | COMMENTARY: good>

["Preference logged" should feel invasive.]

[Instead it feels like someone taking her seriously.]

---

[She loads the machine.]

[Presses start.]

[The drum begins to turn.]

[The sound is ordinary. Domestic. It makes her eyes sting.]

(The ship is doing chores. The ship is treating me like I belong inside chores.)

[Avyanna wipes her face with the edge of her towel before she can be embarrassed by needing one.]

[Bubbles stays outside the doorway, a sentinel for dignity.]

Bubbles: Do you need anything else.

[Avyanna looks at the shelf of folded towels.]

[One is still around her hair. Another around her shoulders. She wants a third, absurdly, because it would mean she's allowed to be wasteful.]

[She takes a breath.]

Avyanna: I... want another towel.

[Silence.]

[Then Cinnamon, brisk as ever:]

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: granted>

[Bubbles adds:]

Bubbles: I will bring it.

[Avyanna's throat tightens. Not with shame. With something worse.]

(They didn't make me justify it.)

[Bubbles returns with a third towel and places it on the counter like it's nothing.]

[Like wanting is nothing.]

[Avyanna doesn't know how to hold that without breaking, so she does what she's learned to do with fragile things.]

[She holds it carefully.]


---

# Chapter 13f: The Yes Reflex

> **[INTERSTITIAL - OCCURS POST-CH13c]**
> *Trigger: Elia demands an answer that isn't obedience*
> *Purpose: prove "yes" as training, not nature*

---

[Elia's lesson doesn't end when the spar ends.]

[It follows Avyanna down the corridor like an afterimage.]

Elia: [earlier, blunt] Stop saying yes like it's oxygen.

[Avyanna has laughed at that like it's a joke.]

[It wasn't.]

---

[She's alone in her quarters, hands shaking over the sink, trying to rinse the taste of adrenaline out of her mouth.]

[She practiced the drill like Elia demanded.]

What is the ask.

What is the risk.

What do I need to answer cleanly.

[The questions felt like heresy.]

[Her body kept trying to answer them with the only word the mine trained into her:]

Yes.

---

## Intercut - The Kennel (What "Yes" Bought)

[A supervisor's shadow crosses the work line.]

[Avyanna is fourteen. Maybe. Time in the mine is counted in quotas, not birthdays.]

[The air smells like heated metal and sour sweat and the sweet rot of too many bodies sharing too little oxygen.]

Supervisor: You.

[A finger points at the boy beside her.]

[He is new. His hands are still soft enough to betray him.]

Supervisor: Step forward.

[The boy hesitates.]

[Hesitation is a visible thing here.]

Supervisor: Now.

[The boy's eyes flick left and right like he's looking for the rule that explains what this is.]

[Avyanna sees the moment his brain tries to calculate a safe response.]

[She sees the moment his mouth opens.]

[And she sees the exact second the mine decides he's too slow.]

Supervisor: Wrong.

[The baton cracks against the boy's ribs.]

[He makes a sound that is mostly surprise.]

[The supervisor smiles like they taught him something.]

Supervisor: Again.

[The boy stumbles forward, breath gone, eyes wet with pain and confusion.]

Supervisor: Do you understand.

[The boy tries to speak.]

[He tries to form a question.]

[The baton hits again.]

Supervisor: Don't waste my time.

---

[Avyanna does not move.]

[Her hands keep sorting glitter like machines.]

[Her face stays blank because blank faces survive longer.]

[But her body takes notes.]

Slow equals pain.

Questions equal pain.

Not-knowing equals pain.

[She learns the real answer the mine wants:]

Fast obedience.

Perfect compliance.

No visible thought.

---

[The supervisor turns to her without warning.]

Supervisor: You. Switch stations. Now.

[The request is impossible. Her station is wired into the line. Switching means breaking rhythm. Breaking rhythm means punishment for everyone near her.]

[A choice shaped like a trap.]

[Avyanna doesn't evaluate.]

[She doesn't ask why.]

[She doesn't even feel the fear until later.]

Avyanna: Yes.

[The word comes out before she's conscious of it.]

[Her legs move.]

[The supervisor watches her like she's a well-trained dog.]

Supervisor: Good girl.

[Avyanna's stomach turns.]

[But her body learns the only lesson that matters:]

Yes can be faster than pain.

---

## Return - Quarters (New Rule)

[Avyanna grips the sink edge until her knuckles go white.]

[There is no baton here.]

[There is no supervisor.]

[But her muscles still expect impact for any pause longer than a breath.]

(Elia wants me to stop saying yes.)

(My body thinks that's how you die.)

[She presses her palm flat against her sternum.]

[Feels her heartbeat like a trapped animal.]

[Then she tries something Elia would approve of.]

[She speaks to the empty room, voice quiet and steady.]

Avyanna: I don't know.

[The sentence lands.]

[Nothing happens.]

[No punishment. No laughter. No baton.]

[Only her own breath, coming back.]

[She says it again, slower.]

Avyanna: I don't understand yet.

[Her shoulders drop by a fraction.]

[Then, because she is learning to be brave in small ways:]

Avyanna: And that's allowed.

---
*End Chapter 13f*



---

# Chapter 13g: Coffee, Before It Was a Weapon

> **[INTERSTITIAL - OCCURS POST-CH13b]**
> *Trigger: Rho's coffee is care, not just habit*
> *Purpose: show Rho's "governance" started as love*

---

[Rho makes coffee like he's sealing a hull breach.]

[Measured. Repeated. Mildly furious at physics.]

[Avyanna watches from the galley doorway with the same caution she uses around armed strangers.]

[Not because Rho is dangerous.]

[Because tenderness is.]

Rho: [without looking up] You going to stare all day or drink something.

Avyanna: I'm not staring.

Rho: You're staring.

[He sets a mug on the counter and slides it toward her.]

[No ceremony. No "you earned it." No invoice tone.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Why do you care so much.

Rho: About coffee.

Avyanna: About... making it right.

[Rho's hand pauses mid-stir.]

[A small stillness, like a door shutting gently.]

Rho: Habit.

[The word is true and not true.]

---

## Intercut - *Grasp of Dawn* (Rho's First Shift)

[The galley is smaller.]

[The ship is smaller too-old metal, cheap insulation, a floor that rattles when the engines push.]

[Rho is younger and not yet tired in the particular ways that never go away.]

[He is holding a mug with both hands like it's a promise.]

[Across from him, Kenna sits cross-legged on the bench seat, hair tied back with a strip of wire because she is an engineer and everything becomes a tool.]

Kenna: That is not coffee.

Rho: [defensive] It's hot.

Kenna: That's not the definition.

[Kenna leans over his shoulder and adjusts the grinder setting with gentle violence.]

Rho: Don't.

Kenna: I'm helping.

Rho: You always say that like it's a legal defense.

Kenna: [mouth twitching] It is.

---

[Kenna watches the brew drip, eyes half-lidded like she's listening to the ship's bones.]

Kenna: You're scared.

Rho: I'm fine.

Kenna: That's also not the definition.

[Rho exhales.]

Rho: New job.

Kenna: I read the contract.

Rho: I read it too.

Kenna: [flat] Then you're scared on purpose.

[Rho looks away.]

Kenna: Hey.

[Her hand hovers near his wrist.]

[She doesn't grab.]

[She waits for consent like it's normal.]

Rho: Yes.

[Kenna touches him, steady pressure, not a claim.]

Kenna: If it goes bad, we leave.

Rho: The paperwork-

Kenna: [sharp] The paperwork doesn't get to kill us.

[Rho's throat tightens.]

Rho: I don't want to lose the crew.

Kenna: Then feed them.

Rho: [confused] What.

Kenna: You do this.

[She points at the coffee.]

Kenna: You make something small and normal and yours.

Kenna: You make the ship feel like a place people come back to.

Kenna: That's governance.

[Rho makes a face.]

Rho: You sound like Rowan.

Kenna: I sound like someone who wants you alive.

---

[Kenna tastes the coffee, then nods once-approval that lands like a medal.]

Kenna: Better.

Rho: You fixed it.

Kenna: I corrected your assumptions.

Rho: That's the same thing.

Kenna: It is not.

Kenna: But I love that you tried.

[Rho laughs, startled by how easy it is.]

[Kenna smiles like she did that on purpose.]

---

## Return - Galley (Now)

[Rho's hand resumes stirring like the pause never happened.]

[Avyanna watches his face for grief.]

[He gives her none.]

Rho: Drink it before it dies.

Avyanna: Coffee dies.

Rho: Everything dies.

[A beat.]

Rho: This is just faster.

[Avyanna lifts the mug.]

[It smells like bitter warmth and competence.]

Avyanna: [soft] It's good.

[Rho grunts like he doesn't know what to do with praise.]

Rho: That's because I'm excellent.

[He is not smiling.]

[He is, somehow, making the galley feel like a place people come back to.]

---
*End Chapter 13g*



---

﻿# Chapter 13: Shipboard Physics

> **LUMEN THIEF - TRAINING PROTOCOL (AMENDED):**
> *Subject: Shipboard Physics*
> *Summary: Gravity is honest. So are we.*
> *Rule 1: Learn how to fall without breaking.*
> *Rule 2: Learn how to prove what happened.*
> *Rule 3: Learn the difference between power and strain.*
> *Addendum: Floors first. Peaks later. If ever.*

---

[The cargo bay is the ship's largest lie.]

[It looks like a place for crates and contraband and emergency repairs.]

[It is also where you teach someone how to survive being thrown to the floor.]

[The deck plating is cold through Avyanna's socks. The air tastes faintly of polymer and recycled coffee. A vibration runs up her shins with each pulse of the engines-a steady reminder that the ship is moving, that motion is being maintained by people she now has names for.]

(This is still a workplace.)

(Different rules. Elia said that. Different place.)

[Elia is already there, barefoot, hair tied back like it's about to commit a crime. No blade in her hands. No armor. Just a woman built out of decisions.]

Elia: [nodding once] Good. You showed up.

[Avyanna's spine tries to lock, the old reflex-attendance as survival. She forces a slow breath instead. In. Out. Count four. Count the exits.]

[Cargo bay door. Corridor. Maintenance ladder.]

[Elia watches her eyes move.]

Elia: Don't stop doing that. Just don't let it freeze you.

Avyanna: [automatic, too formal] Yes-

Elia: [flat] No "yes." Not here. If you don't understand, you say so.

[Elia lifts a hand, palm up-stop signal, not threat.]

[Avyanna's mouth closes. The automatic agreement dies before it escapes.]

Elia: That. Right there. That's the reflex we're breaking.

Avyanna: [careful] I was agreeing with you.

Elia: Were you? Or were you just saying what you think keeps you safe?

[The question hits like cold water.]

[Avyanna doesn't answer. Can't answer. Because Elia's right.]

Elia: At the mine, "yes" meant survival. Here, "yes" when you mean "I don't know" gets people killed.

[Elia sits on the edge of the console, making herself lower, less looming.]

Elia: So we're going to practice. Every time I give you an instruction, you're going to do three things before you move.

[She holds up fingers as she counts.]

Elia: One. State the assumption.

Elia: Two. Ask if the assumption is true.

Elia: Three. If you're still not sure, say "I don't understand."

Avyanna: [quiet] That's going to take forever.

Elia: Good. Fast obedience is how they trained you. Slow thinking is how you survive.

[She gestures at the console.]

Elia: Let's start. I'm going to tell you to check the reactor pressure. What's your assumption?

Avyanna: [hesitant] That... the reactor pressure needs checking?

Elia: Why do you assume that?

Avyanna: Because you told me to.

Elia: [grin] And if I'm wrong? If I'm tired, or distracted, or testing you?

[Avyanna's hands tighten.]

Avyanna: Then I'd check something that doesn't need checking.

Elia: Exactly. So what do you ask?

Avyanna: [slow, trying it out] Why are we checking reactor pressure?

Elia: [approving] Good. And I'd answer: because Jalen flagged an anomaly, or because it's on the maintenance schedule, or because I want you to learn where the readout is.

Elia: Now you know. Now "yes" means something.

[Avyanna processes that.]

Avyanna: But what if there's no time? What if it's an emergency?

Elia: Then I don't give you a choice. I say "Avyanna, do this, now, I'll explain later."

[She leans forward.]

Elia: And you'll know it's real because I never pull that card unless it's life or death. Because I don't train you to obey blindly and then suddenly demand critical thinking when the ship's on fire.

Avyanna: [very quiet] The overseers did that.

Elia: I know. That's why we're doing this.

[She stands, offers a hand up.]

Elia: Three questions. Every instruction. Until it's reflex.

Avyanna: [taking the hand] What. Why. What if.

Elia: [sharp grin] Fast learner. Let's break some more habits.

[Elia lifts a hand, palm up-stop signal, not threat.]

Elia: Three questions.

[She holds up fingers as she counts, like she's teaching a child and a soldier at the same time.]

Elia: What are we doing.

Elia: Why are we doing it.

Elia: What happens if you do it wrong.

[Avyanna stares.]

Avyanna: [automatic] So I-

Elia: Not "so I can obey." So you can decide.

[The sentence lands hard. Decision as a thing Avyanna is allowed to have.]

Elia: If you can't answer those three, you don't move. You ask. You stall. You buy time.

Avyanna: [quiet] In the Kennel, stalling meant-

Elia: I know.

[Elia's gaze is steady in the way a bulkhead is steady. No pity. No softness performance. Just a rule.]

Elia: Here, stalling is how you stay alive.

Avyanna: [swallows] What if you tell me to do something and I don't understand.

Elia: Then you say: "Explain."

Avyanna: And if you get angry.

Elia: Then you'll have learned something about me that needs correcting.

[Cooling beat: Elia's mouth quirks, almost a smile.]

Elia: I'm not allergic to being wrong, Avyanna. I'm allergic to rot.

Elia: Confusion you say out loud is fixable. Silence isn't.

[Avyanna's pulse is loud in her ears.]

(Ask. Out loud. Like it won't cost me skin.)

Elia: Try it.

Avyanna: [a breath] What are we doing.

Elia: Teaching you how to hit the floor without letting it collect you.

Avyanna: Why.

Elia: Because corridors throw people. Bullets throw people. Panic throws people. You don't get to pick when.

Avyanna: What happens if I do it wrong.

Elia: You get hurt.

Elia: Or you die.

Elia: So we learn it on purpose. In here. With mats. With me watching. With you allowed to stop.

[Avyanna nods once. It isn't agreement. It's comprehension. That's different.]

[Silence, the kind Avyanna used to live inside. Elia waits it out like it's weather.]

Avyanna: [quiet] I understand.

Elia: We'll see.

---

[Elia walks a slow circle around her-distance kept deliberate, not crowding. Evaluating stance the way Vesper evaluates contracts: looking for the hidden clause that kills you.]

Elia: You're not going to be a fighter.

[The words land clean and hard. Avyanna's stomach drops anyway.]

(Not useful.)

Elia: [matter-of-fact] That's fine. I don't need another blade. I need you alive.

[Avyanna swallows. Her left hip aches, a reminder from the mine that bodies keep receipts even when you don't.]

Avyanna: I can learn.

Elia: You can learn to survive. That's what this is.

[Elia steps in. Not fast. Not threatening. A demonstration of how little warning "not fast" can be.]

Elia: Stance. Feet under you. Weight where you can move it.

[She adjusts Avyanna's shoulders with two fingers-light touch, no claiming. Just alignment.]

Elia: Knees unlocked. You lock them, you fall wrong. You fall wrong, you break.

[Avyanna tries. Her body wants the mine's posture-small, contained, invisible. Elia's hands hover, correct, withdraw.]

Elia: Good. Now fall.

Avyanna: [blinking] What?

Elia: On purpose. Better you learn it here than in a corridor with bullets.

[Avyanna's throat goes dry.]

(In the Kennel, falling meant someone stepped on you.)

Avyanna: I-

Elia: [cutting in] It's controlled. I'm here. If it hurts, we adjust. If you're scared, you say it.

[The deck hums. The ship keeps going. Elia's face stays steady-no softness performance, no cruelty either. Just the fact of her attention.]

[Avyanna lowers herself, awkward. Her palms slap the mat Elia must have laid out when she wasn't looking.]

Pain spikes up her wrists.

Elia: Wrong.

Avyanna: [breathing through it] I-

Elia: Again.

<WAFFLE.BAT// OBSERVATION: pain response elevated | INFERENCE: old injury fear-loop | CONFIDENCE: 0.73>

[Avyanna stares at the angle-brackets on the wall display. The ship, watching. Not like the Kennel's cameras-hungry, punitive. This feels... clinical. Protective. Weirdly proud.]

Elia: [dry] Don't take advice from the gremlin unless it's about not dying.

Waffle.bat: [over the bay speakers, offended sincerity] I can do both.

[Cooling beat: Elia's mouth twitches. Avyanna's hands flex once, then settle.]

Elia: Roll your shoulder. Turn. Let the floor take the force, not your bones.

[They do it again. Again. Again.]

[Avyanna learns the strange intimacy of impact in a place where nobody uses it as a lever.]

[She learns that falling can be a skill instead of a failure.]

---

[An hour later, her muscles shake with new kinds of exhaustion. Elia calls a stop like she calls everything: no ceremony, just decision.]

Elia: That's enough.

Avyanna: [hoarse] I can-

Elia: [flat] You can't. That's not a moral weakness. It's a body.

[Avyanna sits on the mat, sweat cooling fast in the recycled air. Her hip throbs, but it's a clean throb-use, not damage.]

Elia: Your job is to not die long enough for us to reach you.
