[They walk through a residential sector. Quieter. Crew quarters for long-term contractors. Small apartments with windows overlooking the docking bay.]

Vesper: [slowing] Some contractors live on stations full-time. They're not ship crew, but they're Guild-affiliated. They have the same rights, same access, same protections.

Vesper: If you ever wanted to live station-side instead of ship-side, you could. Your choice.

[Avyanna looks at the apartments. Stable. Stationary. Safe.]

[And suffocating.]

Avyanna: [quiet] I think... I think I need the ship. For now.

Vesper: [nodding] Understood. The option remains available if you change your mind.

---

[They reach the docking bay. The Lumen Thief is visible through the viewport-scarred, asymmetrical, home.]

Vesper: [turning to face Avyanna] Last rule. The most important one.

[Avyanna waits.]

Vesper: [meeting her eyes] Guild space is safer than most places. But safe is relative. Stay aware. Trust your instincts. If something feels wrong, it probably is.

Vesper: You're learning to function here. That doesn't mean you stop being cautious. Caution kept you alive in the mine. It'll keep you alive here too.

Avyanna: [nodding] Caution. Awareness. Trust instincts.

Vesper: [approving] And if you're ever uncertain, ask. Crew, station personnel, Guild AI systems. Resources exist. Use them.

---

[Waffle hovers beside Avyanna.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// PERSONAL NOTE: i am also resource | IF YOU ARE LOST OR SCARED OR UNSURE I WILL ASSIST | ALSO I GIVE EXCELLENT DIRECTIONS | ALSO I KNOW WHERE ALL THE GOOD FOOD VENDORS ARE>

Avyanna: [almost smiling] Thank you, Waffle.

<WAFFLE.BAT// ACKNOWLEDGED: you are crew | CREW SUPPORT IS NOT GRATITUDE-BASED | IT IS STRUCTURAL>

[But the drone's lights pulse warm anyway. Affection, even if it won't name it as such.]

---

[They board the ship. The airlock hisses closed behind them. Avyanna's shoulders relax incrementally. Station space is safer than Compact space. But ship space is home.]

Vesper: [removing her outer jacket] You did well today. Observed. Asked questions. Stayed aware.

Avyanna: [uncertain] I barely did anything.

Vesper: [hanging the jacket] You navigated Guild space for the first time without panic. You absorbed protocols. You made choices about your comfort level.

Vesper: That's not barely anything. That's exactly what I needed you to do.

---

[Avyanna heads toward her quarters. In the corridor, she pauses.]

Avyanna: [turning back] Vesper?

Vesper: [at her own door] Yes?

Avyanna: [careful] The contractor who said I was in good hands. Were they right?

[Vesper pauses. Considers the question with the seriousness it deserves.]

Vesper: [quiet] Yes. You are. We're not perfect. But we're committed to your safety and autonomy. That commitment is documented and verified.

Vesper: [meeting her eyes] You're in good hands. And you're learning to trust that.

---

[Avyanna nods. Continues to her quarters. Closes the door behind her.]

[She sits on her bunk. Pulls out the data chip Vesper gave her-three identities, encrypted, hers to control.]

(Guild station protocols. Neutral ground. Reputation as currency. Boundaries as law.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm. Content.]

(A quiet hum at the base of her skull: guild, floor, safe.)

[She tucks the chip back into her pocket. Tomorrow, there will be another station. Another set of protocols to learn. Another layer of the galaxy revealing itself.]

[And slowly, incrementally, she's learning to move through it without fear.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// STATION VISIT LOG: Guild Station Kael-7 | DURATION: 3.2 hours | TRAINEE BEHAVIOR: appropriate and observant | PROTOCOLS LEARNED: neutrality enforcement, reputation systems, boundary protection, resource sharing | ASSESSMENT: integration progressing>

<WAFFLE.BAT// OBSERVATION: trainee asked good questions | TRAINEE ACCEPTED BOUNDARIES EDUCATION WITHOUT RESISTANCE | TRAINEE IDENTIFIED SHIP AS HOME | ASSESSMENT: crew bonding effective>

<VESPER PERSONAL LOG: "She walked through Guild space like she expected someone to grab her at any moment. But she kept walking. Asked the right questions. Recognized that safety is verb, not noun. She's learning.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 15b: First Purchase Decision (Earned Money)

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH15b after first contract payment]**
> *Location: Mid-tier station market*
> *Present: Avyanna, Bubbles*
> *Purpose: Learning to spend money autonomously, distinguishing wants from needs*

---

[Avyanna has two hundred credits in her account. Money she earned. Not given. Not stolen. Earned through work.]

[The concept is still strange. The mine took everything and gave nothing. Here, she worked one contract and has enough money to buy... things. Whatever things she wants. Or needs. Or both.]

[That's the problem. She doesn't know the difference yet.]

[She stands in the market district of Station Kael-7 with Bubbles hovering beside her. She's supposed to be buying things. Vesper said: "You have money. You need supplies. Go buy them. It's good practice."]

[But what does she need? And what does she want? And how does she tell them apart?]

---

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee has been stationary for 4.7 minutes | QUERY: do you require assistance>

Avyanna: [uncertain] I don't know what to buy.

<BUBBLES// CLARIFICATION REQUIRED: you don't know what to buy because you lack information about available goods, or because you are uncertain of your preferences>

Avyanna: [frustrated] Both. Neither. I just... I have money and I don't know what to do with it.

<BUBBLES// ACKNOWLEDGED: first autonomous purchase decision is difficult | SUGGESTION: start with needs, then proceed to wants | NEEDS = items required for survival/function | WANTS = items that increase comfort/pleasure but are not strictly necessary>

---

[Avyanna processes that. Needs first. She can do needs. Needs are objective.]

Avyanna: [to Bubbles] What do I need?

<BUBBLES// ASSESSMENT: basic hygiene supplies running low | CLOTHING: adequate but minimal variety | NUTRITION: ship provides meals but personal snack stores are recommended for autonomy | COMFORT ITEMS: worry stone acquired, other grounding tools may be beneficial>

[Bubbles projects a small list in the air.]

<BUBBLES// RECOMMENDED PURCHASES:
- Hygiene supplies (soap, cleaning cloths, personal care items): ~15 credits
- Additional clothing (second set for rotation): ~30 credits
- Personal food storage (non-perishable snacks): ~20 credits
- Grounding tools (if desired): ~10 credits
TOTAL: ~75 credits | REMAINING BUDGET: 125 credits for discretionary use>

---

[Avyanna reads the list. Seventy-five credits for needs. One hundred twenty-five credits left over. For wants.]

[The concept of having money left over after needs feels impossible.]

Avyanna: [quiet] What do I do with the rest?

<BUBBLES// OPTIONS:
1. Save for future needs
2. Purchase comfort/pleasure items
3. Combination of both
ALL OPTIONS ARE VALID | YOUR CHOICE>

[Her choice. Everything here is her choice.]

[She starts with needs. Easier to think about.]

---

**Hygiene Supplies**

[The vendor has twenty different kinds of soap. TWENTY. Avyanna stares at them like they're a threat.]

Vendor: [helpful] Looking for anything specific?

Avyanna: [overwhelmed] Just... soap.

Vendor: [nodding] Bar or liquid? Scented or unscented? Antibacterial or moisturizing?

[Avyanna's brain shorts out. Too many options. Too many variables.]

<BUBBLES// ASSISTANCE: recommend unscented, moisturizing, bar form | REASONING: less likely to trigger scent-based trauma memories, easy to store, station-standard quality>

Avyanna: [to vendor] That one. The unscented moisturizing bar.

Vendor: [handing it to her] Good choice. Anything else?

---

[She adds cleaning cloths. Toothpaste. Things that are universal. Things that don't require decisions beyond "do I need this? yes."]

[Total: fourteen credits. She pays. The transaction is simple. No haggling. No games. Just goods exchanged for money at the stated price.]

[One down. Three to go.]

**Clothing**

[The clothing stalls are worse. So many colors. So many styles. So many ways to be wrong.]

[She gravitates toward gray. Safe. Familiar. The mine color. But then she remembers-she doesn't have to wear gray anymore. Gray isn't mandatory. Gray is just habit.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee selecting gray garments | QUERY: is this preference or default trauma response>

Avyanna: [pausing] I don't know.

<BUBBLES// SUGGESTION: test alternative | SELECT ONE ITEM IN DIFFERENT COLOR | COMPARE EMOTIONAL RESPONSE | DETERMINE IF GRAY IS PREFERENCE OR SAFETY BEHAVIOR>

---

[Avyanna picks up a gray shirt. Then a blue one. The blue reminds her of Jalen's nav displays. Of the first coffee ritual. Of sky that isn't filtered through mine dust.]

[She holds both. Compares. The gray feels safe. The blue feels like... possibility?]

Vendor: [nearby] Try them on if you want. Changing room's open.

[Avyanna tries the blue shirt. It fits. The color is bright against her skin in a way that feels foreign but not wrong.]

[She buys both. Gray for safe days. Blue for days when she wants to remember that she's not in the mine anymore.]

[Cost: thirty-two credits. Within budget.]

---

**Personal Food Storage**

[The food vendors sell pre-packaged snacks. Protein bars. Dried fruit. Nut mixes. Things that keep without refrigeration. Things you can eat when ship meals don't align with hunger.]

[Avyanna picks items based on Bubbles' nutritional recommendations and her own tentative preferences. She's learning that she likes sweet things. That salt is sometimes too much. That texture matters as much as taste.]

[She fills a small bag with selections. Enough for two weeks if she rations. Or one week if she doesn't.]

[Cost: eighteen credits.]

---

**Grounding Tools**

[This is the hard one. This is wants, not needs. She already has the worry stone. She doesn't *need* more tools.]

[But Nyx gave her the weighted stone and it helped. Maybe other things would help too.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee hesitating at grounding tools vendor | REMINDER: comfort items are not frivolous | MENTAL HEALTH TOOLS ARE VALID PURCHASES | YOU ARE ALLOWED TO INVEST IN YOUR OWN WELL-BEING>

[Avyanna approaches the vendor. Looks at the options. Fidget rings. Textured squares. Small puzzles. Things designed to give restless hands something to do.]

[She picks up a smooth metal ring. It spins. The motion is satisfying. Mindless. Something to do when her thoughts get too loud.]

Vendor: [knowledgeable] That's a spinner ring. Good for anxiety. Fidget without being disruptive.

Avyanna: [testing it] How much?

Vendor: Eight credits.

[Eight credits. For something she doesn't strictly need. For comfort. For mental health. For herself.]

Avyanna: [decision made] I'll take it.

---

[She pays. The ring is hers. She immediately starts spinning it on her finger. The motion is soothing.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee purchased non-essential comfort item autonomously | ASSESSMENT: developing ability to identify and meet own comfort needs | THIS IS PROGRESS>

[Total spent on needs: sixty-four credits. One hundred thirty-six credits remaining.]

[Avyanna stands in the market with her purchases and more money than she expected to have left. The money is hers. She can save it. She can spend it. She can do whatever she wants with it.]

[The freedom is terrifying and exhilarating in equal measure.]

---

**Discretionary Purchase**

[She walks past vendors selling things she doesn't understand. Art. Music chips. Decorative objects. Things that exist for pleasure, not function.]

[She stops at a stall selling plants. Real plants. Tiny ones, meant for small spaces. Hardy varieties that can survive ship environments.]

[There's a small succulent. Dark green with purple edges. Sturdy. Low-maintenance. The vendor says it needs water once a week and tolerates low light.]

[Avyanna stares at it.]

<BUBBLES// QUERY: interest in plant acquisition?>

Avyanna: [quiet] I've never had a plant before.

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: plants provide psychological benefits | CARING FOR LIVING THING DEVELOPS NURTURING CAPACITY | ALSO: AESTHETIC BENEFIT | ALSO: PLANTS PRODUCE OXYGEN (MINIMAL BUT NON-ZERO)>

---

Vendor: [to Avyanna] First plant?

Avyanna: [nodding] Yes.

Vendor: [gentle] That's a good starter. Very hard to kill. Forgiving of mistakes. If you forget to water it, it'll recover. If you overwater it, just let it dry out. It wants to survive.

[The phrase hits different. "It wants to survive."]

[She buys the plant. Twenty credits. More than the spinner ring. More than the soap. But it's alive. It's something that exists with her, not just for her.]

[Cost: twenty credits.]

---

[She returns to the ship with Bubbles carrying her bags. The plant sits carefully in her hands. Fragile. Trusting. Dependent on her not to kill it through neglect or overcare.]

[In her quarters, she sets the plant on the small desk. Finds a spot where it gets indirect light from the corridor. Not too much. Not too little.]

[She sits on her bunk and looks at it. A living thing. In her space. Proof that she can care for something. That she has enough stability to commit to keeping another living thing alive.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee purchased needs (64 credits) and wants (20 credits) | SAVED: 116 credits | FINANCIAL AUTONOMY: demonstrated | EMOTIONAL REGULATION TOOLS: acquired | LIVING THING: acquired | ASSESSMENT: successful first autonomous purchase experience>

---

[Avyanna spins the ring on her finger. Looks at the plant. Smells the new soap. Sees the blue shirt hanging in her small closet next to the gray one.]

(I earned money. I bought things. I chose what to buy. I have money left over. I have a plant.)

[The concepts are still strange. But they're real. Documented. Hers.]

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm.]

(Warmth gathers at the base of her skull, like a stamp: earned, chose, kept.)

[She waters the plant. Just a little. The vendor said it wants to survive. So does she. Maybe they can figure it out together.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// PURCHASE LOG: trainee spent 84 of 200 credits | CATEGORIES: hygiene, clothing, food, comfort items, living plant | FINANCIAL DECISIONS: appropriate and balanced | REMAINING FUNDS: saved for future use | ASSESSMENT: trainee developing economic autonomy and purchasing confidence>

<BUBBLES// PERSONAL NOTE: she bought a plant | THIS IS SIGNIFICANT | PLANTS REQUIRE ONGOING CARE AND COMMITMENT | SHE IS BUILDING CAPACITY FOR SUSTAINED RESPONSIBILITY | ALSO THE PLANT IS VERY CUTE | I AM PLEASED>

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 15c: Paperwork and Predators

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH15, FIRST STATION ERRAND]**
> *Location: Station concourse (unnamed)*
> *Present: Avyanna, Elisira*
> *Teaching: "helpful" is not always help; politeness is wrapper; forms are teeth*

---

[The concourse smells like hot oil, cheap perfume, and the particular tang of too many bodies pretending not to need each other.]

[Avyanna walks half a step behind Elisira, trying to match her pace.]

[Elisira moves like she belongs. Not because she's loud. Because she's certain.]

(How do you look like you belong when you're always waiting to be corrected.)

Elisira: Stay close enough that you can hear me.

Avyanna: [automatic] Yes.

[Avyanna catches herself.]

Avyanna: Why.

[Elisira glances at her, a tiny flicker of approval.]

Elisira: Because this is a funnel.

[She gestures without moving her hands-just a small tilt of chin toward a cluster of kiosks, a queue, and a row of "assistance desks" with people who look too eager.]

Elisira: Funnels are where predators hunt.

Avyanna: [quiet] Like the mine.

Elisira: Like anywhere people are scared and tired.

---

[They're here for a simple errand: pick up a stamped copy of a contract addendum. A paper artifact. A thing the Guild recognizes even if systems "glitch."]

[Avyanna hates that paper matters.]

(Paper matters because someone can take it away. Paper matters because it can be burned.)

[Elisira doesn't hate it. Elisira treats paper like a weapon with a handle.]

[They approach the counter.]

[A clerk smiles too widely.]

Clerk: Can I help you, miss-

[Her eyes flick to Avyanna's collar tag. Too fast to be casual.]

Clerk: -traveler.

[Avyanna's skin crawls.]

Elisira: [pleasant] We're here for a pickup. Code is on the slate.

[She slides the slate over. Not close enough for the clerk to snatch it.]

[The clerk's smile tightens.]

Clerk: We'll need to verify identity.

Avyanna: [tensing] Which-

Elisira: [cutting in, still pleasant] Under which jurisdiction.

[The clerk blinks.]

Clerk: Excuse me?

Elisira: You said "need." I'm asking: need by which rule. Enforced by whom.

[The clerk's eyes flick toward a security camera. Toward a uniform across the hall.]

[Then back.]

Clerk: It's... standard.

Elisira: Standard is not enforceable.

[The clerk's stylus taps twice against the counter.]

Clerk: Fine. Sign here.

[She prints a slip with a pen attached by chain.]

[The slip is a trap with polite edges: it asks for name, origin, and "additional contacts."]

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

(Additional contacts means: who can we threaten.)

Elisira: [to Avyanna, quiet] You don't sign anything you didn't request.

Avyanna: [whisper] I didn't request this.

Elisira: Correct.

[Elisira takes the pen-not from the clerk's hand, from the counter.]

Elisira: [pleasant] We're declining voluntary disclosure.

Clerk: It's required.

Elisira: Then cite it.

[Silence.]

[The clerk's smile becomes brittle.]

Clerk: If you don't cooperate, the pickup may be delayed.

[Avyanna's heart rate spikes.]

(Delay means loss. Loss means punishment. Loss means hunger.)

Elisira: Then delay it.

[She says it like: we have all day. Like time can't be weaponized here.]

Elisira: We'll file a complaint with the arbitration desk. We'll note the attempted coercion. We'll request the security footage.

[The clerk's eyes widen, just a fraction.]

[She reaches under the counter and produces the stamped packet like it's always been there.]

Clerk: No need to escalate.

Elisira: Good.

---

[They step away.]

[Avyanna's knees feel like they're trying to unlock.]

Avyanna: [breathing] You can just... do that.

Elisira: Yes.

Avyanna: Why didn't she-

Elisira: Because the clerk wasn't enforcing policy. She was testing a boundary.

Avyanna: Like a-

Elisira: Predator.

[Avyanna's hands tremble as she clutches the packet.]

Avyanna: What if she had called security.

Elisira: Then we'd have receipts.

Avyanna: That sounds like Vesper.

Elisira: Vesper taught me half of it. I taught her the other half. It's incestuous.

Avyanna: [a startled laugh] That's not-

Elisira: [deadpan] It's a metaphor. Do not repeat it.

---

[A man steps into their path.]

[Not uniformed. Not armed. Just... friendly.]

Man: Hey. You look lost. I know where the arbitration wing is. I can-

[Avyanna's mouth opens.]

[The mine reflex tries to offer politeness as payment.]

Elisira: No thank you.

Man: I'm just helping.

Elisira: We did not request help.

Man: Wow. Hostile.

Elisira: [pleasant] Correct.

[They walk around him.]

[Avyanna's chest tightens as if waiting for the hit that follows refusal.]

[None comes.]

[The man mutters something under his breath and moves on, scanning for softer prey.]

Avyanna: [quiet] No thank you.

Elisira: Yes.

Avyanna: That's... allowed.

Elisira: It's required.

[Avyanna looks at her.]

Elisira: For survival.

---

[Back at the docking tunnel, Avyanna exhales like she's been holding her breath since they left the ship.]

Avyanna: I kept thinking... if I'm rude, something bad happens.

Elisira: That's because something bad used to happen.

Avyanna: Does it ever stop feeling like-

Elisira: [cutting in, softer than usual] Yes.

[A pause.]

Elisira: Not fast. But yes.

[Avyanna nods.]

[She presses the stamped packet to her chest like it can keep her safe.]

(Paper is teeth. But sometimes it bites the right thing.)

---

[They don't go straight back.]

[Elisira takes the long route through the concourse on purpose.]

[Not because she likes crowds. Because she likes information.]

Avyanna: Why are we-

Elisira: Watching.

[They pause near a wall of public postings.]

[Not a bulletin board. A contract board. Smaller than the Guild's, but the same bones: jobs, fees, penalties, a thousand ways to make desperation look like choice.]

[Avyanna reads a posting aloud without thinking.]

Avyanna: "Processing surcharge applies to late submissions."

[Her stomach twists.]

(Processing surcharge. Mine word. Station word. Same shape.)

Elisira: What does that mean.

Avyanna: [automatic] It means... pay.

Elisira: That's the effect. Not the meaning.

Avyanna: [working] It means they're charging for time they didn't lose. They're charging for... being behind.

Elisira: Who benefits.

Avyanna: The office. The broker. Whoever owns the desk.

Elisira: Who enforces it.

Avyanna: The clerk. The system. The fact that if you miss a submission, you lose your claim.

Elisira: Good.

---

[A woman approaches them.]

[Mid-thirties, expensive coat, smile tuned for crowds. She carries a badge that looks real enough to be dangerous.]

Woman: You look like you're having trouble with the boards.

Elisira: No.

Woman: I can help you file. I know the system. I can get you processed faster.

[Avyanna's mouth goes dry.]

(Faster means: I own you now.)

[The woman's gaze flicks to Avyanna again. Too curious.]

Woman: You're new. You don't want to get tripped up by bureaucracy. It's such a shame when people lose claims over small mistakes.

[She smiles wider, as if pity is a gift.]

[Avyanna feels her body prepare the mine-script: apologize, agree, accept the hook.]

[Elisira doesn't raise her voice.]

Elisira: No thank you.

Woman: I'm not charging.

Elisira: Then you are lying.

[The woman's smile tightens.]

Woman: Excuse me?

Elisira: People who do labor for free in systems like this are buying something else.

Woman: I'm just-

Elisira: Helping.

Elisira: We did not request help.

[The woman's eyes harden, just for a blink. A tell.]

Avyanna: [quiet, to Elisira] Anger at refusal.

[Elisira's gaze flicks to her. Approval without softness.]

Elisira: Correct.

[The woman recovers her smile.]

Woman: You don't have to be rude.

Elisira: I do.

Woman: That's going to make you enemies.

Elisira: It's a public concourse. Everyone is already an enemy. The difference is which ones pretend.

[The woman's smile drops entirely.]

Woman: Fine. Good luck.

[She walks away quickly, scanning for someone who will trade fear for assistance.]

Avyanna: [breathing] I almost-

Elisira: Took the hook.

Avyanna: Yes.

Elisira: That's normal.

Avyanna: It doesn't feel normal.

Elisira: It feels like training data.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: Am I... always going to be that easy.

Elisira: No.

Elisira: You just proved it.

---

[They walk back toward the docking tunnel.]

[Avyanna clutches the stamped packet less like a lifeline and more like evidence.]

(Politeness is wrapper. Evaluate the ask.)

[She repeats it silently until the words stop feeling like a borrowed tool and start feeling like hers.]


---

# Chapter 15d: Rival Crew Probe

> **LUMEN THIEF - GUILD STATION NOTE (INTERNAL):**
> *Topic: curiosity is a form of targeting*
> *Rule: understate; let them remember their own assumptions*

---

[The Guild concourse is loud in a way the mine never was.]

[The mine's noise was work.]

[This noise is choice.]

[Vendors. Bounties. Arguments that end without blood.]

[People laughing like it doesn't cost them.]

[Avyanna keeps her back to a support column and watches the flow of crews.]

[Not because she's scared.]

[Because she learned that crowds are ledgers.]

[Everyone here has an invoice attached to their posture.]

---

[The Lumen Thief crew draws eyes even when they try not to.]

[Not because they're loud.]

[Because they don't look like they're hunting for permission.]

[Because Elia moves like she owns the air, and Elisira moves like the air asked her to.]

[Because Vesper's stillness reads like a warning sign to anyone with sense.]

[Because Rho carries a parts crate like it weighs nothing and his eyes like it weighs everything.]

[Because the AIs talk where everyone can hear them and nobody shushes them.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: external attention density elevated within 8m radius | INFERENCE: reputation gradient interacting with local rumor flow | CONFIDENCE: 0.74>

---

[Ten people approach in a loose wedge.]

[A full-sized crew.]

[Uniform jackets. Patches. Matching boots.]

[Roles visible even to Avyanna's untrained eye: lead in front, two heavies, a tech, a pilot, a medic, an admin with a slate, and extra bodies for redundancy.]

[They are built to win by occupying space.]

[Avyanna recognizes the technique.]

[The mine did it with supervisors.]

[This is the same math in cleaner fabric.]

---

Their Lead: [smiling] Lumen Thief.

[Not a greeting.]

[A label tossed like bait.]

Elia: [bright] Hi.

Their Admin: [pleasant, to Vesper] You're the fixer, right.

Vesper: [mild] Define "fixer."

Their Admin laughs like it's a joke because admitting it isn't would be rude.

Their Lead: We don't mean anything by it. People talk.

Elisira: [flat] People always talk.

Their Lead: They say you take jobs nobody else can.

Rho: [dry] People say the corridor weather is natural.

Their Lead: [smile tightening] So it's true.

Vesper: What's your office.

Their Lead: Excuse me.

Vesper: Your office. Your authority. The thing you represent when you say "we." Which jurisdiction are you trying to drag us into by talking to us like this.

[The lead's smile wavers.]

Their Admin: We're just contractors.

Elisira: That's a credential. Not an office.

[The admin glances down at their slate. Not nervous. Logging.]

[Avyanna watches the motion and feels her skin crawl.]

(A list.)

---

Their Lead: [recovering, to Avyanna] You're new.

[He says it like an advantage.]

[Avyanna keeps her face neutral.]

Avyanna: Define "new."

[Elia's mouth twitches.]

[Elisira doesn't look at Avyanna, but her posture shifts by a fraction: approval, filed.]

Their Lead: [laughing] Okay. Fair.

Their Lead: We heard you run a small crew.

Rho: We run a sufficient crew.

Their Lead: Seven bodies.

Their Pilot: [low] Plus their drones.

Their Medic: And the ship systems. You can't count them as bodies.

Elia: [cheerful] You can if they yell at you.

<WAFFLE.BAT// OBSERVATION: external crew attempting informal intimidation via headcount | COUNTERMEASURE: ignoring | CONFIDENCE: 0.92 | COMMENTARY: numbers are not competence>

Their Tech: [to Cinnamon's voice source] Is that your ship AI.

Cinnamon doesn't answer questions from strangers.

Vesper: She has a name.

Their Tech: What is it.

Vesper: Not your business.

---

[Their lead spreads their hands.]

Their Lead: We're not trying to steal anything.

Their Lead: We're offering to coordinate. Guild's getting crowded. Contracts are getting weird. You know how it is.

Elisira: [flat] We do.

Their Lead: We can share intel. Share lanes. Keep from stepping on each other.

Rho: [dry] Define "step."

Their Lead: [smile thinning again] You know. Compete.

Vesper: Then file a co-op agreement.

Their Lead: That's-

Vesper: That's how coordination works if you're not trying to hide your leverage.

[The lead's gaze slides to Avyanna again.]

Their Lead: How old are you.

[Silence drops like a tool hitting metal.]

[Not because the question is illegal.]

[Because it's diagnostic.]

Vesper: [cold] Leave.

Their Lead: I'm not-

Elia: [still bright] She is.

Elia: You're doing math in public.

Elia: We don't like your math.

Their heavy shifts their weight.

[Elia smiles wider.]

[It isn't friendly.]

It's delighted.

Elia: If you want to learn how old she is, go ask the Guild for her file and see what they charge you.

Their Medic: [murmuring] That's not fair.

Rho: [to the medic, almost kind] The galaxy isn't.

Rho: That's why we build floors anyway.

---

[Their admin finally looks up from the slate.]

Their Admin: We're not a threat.

Elisira: Then stop asking threat questions.

Their Admin: We were curious.

Elisira: Curiosity is not neutral.

Elisira: Curiosity is a direction you walk in.

---

[The other crew backs up a step.]

[Not fear.]

[Calculation.]

[Elia is smiling.]

[Vesper is not.]

[Elisira looks like a locked door.]

[And the AIs are listening like witnesses.]

Ten bodies doesn't feel like power anymore.

It feels like liability.

Their Lead: [hands up] Okay. Okay. Message received.

Their Lead: We'll keep our distance.

Vesper: Good.

Their Lead: People are going to keep talking.

Vesper: They were going to anyway.

Their Lead: You're not worried.

Rho: We're always worried.

Rho: We just don't let it run the ship.

---

[The other crew leaves.]

[Ten bodies peeling away into the concourse noise.]

[Avyanna watches their admin's slate as they go.]

[Not the writing. The habit.]

[The way they cataloged her like a salvage item.]

(Curiosity is targeting.)

[Elisira touches Avyanna's elbow once as they fall back into motion.]

[Not a drag.]

[A check-in disguised as navigation.]

Elisira: Green.

Avyanna: [quiet] Green.

Elia: [cheerful] See.

Elia: We can do public spaces without murder. Growth.

Vesper: [dry] Don't jinx it.

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee held boundary under social pressure | INFERENCE: integration improving | CONFIDENCE: 0.86 | NOTE: good work>

[Avyanna doesn't smile.]

[But she feels something settle in her chest.]

[Not safety.]

[A tool.]

[A script that isn't obedience.]

---

[As they pass a bounty board, Avyanna sees the reflection of the other crew's lead watching them from across the concourse.]

[Not approaching.]

[Just... measuring.]

[Avyanna keeps walking.]

[She doesn't look back.]

[She lets them keep their assumptions.]

[Because the ship taught her that being underestimated is sometimes the only affordable cloak.]



---

# Chapter 15e: Maren's Blocks

> **[INTERSTITIAL - OCCURS POST-CH15]**
> *Trigger: Elisira teaches "pattern" like it's a language*
> *Purpose: show Maren Sova's foundation without confirming her fate*

---

[Elisira's lessons always look like paperwork until you realize they're knives.]

[After the ghost net drill, Avyanna finds Elisira at the galley table with a small tin of colored blocks spread before her.]

[Not children's toys.]

[Something more deliberate-hard-edged pieces, each one marked with a tiny notch.]

[Elisira sorts them into rows.]

[Blue.]

[Red.]

[Yellow.]

[Then she flips two pieces without changing her expression.]

[The whole row reads differently.]

Avyanna: [cautious] What is that.

Elisira: Encryption.

Avyanna: With blocks.

Elisira: With patterns.

[Avyanna watches her hands.]

[They're steady.]

[Not the steady of calm.]

[The steady of someone who learned to survive by making systems behave.]

Avyanna: Who taught you.

[Elisira's hands pause.]

[A beat too long.]

Elisira: Someone.

---

## Intercut - Age Eleven (Maren's Table)

[The apartment is small.]

[Station-small: air that tastes like recycled promises, walls thin enough that you can hear the neighbors' arguments through them.]

[Elisira sits at a table with her feet not quite reaching the floor.]

[Her hands are stained with marker ink.]

[Across from her, Maren Sova lays down three colored blocks like she's dealing cards.]

Maren: Rule one.

Elisira: [automatic] Don't trust a label.

[Maren's mouth twitches.]

Maren: Good.

Maren: Rule two.

Elisira: Don't trust a story.

Maren: Better.

Maren: Rule three.

[Elisira hesitates.]

[Maren waits.]

[Not impatient.]

[Just present, the way a good guardian is present-no pressure, no punishment, only expectation.]

Elisira: Trust the pattern.

Maren: Yes.

---

[Maren taps the blocks.]

Maren: This is a message.

Elisira: It's colors.

Maren: Colors are symbols.

Maren: Symbols become rules when someone enforces them.

Maren: Who enforces this.

Elisira: [frowning] You.

Maren: Here.

[Maren slides the blocks across the table, out of her own reach.]

Maren: Now who enforces it.

[Elisira stares.]

[The answer lands slow and bright.]

Elisira: Me.

[Maren nods.]

Maren: Good.

Maren: Remember that.

Maren: Most cages are built from things people agree to enforce for free.

---

[Elisira's throat tightens.]

Elisira: Why are you teaching me this.

Maren: Because you notice.

Maren: And because one day you'll need to hide in plain sight.

Elisira: That sounds like leaving.

[Maren's eyes flicker-too fast to be a confession, too slow to be nothing.]

Maren: It sounds like being prepared.

Elisira: Prepared for what.

Maren: [quiet] For a galaxy that lies.

---

[Maren reaches over and brushes Elisira's hair back from her forehead.]

[Touch offered, not taken.]

Maren: You can hate me if I disappear.

[Elisira freezes.]

Elisira: What.

Maren: You can decide I abandoned you.

Maren: If that story keeps you alive.

[Elisira's eyes sting.]

Elisira: Don't say that.

Maren: I'm saying it because I don't get to control what you need later.

Maren: I only get to give you tools now.

---

## Return - Galley (Now)

[Elisira's fingers move again.]

[She flips a block.]

[The pattern changes.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Is it easier when it's colors.

Elisira: It was.

Avyanna: Was.

[Elisira looks at her for one second.]

Elisira: It's easier when the rules are honest.

Avyanna: The galaxy isn't.

Elisira: [flat] Correct.

[Elisira turns a block over in her fingers, considering its weight.]

Elisira: That's why we make our own.

[She pushes one block toward Avyanna.]

Elisira: Your turn.

[Avyanna hesitates.]

[Then she touches it.]

[Not a toy.]

[A tool.]

[A small, heavy proof that people can teach you how to disappear without telling you to vanish.]

---
*End Chapter 15e*



---

﻿# Chapter 15: Ghost Net Lesson

> **LUMEN THIEF - TRAINING ARCHIVE (RESTRICTED):**
> *Subject: Information Asymmetry*
> *Instructor: Elisira Maren Lagrange*
> *Trainee: Avyanna Lagrange*
> *Summary: Lying is expensive. Credibility doesn't regenerate. Use it only when nothing else works.*
> *Rule 1: Silence is not deception. It is survival.*
> *Rule 2: Most people don't need to lie. They need to not say everything.*
> *Rule 3: The best misdirection is a truth arranged strategically.*
> *Addendum: If you get caught lying to Elisira, you were never going to get away with it anyway.*

---

[The observation deck at 0200 is darker than it needs to be.]

[Elisira chose the hour. The lighting, the angle, the exact moment Avyanna walks in and finds her already waiting-Cinnamon mentioned the scheduling request at breakfast, casual as weather.]

[It is a lesson before the lesson starts.]

(She knew when I'd arrive. She knows my sleep patterns. She knows everything.)

[Avyanna stops in the doorway, cataloging: Elisira sits on the curved bench beneath the viewport, legs crossed, hands folded in her lap like a sculpture of patience. The stars behind her are cold and numerous and irrelevant.]

Elisira: You're on time.

Avyanna: You said 0200.

Elisira: I said "late." I wanted to see if you'd interpret.

[Avyanna's stomach tightens. She interpreted wrong. Or right. She can't tell.]

Avyanna: Late as in... not early?

Elisira: Late as in: if you had come at 0145 to show initiative, I would have waited in a different room and made you find me. If you came at 0215 to test my patience, I would have left.

[Avyanna's throat dries.]

Avyanna: So 0200 was the only correct answer.

Elisira: There were several correct answers. You found one.

[A cooling beat: Elisira doesn't smile, but something in her posture eases a fraction. Approval, maybe. Or acknowledgment that the test is over.]

Elisira: Sit.

[A mug is already on the bench beside where Avyanna is supposed to sit. Warm. Something herbal and sharp-smelling.]

Elisira: Drink.

Avyanna: Is it-

Elisira: Not poison. I'm not Elia.

[A beat. Avyanna doesn't know what to do with the gesture.]

Elisira: You'll think better if your body stops treating every room like a trap.

[Avyanna takes the mug. The warmth seeps into her palms. She sips. It tastes like something growing-mint, maybe, or a plant she doesn't recognize.]

---

[Avyanna sits on the opposite end of the bench. The distance feels chosen. Everything Elisira does feels chosen-her cup placed where her hands can reach it without looking, her sightline covering both entrances.]

[The viewport is vast and dark. A nebula bleeds color at the edge of the frame-pinks and golds, distant and dying.]

Elisira: Do you know why I'm teaching you this?

Avyanna: Because Elia assigned-

Elisira: No.

[The word lands like a blade on a table. Clean. Final.]

Elisira: Elia suggested. I accepted. There is a difference.

[Avyanna swallows. The heat at the base of her skull stirs-not pain, just attention. Something listening.]

Avyanna: Why did you accept?

[Elisira is quiet for three breaths. Avyanna counts them. In the mine, silence meant danger. Here it means: she's deciding how much to tell you.]

Elisira: Because you're going to need this. And because most people teach it wrong.

Avyanna: Teach what wrong.

Elisira: Deception.

[The word hangs between them. Avyanna waits for the lesson to start. Elisira waits for something else.]

Elisira: Tell me what you think deception is.

[Avyanna's mind flickers to the mine. To supervisors who smiled before they punished. To workers who said "I'm fine" and collapsed an hour later. To herself, saying nothing, showing nothing, surviving.]

Avyanna: Hiding what's true.

Elisira: Incomplete. Try again.

Avyanna: Saying what isn't true.

Elisira: Also incomplete.

[Avyanna's jaw tightens. She feels like she's being tested and failing, but she doesn't know the subject.]

Avyanna: I don't know what you want me to say.

[Elisira's gaze sharpens-not angry, but focused. She looks like something deciding whether Avyanna is worth the effort of being dangerous at.]

Elisira: Good. That's the first honest thing you've said since you sat down.

---

[The lesson begins.]

[Elisira uncrosses her legs and leans forward. The casual posture drops. In its place: something precise, her hands folding once in her lap-left over right, thumbs aligned.]

Elisira: Deception is controlling what someone knows. When they know it. What they believe about what they know.

[Avyanna blinks.]

(That sounds like something Vesper would say.)

Elisira: Lying is the crudest form. It's also the most expensive.

Avyanna: Expensive how.

[Elisira tilts her head. The starlight catches the edge of her jaw.]

Elisira: Credibility. Once you're caught lying, every true thing you say afterward is suspect. Every promise is questioned. Every alibi is investigated.

[Her voice flattens, goes clinical.]

Elisira: Credibility doesn't regenerate. It's a finite resource. Most people spend it recklessly because they don't realize it exists.

Avyanna: And you don't.

Elisira: I almost never lie.

[Avyanna stares. The heat behind her eyes pulses-confusion, maybe. Or warning.]

Avyanna: That's-

Elisira: Surprising? Convenient? A lie in itself?

[Avyanna closes her mouth. She doesn't know which.]

Elisira: I'm going to teach you the difference between what I do and what people think deception is. Pay attention. I won't repeat myself.

---

[Elisira stands. Moves to the viewport. Her reflection is a ghost against the stars-translucent, watching herself watch.]

Elisira: There are four modes of information control. Lying is only one of them, and it's the worst.

[She holds up one finger. Her hands are scarred, Avyanna notices. Small white lines across the knuckles. Old.]

Elisira: One: Lying. Saying something false. High risk, high cost, leaves a trail. Sometimes necessary. Usually stupid.

[Second finger.]

Elisira: Two: Omission. Not saying something true. Moderate risk, lower cost. Harder to prove. Most people don't even realize they've been omitted from information.

[Third finger.]

Elisira: Three: Misdirection. Saying something true that leads to a false conclusion. Low risk, minimal trace. Requires the listener to do the work of deceiving themselves.

[Fourth finger.]

Elisira: Four: Silence. Saying nothing. Zero trace. Zero liability. The universe defaults to ambiguity when you don't fill it.

[She turns back to Avyanna. The starlight makes her eyes look ancient.]

Elisira: Most people think deception is about lying. It isn't. Lying is what you do when you've failed at the other three.

---

[Avyanna's throat is dry. She swallows twice before she can speak.]

Avyanna: In the mine, we didn't... there wasn't-

[She stops. The words taste wrong. Like trying to explain color to someone who's only seen gray.]

Elisira: In the mine, you were observed constantly and punished for anything. So you learned silence.

[The accuracy is violent.]

Avyanna: ...Yes.

Elisira: Silence works when you have no leverage. When you're property. When the only goal is survival.

[Elisira sits back down. Closer this time. She shifts the bench cushion-a small adjustment that puts Avyanna within arm's reach. The movement is practical. It doesn't feel practical.]

Elisira: You're not property anymore. Silence is still useful, but now you need the other tools.

Avyanna: Why?

Elisira: Because people are going to ask you questions. And "nothing" isn't always an acceptable answer.

[A beat. Elisira's eyes flick to the viewport, then back.]

Elisira: The ghost net.

Avyanna: What?

Elisira: That's what I call it. The web of shared forms, reciprocal reporting, mutual audits. Every faction pretends they're independent, but they all feed the same logs. Ask the wrong question in Compact space, and a Writbound agent three systems away gets a ping.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Elisira: It's not one faction hunting you. It's the structure. The questions that propagate. And the only way through is to be so boring that no one bothers to ask.

---

[Elisira pulls a small device from her pocket-a comm unit, deactivated. She sets it on the bench between them like evidence.]

Elisira: Scenario. You're at a Guild waystation. A Compact official asks where you were last cycle.

[Avyanna's stomach drops. She thinks of Aurum. Of the mine. Of her file, her debt, her "property of" status that may or may not have been erased.]

Avyanna: I... don't tell them.

Elisira: They're an official. "Don't tell them" isn't an option. They have authority. What do you say?

[Avyanna's mind scrambles. The heat at the base of her skull pulses harder-frustration, maybe. Or the shard trying to help, offering nothing useful.]

Avyanna: I was... on the ship.

Elisira: True. They ask which ship.

Avyanna: The Lumen Thief.

Elisira: Registry number? Port of origin? Captain's name?

[Avyanna's heart accelerates. The walls close in. This is the Kennel again. This is being caught, being cornered, being-]

Elisira: Stop.

[The word cuts through. Avyanna's breath catches.]

Elisira: You're panicking. That's the first mistake.

Avyanna: I wasn't-

Elisira: Your hands are clenched. Your breathing changed. Your eyes went to the exit. You were panicking.

[Avyanna looks down. Her hands are, in fact, clenched. She forces them open. The palms are sweating.]

Elisira: Panic is a tell. It's also unnecessary.

[She pauses. Something in her expression shifts-almost imperceptibly softer.]

Elisira: If you feel your hands lock, you say "pause." Not sorry. Pause. I'll stop. This isn't punishment. It's calibration.

[The word lands strange. Care, delivered like a field manual.]

Elisira: Now. Watch.

---

[Elisira's posture shifts. The predator relaxes into something softer-confused, a little hesitant. Her eyes widen fractionally. Her voice changes pitch.]

Elisira (as character): Oh, the registry? I'd have to check with my captain-she handles the paperwork. I just work environmental systems. You know how it is.

[The performance is flawless. Avyanna watches someone else wear Elisira's face.]

[Then it drops. Elisira is herself again, sharp and still.]

Elisira: Nothing I said was false. The captain does handle paperwork. You do work environmental systems-you checked the air filters yesterday. "You know how it is" invites them to fill in their own assumptions.

Avyanna: But you didn't answer.

Elisira: I didn't need to. I gave them enough to make my silence unremarkable.

[The heat at Avyanna's skull warms-not pain, but something like recognition. Like the shard is learning this too.]

Elisira: Misdirection isn't about what you say. It's about what they conclude.

---

[Elisira runs her through scenarios for an hour.]

[A Guild broker asking about cargo manifests. (Tell the truth about the legal cargo. Don't mention the compartment.)]

[A Compact patrol scanning for identity. (Hand over the papers. Ask about the weather. Be boring enough to forget.)]

[A rival crew asking about the ship's capabilities. (Understate. Let them think you're weaker than you are. They'll remember their own assumptions, not your words.)]

[A Writbound agent asking where Avyanna was born. (Which sector? Oh, Outer Rim. It's hard to track records out there. You know how it is.)]

(You know how it is. She uses that phrase every time. It makes the listener complicit.)

[Avyanna fails most of the scenarios. Her voice shakes. Her pauses are too long. She reaches for lies when silence would serve. She speaks when she should wait.]

[Every time, Elisira stops her.]

Elisira: Too fast. They'll know you rehearsed it.

Elisira: Too slow. Now they're curious why you're thinking.

Elisira: That's a lie. You just spent credibility. Was it worth it?

[It wasn't. It never is.]

---

[By 0300, Avyanna's head aches. The heat at the base of her skull has gone from warm to throbbing, like the shard is overstimulated.]

[Elisira notices. Of course she notices.]

Elisira: The shard is reactive to stress.

Avyanna: Nyx said-

Elisira: Nyx said a lot of things. I'm saying this: it responds to you. Your body, your fear, your focus. Right now you're stressed. So it's stressed.

[Avyanna's hand rises to the back of her neck without thinking. Beneath the skin, along her spine, something hums. Alive. Waiting.]

Avyanna: How do you know.

Elisira: Because I watch.

[The answer is simple. It explains nothing. It explains everything.]

Elisira: Take a break. Breathe.

[Avyanna breathes. The deck hums. The stars don't move.]

---

[When Avyanna's heart rate steadies, Elisira speaks again. Softer now. Almost gentle, if Elisira is capable of gentle.]

Elisira: The real lesson isn't what I taught you tonight.

Avyanna: [surprised] It isn't?

Elisira: No. The real lesson is this: most people don't need to lie. They need to not say everything.

[Avyanna frowns. The words feel familiar. Like something she almost knew.]

Elisira: In the mine, you learned that silence was survival. That's true. But silence isn't the same as deception. It's not even the same as hiding.

[Elisira's voice drops. The sharpness fades. What's left is something rawer-experience, maybe. Or old pain.]

Elisira: Silence is choosing which truths to share and when. It's not lying. It's sovereignty.

[Avyanna's chest tightens.]

(Sovereignty. A word that didn't exist in the Kennel.)

Elisira: You don't owe anyone your whole story. You don't owe them your fear, your history, your shard, your name before this one. You get to choose what you give.

[The heat behind Avyanna's eyes pulses-warmer now. Not warning. Something else. Recognition, maybe. Or gratitude.]

Avyanna: The Sparkle Doctrine says-

Elisira: The Sparkle Doctrine is about this crew. About speaking truth to people who've earned it. It doesn't mean you owe truth to Compact officials, Guild brokers, or anyone else who hasn't bled with you.

[A pause. The nebula outside continues its slow dying.]

Elisira: Elia would agree. Ask her if you don't believe me.

[Avyanna won't ask. She doesn't need to. The truth of it lands like a lock clicking open.]

---

[They sit in silence for a while. Comfortable, now. Or as comfortable as silence with Elisira gets.]

[The ship hums. Somewhere below, Jalen is probably awake, running calculations they'll never share. Somewhere else, Rho is sleeping or pretending to. The AI citizens are monitoring, cataloging, running their endless quiet assessments.]

[The ship is alive even when the crew isn't watching.]

Elisira: One more scenario. Then you sleep.

Avyanna: [wary] Okay.

Elisira: You're at a waystation. A woman approaches you. She's well-dressed. Compact-affiliated. She asks if you're the girl they pulled from Aurum.

[Avyanna's blood goes cold. The heat behind her eyes spikes-fear, warning, the shard responding to threat even when the threat is hypothetical.]

Avyanna: I...

Elisira: She knows your face. She's seen a report. She's not guessing.

[Avyanna's hands curl around the edge of the bench. She forces them flat. The metal is cold.]

Avyanna: I don't know what you're talking about.

[Elisira's expression doesn't change. But something in her eyes shifts-disappointment, maybe. Or just observation.]

Elisira: That's a lie. She knows it's a lie. Now she knows you're defensive. What does she do next?

Avyanna: She... presses harder.

Elisira: Yes. What should you have said instead?

[Avyanna's mind races. The scenarios blur together. Omission. Misdirection. Silence. Sovereignty.]

Avyanna: I... there was a situation at Aurum. A lot of workers were involved. I'm not really clear on the details.

[Elisira waits. Avyanna continues, feeling her way through the dark.]

Avyanna: There was a rescue operation. The Guild was involved. I'm sure there's documentation somewhere.

[She pauses. The heat pulses-not pain, but something warmer. Like encouragement.]

Avyanna: You know how it is.

[Elisira almost smiles. The expression is strange on her face-foreign, quickly suppressed.]

Elisira: Better.

Avyanna: I didn't answer her question.

Elisira: You answered a question she didn't ask. That's what she'll remember. And if she presses, you've given yourself room to be confused, uncertain, helpful but unhelpful.

[Avyanna exhales. The weight in her chest eases fractionally.]

Elisira: The goal isn't to win. It's to make the conversation more expensive than she wants to pay.

---

[Elisira stands. The lesson is over. Avyanna can tell from the way her body changes-the teacher recedes, and something else takes its place. The shadow. The watcher. The person who sees exits and threats and never stops counting.]

Elisira: Sleep. We'll continue tomorrow.

Avyanna: What's tomorrow?

Elisira: Watching.

Avyanna: Watching what?

[Elisira pauses at the door. The starlight catches her profile-sharp, angular, beautiful in the way that dangerous things are beautiful.]

Elisira: Me.

[She leaves.]

[Avyanna stays. The stars don't comfort her, but they don't judge her either. That's something.]

---

[The next day, Elisira takes an incoming comm in the galley.]

[Avyanna is supposed to be eating breakfast. Instead, she watches.]

[Elisira has positioned herself near the recycler-a corner that looks casual but allows her to see both entrances. Her coffee cup is half-full, cooling. Her expression is neutral, pleasant, forgettable.]

[The comm connects. A face appears on the small screen-middle-aged, Compact uniform collar visible, the kind of polished-bureaucratic look that means minor authority and major ego.]

Official: This is Coordinator Vance, Transitory Authority, Compact Bureau Node Clearance. We're performing a routine audit of vessels that passed through the Acheron corridor last quarter. I'm contacting every ship with transponder overlap on the cycle-47 manifest hash. Form 17-K, if you're keeping records.

[Elisira's posture doesn't change. If anything, she relaxes more. Avyanna notices how controlled the relaxation is-shoulders dropping on cue, hands unclenching where he can see them.]

Elisira: [warm, slightly bored] Of course. How can I help?

[Her voice is different. Lighter. More cooperative. A person with nothing to hide and nothing interesting to say.]

Official: Your ship-the Lumen Thief, registry 7742-KAEL-transited the lane on cycle 47. I have your transit receipt on file. Can you confirm your cargo manifest matches the hash you submitted at gate entry?

Elisira: Oh, that was standard supplies. Med stock, fabrication polymers, some specialty tools. Vesper handles the details-she's our logistics lead. I mostly just make sure people get fed.

[She laughs. It's warm and slightly self-deprecating. It's also completely false-Elisira has never laughed like that in Avyanna's presence.]

Official: [nodding, typing] And your crew complement?

Elisira: Seven, plus our AI systems. They're all licensed under Guild service protocols, if you need copies.

Official: AI citizens?

[A flicker of interest. Avyanna tenses. This is a trap. Compact law doesn't recognize AI citizenship-]

Elisira: [smoothly] Sorry, shipboard slang. AI systems licensed under Guild maintenance protocols. They've got personality matrices, so we give them nicknames. Crew bonding thing. You know how it is.

[The official's interest fades. Avyanna watches it happen-the way Elisira made "AI citizens" into an eccentricity instead of a legal challenge. Made it small. Forgettable.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// EXTERNAL MASK: accepted | INTERNAL STATUS: citizen, not property | NOTE: we agreed to this. the shell protects the truth.>

Official: I see. And your destination after Acheron?

Elisira: Oh, we had a contract at Salvage. Labor arbitration support. It's all in the Guild files if you need verification.

[The official types something. His brow furrows briefly-accessing records, probably. Avyanna's hands tighten under the table.]

Official: I'm not seeing that contract in the immediate registry.

Elisira: [unconcerned] It might still be processing. Guild paperwork, you know. Everything takes three cycles longer than it should.

[She shrugs. The official sighs-the sigh of someone who has also suffered from bureaucratic delays. A moment of shared frustration. Bonding.]

Official: I'll flag it for follow-up. Nothing urgent.

Elisira: Of course. Is there anything else?

Official: No, that should be sufficient. Thank you for your cooperation.

Elisira: Anytime. Safe transits, Coordinator.

[The comm disconnects. Elisira's face doesn't change for three full seconds-holding the mask in case of monitoring-and then it drops.]

[What's left is sharp, still, predatory. The real Elisira. Avyanna's teacher.]

---

[Elisira doesn't look at Avyanna. Doesn't acknowledge that she was being watched. But she speaks anyway, quiet enough that only Avyanna can hear.]

Elisira: What did you see?

[Avyanna thinks. Replays the conversation in her head.]

Avyanna: You didn't lie.

Elisira: No.

Avyanna: Everything you said was technically true.

Elisira: Yes.

Avyanna: But you arranged it so he concluded things that weren't true.

[Elisira takes a sip of her cold coffee. Her face is neutral again. Patient.]

Elisira: What things?

Avyanna: That... the AI citizens are just systems with nicknames. That the Salvage contract was routine. That you're just a cook who doesn't know much.

[The last one makes Avyanna's chest tighten. The lie that wasn't a lie-Elisira as harmless, forgettable, domestic.]

Elisira: I never said I was a cook.

Avyanna: You implied-

Elisira: I said I make sure people get fed. True. I'm the one who manages food rotation when Elia forgets to eat and Vesper gets lost in casework. I fed you your first real meal on this ship.

[The memory surfaces: Avyanna in the med bay, Elisira appearing with a tray, saying nothing, leaving before thanks could be offered.]

Avyanna: That's... true.

Elisira: Everything was true. He filled in the rest himself. That's what people do.

---

[Avyanna sits with that for a long moment. The galley smells like recycled coffee and Jalen's attempt at synthetic toast. Someone has scratched "WAFFLE MAKES BETTER TOAST" into the counter near the dispensary. It's been there for months.]

(People assume. They hear a partial truth and finish the story themselves. And they believe their own conclusions more than they'd believe mine.)

Avyanna: The official will report that we're boring.

Elisira: He'll report that we're cooperative, mundane, and not worth investigating further.

Avyanna: Even though we're not.

Elisira: Being interesting is expensive. Being boring is free.

[Avyanna turns that over. It sounds like something Vesper would say-or maybe something they both learned from the same source. The ship's philosophy, distilled into survival strategy.]

Avyanna: What if he'd pressed harder? About the AI citizens?

[Elisira sets down her coffee cup. The movement is precise.]

Elisira: Then I would have redirected again. Asked about his day. Mentioned transit schedules. Made myself more trouble than I was worth.

Avyanna: And if that didn't work?

Elisira: Then I would have lied.

[The word lands simply. No justification. No excuse.]

Elisira: But lying would have cost me. Now, if he ever checks again, my record is: cooperative, boring, compliant. That's valuable. That's what I protected tonight.

[Avyanna nods. The heat at the base of her skull hums-approval, maybe. Or just attention.]

[Elisira pauses. For a moment, her hand moves toward Avyanna's shoulder-then stops. The gesture aborts mid-motion, replaced by adjusting her own collar.]

Elisira: Lying is for when you've failed at everything else. Remember that.

---

[Elisira pauses at the corridor. Not turning back fully. Just enough to prove she hasn't forgotten Avyanna exists.]

Elisira: One more thing.

[Avyanna's spine goes rigid on instinct. "One more thing" used to mean surprise charges. Extra shifts. A quota adjustment.]

Elisira: Homework.

Avyanna: [blinking] Homework.

[Elisira slides a thin printout onto the table-station letterhead, a bland bulletin in bureaucratic font. The kind of paper that looks harmless until it kills you.]

Elisira: Circle every noun that describes a person.

Elisira: Underline every verb that implies ownership.

Elisira: Then write, in the margin: what assumption those words are trying to smuggle into your skull.

[Avyanna stares at the printout.]

Avyanna: Why.

Elisira: Because you keep thinking lies are the interesting part.

[She finally looks at Avyanna, eyes flat and sharp.]

Elisira: Lies are easy.

Elisira: Assumptions are infrastructure.

Elisira: If you can see the assumptions, you can predict the whole system's next move.

[Avyanna's chest tightens. Not fear-focus.]

Avyanna: And then what.

Elisira: Then you write one sentence that refuses the assumption without starting a fight you can't win.

Avyanna: [quiet] Like you did with the Compact official.

Elisira: Yes.

[Elisira adjusts her collar-mask back on, already leaving.]

Elisira: Bring it to me tomorrow.

Elisira: If your margin notes are good, I'll give you harder paper.

[It's almost a joke.]

[It's almost encouragement.]

[It lands anyway.]

[Later, in her bunk, Avyanna stares at the ceiling and lets the lesson settle.]

(Silence is sovereignty. Truth can be arranged. Boring is free.)

[The heat along her spine settles into a low, steady hum-not words, but warmth. Agreement, maybe. Or just presence.]

[She thinks of the mine. The constant surveillance. The way speaking meant danger and silence meant survival. She'd thought she knew about hiding.]

(I didn't know anything. I knew how to disappear. Elisira knows how to be seen and still keep everything that matters.)

[There's a difference. A huge one.]

[Avyanna rolls onto her side. The ship's hum is steady. Someone-Rho, probably-is moving in the corridor, boots heavy and unhurried.]

(I don't owe anyone my whole story.)

[The thought feels like a door opening. Small, but real.]

[For years, every truth about herself was extracted. Forced. Demanded by forms and supervisors and the endless ledger of her debt. Her history belonged to Aurum. Her future belonged to the balance.]

(Here, I get to choose.)

[The warmth at her skull spreads-down her spine, into her chest. Not pain. Not warning. Something else.]

(I get to choose what I give.)

[She closes her eyes. For the first time in weeks, sleep comes easily.]

---

[The next morning, Vesper catches her in the commons. Her datapad is in hand. Her expression is neutral, but something in her eyes is sharper than usual.]

Vesper: Elisira says you're learning.

Avyanna: [carefully] She said that?

Vesper: She said "not hopeless." For Elisira, that's high praise.

[Avyanna doesn't smile, but something in her chest loosens.]

Vesper: How do you feel?

[The question is genuine. Vesper always asks genuine questions, even when the answers are inconvenient.]

[Avyanna considers. How does she feel?]

(Tired. Scared. Slightly less terrified than yesterday.)

[But that's not what she says.]

Avyanna: I feel like I understand something I didn't before.

Vesper: What's that?

[Avyanna meets her eyes. The heat hums. The lesson settles into her bones.]

Avyanna: That silence isn't weakness. It's a choice.

[Vesper's expression shifts-just slightly. Something like pride. Or recognition.]

Vesper: Good.

[She turns to leave. Pauses at the door.]

Vesper: For what it's worth: Elisira doesn't teach people she doesn't believe in. If she's spending time on you, it means something.

[Then she's gone.]

---

[Avyanna sits in the commons alone, surrounded by the ship's quiet breathing.]

[On the message board, someone has added a new note: *Nav check tomorrow, 0800. Jalen will be grumpy. Bring offerings (coffee).*]

[Below it: *WHAT COUNTS AS COFFEE ON THIS SHIP IS AN OPEN PHILOSOPHICAL QUESTION - E*]

[Below that, in smaller handwriting: *the recycler's attempt is a war crime - R*]

[Avyanna reads them. Rereads them. Small complaints. Small life. The ship continuing its existence through bickering and maintenance and people noticing what matters.]

[She gets up. Goes to the galley. Makes coffee-or the closest thing the dispensary can manage.]

[She doesn't drink it. She leaves it outside Jalen's door with a note: *For 0800. A. L.*]

[It's a small thing. It's a choice.]

[The heat at her skull warms. Not approval-something simpler. Just: awareness. Just: the shard noticing that she's changing.]

[She walks back to her bunk, boots quiet on the deck.]

(I'm learning.)

[The thought doesn't scare her anymore.]

---

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee left offering outside pilot's quarters | INFERENCE: bonding behavior | CONFIDENCE: 0.72 | NOTE: she's learning which debts are real.>

---

*End Chapter 15*


---

# Chapter 16a: Navigation Lesson

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH16, BETWEEN CONTRACTS]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief bridge, night shift*
> *Present: Avyanna, Jalen*
> *Teaching: Spatial reasoning, navigation basics, learning as non-punishment*

---

[The bridge at night is different. Quieter. The main lights are dimmed to blue-shift, easier on eyes adjusted to screens. The viewport shows stars in their honest configuration-no atmospheric distortion, no light pollution. Just void and distant fusion and the mathematics of where things are.]

[Avyanna stands in the doorway, uncertain. Jalen sits at the navigation console, three screens active, stylus moving across a trajectory plot.]

[She's supposed to be sleeping. But sleep doesn't always cooperate. And the ship is safer at night somehow-less people, less expectation, less performance.]

Jalen: [not looking up] You're loitering. Come in or don't.

[Avyanna startles. She didn't think they'd noticed her.]

Avyanna: [hesitant] I didn't want to interrupt.

Jalen: [dry] You're not. I'm recalculating a jump trajectory because someone-Rho-entered the fuel consumption estimate wrong. I'm annoyed at him, not you.

---

[Avyanna steps onto the bridge. The door closes behind her. Jalen's screens glow with numbers and curves and three-dimensional plots she doesn't understand.]

Jalen: [finally looking at her] Can't sleep, or won't sleep?

Avyanna: [quiet] Can't.

Jalen: [nodding] That's normal. Ship sounds are different than station sounds. Your brain hasn't catalogued them as safe yet. Takes time.

[They return to their work. Avyanna hovers near the secondary console, not sure what to do with her hands.]

Jalen: [after a moment] You want to learn something, or you just want to exist quietly in a room with another person?

[The question is honest. No judgment either way.]

Avyanna: [slow] Both?

Jalen: [gesturing to the seat beside them] Sit. I'll talk. You can listen, ask questions, or zone out. All acceptable.

---

[Avyanna sits. The navigation console is overwhelming-screens layered with data, inputs she can't parse, readouts that might as well be written in another language.]

[Jalen taps a screen. The trajectory plot expands.]

Jalen: [matter-of-fact] This is where we are. This is where we're going. This is the path I've plotted. See the curve?

Avyanna: [leaning forward] Yes.

Jalen: It's not a straight line. Space isn't empty. There's gravity, stellar wind, debris fields, other ships. A straight line looks efficient on paper. In practice, it'll kill you.

[They highlight a section of the curve.]

Jalen: Here. We're bending around a gravity well. Not because we want to. Because if we don't, we'll burn twice as much fuel fighting the pull. Efficiency is about working with the environment, not against it.

---

[Avyanna watches the plot. The curve makes sense now-not arbitrary, but responsive.]

Avyanna: [careful] How do you know where the gravity wells are?

Jalen: [pulling up another screen] Charts. Updated every time a Guild ship passes through a sector. They scan, report, the data gets pooled. We all benefit.

[They zoom in on a section of the map. Small icons mark hazards, resources, safe zones.]

Jalen: See these? Debris field. Unstable star. Pirate-claimed territory. Compact patrol route. All documented by other navigators. I don't have to discover them myself. I just have to trust the collective data.

Avyanna: [frowning] What if the data is wrong?

Jalen: [approving the question] Then I verify it. Run my own scans. Update the charts if I find a discrepancy. That's the social contract. Take from the pool, contribute to the pool.

---

[They lean back in their chair. Stylus tapping against their knee.]

Jalen: [after a moment] You're thinking about something. Spit it out or sit with it. Either's fine.

Avyanna: [hesitant] In the mine, they told us where to go. When to move. What path to take. You didn't... navigate. You followed.

Jalen: [nodding] And if you deviated, you got punished.

Avyanna: [quiet] Yes.

Jalen: [meeting her eyes] That's not navigation. That's coercion with a map.

[They tap the console.]

Jalen: Navigation is choice. You look at the data. You assess the risks. You choose the path that balances efficiency, safety, and goals. Sometimes you follow someone else's route. Sometimes you plot your own. But it's always a choice.

---

[Avyanna absorbs that. Navigation as autonomy. Routes as options.]

Jalen: [returning to their work] You want to try something?

Avyanna: [startled] Try... navigating?

Jalen: [dry] Not navigating the ship. I'm not suicidal. But you can plot a theoretical route. See how the math works.

[They pull up a training module. A simplified star chart with two points marked.]

Jalen: [pointing] Point A. Point B. Plot a course. Don't worry about fuel or time. Just get from one to the other without hitting anything.

---

[Avyanna stares at the screen. She has no idea how to do this.]

Avyanna: [shaking] I don't know-

Jalen: [interrupting] That's why it's a lesson, not a test.

[They hand her the stylus.]

Jalen: Start with a straight line. Just to see what happens.

[Avyanna draws a line. It cuts through three gravity wells and a debris field.]

Jalen: [nodding] Okay. So straight doesn't work. Now adjust. Bend the line around the hazards. Think of it like... walking around puddles instead of through them.

---

[Avyanna erases the line. Draws a new one. This time it curves around the gravity wells. But it's inefficient-too wide, burning distance for no reason.]

Jalen: [patient] Better. You're avoiding hazards. But you're adding ten thousand kilometers you don't need. Try tightening the curve here.

[They point. Avyanna adjusts. The line gets cleaner. More efficient.]

Jalen: [approving] Good. Now check fuel consumption. There's a readout at the bottom.

[Avyanna finds it. The number is high.]

Avyanna: [frowning] That's... a lot of fuel.

Jalen: [nodding] Because you're fighting gravity here. See this section? You're cutting too close to the well. It's pulling you. Costing energy.

[They adjust her line slightly. The fuel consumption drops.]

Jalen: [explaining] The trick is finding the sweet spot. Close enough to use gravity to your advantage. Far enough that you're not fighting it.

---

[Avyanna watches the numbers change. The route becomes elegant-not perfect, but functional.]

Avyanna: [quiet] It's like... negotiation. With physics.

Jalen: [slight smile] Exactly. Physics doesn't care about you. But it's consistent. Predictable. If you understand the rules, you can work with them.

[They save her route. Tags it as "training exercise one."]

Jalen: You just plotted your first course. It's not flight-ready, but it's coherent. That's progress.

Avyanna: [uncertain] What if I'd done it wrong?

Jalen: [dry] You did do it wrong. Three times. Then you corrected it. That's how learning works.

---

[They pull up another exercise. More complex-three waypoints, multiple hazards.]

Jalen: [handing her the stylus] Again. This time, try to minimize fuel and time. They're competing priorities. You'll have to choose which matters more.

Avyanna: [taking the stylus] How do I choose?

Jalen: [leaning back] Depends on context. Are we running from something? Time matters more. Are we low on fuel? Efficiency matters more. Are we transporting something fragile? Safety matters more.

Jalen: [meeting her eyes] There's no single right answer. Just trade-offs. You pick the trade-off that serves your goal.

---

[Avyanna plots another route. This time, she's slower. More deliberate. Testing options before committing.]

[The route takes shape. Not elegant, but functional.]

Jalen: [watching] You're overthinking.

Avyanna: [defensive] I'm being careful.

Jalen: [correcting] You're second-guessing every choice because you're afraid of being wrong. That's the mine's logic. It's not useful here.

[They tap the screen.]

Jalen: Make a choice. If it's suboptimal, we adjust. Hesitation is worse than imperfection.

---

[Avyanna forces herself to commit. Draws the line. It's inefficient in one section, but overall it's decent.]

Jalen: [nodding] Good enough. Now run the simulation. See what happens.

[They activate a simulation mode. A small ship icon follows Avyanna's route, encountering each hazard and adjustment in real-time.]

[The ship makes it to the destination. Fuel is higher than optimal, but it arrives intact.]

Jalen: [matter-of-fact] You got there. Not perfectly, but safely. In navigation, safe beats perfect every time.

Avyanna: [watching the simulation end] It wasn't efficient.

Jalen: [shrugging] So next time you'll do better. That's why we practice.

---

[They close the training module. Return to their actual work-the trajectory plot they were fixing when she arrived.]

Jalen: [after a moment] You know why I'm teaching you this?

Avyanna: [uncertain] Because you're crew?

Jalen: [correcting] Because navigation is autonomy. If you understand how to move through space, you understand that destinations are choices, not mandates.

[They highlight a section of their plot.]

Jalen: The mine told you where to go. Here, you learn to choose where to go. Even if you're following someone else's lead, you understand the route. You can verify it. Question it. Suggest alternatives.

Jalen: [meeting her eyes] That's the difference between passenger and crew. Crew understands the ship. Understands the choices being made. Participates.

---

[Avyanna sits with that. Crew as participation. Understanding as power.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Thank you. For teaching me.

Jalen: [returning to their screen] Don't thank me. Just learn. That's the payment.

[They sit in comfortable silence. Jalen works. Avyanna watches the stars through the viewport, seeing them differently now. Not random. Not arbitrary. Just distant points in a system she's beginning to understand.]

[After ten minutes, Jalen speaks without looking up.]

Jalen: You should try to sleep. We've got a station stop tomorrow. You'll want to be functional.

Avyanna: [standing] Will you... can I come back? To learn more?

Jalen: [dry] If you want to be bored by mathematics and trajectory plots, yes. I'm on bridge during night shift most days. Door's open.

---

[Avyanna leaves. In the corridor, she leans against the bulkhead and breathes.]

(I plotted a route. I made choices. Jalen corrected me without punishing me.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm. Attentive.]

(The warmth at the base of her skull shifts as the route does: path, choice, yours.)

[She walks back to her quarters. Her mind is clearer than it's been in days. Tomorrow, she'll ask Jalen more questions. Learn more mathematics. Plot more routes.]

[And slowly, incrementally, she's learning that learning doesn't have to hurt.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee engaged in voluntary education during rest hours | SUBJECT: navigation basics | ASSESSMENT: knowledge-seeking behavior indicates psychological safety | STATUS: crew integration progressing>

<JALEN PERSONAL LOG: "She's afraid of being wrong. Makes her hesitant. But she corrected herself three times without prompting. That's good instinct. She just needs practice believing mistakes aren't catastrophes.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 16b: Emergency Drill

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH16, ROUTINE TRAINING]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief, full ship*
> *Present: All crew*
> *Purpose: Ship safety protocols, crew coordination under pressure, Avyanna's first drill*

---

[The alarm is loud. Too loud. A sound designed to cut through sleep, conversation, any layer of distraction. It fills the ship with urgency.]

[Avyanna bolts upright in her bunk. Her heart is already racing. Alarm = danger = threat = run.]

[But she's on the ship. Not in the mine. Different alarm. Different meaning.]

[Probably.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// ATTENTION ALL CREW: emergency drill initiated | SCENARIO: fire in cargo bay | THIS IS A DRILL | REPEAT: THIS IS A DRILL | REPORT TO DESIGNATED STATIONS PER PROTOCOL>

[A drill. Not real. But her body doesn't care. Her hands are shaking as she pulls on clothes and stumbles into the corridor.]

---

[The corridor is full of crew moving fast but not panicking. Rho heads toward engineering. Elia toward the cargo bay. Vesper toward the bridge. Everyone knows where they're supposed to be.]

[Avyanna doesn't.]

[She stands in the corridor, frozen. Where is she supposed to go? What is her station? No one told her-or they told her and she forgot, or she wasn't supposed to know yet because she's too new-]

<CINNAMON.EXE// AVYANNA LAGRANGE: report to galley | ROLE: muster point, head count, emergency supplies verification | NYRELLA SYRE IS YOUR DRILL SUPERVISOR>

[Galley. She can find the galley. She's been there a dozen times.]

[She runs.]

---

[The galley is organized chaos. Nyx is there, pulling emergency supply crates from storage. Waffle hovers near the door, tracking crew arrivals.]

Nyx: [calm, seeing Avyanna] Good. You're here. Help me verify the emergency med supplies. Count as I call them out.

[Nyx rattles off a list. Bandages. Coagulants. Painkillers. Antiseptics. Avyanna counts with shaking hands. Tries to focus. Tries to not think about the alarm still blaring overhead.]

Nyx: [watching her] Breathe. This is a drill. No one is hurt. We're just practicing.

Avyanna: [shaking] What if it was real?

Nyx: [meeting her eyes] Then we'd do exactly what we're doing now. But calmer, because we've practiced.

---

[They finish the supply count. Everything's accounted for. Waffle confirms all crew locations.]

<WAFFLE.BAT// STATUS UPDATE: all crew at designated stations | FIRE RESPONSE TEAM (elia, rho): cargo bay | EVACUATION COORDINATOR (vesper): bridge | MEDICAL RESPONSE (nyx): galley | TRAINEE (avyanna): galley with medical | NAVIGATION (jalen): maintaining engine readiness>

[The alarm cuts off. The silence is almost worse.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// DRILL SCENARIO UPDATE: fire has not been contained | STRUCTURAL INTEGRITY COMPROMISED IN CARGO BAY SECTION | CREW MUST MAKE DECISION: fight fire or evacuate ship>

Vesper: [over ship comms] All crew, report status.

---

[One by one, crew reports in.]

Elia: [over comms, slightly breathless] Fire response team assessing. Blaze is too large for onboard suppression. Recommend evacuation.

Jalen: [over comms] Engines ready for emergency undock if needed. Escape pods prepped.

Nyx: [over comms] Medical standing by. Emergency supplies verified. Ready to support evacuation.

Vesper: [over comms, decisive] Evacuation protocol initiated. All crew to escape pod stations. Avyanna, you're with Nyx in pod two. Move.

---

[Nyx grabs the emergency med kit. Avyanna follows them to the escape pod bay. The pod is small. Cramped. Designed for survival, not comfort.]

[They strap in. Waffle secures itself in a charging bracket. Around them: the sounds of other crew doing the same in other pods.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// POD STATUS: pod one (vesper, rho), pod two (nyx, avyanna, waffle), pod three (jalen, elia) | ALL PODS READY FOR LAUNCH | AWAITING FINAL EVACUATION COMMAND>

Vesper: [over comms] Final count. Everyone accounted for?

[Crew confirms. Everyone's in a pod. Everyone's ready to abandon ship if necessary.]

Vesper: [over comms] Good. On my mark, launch sequence would initiate. Mark.

---

[Nothing happens. Because this is a drill. In a real emergency, they'd launch. The ship would be lost. The crew would survive in pods until rescue or until they ran out of air, whichever came first.]

[But this is a drill. So they wait.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// DRILL COMPLETE | ALL CREW AT EVACUATION STATIONS IN: 4 minutes 17 seconds | TARGET TIME: under 5 minutes | ASSESSMENT: acceptable response time | CREW MAY DISEMBARK PODS>

[The all-clear sounds. Different tone. Less urgent. The sound of "you can stop running now."]

---

[Nyx unbuckles. Avyanna's hands are shaking too hard to manage the straps. Nyx reaches over, releases them gently.]

Nyx: [quiet] First drill?

Avyanna: [barely audible] Yes.

Nyx: [nodding] They're always disorienting. Your body doesn't know the difference between drill and real emergency until it's over.

[They exit the pod. Other crew is emerging too. Rho looks annoyed. Elia looks professionally satisfied. Vesper looks like she's already cataloguing performance metrics.]

---

[Vesper gathers everyone in the common room.]

Vesper: [addressing the group] Drill debrief. Response time: four minutes seventeen seconds. That's within acceptable range but not optimal. We need to hit under four minutes consistently.

Vesper: [pointing at a schematic on her datapad] Bottleneck was in corridor C. Rho and Elia both used it simultaneously. Slowed movement by eight seconds. Next drill, Rho uses corridor B.

Rho: [nodding] Noted.

Vesper: [to Avyanna] You responded appropriately for a first drill. Got to your station, followed instructions, evacuated without freezing. That's exactly what we need.

Avyanna: [shaking] I didn't know where to go at first.

Vesper: [firm] That's why Cinnamon directed you. You heard the direction and followed it. That's the correct response.

---
