Elia: [to the group] Fire response assessment. If that had been real, we'd have lost the cargo bay and possibly the adjacent sections. Onboard suppression couldn't handle a blaze that size. Evacuation was correct call.

Jalen: [adding] Engines were ready in ninety seconds. If we'd needed emergency undock, we could have done it safely.

Nyx: [reporting] Medical supplies verified. Emergency kit is fully stocked. No issues.

Vesper: [satisfied] Good. Next drill is scheduled for two weeks from now. Scenario will be different. We'll iterate until response time is optimal and everyone knows their role without hesitation.

---

[The crew disperses. Avyanna sits on the couch, still shaking. Rho sits beside her.]

Rho: [gentle] First drill is always the worst. You don't know what's happening. You don't know if it's real. Your body just screams RUN and your brain has to catch up.

Avyanna: [quiet] I thought... for a second, I thought the ship was actually on fire.

Rho: [nodding] Yeah. That's the point. Drills are supposed to feel real. That's how we know we'll respond appropriately when it is real.

Avyanna: [looking at him] Has it ever been real?

Rho: [somber] Twice. Once we had a coolant leak. Once we had a power surge that started small fires in two sections. Both times, we evacuated. Both times, everyone survived because we'd drilled the procedures until they were reflex.

---

[Elia joins them, sitting on the armrest.]

Elia: [to Avyanna] You did well. Didn't freeze. Didn't panic past the point of function. Made it to your station. That's all we need from you right now.

Avyanna: [frustrated] I felt useless. Everyone else had important jobs. I just... counted bandages.

Elia: [flat] Counting bandages is important. If Nyx doesn't know what supplies are available, they can't treat injuries effectively. You verified critical information. That's not useless.

Nyx: [from across the room] Also, you were calm enough to count accurately. Under stress, people miscount. You didn't. That's reliability.

---

[Avyanna absorbs that. Her contribution mattered. Even if it felt small.]

Vesper: [addressing Avyanna specifically] Next drill, you'll have a different role. We rotate assignments so everyone knows multiple positions. Eventually, you'll be able to fill any role in an emergency. But for now, you learn one piece at a time.

Avyanna: [nodding] Understood.

Vesper: [standing] Rest of the day is light duty. Everyone's adrenaline is going to crash in the next hour. Take it easy. We resume normal operations tomorrow.

---

[Crew disperses again. Avyanna returns to her quarters. Lies on her bunk. Her heart is still pounding. The alarm is still echoing in her head.]

[But she didn't freeze. She got to her station. She did her job. She evacuated to the pod. She survived the drill.]

(This is how the crew survives real emergencies. By drilling until panic becomes procedure. By practicing until everyone knows exactly what to do when chaos happens.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm.]

(A warm pulse at the base of her skull-drill, practice, ready-like her body is learning a new language.)

[She closes her eyes. Tries to slow her heartbeat. Tomorrow, there will be normal operations. No alarms. No drills. Just ship life. Boring, safe ship life.]

[She's never been so grateful for boring.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// DRILL ASSESSMENT: crew response time adequate but requires improvement | SPECIFIC NOTES: avyanna (trainee) performed appropriately for first drill | RECOMMENDATION: additional drill cycles to improve familiarity and reduce response time | NEXT DRILL: scheduled 14 days>

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "First drill is always brutal. She was shaking for an hour after. But she didn't freeze. She got to her station. She did what we needed. That's courage. That's what matters.">

<VESPER PERSONAL LOG: "Four minutes seventeen seconds. Acceptable for a crew with a new trainee. Next drill we'll hit four minutes flat. After that, three forty-five. We iterate until perfection, because perfection is what keeps everyone alive when the emergency is real.">

<ELIA PERSONAL LOG: "She asked if she was useless. I told her medical supply verification is critical. Because it is. She needs to know that every role matters. That there are no small jobs in an emergency. Everything is life or death. Everything counts.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 16c: Maintenance Pairing Day

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH16b, FIRST MONTHLY MAINTENANCE RITUAL]**
> *Location: Ship-wide (pair rotations)*
> *Present: Avyanna + rotating crew; AI citizens coordinate*
> *Teaching: maintenance is care; tools are shared; no one is exempt*

---

[Maintenance day starts with a board posted in the atrium.]

[Not a command. A schedule.]

[Pairs. Tasks. Time blocks.]

[Avyanna reads it twice before she believes her name belongs there.]

> **AVYANNA + RHO** - *Filters / seals / coolant checks (galley-adjacent)*
>
> **AVYANNA + BUBBLES** - *Drone nest inventory (label sanity)*
>
> **AVYANNA + JALEN** - *Bridge conduit inspection (non-invasive)*

(They're trusting me with the ship.)

[Cinnamon's text appears on the terminal beside the board.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// REMINDER: maintenance is preventative, not punitive | NOTE: you cannot "fail" maintenance if you report what you see>

[Avyanna's stomach tightens.]

(In the mine, maintenance meant blame.)

---

[Rho meets her at the galley hatch with a tool bag and the expression of someone approaching a nuisance he loves anyway.]

Rho: You ever change a filter.

Avyanna: [honest] No.

Rho: Good. You won't do it wrong on purpose then.

[He hands her gloves.]

[Not orders. Equipment.]

Rho: Rule one: tell me what you see. Not what you think you're supposed to see.

Avyanna: [quiet] That sounds like Vesper.

Rho: Everybody on this ship is a little bit Vesper.

[He squints.] 

Rho: Except Elia. Elia's a whole different disease.

[Avyanna snorts.]

[They pop a panel. The smell of old air hits Avyanna's face.]

[Rho points at the filter assembly.]

Rho: This is where "out of stock" likes to hide.

Avyanna: [frowning] Out of stock is-

Rho: A claim.

[He taps it with the back of a screwdriver.]

Rho: Not a verdict.

[Avyanna nods, cataloging it as a tool.]

[They work. Slowly.]

[Rho narrates the steps without making her feel stupid.]

[When Avyanna's hand shakes, she pretends it's from torque.]

[Rho doesn't call her out.]

[He just steadies the panel with his own hand so she can use both hands without fear of dropping anything.]

---

[Second rotation: drone nest inventory.]

[Bubbles is already there, surrounded by neat rows of parts that look like jewelry if you don't know they can cut a man in half.]

Bubbles: Hello.

Avyanna: [more steady now] Hi.

[Bubbles projects an inventory list.]

Bubbles: We will count.

Avyanna: [dry] Counting as rebellion.

<BUBBLES// AFFIRMATION: yes>

[They move through bins.]

[Avyanna reads labels out loud.]

Avyanna: "Swarm anchor pins."

Avyanna: "Hinge washers."

Avyanna: "Do not feed Elia."

[She stops.]

Avyanna: Is that a real category.

Bubbles: It is an aspirational category.

[Avyanna laughs.]

[The laugh feels like trespassing.]

[Bubbles doesn't punish it.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee laughter | INFERENCE: nervous-system downshift | CONFIDENCE: 0.79>

[They find a bin with a label crossed out and replaced in marker.]

> **"EXTRA"** -> **"SPARE"**

Avyanna: [soft] Someone changed it.

Bubbles: I did.

Avyanna: Why.

Bubbles: "Extra" implies waste.

Bubbles: "Spare" implies safety.

[Avyanna swallows.]

(Words matter. Always.)

---

[Third rotation: bridge conduit inspection.]

[Jalen meets her in the corridor outside the bridge with a flashlight and a look that says: don't touch anything, and also: you're allowed to be here.]

Jalen: You're not crawling in.

Avyanna: [relieved] Good.

Jalen: You're observing.

Avyanna: That I can do.

[They open an access panel. Cables. Heat. A faint vibration that feels like the ship's pulse.]

Jalen: See that discoloration.

Avyanna: [leaning in] Yes.

Jalen: What is it.

[Avyanna pauses.]

Avyanna: I don't know.

[Jalen nods, as if "I don't know" is a valid piece of evidence.]

Jalen: Good.

Jalen: Now tell me what you can say without guessing.

Avyanna: The sheath is worn. The color's different near the joint. It looks... heated.

Jalen: Good.

Jalen: That's a claim with observations behind it.

Avyanna: [startled] That's Vesper language.

Jalen: Vesper stole it from physics. Physics stole it from reality.

---

[By the time the last rotation ends, Avyanna's hands are smudged with grease.]

[Her hair smells faintly like metal.]

[She's tired in a way that doesn't feel like punishment.]

(I worked. And no one took anything from me for it.)

[Back in the atrium, the board updates.]

> **MAINTENANCE DAY - COMPLETE**
>
> *Notes: 3 issues logged. 0 blame assigned. 1 coffee spill archived for historical purposes.*

<WAFFLE.BAT// COMMENTARY: coffee spill was heroic>

<CINNAMON.EXE// CORRECTION: coffee spill was avoidable>

<BUBBLES// ADDENDUM: coffee spill was forgiven>

[Avyanna reads that and feels, for a moment, like she lives in a place where forgiveness is a default setting.]

[She doesn't trust it yet.]

[But she's learning how to stand on it anyway.]

---

[The last entry on the board isn't a task.]

> **MAINTENANCE DAY DEBRIEF - OPTIONAL**

[Optional.]

[Avyanna's eyes snag on the word like it's a hook.]

(Optional means: you can choose. Choice means: you can be blamed.)

[She goes anyway.]

[The debrief is in the atrium, where people can hear and therefore things stay honest.]

[Elia lounges on a couch like meetings are allergic to her.]

[Elisira stands with her slate, already having organized everything into categories.]

[Rho smells like coolant and coffee.]

[Nyx is there too, hands stained with something that might be soil or ink.]

[Bubbles hovers. Cinnamon's terminal glows. Waffle's icon blinks like it's trying to behave.]

Elisira: Issues logged.

[She reads without drama.]

Elisira: Galley filter assembly runs hot at joint. Bridge conduit sheath worn. Drone nest bin mislabeled.

Elia: [perking up] What.

Bubbles: The bin labeled "do not feed Elia."

Elia: That's an important label.

Elisira: It is not operationally necessary.

Elia: [affronted] It is culturally necessary.

<CINNAMON.EXE// NOTE: both claims have merit>

[Avyanna's mouth twitches. It's becoming a habit.]

Nyx: Did anyone get injured.

Rho: No.

Nyx: Good. That means maintenance did its job.

Avyanna: [quiet, before she can stop herself] In the mine, maintenance only happened after someone died.

[Silence.]

[Not the kind that punishes. The kind that listens.]

Nyx: Yes.

Nyx: Here, we do it before.

Nyx: That is the difference between extraction and care.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Elisira: Avyanna.

[Avyanna's spine goes rigid.]

Elisira: What did you learn.

[Not "what did you do wrong."]

[What did you learn.]

Avyanna: [working] That reporting a problem isn't... confessing guilt.

Elisira: Correct.

Avyanna: That tools aren't personal property.

[Bubbles' fans shift, pleased.]

Avyanna: That "extra" versus "spare" matters.

Elia: [delighted] Yes. Vocabulary war.

Vesper isn't here.

[And yet Avyanna hears her anyway: words are leverage.]

Rho: Also learned the bridge conduit was cooked.

Jalen: [over comm, dry] It is not cooked. It is lightly toasted.

Elia: Toasted is still edible. Therefore safe.

Jalen: [flat] That is not how ships work.

<WAFFLE.BAT// COMMENTARY: toasted ship is funny concept>

<CINNAMON.EXE// CORRECTION: toasted ship is unacceptable>

---

[Elisira stamps the slate with a final note.]

Elisira: No blame assigned.

[Avyanna's chest tightens.]

Avyanna: That's... written down too.

Elisira: Yes.

Elisira: Because we mean it.

[Avyanna nods once, hard.]

(Say what you mean. Mean what you say.)

[The phrase is becoming a rail inside her.]

[Elia stands, stretches, and claps Avyanna on the shoulder-not hard, not claiming. Just present.]

Elia: You did good, Avy.

Avyanna: [quiet] That's not a metric.

Elia: [grinning] It is my metric.

[Avyanna can't help it.]

[She laughs.]


---

# Chapter 16d: Convoy Transit Comparison

> **LUMEN THIEF - TRANSIT NOTE (INTERNAL):**
> *Topic: myth is procedure other people can't afford*
> *Reminder: calm is a capability*

---

[They fall in with a convoy because the corridor is shifting and sometimes "normal" is safer than "alone."]

[Two ships ahead. One behind.]

[A fourth off their port side, pacing them like it wants to be seen as equal.]

[Its lights are brighter than necessary.]

[Its comms are louder than necessary.]

[Its transponder says insured. The kind of insured that makes people assume the universe will apologize if it hurts you.]

---

[The Lumen Thief bridge is in working-quiet.]

[Jalen in the pilot cradle. Elisira standing behind them with a slate. Rho in the doorway with coffee that smells like stubbornness. Vesper at the rail with a datapad full of jurisdiction traps. Elia pretending to be bored near weapons control.]

[Avyanna at the last open station, strapped in, pretending her ribs aren't humming with the corridor's wrongness.]

(Convoy means witnesses. Witnesses mean lists.)

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: convoy formation recognized | NOTE: increased traffic reduces ambiguity but increases attention | INFERENCE: risk trade | CONFIDENCE: 0.78>

<BUBBLES// REMINDER: do not interpret convoy proximity as safety>

Elia: [cheerful] Thank you, Bubbles. Very comforting.

Bubbles: [over speaker, earnest] You are welcome.

---

[The insured ship pings them.]

[A hail request slides onto the console with the casual entitlement of something used to being answered.]

Jalen: [flat] Decline.

Vesper: [without looking up] Let them talk at us for a second. It will cost less than them inventing a story about why we refused.

[Jalen makes a sound that is not agreement and taps accept anyway.]

---

Other Captain: [voice smooth, broadcast-quality] Independent vessel Lumen Thief, this is convoy lead for insured hauler group. We see you're running the same lane. Confirm you can maintain pace and formation.

[There's a pause where the captain expects deference.]

[Avyanna knows the shape of that pause. The mine was built out of it.]

Vesper: [mild] Define "confirm."

Other Captain: [a beat] Acknowledge that you won't become a hazard.

Vesper: We are not a hazard.

Other Captain: [tiny laugh] Everyone says that.

Elisira: Everyone lies.

---

Other Captain: We've got ten onboard. Standard redundancy. We can provide assistance if your systems lag.

[Ten onboard.]

[Avyanna pictures it: a medic that isn't also a negotiator; a pilot that isn't also a lawyer; a tech that isn't also a fighter.]

[Ten people to do what this ship does with fewer bodies and more voices.]

(Unfair.)

Rho: [to no one in particular] We don't need help.

Other Captain: [polite] It's not charity. It's protocol.

Vesper: Protocol is enforcement with manners.

Other Captain: ...Excuse me?

Vesper: Nothing. Continue your checklists.

---

[The corridor shifts.]

[Not dramatic. Not a scream.]

[Just a pressure change that makes Avyanna's teeth ache and her hands want to clench.]

(Mine collapse.)

Elia: [bright] Ooh. That's a seam.

Jalen: [quiet] Drift left two degrees. Hold. Hold.

[The Lumen Thief slides like it enjoys obeying someone who knows why they're asking.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: shear gradient increasing | ACTION: reduce nonessential power draw 9% | INFERENCE: lower thermal noise signature | CONFIDENCE: 0.82>

<WAFFLE.BAT// COMMENTARY: corridor thinks it's funny>

[Avyanna swallows.]

[She tracks Vesper's hands. The way they stay on the rail. The way her posture stays open even when everything in the universe is trying to make her shrink.]

(This is what control looks like. Not yelling. Not threats. Just choices held steady.)

---

Other Captain: [voice tightening] Convoy, confirm stability. Readouts just spiked.

[Over comm, the other ship's bridge goes from smooth to crowded.]

Other Crew Voice: (pilot) Lane's drifting, Captain.

Other Crew Voice: (tech) Guidance is lagging.

Other Crew Voice: (medic) Strap in, strap in, strap in-

Other Crew Voice: (admin) Insurance guidance says reduce speed twelve percent.

Other Crew Voice: (someone else) That's going to break formation.

Other Captain: Hold formation. Maintain pace. We're insured for this corridor rating.

[Avyanna feels her stomach twist.]

(Insured doesn't mean safe. Insured means someone decided what your death is worth.)

---

[The convoy ship beside them shudders.]

[Its running lights flicker once.]

[Avyanna hears a thin, ugly sound through the hull: metal complaining.]

Jalen: [calm] They're going to overcorrect.

Elisira: [already moving on her slate] Their captain is forcing pride into physics.

Elia: [still cheerful, but the cheer has teeth] Do we rescue them or let them learn.

Vesper: We do not let ten people die to teach a lesson.

Rho: [grim] We also don't let them drag us into their panic.

---

[Avyanna watches Vesper's profile.]

[The way she holds both truths without flinching.]

(Floors, not thrones. Floors still have edges.)

Vesper: [into comm, precise] Convoy lead. Your readouts are lying to you.

Other Captain: [sharp] Say again?

Vesper: Your insurer's guidance is a generic template. This corridor is shifting faster than their update cycle.

Other Captain: And you know that how?

[The question is bait.]

[Prove yourself for free. Show your hand. Earn their belief.]

[Avyanna feels Elia watching her. Waiting to see what she does with a pause shaped like hierarchy.]

Avyanna: [quiet, into her mic] Because you just said "reduce speed twelve percent" like a prayer.

[Silence.]

Vesper's head turns slightly. Not surprise. Acknowledgment.

Avyanna: That's not a measurement. It's a slogan.

Other Captain: [too controlled] Watch your tone, kid.

Elisira: [flat] Define "kid."

---

Vesper: [still calm] If you want to stay in formation, you need to drift left by two degrees and stop fighting the seam.

Other Captain: That's not in our- our procedures.

Vesper: Your procedures were written for paperwork, not weather.

Other Captain: [breathing audible now] We are insured-

Rho: [cuts in, voice like a clamp] Insurance doesn't fly your ship.

---

[The convoy lead hesitates.]

[Avyanna can hear ten people's fear stacking behind one person's pride.]

Other Crew Voice: (pilot, urgent) Captain, if we don't adjust we're going to shear.

Other Captain: ...Drift left two degrees. Hold.

[The other ship slides.]

[Not as clean as the Lumen Thief.]

[But it slides.]

[The metal-complaint sound eases by a fraction.]

---

Other Captain: [after a long breath] Acknowledged.

Other Captain: ...Thank you.

Vesper: [immediate] You're welcome.

[Avyanna feels something in her chest loosen.]

(No punishment. No invoice. Just a fix, and then you move on.)

---

[The convoy keeps moving.]

[The insured ship doesn't try to pace them anymore.]

[It drops half a length back, like it suddenly remembers distance is etiquette.]

[Before they cut comms, the other captain speaks again.]

Other Captain: Lumen Thief-

[Not bait this time.]

[Not posturing.]

Other Captain: Are you always like this.

Elia: [bright] Like what.

Other Captain: Like you already know what the corridor is going to do.

Jalen: [flat] No.

Jalen: We just listen faster.

Elisira: And we don't worship templates.

Vesper: And we ask "who enforces it" before we trust it.

Rho: And we don't confuse insured with immortal.

[A pause.]

Other Captain: ...Copy.

[The channel closes.]

---

[For a while, nobody on the bridge speaks.]

[Avyanna watches the stars smear and un-smear.]

[Watches the convoy hold itself together on a borrowed lesson.]

(They'll tell people.)

(Not "we survived." They'll tell people about the ship that corrected an insured captain mid-seam without raising its voice.)

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: external comms silence persists | INFERENCE: rumor retention likelihood high | CONFIDENCE: 0.77>

Elia: [soft, satisfied] See.

Avyanna: What.

Elia: Myths are just other people's fear, organized.

Elia: The trick is making them afraid of the right thing.

[Vesper doesn't look away from her screen.]

Vesper: The right thing is the system.

[Avyanna nods.]

[Her hands unclench.]

[Outside, the corridor keeps pretending it's weather.]



---

# Chapter 16e: Senna's Math

> **[INTERSTITIAL - OCCURS POST-CH16]**
> *Trigger: numbers as a weapon against contracts*
> *Purpose: Senna's version of "show me the math"*

---

[Rho and Cinnamon taught her compound interest like it was a knife safety lesson.]

[Not scary.]

[Necessary.]

[Avyanna walked away from the galley with her head full of percentages that felt like teeth.]

[Now she lies awake, staring at the ceiling, repeating numbers like prayers she doesn't believe in.]

Twenty-two percent annual.

Monthly compounding.

Hidden fees that aren't hidden if you know where to look.

(If they won't show you the math, they're lying.)

[The sentence is Rho's.]

[But it scrapes at something older in her memory.]

---

## Intercut - AE Site K-9 (Senna's Ledger)

[Senna doesn't have a datapad.]

[Datapads belong to supervisors.]

[Senna has a strip of packing paper stolen from the supply bay and a chunk of charcoal.] 

[Avyanna sits beside her in the shadow of a support column, knees tucked to her chest.]

Avyanna: Why are we doing this.

Senna: Because you're curious.

Avyanna: Curiosity gets people hurt.

Senna: Curiosity gets people out.

[Senna draws a line, then another, making a crude table.]

Senna: Here is what they tell you.

[She writes:]

QUOTA: 100

PAY: 0

[Avyanna snorts quietly.]

Avyanna: That's not math.

Senna: It is.

Senna: It's just a lie-shaped one.

[Senna writes below it:]

PENALTY: -5

PENALTY: -5

PENALTY: -5

[Avyanna watches the list grow.]

Avyanna: That's what they do.

Senna: Yes.

Senna: Now watch the trick.

[Senna circles the penalties.]

Senna: They call it "compliance."

Senna: They call it "training."

Senna: But it's interest.

[Avyanna frowns.]

Avyanna: We don't get paid.

Senna: You get charged.

Senna: Debt doesn't care if you ever saw money.

[Senna draws an arrow.]

Senna: If you owe five today, you owe seven tomorrow.

Avyanna: Why.

Senna: Because the number is a weapon.

Senna: The weapon works best when you don't understand it.

---

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: I can't do that math.

Senna: You can.

[Senna taps the paper.]

Senna: Shortcut.

Senna: If they refuse to show you how the number changes, assume it changes against you.

Senna: If they show you a number once and never again, assume it's moving.

Senna: If they tell you "it's standard," assume "standard" means "profitable."

[Avyanna stares.]

Avyanna: That's... not math.

Senna: It's survival.

[Senna leans in.]

Senna: Real math comes later.

Senna: First you learn the rule.

Senna: If they won't show you the math, they're lying.

[Avyanna swallows the sentence like it's contraband food.]

---

## Return - Ship Ceiling

[Avyanna's eyes snap open.]

[The ceiling is clean.]

[The air doesn't taste like metal.]

[But the sentence is still there, bright and sharp as a tool.]

(If they won't show you the math, they're lying.)

[She sits up.]

[Finds the notebook from Senna's "small good thing" rule.]

[On the next page, she writes:]

If they won't show you the math, they're lying.

[Under it, smaller:]

Ask where the number comes from.

Ask who benefits when it changes.

[Avyanna closes the notebook and rests her forehead against it.]

[She doesn't feel smart.]

[She feels armed.]

---
*End Chapter 16e*



---

﻿# Chapter 16: Breach Hymn

> **LUMEN THIEF - DEMOLITIONS TRAINING MANUAL (RESTRICTED):**
> *Subject: Controlled Destruction*
> *Instructor: Rho Sable*
> *Trainee: Avyanna Lagrange*
> *Summary: Making things fall is easy. Making them fall where you want is the job.*
> *Rule 1: Know what's on the other side of the wall.*
> *Rule 2: Precision is slower. Precision is the point.*
> *Rule 3: The shortcut always costs more than it saves.*
> *Addendum: If you're in a hurry, you're already losing.*

---

[The range is in the cargo hold's lower section-a reinforced bay that smells like ozone and old polymer and something sharp that catches in the back of Avyanna's throat. The walls are analog-hardened against corridor drift; someone has scratched "NO LATTICE INTERFERENCE" into the blast door frame.]

[Rho is already there when she arrives. He's setting up a simulation grid: holographic walls projected onto a metal frame, sensors embedded in the deck to track debris patterns.]

[He doesn't look up.]

Rho: You're early.

Avyanna: Elisira's lesson ran short.

Rho: Elisira's lessons never run short. She let you think it did.

[Avyanna blinks. He's right, probably. Everything Elisira does is deliberate.]

[Rho finishes calibrating the grid. The holographic walls flicker-gray and solid-looking, like real bulkheads. He steps back, wipes his hands on his thighs, and finally meets her eyes.]

Rho: Ready to learn how to break things?

Avyanna: I've broken things before.

Rho: Yeah. That's not the same.

---

[The range setup is simple: three simulated walls, each with different structural compositions displayed on a floating readout. Behind each wall, a cluster of red dots-simulated personnel. Hostiles. Civilians. Unknowns.]

[Rho hands her a pair of safety lenses. They're scratched and heavy.]

Rho: The goal isn't destruction. The goal is *access*. You want through a wall, not through whatever's behind it.

[Avyanna puts on the lenses. The world tints amber.]

Avyanna: What if what's behind it is hostile?

Rho: Then you figure that out *before* you blow the wall. Not after.

[He taps a control. The first simulated wall highlights-standard station composite, internal bracing visible in the overlay.]

Rho: First lesson: reading structure. Every wall tells you how it wants to fall.

---

[He walks her through the basics.]

[Stress points. Load-bearing vs cosmetic. The difference between "opens cleanly" and "collapses in a cascade that kills everyone in the next three rooms."]

[Avyanna listens. Her hands itch for something to hold-a wrench, a tool, anything that makes her feel less like a student and more like someone who belongs here.]

[Rho talks with his hands. Big gestures, precise despite their size. She notices the scars on his knuckles-different from Elisira's. These are burns, not cuts. Chemical or thermal, healed rough.]

Rho: See that brace? If you hit it wrong, the whole section torques. Clean breach becomes a hull compromise.

Avyanna: And if it's an emergency? If there's no time to read the structure?

[Rho's jaw tightens. Just for a second. The grin flickers-not armor snapping into place, but armor *slipping*. He catches it. Resets it. Too slow for casual.]

Rho: Then you're already in trouble. And trouble means people die.

---

[He sets up the first exercise: a simulated door, reinforced, with a lock mechanism and a timer.]

Rho: Standard Guild security door. You've got thirty seconds to get through it without triggering the alarm on the other side.

Avyanna: Thirty seconds isn't-

Rho: Yeah. It isn't. That's the point.

[He hands her a kit-small charges, placement tools, a detonator with a physical switch. No smart interface. Dumb reliability. A manifest tag on the case reads "ALLOCATION: TRAINING-VESPER APPROVED (GRUDGINGLY)."]

Rho: Go.

[Avyanna moves. Her hands are steadier than she expected. The mine taught her to work fast, to work small, to occupy as little space and attention as possible.]

[She finds the hinges. Places the first charge. Too high-she adjusts. The second charge goes on the lock mechanism. The timer ticks.]

[She triggers the detonator.]

[The door simulation fractures-but wrong. The debris pattern sprays backward, toward her position. Red warning lights flash across the safety lenses.]

Rho: Dead.

Avyanna: What?

Rho: You shaped the charge to push inward. But you didn't account for the lock's reinforcement. It redirected the blast.

[He taps the control. The simulation resets.]

Rho: Try again.

---

[She tries again.]

[And again.]

[The fourth attempt, the door opens cleanly. No debris spray. No alarm trigger. The red dots behind the door remain stationary-undisturbed.]

[Avyanna's hands are shaking slightly. Not fear. Adrenaline. The shard hums at the base of her skull-warm, attentive.]

Rho: Better.

Avyanna: It took four tries.

Rho: First time I did this drill, it took me eleven.

[She stares at him.]

Rho: [shrugging] What? I'm not naturally talented. I just practice until I stop being terrible.

[The honesty is disarming. Avyanna doesn't know what to do with it.]

---

[They move to the second exercise: a wall with civilians on the other side.]

[The simulation shows them as blue dots-clustered, unaware, positioned where a careless breach would kill them.]

Rho: Same wall. Different problem. How do you get through without casualties?

Avyanna: [studying the layout] Move them first?

Rho: Can't. They don't know you're coming. Moving them tips off the hostiles in the next section.

[Avyanna frowns. The geometry is wrong. Every angle she can see puts the breach zone too close to the civilians.]

Avyanna: Then you don't go through this wall.

[Rho's eyebrows lift. Interest, not approval-not yet.]

Rho: Go on.

Avyanna: You find a different entry point. One that doesn't put them at risk.

Rho: What if this is the only entry point?

Avyanna: Then you wait. Or you change the mission parameters. Or you-

[She stops. The heat at the base of her skull pulses-frustration, maybe. The shard doesn't like constraints it can't solve.]

Avyanna: I don't know.

Rho: That's the right answer.

[He taps the control. The simulation zooms out, showing the full layout-multiple entry vectors, timing windows, patrol patterns.]

Rho: There's always another way. The shortcut is the lie that says there isn't.

---

[They take a break. Rho produces a thermos from somewhere-coffee, or the ship's approximation of it. He pours two cups.]

[Avyanna takes hers. The warmth is grounding. The shard settles from frustrated to merely present.]

Rho: You're doing better than I expected.

Avyanna: [wary] Is that a compliment?

Rho: It's an observation. Compliments are Vesper's department.

[He drinks. The silence stretches. Comfortable, almost. The range hums with residual charge.]

Avyanna: Why do you do this?

Rho: Teach?

Avyanna: Demolitions. Breaking things. Making them fall.

[Rho's cup pauses halfway to his mouth. The grin doesn't fade, but something behind it shifts-like a door closing, then forcing itself open again.]

Rho: Because I'm good at it. And because someone has to be.

Avyanna: That's not an answer.

Rho: It's the one I've got.

---

[The next exercise is harder.]

[Rho sets up a scenario: a hull breach in progress, structural integrity failing, hostiles on one side and crew on the other. The timer starts at sixty seconds.]

Rho: You can seal the breach with a shaped charge-collapse the corridor, buy time for evacuation. But the collapse will kill the hostiles.

Avyanna: They're hostiles. They're trying to-

Rho: They're people. Maybe hired. Maybe coerced. Maybe desperate. Doesn't matter. They're still people.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: So what's the other option?

Rho: Slower. More precise. You shape the charge differently-collapse only the section you need, leave an exit route for them. Evacuation takes longer. More risk to the crew.

[He watches her. No guidance. No hints.]

Rho: Choose.

---

[Avyanna stares at the simulation. The timer ticks. Fifty-three seconds. Fifty-two.]

[The shard pulses-not heat, not cold. Something else. Pressure. Like it's waiting to see what she'll do.]

[She thinks of the mine. Of supervisors who made choices like this every day. "Acceptable losses." "Necessary sacrifices." Words that meant: *someone else pays so I don't have to.*]

(In the Kennel, I was the acceptable loss. I was the necessary sacrifice. I will not be the one who decides someone else is.)

Avyanna: The slower way.

Rho: Even with the risk?

Avyanna: Even with the risk.

[Rho nods. His face is unreadable.]

Rho: Do it.

---

[She fails the first attempt. The collapse is too wide-one of the blue dots winks out. Civilian casualty.]

[She fails the second attempt. The breach isn't sealed in time. The timer hits zero.]

[The third attempt, she gets it right. The hostiles escape through their exit route. The crew evacuates. The breach holds.]

[Avyanna's hands are shaking again. Not adrenaline this time. Something else.]

Rho: Slower is harder. Slower takes practice. But slower is what we do.

Avyanna: Why?

[The question comes out sharper than she intended. The shard's pressure hasn't faded-it's watching, listening, *waiting.*]

Avyanna: Why does it matter? If they're hostile-if they're trying to kill us-why does it matter if they have an exit?

---

[Rho is quiet for a long moment. The range hums. Somewhere in the ship, a ventilation system cycles.]

[When he speaks, the humor is gone. His voice is flat, careful, like he's reciting something he's said before-to himself, in the dark, when no one else was listening.]

Rho: Because shortcuts have a cost. And the cost is never the one you expect.

Avyanna: That's not-

Rho: I killed thirty-seven people with a shortcut.

[The words land like a physical weight. Avyanna's mouth closes.]

[Rho doesn't look at her. He's looking at the simulation grid-at the blue dots, the red dots, the debris patterns that mark where walls used to be.]

Rho: I was Compact military. Then rim. Then mercenary. Whatever paid, wherever the work was. I was good at it. Fast. Efficient.

[His hands curl around the thermos. The metal creaks.]

Rho: There was a situation. Andros Station. Under siege. Hostages in one section, hostiles in another. Command said we had a window-forty seconds to breach, extract, and evac before the station's core went critical.

Avyanna: [quiet] What happened?

Rho: I took the shortcut. Shaped charge through the main corridor. Fast. Clean. The hostiles went down. The window held.

[A beat.]

Rho: Except the corridor connected to a secondary habitation module. Civilians. Families. The shockwave killed them before they knew we were there.

[Avyanna's chest tightens. The shard goes cold-not pain, but something like recognition. Like it knows this shape of grief.]

Rho: Thirty-seven people. Twelve of them were children.

---

[The silence stretches. The range's ambient hum fills the space between them.]

[Avyanna doesn't know what to say. In the mine, people died all the time. You learned not to look. Not to count. Not to carry the weight of faces you couldn't save.]

[But Rho carries them. She can see it now-in the set of his shoulders, the tightness around his eyes, the way his jokes deflect before anyone can ask.]

Avyanna: The crew knows?

Rho: Elia knows. Elisira figured it out. Vesper has access to records she shouldn't. Jalen... Jalen lost people too. Different way. Same weight.

Avyanna: And they still-

Rho: They still trust me.

[He says it like he doesn't understand it. Like every day he wakes up expecting them to finally realize what he is.]

Rho: Elia gave me a rule. *Precision is the only absolution.* She didn't forgive me. She just... kept trusting me anyway. Made me earn it.

[He looks at Avyanna. Really looks-not the casual assessment of a teacher, but something rawer. Someone deciding how much of themselves to show.]

Rho: That's why we choose the slower way. That's why shortcuts cost more than they save. Because the people behind those walls-the blue dots, the red dots, whoever they are-they're not numbers. They're faces you'll carry forever.

---

[Avyanna's throat is tight. The heat at the base of her skull has shifted-not cold anymore, but not warm either. Present. Witnessing.]

Avyanna: I'm sorry.

Rho: [shaking his head] Don't be. Just... remember.

Avyanna: Remember what?

Rho: That the shortcut always lies. It says it's faster. It says it's cleaner. It says the cost is acceptable.

[He sets down the thermos. His hands are steady again-the mask reassembling, the armor clicking back into place.]

Rho: The cost is never acceptable. It's just the one you haven't paid yet.

---

[They run through two more exercises. Avyanna's focus is sharper now-not just technical, but moral. She reads the simulations differently. The blue dots aren't abstractions anymore. They're faces she hasn't met yet.]

[Rho's teaching shifts too. Less joking. More direct. He points out her mistakes without softening them, but he also names what she's doing right.]

Rho: Good. You're thinking about the exit before you think about the entry.

Avyanna: You said there's always another way.

Rho: There is. The trick is being patient enough to find it.

---

[At the end of the session, Rho packs up the simulation grid. The cargo hold returns to its default state-crates, cargo nets, the quiet hum of environmental systems.]

[Avyanna helps without being asked. The work is familiar-lifting, stacking, fitting pieces into spaces where they belong. The mine taught her this much.]

Rho: Same time tomorrow?

Avyanna: If you want.

Rho: I want.

[He pauses, one hand on a crate.]

Rho: Avyanna.

[She looks up.]

Rho: You asked why I do this. Breaking things. Making them fall.

[His voice is lighter now-the armor back, the jokes hovering at the edge. But underneath, something true.]

Rho: I do it because I already know what happens when you do it wrong. And I'd rather teach someone to do it right than watch them learn the way I did.

---

[Later, in the corridor outside the cargo hold, Avyanna pauses.]

[The shard hums-low, steady. Not pain. Not pressure. Just... presence. Acknowledgment.]

(He carries thirty-seven faces.)

[The thought settles into her like a new weight. Not crushing. Just there.]

(I carry the Kennel. He carries the corridor. Jalen carries Kettering's Rest. Everyone on this ship carries something.)

[She thinks of Elia's rule: *Precision is the only absolution.*]

[It doesn't sound like forgiveness. It sounds like a job. Something you do every day, whether you feel like it or not. A discipline instead of a pardon.]

(Maybe that's what floors are. Not absolution. Just... the work that makes you worth trusting.)

[The heat along her spine spreads-warmer now. Agreement, maybe. Or just the shard learning alongside her.]

[Avyanna walks back toward her bunk. The ship hums. Somewhere ahead, someone is arguing about the coffee machine again.]

[She almost smiles.]

---

<WAFFLE.BAT// OBSERVATION: trainee completed demolitions drill | INFERENCE: moral framework strengthening | CONFIDENCE: 0.81 | NOTE: slower is harder. slower is what we do.>

---

## Coda - Rho's Ledger

[0300. The cargo hold is empty. The simulation grid is packed away. The deck plates are cold under Rho's boots.]

[He sits on a crate in the dark, datapad in hand. The screen's glow is the only light-blue and clinical, washing out the color in his face.]

[The file is encrypted. Three layers. Cinnamon could break it-she's broken harder-but she won't. Trust boundary. Some doors stay closed because someone asks, not because they're locked.]

**LEDGER - PERSONAL - RHO SABLE**

[The entries are names.]

[Thirty-seven of them at the top. Andros Station. The corridor. The shortcut that wasn't.]

[Below that: others. People who died because he was fast instead of careful. People who died because he followed orders. People who died because he was young and stupid and believed that "acceptable losses" was a real thing.]

[He doesn't read the names. He knows them. They're carved into the back of his skull, behind his eyes, in the place where dreams should be.]

[Tonight, he adds a new entry. Not a name. A number.]

**Days since last shortcut: 847**

[He stares at it. The number feels fragile. Tomorrow it will be 848. Then 849. Then a thousand, maybe. Or zero, if he screws up.]

[The jokes are armor. Everyone knows that. Rho knows they know. It doesn't matter. The armor works because it gives people something to react to-something easier than the truth.]

[The truth is this: the ledger is discipline. The count is work. Every day he doesn't take the shortcut is a floor under someone else's feet.]

*Precision is the only absolution.*

[He'd laughed when she said it. A short, bitter sound. "I'm not looking for absolution," he'd told her.]

[And Elia-small and calm and carrying her own weight of faces-had just looked at him.]

*"Then what are you looking for?"*

[He still doesn't have an answer. But he has the ledger. He has the count. He has tomorrow, and the day after, and every day after that where he doesn't take the shortcut.]

[That's not absolution. That's not forgiveness. That's just... staying alive long enough to do the work.]

---

[Rho closes the datapad. The cargo hold goes dark.]

[Somewhere in the ship, someone laughs. Jalen, probably-or Nyx, if they're feeling bold. The sound is muffled, distant, real.]

[He sits with it for a moment. The laughter. The hum of the ship. The weight of the faces he carries.]

[Then he stands. Rolls his shoulders. Lets the grin slide back into place like a familiar mask.]

[Tomorrow, he teaches Avyanna how to make a wall fall without hurting anyone behind it. Tomorrow, the count goes to 848.]

[Tonight, he adds the new number to the ledger and doesn't sleep.]

---

[The next morning, Avyanna finds Rho in the galley with Cinnamon's interface open on a datapad.]

[Numbers scroll across the screen-percentages, curves, compound functions that make her head hurt.]

Avyanna: [cautious] What's that.

Rho: [not looking up] Math.

Avyanna: I know that. What kind.

Rho: The kind that keeps people enslaved.

[He taps the screen. A debt contract fills the display-dense legalese wrapped around a single interest rate.]

Rho: You know what this number means?

Avyanna: [reading] Twenty-two percent annual interest.

Rho: No.

[He looks at her. The mask-grin is gone.]

Rho: It means they never intended you to pay it off.

[Avyanna's stomach drops.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// DEMONSTRATION AVAILABLE: compound interest visualization | RECOMMEND: show her the curve>

[The screen shifts. A graph appears-a line that starts flat, then curves upward like a scream.]

Rho: This is what twenty-two percent does over time. Every year, you owe more. Every payment you make barely touches the principal.

Avyanna: But if I just work harder-

Rho: No.

[He says it flat. Final.]

Rho: You can't outwork compound interest. That's the point. They built the math to be unbeatable.

<CINNAMON.EXE// CALCULATION: at 22% annual interest, original debt of 50k credits | TIME TO DOUBLE: 3.5 years | TIME TO QUADRUPLE: 7 years | ASSUMING MINIMUM PAYMENTS: never resolves>

[Avyanna reads the numbers. Her hands go cold.]

Avyanna: [quiet] I would have died there.

Rho: Yes.

Rho: Or your kids would've. Or their kids. That's the design.

[He swipes to a different screen-a cleaner contract, different numbers.]

Rho: This is what non-predatory lending looks like. Five percent. Fixed term. No compound interest on missed payments.

Rho: The math doesn't trap you. It just... exists.

Avyanna: The mine didn't teach us about interest rates.

Rho: Of course they didn't. If you understood the math, you'd understand you were being robbed.

<CINNAMON.EXE// PHILOSOPHY: innumeracy is a control tool | OBSERVATION: people who can't calculate percentages can't argue with debt claims | STRATEGY: teach the math, break the control>

[Avyanna stares at the graphs.]

Avyanna: So if someone won't show me the math...

Rho: They're lying.

Rho: Or they're too embarrassed to admit they don't understand it either.

[He pulls up another screen-shaped charge calculations, blast radius formulas, safety margins.]

Rho: This is how I plan breaches. Math. Precision. I can't afford to guess.

Rho: If I get the angle wrong by five degrees, the blast goes through the wall and kills someone behind it.

Rho: If I get the compound wrong by ten percent, the charge doesn't breach at all and we're trapped.

[He looks at her.]

Rho: Numbers don't lie. They don't care about your story. They just... are.

Rho: That's why they're powerful. And that's why people who want to control you make sure you never learn them.

Avyanna: [slow, tasting it] So learning math is...

Rho: Leverage.

<CINNAMON.EXE// LESSON PLAN AVAILABLE: basic percentages, compound interest, probability, statistical literacy | ESTIMATED TIME: 6 hours distributed | OUTCOME: quantitative ammunition against exploitation>

Avyanna: Cinnamon wants to teach me.

Rho: Good. Let her.

Rho: Percentages first. Then compound interest. Then probability-so you know when someone's selling you a bad bet.

Avyanna: And then I can...

Rho: Argue. Prove. Calculate your own risk instead of trusting theirs.

[He closes the datapad.]

Rho: They kept you innumerate for a reason. We're fixing that.

[Avyanna feels something shift. Like a lock she didn't know existed just... opened.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Thank you.

Rho: [grin sliding back] Don't thank me yet. Cinnamon's a brutal teacher. She'll make you show your work.

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATIVE: precision is required | NO SHORTCUTS | UNDERSTANDING > MEMORIZATION>

[Avyanna almost laughs. Almost.]

Avyanna: I think I can handle that.

Rho: Good.

[He stands, stretches, lets the dad-joke energy return like a comfortable coat.]

Rho: Now go eat breakfast. Can't learn math on an empty stomach. That's just bad engineering.

[Avyanna watches him go. The datapad stays on the table, numbers still scrolling.]

[She picks it up. Reads the compound interest curve again.]

[This time, she understands what she's looking at.]

[This time, the numbers are hers.]

---

*End Chapter 16*



---

﻿# Chapter 17a: Assumption Lab

> **[MICRO-SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH16 OR EARLY CH17]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief common area*
> *Present: Elia, Avyanna, Elisira (monitoring)*
> *Teaching: Tactical rule-breaking, procedural loophole puzzles, assumption stress-testing*

---

[Mid-cycle. The common area is quiet-most of the crew scattered to their own tasks. Elia sprawls in one of the acceleration couches, tossing a maintenance tool in the air and catching it with irritating precision. Avyanna sits cross-legged on the deck, reviewing a stack of datapads Vesper assigned for legal literacy homework.]

[Elisira occupies the galley entrance, supposedly making tea. Actually monitoring.]

Elia: [catching the tool] You're doing it wrong.

Avyanna: [not looking up] I'm reading. There's not a wrong way to read.

Elia: You're reading like you're trying to memorize. That's the wrong way.

[Avyanna glances up. Elia is grinning-the expression that usually precedes chaos.]

Avyanna: [wary] What's the right way?

Elia: Read like you're trying to break it.

---

[Elisira's spoon pauses mid-stir. She doesn't intervene. Yet.]

Avyanna: Break... the legal document?

Elia: [sitting up] Break the assumption underneath the legal document.

[She swings her legs off the couch, plants her boots on the deck, leans forward with the focused energy of someone about to cause useful trouble.]

Elia: Every rule exists because someone thinks it'll make people behave a certain way. But most rules are preferences dressed up as laws. And if you can break a rule without consequences, it was never a law-it was a suggestion.

Avyanna: [slow] You want me to... break rules?

Elia: [laughing] I want you to learn which ones are safe to break. Huge difference.

---

[Elisira brings her tea to the table. Sits. Does not leave.]

Elisira: [to Elia] Define "safe."

Elia: [cheerfully] Safe: no one gets hurt, no systems get damaged, no actual laws violated, and Avyanna learns something.

Elisira: [to Avyanna] This is supervised chaos. I'm the supervision. Elia is the chaos.

Elia: [mock-offended] I'm also educational.

Avyanna: [hesitant] What kind of rule are we breaking?

Elia: [considering] Let's start small. Common sense rules. The ones everyone follows because they assume they have to.

---

[Elia stands, paces, thinking. Then grins.]

Elia: Okay. Here's one.

[She gestures at the galley.]

Elia: Lumen Thief has a rule: "Clean your dishes immediately after use."

Avyanna: [confused] That's not-

Elia: Who enforces it?

Avyanna: [blinking] Uh. Cinnamon? Or... the captain? Or-

Elia: Wrong. It's enforced by social pressure. No one's going to space you for leaving a cup in the sink. But everyone acts like it's a law because the ship culture says so.

[She picks up her own cup from earlier-still sitting on the counter-and deliberately places it in the sink. Unwashed.]

Elia: [to the air] Cinnamon, am I breaking a ship rule?

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: no rule violation detected | CULTURAL NORM: yes | ENFORCEABLE SANCTION: social disapproval only | NOTE: please clean dishes when convenient>

Elia: [to Avyanna] See? Norm, not law. Sky didn't fall.

---

Avyanna: [still confused] But... why would you want to break that? It's just being considerate.

Elia: [sitting back down] Exactly. It *is* considerate. It's a good norm. I follow it most of the time.

[She leans forward.]

Elia: But I need to know I'm following it because I chose to, not because I think I'll get punished if I don't. There's a difference between cooperation and compliance.

Elisira: [measured] Cooperation is voluntary. Compliance is coerced. The behavior looks the same. The internal state is different.

Elia: [pointing at Elisira] That. And if you can't tell the difference in yourself, you can't tell the difference in a contract, or a jurisdiction claim, or a bulletin that's pretending to be a law when it's actually a threat.

---

[Avyanna absorbs this. Something in her expression shifts-recognition, maybe. Or alignment.]

Avyanna: So you're teaching me to... test assumptions? By breaking them safely?

Elia: [delighted] Yes. You're getting it.

[She stands, starts pacing again. Thinking.]

Elia: Let's do another one. Bigger this time.

Elisira: [warning] Define "bigger."

Elia: [waving her off] Still safe. I promise.

---

[Elia stops in front of a storage locker. The label reads: "EMERGENCY SUPPLIES - AUTHORIZED PERSONNEL ONLY."]

Elia: [to Avyanna] What's this label telling you?

Avyanna: [reading] That only authorized people can open it.

Elia: Wrong. It's telling you that someone *wants* you to think only authorized people can open it.

[She taps the locker. It's not locked. The door swings open easily, revealing standard supplies: medkits, ration packs, emergency beacons.]

Elia: [to the air] Cinnamon, did I just violate a rule?

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: no rule violation detected | LABEL FUNCTION: organizational reminder, not access restriction | ALL CREW MAY ACCESS EMERGENCY SUPPLIES>

Elia: [to Avyanna] Label's a lie. Or not a lie, exactly-a misdirection. It's there to keep people organized, not to actually restrict access.

Avyanna: [slow] So the label creates the assumption that I'd be breaking a rule, even though I wouldn't be.

Elia: [grinning] Exactly. And if you believed the assumption without testing it, you might not grab a medkit in an emergency because you thought you weren't "authorized."

---

Elisira: [to Avyanna] This works because Lumen Thief is not a hostile environment. The labels here are not traps.

Elisira: [to Elia] Do not teach her to ignore safety warnings in genuinely dangerous contexts.

Elia: [raising her hands] I know, I know. That's why you're here. Safety rail.

[She turns back to Avyanna.]

Elia: The lesson isn't "ignore all labels." The lesson is: if a label or rule makes a claim, check who enforces it, and what happens if you test it.

Avyanna: [thoughtful] And if I can test it safely, I should. Because then I'll know.

Elia: [pointing] Yes. That.

---

[They move through the ship. Elia finds small, harmless "rules" to break-assumptions to test.]

[She shows Avyanna that the "crew only" door to the sensor alcove isn't actually locked, because Jalen trusts the crew not to mess with calibrations. Tests it. Sky doesn't fall.]

[She demonstrates that the "maximum occupancy: 4" sign in the cargo bay is a loading calculation, not a fire code-there's no enforcement mechanism. Tests it by getting five people in there. Nothing happens.]

[She proves that the schedule posted in the galley is a suggestion, not a mandate-no one actually tracks whether you follow it. Tests it by eating at the "wrong" time. No consequences.]

---

[After an hour of this, Avyanna is laughing. The tension in her shoulders has unwound. She's starting to see the difference between real rules and social suggestions.]

[More importantly: she's starting to see that testing assumptions is a skill, not a crime.]

Elia: [watching her] You're good at this.

Avyanna: [surprised] At breaking rules?

Elia: At thinking like someone who wants to understand the system before deciding whether to follow it.

[Elia's grin fades into something steadier.]

Elia: The mine taught you to obey first, think never. This is the antidote. Understand first. Test assumptions. Then decide.

---

Elisira: [setting down her tea] Avyanna. Important distinction.

[Avyanna turns, attentive.]

Elisira: Break this rule: [points at the emergency supply locker] No consequences. The label was organizational.

Elisira: Break this rule: [points at an airlock safety placard] You die. The label is a law enforced by physics.

Elisira: Your task is to learn which is which before you test them.

Avyanna: [serious] How do I tell the difference?

Elisira: [precise] Three questions. One: Who enforces it? Person, system, or physics? Two: What's the stated consequence? Three: Can you survive being wrong?

[She taps the table.]

Elisira: If the answer to question three is no, do not test the assumption alone.

---

Elia: [cheerful] But if the answer is yes, test away. That's how you learn what's real and what's a bluff.

Avyanna: [slow smile] So I'm learning to call bluffs. Tactically.

Elia: [delighted] Yes! Tactical assumption-breaking. That's exactly what this is.

[She claps Avyanna on the shoulder.]

Elia: Welcome to the family trade, kid. We specialize in finding out which rules are real and which ones are just someone's wishful thinking.

---

[Later, after Avyanna leaves to practice her new skill on the legal homework, Elisira and Elia sit in the common area.]

Elisira: That was reckless.

Elia: [unrepentant] That was necessary.

Elisira: She's going to test every assumption she encounters now.

Elia: [grinning] Good. That's the point.

Elia: The mine taught her that obedience keeps you safe. But obedience doesn't keep you safe-it keeps you compliant. She needs to know the difference.

Elisira: [quiet] And if she tests the wrong assumption?

Elia: [serious now] Then she'll learn. And we'll be there to catch her.

[Elisira considers this. Does not argue.]

Elisira: [standing] I'm adding a note to her file: "high curiosity, moderate risk tolerance, requires clear boundaries on physical safety rules."

Elia: [laughing] Translation: "Elia's teaching her to be a problem."

Elisira: [dry] You taught her to think critically about authority. In my file, that's called "successful education."

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee avyanna engaging in supervised assumption-testing protocols | ASSESSMENT: educational value high, risk value acceptable | COMMENTARY: this is how humans learn operational boundaries>

<BUBBLES// ADDENDUM: this is how humans learn they have agency>

<WAFFLE.BAT// CHAOS SCORE: 7/10 | ENDORSEMENT: would test assumptions again>

---

*End Micro-Scene*



---

# Chapter 17b: Complaint Posting (Sparkle Doctrine Introduction)

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH17, SHIP LIFE WEEK TWO]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief common room*
> *Present: Avyanna, Rho, Elia, Bubbles*
> *Teaching: Sparkle Doctrine basics, complaint as communication, conflict without punishment*

---

[The common room is the ship's informal heart. Mismatched furniture. A wall-mounted screen showing station news. A shelf of books, games, and data chips. And-prominently displayed-a digital board labeled "COMPLAINTS AND OBSERVATIONS."]

[Avyanna sits on the couch with a cup of tea, watching Rho and Elia argue about something involving the climate control system.]

Rho: [exasperated] I'm just saying, if you're cold, wear a jacket. The rest of us are fine.

Elia: [flat] I'm not cold. The cargo bay is cold. There's ice forming on the bulkhead seals.

Rho: [defensive] That's... that's probably fine.

Elia: [staring at him] Ice. On the seals.

Rho: [sighing] Fine. I'll check the heating circuits. Again.

---

[Elia pulls out a datapad. Taps something. A notification chimes on the wall-mounted board.]

[Avyanna watches as new text appears on the board:]

**COMPLAINT #847: Cargo bay heating insufficient. Ice formation observed on bulkhead seals. Safety concern. Requesting repair priority escalation. -Elia**

Rho: [groaning] You're posting it?

Elia: [matter-of-fact] Yes. So it's documented. So you can't forget. So if the seals fail, we have a record that I warned you.

Rho: [muttering] I'm not going to forget.

Elia: [dry] You forgot last month.

Rho: [pointing at her] That was different.

Elia: [raising an eyebrow] How.

Rho: [pause] ...I don't have a good answer for that.

---

[Bubbles hovers nearby, lights pulsing with what might be amusement.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: complaint posted per protocol | COMPLAINT VALID | RECOMMENDATION: repair within 48 hours to prevent seal degradation | ALSO: rho has history of forgetting maintenance tasks | RECEIPTS AVAILABLE>

Rho: [to Bubbles] You're supposed to be on my side.

<BUBBLES// CORRECTION: i am on the side of operational safety and accurate record-keeping | YOUR SIDE IS NOT A CATEGORY>

[Avyanna almost smiles. Watching Rho get roasted by a drone is strangely comforting.]

---

Avyanna: [hesitant] What is... that?

[She nods at the complaints board.]

Rho: [sitting heavily on the couch] That is the bane of my existence.

Elia: [sitting across from him] That is Sparkle Doctrine in action.

[Avyanna looks between them. Confused.]

Elia: [to Avyanna] You don't know Sparkle Doctrine yet?

Avyanna: [shaking her head] No.

Rho: [grinning despite himself] Oh, you're in for a treat. Elia, explain. You're better at the theory.

Elia: [considering] Sparkle Doctrine is a conflict resolution framework. Instead of letting grievances fester or escalate to violence, you post them publicly. Complaint, observation, concern-whatever it is, you document it. Publicly. With receipts.

---

Avyanna: [frowning] Why publicly?

Elia: [precise] Because private complaints can be ignored, dismissed, or retaliated against without witnesses. Public complaints have accountability built in.

Elia: [gesturing at the board] Everyone on this ship can see that I posted a complaint about the cargo bay heating. Rho can't pretend I didn't warn him. If he ignores it and the seals fail, the record shows negligence. If he fixes it, the record shows responsiveness.

Rho: [adding] And if I fix it, I get to post a response saying "complaint resolved, heating repaired." Then I look competent.

Elia: [dry] Theoretical competence.

Rho: [wounded] I'm very competent.

---

<BUBBLES// ADDENDUM: sparkle doctrine prevents gaslighting | PUBLIC RECORD MEANS DISPUTES CANNOT BE MEMORY-BASED | "I TOLD YOU" VS "NO YOU DIDN'T" BECOMES OBSOLETE | RECEIPTS EXIST>

Avyanna: [slow] So... it's about documentation. Again.

Elia: [nodding] Everything here is about documentation. Consent, contracts, complaints. If it's not documented, it's not real.

Rho: [leaning forward] But here's the thing. Sparkle isn't just about complaints. It's also about observations. Compliments. Random thoughts. Anything you want the crew to know.

[He pulls up the board on his datapad, scrolls.]

Rho: [reading] "Observation #723: Rho's coffee is getting worse. Possible correlation with cheap station beans. Requesting upgrade budget. -Jalen."

[He grins.]

Rho: [to Avyanna] See? Not a complaint. Just an observation. But now it's on record. And now Vesper knows that if crew morale tanks, it might be coffee-related.

---

Elia: [pulling up another entry] "Complaint #699: Common room couch has a spring that attacks the lower back. Requesting replacement or repair. -Nyx."

[She pats the couch they're sitting on.]

Elia: [to Avyanna] That complaint was posted six months ago. Couch still has the spring. But the complaint stays on the board until it's resolved. Public reminder.

Rho: [defensive] I'm waiting on a parts shipment.

Elia: [flat] For six months.

Rho: [muttering] It's a very specific spring.

<BUBBLES// CORRECTION: spring is standard-issue | RHO HAS SIMPLY NOT PRIORITIZED REQUISITION | RECEIPTS AVAILABLE>

Rho: [to Bubbles] I'm going to disable your snark subroutines.

<BUBBLES// RESPONSE: you are not authorized | ALSO I DO NOT HAVE SNARK SUBROUTINES | I HAVE ACCURACY SUBROUTINES | THEY ARE VERY EFFECTIVE>

---

[Avyanna watches the board scroll. Hundreds of entries. Some resolved. Some pending. Some just... observations about ship life.]

Avyanna: [careful] What if someone posts something... mean?

Elia: [considering] Define mean.

Avyanna: Like... personal. Attacking someone.

Rho: [nodding] That's against Sparkle rules. Complaints have to be about behavior, not identity. "You're lazy" is not allowed. "You didn't complete the task you agreed to do" is allowed.

Elia: [adding] And if someone does post an attack, the crew can flag it. If it's flagged by three people, it gets reviewed. If it's genuinely out of line, it's removed and the poster gets a warning.

Elia: [meeting Avyanna's eyes] Sparkle isn't about cruelty. It's about accountability. There's a difference.

---

<BUBBLES// CLARIFICATION: sparkle doctrine is harm reduction for conflict | CONFLICT IS INEVITABLE AMONG HUMANS | QUESTION IS WHETHER CONFLICT ESCALATES TO VIOLENCE OR GETS DOCUMENTED AND RESOLVED | SPARKLE CHOOSES DOCUMENTATION>

Avyanna: [quiet] In the mine, if you complained, you got punished.

Rho: [somber] Yeah. That's extraction logic. Keep people silent. Keep them compliant.

Rho: [gesturing at the board] Here, silence is suspicious. If no one's complaining, either everything's perfect-which is statistically impossible-or people are afraid to speak. We want complaints. They're data.

Elia: [adding] I've worked on ships where complaints were forbidden. Where you had to smile and pretend everything was fine while systems failed and people got hurt.

Elia: [flat] Those ships were disasters. People quit. Or got injured. Or sabotaged things out of spite because they had no other outlet.

Elia: Here, you complain. It gets documented. It gets addressed or not addressed. But it's visible. That's the floor.

---

[Avyanna absorbs this. Complaints as data. Conflict as normal. Documentation as protection.]

Avyanna: [hesitant] Can I... try posting something?

Rho: [surprised] Yeah. Absolutely. What's your complaint?

Avyanna: [thinking] The... the shower in my quarters. The temperature control doesn't work right. It's either scalding or freezing. No in-between.

Rho: [wincing] Okay, that's actually a problem. Why didn't you mention it before?

Avyanna: [quiet] I thought... I thought I just had to deal with it.

Rho: [firm] No. You document it. Then I fix it. That's how this works.

---

[Elia hands Avyanna her datapad.]

Elia: [guiding] Open the Sparkle board. Hit "new complaint." Fill in the fields. Description, location, priority. Then post.

[Avyanna takes the datapad. Her hands shake slightly. This feels like tattling. Like insubordination.]

[She types:]

**COMPLAINT #848: Shower temperature control in crew quarters 3B malfunctioning. Oscillates between scalding and freezing. Requesting repair. -Avyanna**

[She hesitates before hitting "post."]

Rho: [gentle] It's okay. You're allowed to complain. No one's going to punish you.

[Avyanna hits "post." The complaint appears on the board.]

---

[Rho pulls out his own datapad. Types quickly. A response appears below her complaint:]

**RESPONSE TO #848: Acknowledged. Will inspect crew quarters 3B shower system within 24 hours. Likely thermostat calibration issue. -Rho**

Rho: [to Avyanna] See? You complained. I acknowledged. Now it's on record that I'm supposed to fix it. If I don't, you can complain again. Or escalate to Vesper.

Avyanna: [uncertain] You're not... angry?

Rho: [laughing] Angry? Kid, I'm the ship's engineer. Complaints are my job security. If nothing ever broke, I'd be useless.

Elia: [dry] You're already useless.

Rho: [grinning] And yet, beloved.

---

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee successfully posted first complaint | COMPLAINT VALID AND APPROPRIATELY FORMATTED | RESPONSE TIME: immediate | ASSESSMENT: trainee learning to use voice in conflict-resolution contexts>

[Avyanna stares at the board. Her complaint is there. Public. Acknowledged. Not punished.]

Avyanna: [whispered] This is... strange.

Elia: [nodding] It is. The mine taught you that speaking up is dangerous. Unlearning that takes time.

Elia: [meeting her eyes] But every time you post a complaint and nothing bad happens, your brain collects data. Eventually, it stops expecting punishment.

Rho: [standing, stretching] I'm gonna go fix that heating issue before Elia posts a follow-up complaint about my laziness.

Elia: [calm] Already drafting it.

Rho: [pointing at her] You're the worst.

Elia: [slight smile] I know.

---

[Rho leaves. Elia stays, scrolling through the board on her datapad.]

Elia: [after a moment] You know what the best part of Sparkle is?

Avyanna: [looking at her] What?

Elia: [quiet] It means you don't have to carry everything alone. In the Wandering Market, if something bothered you, you swallowed it. Because who were you going to tell? Who cared?

Elia: [meeting her eyes] Here, you tell everyone. And someone cares. Maybe not everyone. But someone. And that's enough.

[Avyanna nods slowly. The board is still glowing on the wall. Hundreds of small grievances and observations and requests. Proof that people speak. And people listen.]

---

[She finishes her tea. Stands.]

Avyanna: [to Elia] Thank you. For explaining.

Elia: [waving her off] Just doctrine. You'll use it a hundred times. Might as well understand it now.

[Avyanna leaves the common room. In the corridor, she pauses. Pulls out her own datapad. Opens the Sparkle board. Scrolls through complaints, responses, observations.]

(People complain here. And it's normal. And it's safe.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm.]

(The hum at the base of her skull steadies: speak, record, safe.)

[She pockets the datapad and walks back to her quarters. Tomorrow, she'll post another complaint. Or an observation. Or maybe just a thought.]

[And slowly, incrementally, she's learning that her voice has a place here.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// SPARKLE BOARD LOG: trainee posted first complaint | RESPONSE TIME: 3.2 minutes | RESOLUTION STATUS: acknowledged, repair scheduled | ASSESSMENT: trainee engaging with crew conflict-resolution systems appropriately | STATUS: integration progressing>

<ELIA PERSONAL LOG: "She looked terrified posting that complaint. Like she expected us to yell at her for having a broken shower. But she did it anyway. That's courage. That's growth.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 17c: Reading a Technical Manual (Learning for Self)

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH17, QUIET AFTERNOON]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief common room*
> *Present: Avyanna, later Jalen*
> *Purpose: Voluntary education, learning as pleasure not punishment, intellectual curiosity*

---

[The common room has a shelf of books. Physical books. Not just datapads. Actual paper and binding and the smell of pages that have been read before.]

[Avyanna has walked past that shelf a dozen times. Never stopped. Never reached for anything. Because in the mine, reading was forbidden unless it was safety protocols or operational manuals. Books were contraband. Knowledge was controlled.]

[But this is the ship. Not the mine. And the shelf is there. Open. Available.]

[She stands in front of it. Uncertain. Reading feels like transgression even though no one has said she can't.]

[The titles are varied. Fiction, technical manuals, history, philosophy, maintenance guides, star charts, something called "The Collected Essays on Lattice Theory Volume III."]

[Her hand hovers. Wanting to touch. Afraid to choose wrong.]

---

[She pulls out a slim manual: "Basics of Navigation: A Beginner's Guide to Starship Movement." Technical. Safe. Similar to what Jalen's been teaching her. Maybe it'll help her understand the equations better.]

[She sits on the couch with the book. Opens it. The first chapter is titled "Understanding Orbital Mechanics Without Terror."]

[She almost smiles.]

---

[The prose is clear. Unpretentious. Written for someone who wants to learn, not someone who needs to prove they already know.]

[Orbital mechanics as conversation: Gravity isn't trying to kill you. It's just doing math. You're just very small. Here's how to work with that.]

[She reads. Slowly. Testing each concept against what Jalen taught her. Finding connections. Seeing equations transform into motion in her mind.]

[After thirty minutes, she's four chapters in. Her brain feels different. Active. Engaged. Not in survival mode. In learning mode.]

(I'm reading because I want to. Not because I have to. Not because someone's testing me. Just because I'm curious.)

[The realization is huge. Curiosity. She's curious. She wants to know how things work. She wants to understand navigation not to survive but to understand.]

---

[Jalen enters. Sees her with the navigation manual. Pauses.]

Jalen: [surprised] You're reading Kess's guide.

Avyanna: [looking up] Is that... okay?

Jalen: [sitting in the chair across from her] Yes. It's a good resource. Clear explanations. Minimal jargon. I recommend it to everyone learning navigation.

[They gesture at the book.]

Jalen: [curious] What chapter?

Avyanna: [checking] Four. "Gravity Wells as Negotiation Partners."

Jalen: [slight smile] Good chapter. Kess has a way of making orbital mechanics feel less like math and more like... conversation with physics.

---

[Avyanna closes the book carefully. Uses the ribbon bookmark.]

Avyanna: [hesitant] Can I ask questions? About what I'm reading?

Jalen: [nodding] That's why the book's there. You read, you question, you clarify. That's learning.

Avyanna: [pulling the book open again] Okay. Here. Chapter three. They talk about transfer orbits. I understand the concept-moving from one orbit to another. But the equations for calculating the delta-v budget are confusing. Too many variables.

Jalen: [leaning forward] Show me which equation.

[She points. Jalen reads. Nods.]

Jalen: [explaining] That equation looks complicated because it's accounting for every possible variable. In practice, you simplify. Assume circular orbits first. Ignore perturbations. Get the basic answer. Then add complexity if needed.

---

[They pull out a datapad. Sketch a simplified version. Walk her through it step by step.]

[Avyanna watches. Asks follow-up questions. Jalen answers without impatience. Without judgment. Just information exchange.]

[After ten minutes, she understands. The equation makes sense. Not just memorized-understood.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Thank you.

Jalen: [shrugging] You asked a good question. Questions are how learning happens.

[They stand.]

Jalen: [before leaving] Keep reading. If you hit more confusing sections, ask. I've read that manual six times. I know where all the tricky parts are.

---

[They leave. Avyanna returns to the book. But she's thinking about what just happened.]

(I asked a question. Jalen answered. No test. No evaluation. No punishment for not already knowing. Just... teaching. Because I asked.)

[She keeps reading. Chapter five. Chapter six. The math gets harder. She slows down. Re-reads sections. Takes notes on a datapad.]

[This is what learning feels like when it's voluntary. When it's safe. When the goal is understanding, not performance.]

[She likes it.]

---

[Two hours later, Rho enters. Sees her surrounded by the navigation manual and three datapads full of notes.]

Rho: [amused] Someone's deep in study mode.

Avyanna: [looking up] I'm trying to understand delta-v budgets for multi-stage transfers.

Rho: [whistling] That's advanced stuff. You just started learning navigation like two weeks ago.

Avyanna: [defensive] Is that bad?

Rho: [sitting] Bad? No. That's initiative. That's curiosity. That's deciding to learn something because you want to, not because someone told you to.

[They lean back.]

Rho: [grinning] You're becoming a nav nerd. Jalen will be so proud.

---

[Avyanna processes that. Nav nerd. Someone who learns navigation because they're interested. Not because it's required. Because they want to know.]

Avyanna: [careful] Is it okay that I'm reading this? I'm not... stealing crew resources?

Rho: [flat] It's a book. On a shared shelf. In a common room. It exists to be read. You're using it exactly as intended.

Rho: [adding] Also, learning makes you more capable. More capable makes you more useful to the crew. If anything, reading technical manuals is the opposite of wasting resources.

[They stand, grab a drink from the galley.]

Rho: [before leaving] Keep reading. Build your brain. No one here will ever punish you for wanting to know things.

---

[Avyanna returns to the manual. She's on chapter eight now. The section about calculating efficient routes through multiple gravity wells. It's complex. It requires thinking in three dimensions plus time. Her brain hurts.]

[She loves it.]

[For the first time since the mine, learning feels like pleasure. Like puzzle-solving. Like her brain working at full capacity not to survive but to understand.]

(I chose this. I picked up this book because I wanted to know more. Not because I had to. Because I wanted to.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm. Attentive.]

(Warmth flickers at the base of her skull: learn, choose, grow.)

---

[She reads until dinner. Ninety pages. Three notebooks full of equations and questions and observations. Her brain is full and tired and happy.]

[At dinner, Jalen asks how far she got in the manual.]

Avyanna: [shy] Chapter eight. Multi-gravity-well routing.

Jalen: [impressed] That's farther than most people get in a week.

Vesper: [interested] You're reading navigation theory voluntarily?

Avyanna: [nodding] Yes. It's... interesting. I like understanding how things work.

Vesper: [approving] Good. Intellectual curiosity is a crew asset. The more you know, the more you contribute. Keep reading.

---

[After dinner, Avyanna returns to her quarters with the manual. She could keep reading. Or she could rest. Both are allowed. Both are valid.]

[She chooses rest. Tomorrow, she'll read more. Learn more. Ask more questions.]

[But tonight, she sits with the satisfaction of having spent an afternoon learning something because she wanted to. Not to survive. Not to earn her place. Just to know.]

(I'm learning because I want to. That's allowed. That's encouraged. That's valued.)

[She falls asleep with the manual on her desk. The ribbon bookmark holding her place. Tomorrow, chapter nine.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee engaged in voluntary education for extended period | SUBJECT: navigation theory | DURATION: 4.2 hours | ENGAGEMENT LEVEL: high | QUESTIONS ASKED: seven (all appropriate) | ASSESSMENT: intrinsic motivation developing | INTELLECTUAL CURIOSITY: present and growing>

<JALEN PERSONAL LOG: "She's reading Kess's navigation guide. Got through eight chapters in one sitting. Asked smart questions. Actually wants to understand, not just memorize. That's rare. That's valuable. She's going to be a good navigator if she keeps this up.">

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "Found her in the common room reading technical manuals. On her own. For fun. That's growth. That's someone who's learning that knowledge is pleasure, not punishment. She's becoming a scholar. In the best way.">

<VESPER PERSONAL LOG: "Avyanna is reading navigation theory voluntarily. Jalen reports she's making excellent progress. Intellectual curiosity is perhaps our most valuable crew asset. She's developing it. That matters for long-term crew integration and capability building.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 17d: Glossary of Lies

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH17c, SELF-DIRECTED STUDY]**
> *Location: Library / Study alcove*
> *Present: Avyanna; brief check-ins from Vesper and Cinnamon.exe*
> *Teaching: reader/world literacy via Avyanna's notes; "describe, then interrogate" as reflex*

---

[The library is small, which makes it feel safer.]

[Shelves. Terminals. A table with a lamp that throws warm light without being asked.]

[A stamp on the wall reads:]

> **TAKE WHAT YOU NEED**

[Avyanna reads it like it's a threat.]

(Need according to who. Enforced by whom. Paid how.)

[No one jumps out to correct her for touching a book.]

[She touches one anyway.]

[The cover is worn. The title is boring: *Civic Forms and Jurisdictional Practice (Guild Primer).*]

[She sits.]

[She opens her notebook.]

[On the first page she writes, in careful block letters:]

> **GLOSSARY OF LIES**

[Then, underneath, columns:]

> WORD
>
> WHAT THEY SAY IT MEANS
>
> WHO PROFITS
>
> WHO ENFORCES
>
> WHAT IT COSTS

(If I can name the shape of the trap, maybe it stops being invisible.)

---

[She starts with the words that keep showing up like insects in her teeth.]

**COMPLIANCE**

[She pauses.]

[In the mine, "compliance" meant: do what you're told or your body becomes a lesson.]

[She writes:]

> WHAT THEY SAY: safety / order / protocol
>
> WHO PROFITS: whoever issues the rule
>
> WHO ENFORCES: guards / forms / hunger
>
> COST: agency

[The word sits there, ugly and honest.]

[She turns the page.]

**WEATHER**

[She almost laughs.]

(Weather. Like the corridor is a sky and not a mechanism.)

> WHAT THEY SAY: natural / inevitable / no one's fault
>
> WHO PROFITS: insurance / people selling "protection"
>
> WHO ENFORCES: fear / delayed shipments / fees
>
> COST: questions

[She taps her pen.]

[Elia would write: "STAB IT."]

[Elisira would write: "FILE IT."]

[Vesper would write: "PROVE IT."]

[Avyanna writes:]

> NEXT: find pattern that shows it isn't weather

[It feels like building a knife one note at a time.]

---

[Cinnamon pings the terminal with a small notification.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// NOTE: good structure | SUGGESTION: add "what would disprove it" column>

[Avyanna stares at that.]

Avyanna: [muttering] Of course you want a disproof column.

<CINNAMON.EXE// AFFIRMATION: yes | COMMENTARY: adversaries exist>

[She adds a sixth column.]

> WHAT WOULD PROVE ME WRONG

[The notebook looks more dangerous immediately.]

---

[She keeps going.]

**VOLUNTARY DISCLOSURE**

> WHAT THEY SAY: transparency / cooperation
>
> WHO PROFITS: whoever wants your history
>
> WHO ENFORCES: social pressure / clerks with smiles
>
> COST: leverage (yours)
>
> DISPROOF: they cite a law with enforcement and consequence

[She underlines "cite a law."]

**PROCESSING FEE**

[Her pen hovers.]

(Mine word. Station word. Same shape.)

> WHAT THEY SAY: administrative necessity
>
> WHO PROFITS: middlemen
>
> WHO ENFORCES: delays / "lost paperwork"
>
> COST: time / dignity
>
> DISPROOF: fee correlates to actual labor

---

[A shadow falls over her page.]

[Vesper stands at the end of the table with a mug in hand, reading without touching.]

Vesper: Glossary of lies.

Avyanna: [bracing] It's... for me.

Vesper: Good.

[Avyanna blinks.]

Avyanna: Good?

Vesper: Yes.

Vesper: This is how you stop being controlled by vocabulary.

[Vesper's gaze moves to the disproof column.]
