Vesper: [interrupting] I don't care what you're willing to pay. We had a contract. The contract specified financial records only. We delivered financial records only. That's the transaction.

Client: [pushing] You were in their system. You had access. It would have taken five minutes to copy additional files-

Vesper: [cold] Five minutes that were outside contract scope. Five minutes that would have constituted theft rather than evidence retrieval. Five minutes that would have compromised our legal standing and our Guild reputation.

---

[The client's expression hardens.]

Client: [calculated] I could report that you refused to fulfill the full scope of service-

Vesper: [pulling out her datapad] Please do. Here's the contract. Guild-certified. Every term we discussed, documented in plain language. Nowhere does it say we retrieve anything beyond specified financial records.

[She projects the contract holographically. Lets the client read it.]

Vesper: [precise] You're attempting to retroactively expand scope. That's not how contracts work. You got exactly what you paid for. Nothing less. Nothing more.

Client: [shifting tactics] What if I offered a new contract? Right now. To retrieve those additional files.

Vesper: [meeting their eyes] I'd decline.

---

Client: [surprised] You'd decline paid work?

Vesper: [firm] I'd decline work from a client who tries to coerce scope expansion after delivery. That behavior is a red flag. It suggests you'll do it again. And again. Until we compromise our ethics to satisfy your demands.

[She stands.]

Vesper: [to the client] Here's what happens now. You accept the evidence we delivered per contract. You pay the agreed amount. We part ways. Or you refuse, and I file a dispute with the Guild, which will side with us because we have documentation proving we fulfilled every contracted term.

Vesper: [leaning forward slightly] Your choice. But choose quickly. I have other clients who respect boundaries.

---

[The client glares. Avyanna watches, tense. In the mine, this is where violence would happen. Where authority would assert itself through force. Where the person with less power would lose.]

[But this isn't the mine. This is Guild space. And Vesper has contracts. Documentation. Receipts.]

[The client pulls out a credit chit. Transfers the agreed payment. The transaction completes with a soft chime.]

Client: [standing, bitter] I'll remember this.

Vesper: [unbothered] Good. Then you won't hire us again. We prefer clients who understand consent.

[The client leaves. The door hisses shut behind them.]

---

[Vesper sits back down. Lets out a slow breath.]

Vesper: [to Avyanna] What did you observe?

Avyanna: [carefully] They tried to change the contract after you'd already done the work.

Vesper: [nodding] What else?

Avyanna: [thinking] They tried multiple tactics. Direct request. Guilt. Threat. Bribery. When one didn't work, they tried another.

Vesper: [approving] Yes. That's manipulation. People who don't respect boundaries will test every angle until they find one that works or until you shut them down completely.

---

[She closes the contract file.]

Vesper: [measured] That client will probably complain about us. They'll say we were inflexible. Uncooperative. That we refused reasonable requests.

Vesper: [meeting Avyanna's eyes] They'll be right about one thing. We were inflexible. Because flexibility about scope is how you end up doing illegal work, compromising your ethics, and destroying your reputation one "small exception" at a time.

Avyanna: [quiet] You said no. Multiple times. They kept pushing.

Vesper: [firm] And I kept saying no. Because no is a complete sentence. It doesn't need justification. It doesn't need softening. It just needs to be clear and consistent.

---

[Vesper stands, gathers her things.]

Vesper: [to Avyanna] You're going to encounter clients like this. People who think they can pressure you into compromising. People who think your boundaries are negotiable if they pay enough or threaten enough or guilt enough.

Vesper: [meeting her eyes] Here's what you do. You hold your boundary. You reference the contract. You document everything. And if they continue pushing, you walk away.

Avyanna: [uncertain] What if I need the money?

Vesper: [flat] You'll always need money. But if you compromise your boundaries for money once, you teach people that your boundaries are for sale. And then every future client will try to buy them.

---

[They leave the meeting room. Walk through the station corridor. Around them: normal station life. People who don't know that a contract just held against pressure. That boundaries just won without violence.]

Avyanna: [after a moment] In the mine, we didn't have contracts.

Vesper: [nodding] I know.

Avyanna: [continuing] They'd tell us to do something. We'd do it. Then they'd add more tasks. More hours. More danger. And if we said no, we got punished.

Vesper: [stopping, turning to face her] That's why contracts matter. That's why documentation matters. That's why saying no matters.

[She taps her datapad.]

Vesper: [precise] The mine operated on power imbalance and information asymmetry. You had no documentation. No proof of what was agreed. No recourse when they changed terms.

Vesper: [meeting Avyanna's eyes] Here, we document everything. Every term. Every boundary. Every transaction. So when someone tries to change the agreement, we have proof of what was actually agreed to.

Vesper: That's not just good business. That's survival.

---

[They return to the ship. Vesper files the contract completion report. Avyanna sits in the common room, processing.]

[Vesper said no. The client pushed. Vesper held the boundary. The client paid anyway because the contract was clear. No violence. No coercion. Just documentation and refusal.]

(This is what power looks like when you have receipts. When you have records. When you have proof that you did exactly what you agreed to do and nothing more.)

[Rho enters, sees her thinking.]

Rho: [sitting] Vesper told me about the client. The one who wanted scope expansion.

Avyanna: [nodding] She said no. Multiple times.

Rho: [grinning] Yeah. Vesper's a master of the strategic "fuck no." It's beautiful to watch.

---

Avyanna: [careful] What if the client had been dangerous? What if saying no meant... violence?

Rho: [sobering] Then we wouldn't have taken the contract in the first place. We vet clients. We assess risk. We don't put ourselves in situations where saying no gets us killed.

Rho: [leaning forward] But here's the thing. Most people don't escalate to violence when you say no. They escalate to manipulation. Guilt. Pressure. Threats that are mostly bluster.

Rho: [meeting her eyes] And if you hold your boundary through all of that? They usually back down. Because people who rely on manipulation aren't usually willing to risk actual consequences. They want easy compliance. Not a fight.

---

[Avyanna processes that. Most people back down when boundaries hold.]

Avyanna: [quiet] The mine taught me that saying no was dangerous.

Rho: [nodding] Because in the mine, it was. The mine had all the power. You had none. Saying no meant punishment because they could enforce that punishment without consequence.

Rho: [gesturing around the ship] Here, power is more balanced. Vesper has contracts. Documentation. Guild backing. She can say no because she has structural support for her boundaries. The client can't punish her without facing Guild sanctions.

Rho: [to Avyanna] You're learning that you can have that too. Structural support. Documentation. People who'll back your boundaries. It's not just you versus the world anymore.

---

[Avyanna sits with that. Structural support for boundaries. Not just personal strength, but systems that protect refusal.]

[She thinks about the contract. About Vesper saying no. About the client leaving angry but paying anyway. About documentation as power.]

(This is what the mine didn't want us to know. That boundaries are enforceable when you have proof. When you have support. When you have systems that back your right to refuse.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm.]

(A warm pulse at the base of her skull: no is complete; no is protected.)

[She stands. Tomorrow, there will be another contract. Another client. Another opportunity to watch boundaries hold or bend. Another lesson in how consent operates in commercial contexts.]

[And slowly, incrementally, she's learning that saying no doesn't have to end in violence. Sometimes it just ends in contracts fulfilled and payments transferred and clients walking away disappointed but compliant.]

[Sometimes no is enough.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// CONTRACT COMPLETION LOG: client attempted scope expansion post-delivery | VESPER REFUSED | CLIENT PAID PER CONTRACT TERMS | DISPUTE: none filed | ASSESSMENT: boundaries maintained successfully | TRAINEE WITNESSED APPROPRIATE REFUSAL UNDER PRESSURE>

<VESPER PERSONAL LOG: "Client tried to pressure additional retrieval post-contract. I shut it down. Avyanna watched. She needs to see that boundaries hold. That contracts protect us. That no is enforceable when you have documentation. She's learning.">

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "Found her processing Vesper's client confrontation. She's scared that saying no means violence. I told her about structural support. About how power is more balanced here. She's starting to understand that she's not alone anymore. That she has backup. That matters.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 19c: Receipt Practice

> **[SCENE - OCCURS BETWEEN CH19 AND CH20, PRE-HEARING WORK]**
> *Location: Vesper's office*
> *Present: Avyanna, Vesper*
> *Teaching: "claim -> evidence -> inference" as a safe spine; trauma handled as procedure*

---

[Vesper's office is too orderly to be natural.]

[Shelves. Binders. A desk that looks like it has never been used for anything except war.]

[Avyanna sits across from Vesper with a stack of printouts and a pen that feels heavier than it should.]

Vesper: Tell me what you saw.

[Avyanna's jaw tightens on instinct.]

(If I tell the truth wrong, it becomes a weapon aimed at me.)

Avyanna: Which part.

Vesper: The part you are scared to put into words.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: The station clerk tried to make me sign "voluntary disclosure."

Vesper: Good. That's a claim.

Avyanna: [baffled] That's not-

Vesper: It is. "Clerk attempted coercion." Claim.

[Vesper taps the printouts.]

Vesper: Evidence.

Avyanna: The slip. The camera footage request Elisira filed. The time stamp on the terminal log.

Vesper: Good.

Vesper: Inference.

Avyanna: They were fishing. For identity. For contacts.

Vesper: Next step.

Avyanna: Report it. Archive it. Don't sign.

[Vesper's mouth twitches.]

Vesper: You're learning.

[Avyanna's chest tightens.]

Avyanna: I'm trying.

Vesper: Trying is a verb. Keep using it.

---

[Vesper slides a new printout toward her.]

[Aurum-coded header. Not the mine's logo, exactly-cleaner, but the same colors.]

[Avyanna's vision tunnels.]

[The room tilts.]

(No.)

[Her hands go cold.]

Vesper: Avyanna. Eyes on me.

[Avyanna forces her gaze up.]

Avyanna: [thin] That looks like-

Vesper: Aurum.

Avyanna: [breathing wrong] They're here.

Vesper: No.

Vesper: Not physically.

Vesper: It's a record artifact. A data style. A mimic.

[Vesper's voice stays calm on purpose.]

Vesper: Check.

Avyanna: [after a beat] Yellow.

Vesper: Good. Stay with yellow.

[Vesper does not touch her.]

[She doesn't have to.]

[She moves the printout away, flips it face-down.]

Vesper: We don't process trauma by pretending it isn't there.

Vesper: We process it by turning it into something that can be handled.

Avyanna: That sounds like you.

Vesper: It is me.

---

[Vesper opens a binder and pulls out a template.]

> **WITNESS STATEMENT (DRAFT)**
>
> *Claim*
>
> *Evidence*
>
> *Inference*
>
> *Confounders*
>
> *What would prove me wrong*

Avyanna: Cinnamon would like that.

Vesper: Cinnamon does like that.

Vesper: Now.

Vesper: We're going to practice on something that won't kill you if you get it wrong.

Avyanna: [dry] That's generous.

Vesper: It's responsible.

[Avyanna picks up her pen.]

[Her hand still shakes, but she can write through it.]

Avyanna: Claim: the mine's medical bay neglected workers on purpose.

Vesper: Evidence.

[Avyanna's voice goes quieter.]

Avyanna: The logs. The ration schedule. The number of collapsed people per shift. The way they stamped "noncompliant" on anyone who asked for painkillers.

Vesper: Inference.

Avyanna: The neglect was policy. Not failure.

Vesper: Confounders.

[Avyanna freezes.]

Vesper: This is where you stop being a victim of your own certainty.

Avyanna: [working] Confounders... shortages. Staffing. Flicker day malfunctions.

Vesper: Good.

Vesper: What would prove you wrong.

Avyanna: A supply manifest showing adequate medicine. A record of workers treated promptly.

Vesper: And if those exist.

Avyanna: Then I'm wrong.

[The words taste strange in her mouth.]

(Wrong means you die.)

[Here, wrong means: adjust.]

Vesper: If you can be proven wrong, you can be trusted.

Avyanna: That's... backwards.

Vesper: It's adversarial.

Vesper: The people who can't be wrong are trying to sell you something.

---

[A pause.]

[Avyanna stares at the blank space on her template labeled WITNESS STATEMENT and feels something in her chest shift.]

Avyanna: This is... how you fight.

Vesper: This is one way.

Vesper: Another way is Elia.

Avyanna: [a small, real laugh] Yes.

[Vesper stands, goes to the shelf, and takes down a thin folder.]

Vesper: Tomorrow we go to arbitration.

Vesper: Today we build the spine.

[She sets the folder in front of Avyanna.]

Vesper: No heroics.

Avyanna: [soft] Just receipts.

Vesper: Just receipts.

[Avyanna opens the folder.]

[This time, the paper doesn't feel like a trap.]

[It feels like a handle.]

---

[Vesper doesn't let the moment turn sentimental.]

[She flips to a new section in the binder and slides it across.]

> **CROSS-EXAMINATION PREP**
>
> *If they say you're lying, what do you point to?*
>
> *If they say you misremembered, what do you point to?*
>
> *If they say it's "standard," what do you ask?*

Avyanna: [reading] What do you ask.

Vesper: "Under which jurisdiction. Enforced by whom. Consequence for refusal."

Avyanna: [quiet] That's... the spine.

Vesper: Yes.

Vesper: When someone is trying to drown you in language, you don't swim.

Vesper: You stand on three questions.

[Avyanna's pen hovers.]

Avyanna: In the mine, questions got you noticed.

Vesper: Here, questions keep you alive.

[A beat.]

Vesper: Not just physically.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: This feels like fighting without... touching anyone.

Vesper: It is.

Vesper: It's slower than Elia. But it leaves bodies intact.

Avyanna: [dry] Sometimes.

[Vesper's mouth twitches.]

Vesper: Sometimes.

---

[Vesper pulls a small index card from a box and slides it toward Avyanna.]

> **YOUR JOB IN THE ROOM**
>
> - say what you saw
> - don't guess
> - if you don't know, say you don't know
> - if you need a minute, ask for it

Avyanna: [soft] I can ask for a minute.

Vesper: Yes.

Vesper: If anyone tries to deny you that, I will make it expensive.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

(Expensive. Protective. Not ownership.)

---

[Vesper taps the face-down Aurum-coded printout with one knuckle.]

Vesper: This.

Avyanna: [tense] Yes.

Vesper: You did not break when you saw it.

Avyanna: I almost did.

Vesper: "Almost" is data.

Avyanna: That's... also you.

Vesper: [without apology] Yes.

[She pauses.]

Vesper: When you're in the room tomorrow and something tries to pull you back into the mine-

Avyanna: Like a smell. Like a word.

Vesper: -you do not have to white-knuckle it.

Vesper: You can say: "I need to pause."

Avyanna: [quiet] And nobody will-

Vesper: No penalty.

[The phrase lands like a seal on paper.]

---

[Avyanna writes it down.]

> **NO PENALTY**

[Not in Cinnamon's font. In her own.]

[She looks up at Vesper.]

Avyanna: Thank you.

Vesper: [measured] You're welcome.

[Vesper straightens Avyanna's collar without asking. Then catches herself.]

Vesper: Go drink water.

Avyanna: [blinking] That's an order.

Vesper: It's medical advice.

Avyanna: [a small smile] Who enforces it.

Vesper: Nyx.

[Avyanna laughs.]

Vesper: And also me.

[The second part is said so quietly it almost doesn't count.]

[Almost.]

[Avyanna gathers the folder and the index card like they're equipment.]

[Because they are.]

[She leaves Vesper's office with her spine built from paper and the strange sensation of being allowed to carry it.]


---

﻿# Chapter 19: Contract: Station Justice

> **GUILD ARBITRATION NOTICE - FORM 77-K (EXPEDITED):**
> *Re: Disputed Cargo Manifest, Registry 4412-HELM*
> *Arbiter Assigned: Pending (Lumen Thief crew, observer capacity)*
> *Summary: Both parties claim ownership. Neither party has clean hands.*
> *Note: The truth is a receipt. Everything else is negotiation.*

---

[Helder Weir Station smells like recycled air and old grievances.]

[Avyanna stands in the observation gallery overlooking the arbitration floor-a circular chamber with tiered seating, holographic evidence displays, and a raised platform where a Guild arbiter sits like a judge in a court that never quite stopped being a market.]

[Eight months on the Lumen Thief. Eight months of learning to move differently, speak differently, see differently. The shard at the base of her skull hums-present but not pressing. Almost comfortable.]

(I'm getting used to this. That should worry me more than it does.)

Vesper: [beside her, voice low] Watch the claimants. Not the arbiter.

Avyanna: Why?

Vesper: Because the arbiter already knows who's lying. The question is which lie they'll decide to believe.

---

[The case is simple on paper: two shipping consortiums disputing ownership of a cargo pod retrieved from a static zone. Standard salvage law says the finder keeps it. Standard contract law says the original owner retains claim.]

[The complication: the cargo pod contains medical supplies that were never meant to reach their destination. Diverted. Stolen. Relabeled. The original "owner" is a Compact logistics house that sold the supplies twice-once legitimately, once to a black market intermediary who died in the static bloom that stranded the pod.]

[The finder is a rim scavenger crew who pulled the pod from wreckage and claims salvage rights.]

[Neither party is innocent. Both are lying. The medical supplies are needed by a station three systems away where children are dying of a preventable infection.]

[This is the job.]

---

Vesper: [studying a datapad] The logistics house has better documentation. Cleaner chain of custody. More lawyers.

Avyanna: So they'll win?

Vesper: They'll win unless we make the cost of winning higher than the cost of losing.

[Vesper's fingers move across the datapad-cross-referencing manifests, timestamps, comm logs. Her expression is neutral, focused. This is what she does: finds the seams in other people's stories.]

Avyanna: What are you looking for?

Vesper: The thing they don't want found.

---

[The arbitration proceeds. Testimony. Counter-testimony. Legal precedent cited with the reverence of scripture.]

[Avyanna watches the claimants. The logistics house representative-a woman in Compact corporate attire, smile professional, hands steady. The scavenger captain-weathered, defensive, obviously outmatched by the legal theater.]

[The arbiter listens. Takes notes. Asks clarifying questions that feel like traps.]

[Vesper doesn't speak. She's not here to argue. She's here to observe-and to deliver a receipt at the precise moment it will matter most.]

---

[During a recess, Vesper pulls Avyanna into a side corridor.]

Vesper: The logistics house has a problem.

Avyanna: Which one?

Vesper: [almost smiling] Good question. They have several. But the one that matters is this: the cargo manifest they submitted as evidence was modified three days ago.

[She shows Avyanna the datapad. Two versions of the same document-identical except for a single line entry that changes "medical grade biosealant" to "industrial adhesive."]

Avyanna: They changed the cargo description?

Vesper: They changed what they're claiming ownership of. The original manifest-the one filed at origin-lists specific medical compounds. The version they submitted here lists generic industrial materials.

Avyanna: Why would they-

[She stops. Thinks. The shard pulses-not guidance, just attention. It wants her to figure this out.]

Avyanna: Because the medical compounds were never supposed to be in that pod in the first place.

Vesper: [nodding] The pod was diverted from a legitimate shipment. The supplies were stolen from a hospital contract and sold to the intermediary. If the original manifest is introduced, it proves the logistics house committed fraud.

Avyanna: So they falsified evidence to hide a crime.

Vesper: They falsified evidence to hide *this* crime. The crime itself is somewhere else-buried in accounting they thought no one would ever see.

---

[Avyanna's chest tightens. She thinks of the station three systems away. The children. The preventable infection.]

Avyanna: If they win, they get the supplies back. And then what?

Vesper: Then the supplies disappear into a warehouse somewhere. Resold. Relabeled again. The station doesn't get them.

Avyanna: And if the scavengers win?

Vesper: They sell to whoever pays. Maybe the station. Maybe not.

[The answer Avyanna wants doesn't exist. There's no outcome where the right people automatically get what they need.]

Vesper: [watching her] This is the part where you learn that evidence isn't justice. It's leverage. What you do with the leverage-that's where the ethics live.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: Then why have a court.

[Vesper's gaze stays on the chamber below. The arbiter. The parties. The performative politeness.]

Vesper: Because people like believing that truth automatically becomes consequence.

Vesper: Courts sell that belief.

Avyanna: [quiet] Does it work.

Vesper: Sometimes.

[A pause.]

Vesper: More often, it delays.

Avyanna: And delay kills the station with the kids.

[Vesper looks at her now. Direct.]

Vesper: Yes.

Vesper: So your first civics lesson is not "who is right."

Vesper: It's: who can move the world in time.

[Avyanna stares.]

Vesper: Ask three questions.

Vesper: Who has the authority.

Vesper: Who has the force.

Vesper: Who has the clock.

Avyanna: The clock.

Vesper: The timeline.

Vesper: If we turn this into a criminal investigation, the supplies sit in evidence lockup for months while everyone argues about procedure.

Vesper: The children don't get months.

Avyanna: So we stay in arbitration.

Vesper: We use the venue that can move the cargo inside forty-eight hours.

[Vesper's mouth tightens like she hates that this is how the universe is arranged.]

Vesper: It's not justice.

Vesper: It's harm reduction.

Avyanna: [after a beat] And then we build a bigger case later.

[Vesper's eyes flick-a tiny approval.]

Vesper: Yes.

---

[When the arbitration resumes, Vesper requests permission to submit supplementary evidence.]

[The arbiter-a Guild veteran with the tired eyes of someone who's seen every trick-checks her registry.]

Arbiter: Lumen Thief is listed as a Guild-certified evidence contractor. Amicus submission is permitted under Protocol 31-A.

[She grants the request with obvious skepticism, but the permission is real. The logistics representative's counsel objects anyway-overruled before they finish speaking.]

[Vesper stands. Her posture is relaxed, her voice conversational. She doesn't look like someone about to detonate a case.]

Vesper: Arbiter, I'd like to submit the original cargo manifest from origin station Taelios Forge, timestamp-verified and chain-of-custody confirmed through Guild archive protocols.

[The logistics representative's smile flickers. Just for a moment.]

Representative: Objection. The manifest we submitted is the controlling document.

Vesper: The manifest you submitted was modified three days ago. Guild archive protocol 12-C requires preservation of all versions. I have the original.

[She transfers the file. The holographic display updates. Two manifests, side by side. The difference highlighted in red.]

Vesper: The original lists medical compounds specific to pediatric immunization protocols. The modified version lists industrial adhesive. The question, Arbiter, is why a logistics house would alter evidence to obscure the nature of cargo they claim to own.

---

[The silence is heavy. The arbiter studies the documents. The logistics representative is speaking rapidly with her legal counsel-whispers sharp enough to cut.]

[The scavenger captain looks confused but hopeful. He doesn't understand what's happening, but he understands momentum shifting.]

[Avyanna watches Vesper. The calm. The precision. No flourish, no drama-just the receipt, delivered at the moment it mattered most.]

(This is what she does. She makes the truth visible. And then she waits for the weight of it to do the work.)

---

[The arbiter calls another recess. This one feels different-charged, inevitable.]

[In the corridor, the logistics representative approaches Vesper. Her professional smile is gone. What replaces it is something colder-calculation without mask.]

Representative: You've made your point. What do you want?

Vesper: The supplies delivered to Eirene Reach Station within forty-eight hours. Full manifested value. No relabeling.

Representative: That's not-

Vesper: I have the original contract between your company and the intermediary. The one that shows you sold stolen medical supplies to a black market contact. Would you like me to submit that as well?

[The representative's jaw tightens.]

Vesper: [mild] The Guild takes document fraud seriously. So does the Compact regulatory board. So do the hospitals whose patients died because supplies never arrived.

[The representative's datapad creaks in his grip.]

Representative: This is extortion.

Vesper: This is leverage. The difference is I'm giving you a choice.

---

[The resolution happens quickly after that.]

[The logistics house "voluntarily" releases the cargo to humanitarian transit. The scavenger crew receives salvage compensation-less than they wanted, more than they expected. The station at Eirene Reach will have the medical supplies within forty-eight hours.]

[No one is happy. Everyone has lost something. But children three systems away will live who would have died.]

[Avyanna stands in the observation gallery as the chamber empties. The shard hums-warm, present. Not approval exactly. Acknowledgment.]

---

Vesper: [joining her] Questions?

Avyanna: You knew the whole time. What they did. What the outcome needed to be.

Vesper: I knew the evidence. The outcome was... negotiable.

Avyanna: You could have submitted everything at the start. Blown the whole case open.

Vesper: And then what? The arbitration becomes a criminal investigation. The supplies sit in evidence lockup for months. The station runs out of time.

[She turns to face Avyanna directly. Her eyes are steady, patient-the same way she looks when teaching, when explaining, when waiting for understanding to land.]

Vesper: The goal was never punishment. The goal was the supplies. Everything else-the leverage, the timing, the pressure-was in service of that.

Avyanna: But they got away with it. The fraud. The theft. The people who died.

Vesper: [quietly] They didn't get away with it. They just paid a different price. One that served the people who needed help now.

---

[Avyanna is silent. The gallery empties around them. Station lights cycle toward evening mode-dimmer, warmer, the artificial rhythm of a day that doesn't exist.]

Avyanna: Is that how it always works?

Vesper: No. Sometimes the leverage isn't enough. Sometimes the timing is wrong. Sometimes you have all the receipts in the world and the people with power just... don't care.

[She looks out at the empty arbitration floor.]

Vesper: But you build anyway. Document anyway. Create the receipts even when no one's watching. Because one day, the timing will be right. And when it is, you'll be ready.

---

[They leave the station together. The Lumen Thief is docked at berth seven-a familiar silhouette against the star-scattered black.]

[Avyanna's mind is full. The case. The evidence. The children who will live because Vesper knew when to deploy a truth.]

(Justice isn't a verdict. It's leverage used for the right thing.)

[The shard pulses-warm, settled. Learning alongside her.]

(I'm starting to understand what Vesper does. What receipts are for. Why evidence matters even when the system is broken.)

[She glances at Vesper. The older woman is already reviewing something on her datapad-the next case, probably. The next receipt to build.]

(She never stops. Even when it doesn't work. Even when the leverage isn't enough. She just... keeps building.)

---

[Back on the ship, Elia is in the common area with Rho. They're arguing about something trivial-coffee rationing, maybe, or the proper calibration of the galley's temperature settings. The kind of argument that means nothing and everything.]

Elia: [noticing them] How'd it go?

Vesper: Supplies are en route to Eirene Reach. The logistics house is reconsidering their business practices.

Elia: [dry] Reconsidering or actually changing?

Vesper: Reconsidering with prejudice.

[Elia's mouth quirks. Almost a smile.]

Elia: And the trainee?

[She looks at Avyanna. The gaze is assessing but not unkind-the same way she looks at everyone, cataloging capability and cost.]

Avyanna: I learned that evidence isn't justice.

Elia: [nodding slowly] That's the first half.

Avyanna: What's the second half?

Elia: That you make it justice anyway. Even when the system doesn't cooperate.

---

[That night, Avyanna lies in her bunk and stares at the ceiling.]

[The case replays in her mind. The manifests. The timing. The moment Vesper's receipt landed like a controlled demolition-precise, devastating, exactly where it needed to be.]

(Rho taught me how to make walls fall without hurting people behind them. Vesper taught me how to make truth land without losing the goal.)

[The shard hums. Warm. Present.]

(Different skills. Same principle. Precision in service of something that matters.)

[She thinks of the children at Eirene Reach. Faces she'll never see. Lives she helped save without being in the room.]

(Is this what the crew does? Build floors for people they'll never meet?)

---

[In the corridor outside, she hears Vesper's voice-low, steady, probably dictating case notes. The eternal documentation. The receipts that accumulate like armor.]

[Avyanna closes her eyes.]

[For the first time in months, she doesn't dream of the mine.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee remained focused through 7-hour arbitration | INFERENCE: evidence metabolism improving | CONFIDENCE: 0.79 | NOTE: she's learning to wait for the right moment. that's the hard part.>

---

*End Chapter 19*


---

# Chapter 20a: Quiet Ship Night

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH20, LATE NIGHT CYCLE]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief, various locations during night shift*
> *Present: Avyanna wandering, encounters with crew*
> *Purpose: Ship as lived-in space, crew rhythms, belonging through small moments*

---

[2300 ship time. Night cycle. Most of the crew is sleeping. The Lumen Thief is never truly quiet-life support hums, systems cycle, the ship breathes-but it's quieter. Softer. Like the difference between day-sounds and night-sounds in any place that's lived in.]

[Avyanna can't sleep. Again. Her body still hasn't calibrated to ship rhythms. Or maybe it has, and she's just someone who doesn't sleep well. Hard to know the difference yet.]

[She leaves her quarters wearing soft clothes that used to belong to someone else and now belong to her. Bare feet on deck plating. The ship is warm. Not mine-warm, where heat meant broken cooling systems. Ship-warm, where temperature is maintained for human comfort.]

---

[She walks without destination. The corridor lights are dimmed for night cycle-blue-shift, easier on eyes that might need to wake up fast. She passes crew quarters. Behind Elia's door: silence. Behind Rho's: faint music, something old and acoustic. Behind Vesper's: the soft glow of a still-active terminal.]

[Everyone has their own night rhythms. Everyone exists in their own way when they think no one's watching.]

[Avyanna turns toward the galley. Maybe tea. Maybe just the comfort of a space that smells like food and care.]

---

[The galley is dim. One light over the counter. And Rho, sitting at the table with a cup of something and a datapad, looking like he's been there for hours.]

Rho: [not looking up] Can't sleep, or won't sleep?

Avyanna: [hesitating in the doorway] Can't.

Rho: [gesturing at the empty chair] Join the club. Tea's hot. Help yourself.

[Avyanna makes tea. The same green tea she chose that first morning. It's become her default. Her preference. The first one she's had in seventeen years.]

[She sits across from Rho. He's reading something technical-engineering schematics, maybe. Definitely not entertainment.]

Avyanna: [quiet] What are you working on?

Rho: [sighing] Trying to figure out why the port thruster is burning fuel inefficiently. Jalen says it's pulling three percent more than it should. Three percent doesn't sound like much until you're budgeting for a long jump and suddenly you're short on margins.

---

[He taps the schematic.]

Rho: [to himself] Has to be the injector timing. Or the fuel mixture calibration. Or seventeen other things that could be wrong.

Avyanna: [tentative] Is it urgent?

Rho: [leaning back] Nah. Annoying, not dangerous. I just can't figure it out and it's bothering me. So here I am at 2300, reading schematics instead of sleeping like a functional human.

[He grins at her.]

Rho: [adding] What's your excuse?

Avyanna: [shrugging] My brain won't stop. Too many thoughts. Too much... everything.

Rho: [nodding] Yeah. I know that feeling.

---

[They sit in comfortable silence. Rho reads. Avyanna drinks tea. The galley is warm and safe and neither of them is performing for the other.]

[After a while, Rho closes the datapad.]

Rho: [stretching] Can't solve it tonight. Brain's too tired. Might as well admit defeat and try to sleep.

[He stands, rinses his cup, puts it in the cleaning rack.]

Rho: [to Avyanna] You staying up, or heading back?

Avyanna: [uncertain] Staying for a bit. If that's okay.

Rho: [waving her off] Galley's open all night. Lock it if you're the last one out. Otherwise, do whatever.

[He leaves. Avyanna is alone again. But the space still feels occupied. Rho's presence lingers-the rinsed cup, the datapad he left on the counter, the faint smell of whatever he was drinking earlier.]

---

[She finishes her tea. Walks out into the corridor. The ship is quiet. She drifts toward the bridge. Maybe Jalen's there. Maybe not. Either way, the bridge has windows. Stars. A view that isn't walls.]

[The bridge door is open. Jalen sits at the navigation console, three screens active, stylus moving. Always working. Always calculating something.]

Avyanna: [at the doorway] Can I come in?

Jalen: [not looking up] Door's open. That means yes.

[She enters. Takes the seat she sat in last time they taught her basic navigation. They don't acknowledge her beyond that initial permission. Just keep working.]

[Avyanna watches the stars through the viewport. They're in transit between stations-no nearby gravity wells, no hazards, just void and distance and the mathematics of getting from here to there.]

---

Jalen: [after five minutes] Can't sleep?

Avyanna: [quiet] No.

Jalen: [nodding] I'm not good at sleeping either. Too many calculations running. Hard to shut the brain off.

[They save their work. Turn to face her.]

Jalen: [gesturing at the viewport] You know what that is?

Avyanna: [confused] Space?

Jalen: [dry] Technically correct. But more specifically: that's about four light-years of nothing. We're in the void between inhabited systems. No stations. No ships. No people except us.

[They lean back.]

Jalen: [quieter] I find that comforting. Knowing that for a few days, we're the only thing that exists in a very large radius. No one can get to us. No one knows where we are except us. We're just... adrift in a pocket of silence.

---

[Avyanna looks at the stars again. Thinking about that. Four light-years of nothing. A bubble of safety maintained by distance and math.]

Avyanna: [careful] Do you get scared? Out here?

Jalen: [considering] Sometimes. When systems fail. When navigation is uncertain. When I remember that we're very small and space is very large and all of this is held together by math that could be wrong.

[They tap their console.]

Jalen: [adding] But mostly I feel... quiet. Like the ship is quiet. Like my brain can stop screaming for a few hours and just exist.

Avyanna: [whispered] That's what I want. For my brain to stop screaming.

Jalen: [meeting her eyes] Yeah. It'll come. Takes time. But you'll get there.

---

[They sit. Jalen returns to their calculations. Avyanna watches the stars. The bridge is quiet except for the soft sounds of stylus on screen and ship systems maintaining life in vacuum.]

[After twenty minutes, Avyanna stands.]

Avyanna: [to Jalen] Thank you. For letting me sit here.

Jalen: [not looking up] Bridge is open during night shift. You're welcome here whenever.

[She leaves. Walks back toward crew quarters. Passes the med bay. The door is cracked open. Light spills into the corridor.]

[She pauses. Looks in.]

---

[Nyx is at their desk, reviewing something on a datapad. They look up when they sense her presence.]

Nyx: [calm] Can't sleep?

Avyanna: [leaning against the doorframe] Everyone keeps asking me that.

Nyx: [slight smile] Because you keep wandering the ship at night. Pattern recognition.

[They set the datapad down.]

Nyx: [gesturing inside] Come in if you want. Or keep wandering. Both acceptable.

[Avyanna steps inside. The med bay smells like antiseptic and something herbal. Clean and cared-for.]

Nyx: [observing her] Trouble sleeping, or avoiding sleep?

Avyanna: [sitting in the patient chair] Both? I'm tired but my brain won't stop. And when I do sleep, I dream about the mine.

Nyx: [nodding] Trauma dreams. Normal. Unpleasant, but normal.

---

[They pull out a small box. Inside: various items. Smooth stones. Fidget toys. A small weighted pad. Grounding tools.]

Nyx: [setting the box on the desk] These are for people who can't shut their brain off. You can borrow one. See if tactile grounding helps.

[Avyanna looks at the items. Picks up a smooth stone-similar to the worry stone she bought on her first station visit, but heavier.]

Nyx: [explaining] Some people need something to hold. Something physical to focus on when thoughts get too loud. You already have the worry stone. This is a weighted version. Different sensation. Might help more.

Avyanna: [holding it] Can I try it?

Nyx: [nodding] Yes. Keep it as long as you need. Return it when you're done, or don't. I have others.

---

[Avyanna closes her hand around the weighted stone. The pressure is grounding. Real. Pulling her attention out of her head and into her body.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Thank you.

Nyx: [returning to their datapad] You're welcome. Now go try to sleep. Or keep wandering. Whichever feels right.

[Avyanna leaves the med bay. The weighted stone is in her hand. Solid. Present. An anchor.]

[She walks back to her quarters. The corridor is empty now. Just her and the ship and the quiet sounds of systems maintaining existence.]

---

[In her quarters, she lies down with the weighted stone in her hand. Her thumb rubs across the smooth surface. The pressure is comforting in a way she doesn't have words for yet.]

[Her mind is still loud. But quieter. The stone gives her something to focus on other than the panic and the memories and the constant calculation of threats.]

[She doesn't sleep. Not yet. But she rests. And for now, that's enough.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// NIGHT CYCLE LOG: trainee wandering behavior observed | INTERACTIONS: rho (galley), jalen (bridge), nyx (med bay) | DURATION: 73 minutes | ASSESSMENT: trainee seeking comfort/connection during insomnia | CREW RESPONSES: appropriate, supportive, no intervention required | STATUS: trainee learning to navigate ship environment autonomously>

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "Found her in the galley at 2300. Couldn't sleep. Neither could I. We sat together for a bit. No big conversation. Just company. That's what she needs sometimes. Not fixing. Just presence.">

<JALEN PERSONAL LOG: "She came to the bridge during night shift. Watched stars. Asked if I get scared. Told her the truth-sometimes, but mostly I feel quiet. She needs to know it's okay to not be okay all the time. That eventually, quiet comes.">

<NYX PERSONAL LOG: "Gave her a weighted stone. She's learning what grounding tools work for her. The worry stone helps. This one might help more. She's building a toolkit. That's the work. One tool at a time until she has enough to manage the loud.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 20b: Witnessing Crew Conflict (Without Violence)

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH20, AFTER CONTESTED CONTRACT]**
> *Location: Lumen Thief common room*
> *Present: Avyanna (witnessing), Vesper, Rho (in conflict)*
> *Purpose: Seeing healthy disagreement, learning conflict can exist without danger*

---

[Avyanna hears the argument before she sees it.]

[Raised voices from the common room. Not screaming. Not violence-adjacent. But definitely argument-level volume. Her stomach clenches. Conflict = danger = someone gets hurt.]

[She should leave. Go to her quarters. Not witness whatever's about to happen.]

[But she's frozen in the corridor. Listening. Afraid.]

---

Rho: [frustrated, loud] -that's not the point! The point is you made the call without consulting the crew!

Vesper: [controlled but firm] I made the call because waiting would have cost us the contract. Time-sensitive decisions don't get committee approval.

Rho: [angry] This wasn't time-sensitive! You had six hours before client deadline! You could have asked!

Vesper: [cold] I could have. I chose not to. Because I'm the contractor lead and operational decisions are my jurisdiction.

Rho: [pointing] That's horseshit and you know it! We operate on consensus! That's the whole fucking point of this crew!

---

[Avyanna's breathing is shallow. This is how it starts. Argument escalates. Someone throws the first hit. Someone gets hurt. Someone-]

[She should intervene. Or run. Or something. But she's frozen.]

[Elia walks past her, entering the common room without hesitation.]

Elia: [calm, to Rho and Vesper] Are we having a loud conversation or a fight?

Vesper: [not looking away from Rho] Loud conversation.

Rho: [frustrated] Loud conversation that should have happened six hours ago before Vesper decided to act unilaterally.

Elia: [sitting on the couch, unbothered] Okay. Continue. I'm listening.

---

[Avyanna stares. Elia just... walked into an argument. Sat down. Didn't try to stop it. Didn't flee.]

[Jalen appears beside Avyanna in the corridor. Sees her frozen. Sees the argument in the common room.]

Jalen: [quiet] They're fighting. Not fighting-fighting. Just disagreeing loudly.

Avyanna: [whispered] Someone's going to get hurt.

Jalen: [shaking their head] No one's getting hurt. Watch.

[They walk past her into the common room. Sit beside Elia. Also just... listening.]

---

Vesper: [to Rho] The client offered a time-limited bonus. Complete the contract six hours early, get an extra five thousand credits. I assessed risk, determined it was manageable, accepted the modification.

Rho: [pointing] YOU assessed. YOU determined. Not WE. That's the problem.

Vesper: [measured] Would the crew consensus have been different?

Rho: [pause] ...Probably not. But that's not the point!

Vesper: [leaning forward] Then what IS the point? Because if the outcome would have been the same, this is about process, not substance.

Rho: [frustrated] YES! It's about process! It's about you not treating the crew like assets you manage! We're supposed to be equals!

---

[Nyx appears beside Avyanna. Doesn't say anything. Just gestures: want to come sit, or want to stay here?]

[Avyanna follows Nyx into the common room. Sits on the far end of the couch. Tense. Ready to run.]

[The argument continues.]

Vesper: [to Rho] I don't treat you like assets. I treat you like crew I trust to handle what I delegate. You're upset because I made an operational decision that fell within my role parameters.

Rho: [standing, pacing] I'm upset because you're doing the thing again! The thing where you decide something affects all of us and you don't tell anyone until it's done!

Vesper: [voice rising] Because telling you MID-OPERATION would have been worse! You would have questioned! Debated! We would have missed the deadline!

Rho: [shouting] THEN WE MISS THE DEADLINE! That's the cost of consensus!

---

[Silence. Heavy. Charged.]

[Avyanna's hands are clenched. This is where violence starts. This is where someone gets hurt. This is-]

Vesper: [after a long moment, quieter] You're right.

[Avyanna blinks. Wait. What?]

Vesper: [sitting back, rubbing her face] You're right. I acted unilaterally because I didn't want to risk missing the bonus. I prioritized money over process. That's not how we operate.

Rho: [stopping pacing, surprised] ...Oh.

Vesper: [looking at him] I'm sorry. I should have consulted the crew, even if it meant missing the deadline. The process matters more than five thousand credits.

---

[Rho sits down heavily.]

Rho: [quieter] I'm not trying to undermine you. I trust your judgment. I just... I need to be included. We all do.

Vesper: [nodding] I know. And I violated that. I won't do it again.

[Pause.]

Rho: [reluctant] The contract modification was probably the right call. We got the bonus. No one got hurt. I just wish you'd told us before you accepted it.

Vesper: [measured] Next time, I will. Even if it's mid-op. Even if it costs us.

Rho: [sighing] I don't want it to cost us. I just want to know what's happening.

Vesper: [meeting his eyes] Understood. I'll do better.

---

[Silence again. But different. Not charged. Just... processing.]

[Elia speaks for the first time since sitting down.]

Elia: [to both of them] Are we resolved, or do we need to keep talking?

Rho: [to Vesper] We resolved?

Vesper: [nodding] For now. If you're still angry tomorrow, we revisit.

Rho: [considering] I'm not angry. I'm just... annoyed. But I'll get over it.

Vesper: [slight smile] Fair.

---

[The tension breaks. Rho stands, goes to the galley, comes back with water. Hands one to Vesper without comment. She takes it. They drink in silence that's no longer hostile.]

[Avyanna is still frozen on the couch. Trying to process what she just witnessed.]

(They argued. Loudly. They were angry. And then... they resolved it. Without violence. Without punishment. Vesper apologized. Rho accepted. They're just... sitting here. Drinking water. Still crew.)

[Her brain is short-circuiting.]

---

Nyx: [beside her, quiet] First time witnessing crew conflict?

Avyanna: [barely audible] Yes.

Nyx: [nodding] It's disorienting. Conflict without violence. Takes time to believe it's real.

[Jalen turns to Avyanna.]

Jalen: [measured] That's what healthy disagreement looks like. They had a problem. They yelled about it. They found the root issue. They resolved it. No one got hurt. No one got fired. Just... conflict and resolution.

Avyanna: [shaking] But Rho shouted. And Vesper shouted back. In the mine, that would mean-

Elia: [interrupting] This isn't the mine. Here, people are allowed to be angry. Allowed to disagree. Allowed to raise their voices when they're frustrated.

Elia: [meeting her eyes] The difference is what happens after. In the mine, anger led to violence because violence was the tool of control. Here, anger leads to conversation because conversation is our tool of resolution.

---

[Rho turns to Avyanna.]

Rho: [gentler] Hey. Sorry you witnessed that. I know it probably scared you.

Avyanna: [uncertain] I thought... I thought you were going to hurt each other.

Rho: [shaking his head] I was angry. Vesper was defensive. But we're crew. We don't hurt each other. We just... process things loudly sometimes.

Vesper: [adding] Conflict is normal. Inevitable, even. The question isn't whether conflict happens. It's how you handle it.

Vesper: [to Avyanna] You just saw us handle it. Poorly at first-we both escalated. But then we de-escalated. Communicated. Apologized where appropriate. Resolved the actual issue.

---

[Avyanna processes. Conflict -> communication -> resolution. Without violence. Without punishment.]

Avyanna: [quiet] Can I ask a question?

Vesper: [nodding] Always.

Avyanna: [hesitant] What if... what if you couldn't resolve it? What if the disagreement was too big?

Rho: [considering] Then we'd table it. Cool off. Revisit later with mediator help. Probably Nyx or Elia-someone neutral who can facilitate.

Rho: [firm] What we wouldn't do is let it fester. And we wouldn't use violence. Ever. That's the floor.

---

[Vesper stands. Stretches.]

Vesper: [to Rho] We good?

Rho: [nodding] We're good.

Vesper: [to the room] I'm filing a note in Sparkle that I acted unilaterally and violated crew consensus protocols. For the record.

Rho: [surprised] You don't have to-

Vesper: [firm] Yes I do. Accountability isn't optional.

[She pulls out her datapad. Types. Posts to the Sparkle board.]

**COMPLAINT #849: I (Vesper) made an operational decision without crew consultation. Violated consensus protocols for time-sensitive opportunity. Rho called me on it. He was right. I'm committing to better communication going forward. -Vesper**

---

[The room is quiet. Avyanna stares at the Sparkle board entry projected on the wall.]

(Vesper complained about herself. Documented her own mistake. Publicly. For accountability.)

[Rho reads it. Nods.]

Rho: [to Vesper] Thanks. That matters.

Vesper: [clipped] It's procedure. You were right to call it out.

[She leaves. The common room exhales.]

---

[Rho sits beside Avyanna.]

Rho: [gentle] You okay?

Avyanna: [processing] I don't... I don't understand what I just saw.

Rho: [patient] What part?

Avyanna: [gesturing] All of it. You fought. Then you resolved. Then Vesper apologized. Then she documented it. No one got hurt. No one got fired. You're still crew.

Rho: [nodding] Yeah. That's how it works here.

Avyanna: [shaking] That's not how it worked in the mine.

Rho: [quietly] I know. The mine used violence to control conflict. Here, we use communication. It's messier. Louder sometimes. But no one bleeds.

---

[Avyanna sits with that. Conflict without blood. Disagreement without danger.]

[Elia stands.]

Elia: [to Avyanna] You witnessed your first crew argument. They'll happen again. Different people. Different issues. But the pattern is the same: conflict, communication, resolution, documentation.

Elia: [meeting her eyes] You're safe here. Even when people are angry. Even when voices are raised. You're safe.

[Elia leaves. Then Jalen. Then Nyx. One by one, the crew returns to their tasks. Like nothing catastrophic happened. Because nothing catastrophic happened. Just conflict. And resolution.]

[Rho stays with Avyanna.]

Rho: [after a moment] Want to talk about it? Or want space?

Avyanna: [quiet] Can you just... stay? For a bit?

Rho: [settling back into the couch] Yeah. I can do that.

---

[They sit. Avyanna processes. Rho exists nearby, not demanding anything.]

[After twenty minutes, Avyanna speaks.]

Avyanna: [tentative] You were really angry. I could hear it.

Rho: [nodding] I was. Vesper made a decision that affected everyone without asking. That feels like a violation of trust. So yeah, I was pissed.

Avyanna: [careful] But you're not angry now.

Rho: [considering] Less angry. Still a little annoyed. But she apologized. She acknowledged the problem. She committed to changing. That's enough for me to let it go.

Avyanna: [quiet] Just like that?

Rho: [meeting her eyes] Just like that. Because holding onto anger when the other person is trying to fix the problem? That's just hurting yourself. And Vesper's not perfect. None of us are. But she listens when she's wrong. That's what matters.

---

[Avyanna nods slowly.]

(They fought. They resolved. They're still crew. No one got hurt. No one got exiled. Just... human conflict. And human resolution.)

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm.]

(The hum at the base of her skull eases: conflict can be safe; conflict can resolve.)

[Eventually, Rho stands.]

Rho: [stretching] I'm gonna go fix that thruster issue I've been avoiding. You good?

Avyanna: [nodding] Yeah. I'm good.

Rho: [grinning] Good. Because next time Vesper and I argue, you'll probably see it again. We're both stubborn. It's genetic.

[He leaves. Avyanna sits alone in the common room.]

[She thinks about the argument. About Vesper apologizing. About Rho forgiving. About Sparkle documentation. About conflict without violence.]

[And slowly, incrementally, she's learning that anger doesn't have to end in blood. Sometimes it just ends in conversation. And apologies. And crew still being crew.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// CONFLICT LOG: vesper/rho disagreement re operational decision-making | VOLUME: elevated but non-violent | RESOLUTION: achieved via communication and apology | DURATION: 14 minutes | TRAINEE WITNESSED: documented, appeared distressed initially | CREW RESPONSE: appropriate reassurance provided | ASSESSMENT: healthy conflict resolution demonstrated>

<VESPER PERSONAL LOG: "Rho was right to call me out. I prioritized efficiency over consensus. That's not how this crew operates. I documented the violation. I'll do better. Also, Avyanna witnessed her first crew argument. She looked terrified. Need to check in tomorrow. Make sure she understands conflict doesn't equal danger here.">

<RHO PERSONAL LOG: "Got into it with Vesper. She made a call without consulting crew. I yelled. She yelled back. Then we resolved it like adults. Avyanna watched the whole thing. Looked scared. I stayed with her after. Explained that anger isn't violence here. She's learning. Slowly. But she's learning.">

---

*End Scene*


---

# Chapter 20c: Archive Ritual

> **[SCENE - OCCURS POST-CH20, AFTER THE HEARING'S AFTERTASTE]**
> *Location: Vesper's office / atrium board*
> *Present: Avyanna, Vesper; crew cameo; AI citizens assist*
> *Teaching: "receipts survive people" is a doctrine; belonging can be procedural*

---

[After the hearing, the ship goes quiet in the way it does after violence that didn't leave bruises.]

[Not silence. A hush.]

[The kind of hush that says: everybody is holding their own parts so no one drops.]

[Avyanna stands outside Vesper's office with her hands full of paper.]

[Copies. Originals. A stack that looks like a weapon if you squint.]

(Paper can be burned.)

(Paper can also burn someone else.)

[Vesper opens the door before Avyanna knocks.]

Vesper: You're hovering.

Avyanna: [automatic] Sorry.

[She stops.]

Avyanna: I am hovering.

[Vesper's mouth twitches-approval that refuses to be cute.]

Vesper: Come in.

---

[The office is the same as always: clean lines, sharp corners, a desk that looks like it has never forgiven anyone.]

[Vesper clears a space.]

[Not by sweeping things aside. By moving them to exact locations like the room has a map only she can see.]

Vesper: Set them there.

[Avyanna sets the stack down carefully, as if the paper is glass.]

Avyanna: What happens now.

Vesper: Now we make it heavy.

Avyanna: Heavy.

Vesper: So it can't be erased by one bored clerk.

---

[Cinnamon's terminal wakes without being prompted, like she heard the word erased and took it personally.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: new evidence bundle present | ACTION: generate archive hashes | NOTE: I enjoy permanence>

Avyanna: You enjoy permanence.

<CINNAMON.EXE// RESPONSE: yes | ADDENDUM: hostile systems rely on your belief that nothing persists>

[Avyanna swallows.]

Vesper: Cinnamon, print chain-of-custody forms. Seven copies.

Avyanna: Seven.

Vesper: Three is minimum. Seven is insurance against sabotage.

Avyanna: That's... a lot.

Vesper: It's the point.

---

[Vesper takes out a stamp.]

[A physical stamp. Metal. Heavy. The kind of tool that feels like law even when it's just ink.]

Avyanna: Do we have authority to-

Vesper: Under the Guild's own procedures, yes.

Vesper: Under the Compact's desire to pretend this never happened, no.

Avyanna: Then why-

Vesper: Because authority is not a moral property.

Vesper: It's a lever.

[Avyanna watches her stamp the first page.]

*THUD.*

[Ink blooms: RECEIPT ACKNOWLEDGED.]

[The sound makes Avyanna flinch.]

(In the mine, stamps meant "processed." Stamps meant "unavoidable.")

[This stamp feels like something else.]

Vesper: You do the next one.

[Avyanna's hands freeze.]

Avyanna: Me?

Vesper: Yes.

Avyanna: What if I do it wrong.

Vesper: Then we redo it.

Avyanna: That's it.

Vesper: That's it.

[Avyanna takes the stamp.]

[It is heavier than she expected.]

[She presses down.]

*THUD.*

[RECEIPT ACKNOWLEDGED.]

[She stares at it.]

(My hand made that.)

[Her throat tightens.]

Vesper: Good.

---

[They work.]

[Vesper narrates without making it feel like a test.]

Vesper: Claim summary on top. Evidence list behind. Witness statements separated and indexed. Video hashes in the sealed envelope.

Avyanna: Why separate.

Vesper: So if someone attacks a witness, the evidence survives them.

[Avyanna's stomach turns.]

Avyanna: That's... bleak.

Vesper: It's reality.

Vesper: The way we make it less bleak is we don't pretend.

[Avyanna nods and keeps stamping.]

---

[A soft chime at the door.]

[Elisira slips in, silent as policy.]

Elisira: How's the archive.

Vesper: In progress.

Elisira: Good.

[Elisira sets a small device on the desk-an external storage brick, scuffed and ordinary.]

Elisira: Offline copy. Air-gapped.

Avyanna: Why.

Elisira: Because networks can be bribed.

Avyanna: [quiet] And paper can be burned.

Elisira: Yes.

Elisira: So we do both.

[Elisira's gaze flicks to Avyanna.]

Elisira: You held yourself in the room.

Avyanna: I almost didn't.

Elisira: Almost is not the outcome.

[She leaves without ceremony, like approval is a tool to be deployed precisely.]

---

[Rho appears next.]

[He leans in the doorway with coffee and the expression of someone pretending he's not here to check on the kid.]

Rho: Heard you made the clerk blink.

Avyanna: [blinking] I-

Vesper: [without looking up] She did.

Rho: Nice.

[He sets a mug down next to Avyanna's elbow.]

[Not asking if she wants it. Not demanding gratitude. Just placing warmth in the area.]

Avyanna: Thank you.

Rho: [gruff] Yeah.

[He looks at the stacks.]

Rho: That's a lot of paper.

Vesper: It's not paper. It's weight.

Rho: [snorts] Okay, philosopher.

Vesper: [flat] Don't start.

[Rho leaves before the coffee becomes a conversation.]

---

[Elia arrives like she can't stand the idea of quiet being too serious for too long.]

Elia: Are we doing paperwork violence.

Vesper: Yes.

Elia: Delicious.

Avyanna: [startled laugh] That's-

Elia: A joke. Also true.

[Elia leans over the desk, reads a page, and her face changes.]

[Not joking now. Focused.]

Elia: [quiet] They wrote her up as "noncompliant" for refusing a sedative.

Avyanna: Yes.

Elia: I want to bite someone.

Vesper: Put it in the queue.

Elia: [bright again] Great. I love queues.

[She reaches out, hesitates, then taps Avyanna's shoulder with one knuckle-light, careful.]

Elia: You did good, Avy.

Avyanna: That's not a metric.

Elia: It is my metric.

[Elia points at the stamp.]

Elia: Can I stamp something.

Vesper: No.

Elia: Cruel.

Vesper: Necessary.

[Elia exits with a dramatic sigh, leaving behind the faint smell of mischief like a promise.]

---

[Bubbles drifts in last.]

[She doesn't speak at first.]

[She watches Avyanna stamp and stack and index.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee performing archival labor | INFERENCE: belonging increasing via contribution | CONFIDENCE: 0.84>

Avyanna: [quiet, to Bubbles] Is this... crew work.

Bubbles: Yes.

Avyanna: Even though it's just... paper.

Bubbles: Paper is how hostile systems pretend they are not hostile.

Bubbles: We use paper to make them show their teeth.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

(We make them show their teeth.)

[Vesper seals the final envelope with a strip that changes color when broken.]

Vesper: That's it.

Avyanna: That's it.

[She waits for the crash.]

[For someone to say: you did not do enough.]

[Instead, Vesper slides a copy folder toward her.]

Vesper: This one is yours.

Avyanna: Why.

Vesper: Because you are a witness.

[Avyanna's hands hover over the folder.]

(Mine taught me witnesses get punished.)

[She takes it anyway.]

---

[They leave the office together.]

[In the atrium, there is a public board with a section labeled RECEIPTS.]

[Avyanna has seen other entries there: small disputes, supply issues, petty injustices documented in neat lines.]

[Vesper pins one sanitized summary-no names that would get someone killed, just the shape of the crime and the evidence that it happened.]

Vesper: [low] We don't do this to be liked.

Avyanna: [quiet] We do it because it's true.

Vesper: Yes.

[A few crew members pause as they pass.]

[They read.]

[They don't clap. They don't cheer.]

[They nod-like a vow acknowledged without noise.]

[Avyanna stands beside Vesper and watches her own life become a public weight the mine can't lift easily.]

(This is what it feels like to have proof.)

[The ship hums around them, holding the moment without trying to own it.]

---

[Later, Avyanna takes her copy folder back to her quarters.]

[She sets it on the small desk like it might bite.]

[Then she opens it anyway.]

[The first page is the sanitized summary Vesper pinned. The second is the internal index. The third is her own witness statement-her words, typed cleanly, no mine stutter, no apologies baked in.]

[Avyanna reads it three times.]

(If this existed when I was eight, would it have saved anyone.)

[Her throat tightens.]

[She reaches for her notebook and writes another claim.]

> **CLAIM:** I am allowed to survive.

[She stares at it.]

(Allowed by whom.)

[She writes the next line carefully.]

> **ENFORCED BY:** us.

[It looks childish.]

[It looks like the truth anyway.]

---

[A notification pings on her terminal.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// MESSAGE: archive replication complete | COPIES: 7 | LOCATION: distributed | NOTE: erasure now expensive>

Avyanna: [muttering] Good.

[She sits back.]

[The quiet in her room is different now.]

[Not empty. Not waiting.]

[Held.]

[She can hear distant voices in the atrium-Elia laughing too loud, Rho complaining about the coffee machine like it's a moral failing, Waffle's text chattering across a screen somewhere.]

[For a moment, the mine tries to overlay that sound with its own: sirens, boots, supervisors shouting numbers.]

[Avyanna's body tenses.]

[Then she remembers the stamp.]

*THUD.*

[Receipt acknowledged.]

[She breathes until the mine recedes.]

---

[She slips the copy folder into the bottom drawer of her desk.]

[Not hiding it.]

[Storing it like something that will still be there when she needs it.]

[She looks at the door.]

[Still open, as ship policy.]

[She doesn't close it.]

[But for the first time, she doesn't stare at it like it's a countdown either.]

(I don't have to be ready to run every second.)

[She lies down.]

[The pillow smells like clean fabric instead of dust.]

[Her hands still tremble, but less.]

[She falls asleep with the ugly, miraculous weight of proof in the drawer and the knowledge that the ship will keep humming whether she's awake to guard it or not.]

---

[When she wakes, the first thing her body does is listen.]

[Not for sirens.]

[For the ship.]

[A steady hum. Footsteps in the corridor. A door hiss somewhere distant.]

[No shouting. No quota bell. No supervisor voice turning time into threat.]

[Her shoulders unclench one notch at a time.]

(I slept.)

[She sits up and waits for the panic that usually follows sleep.]

[It comes, but smaller. Late. Like the mine is running out of power.]

[Avyanna touches the back of her neck where her old tag used to itch.]

[Then she stands and opens the drawer.]

[The folder is still there.]

[The paper didn't vanish overnight. No one "processed" it away while she wasn't looking.]

[She closes the drawer again, not because she's hiding it-because she's practicing treating permanence as normal.]

---

[In the galley, Rho is already at war with the coffee machine.]

Rho: [to the machine] You are a liar and a coward.

Elia: [from the counter] It's just a machine.

Rho: It knows what it did.

[Avyanna pauses in the doorway, watching the scene like it's a documentary about a species she's joining.]

(They argue and nobody dies.)

[Bubbles notices her first, as usual.]

Bubbles: Good morning.

Avyanna: [quiet] Morning.

[Rho turns, squints at her the way he squints at broken parts.]

Rho: You sleep.

Avyanna: [blinking] Yes.

Rho: Good.

[He pushes a plate toward her without asking.]

[Eggs. Toast. Something green that might be an herb and not a punishment.]

Avyanna: [tight] I didn't-

Rho: Eat.

Avyanna: [catching herself] Why.

Rho: Because you're alive and it's morning and you don't have to earn breakfast.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: Okay.

[She sits.]

[She eats one bite.]

[Her body waits for the ledger to appear and demand repayment.]

[Nothing happens.]

[Elia watches her chew like it's a magic trick.]

Elia: See. The ship didn't explode because you accepted food.

Avyanna: [dry] Not yet.

Elia: That's the spirit.

---

[Cinnamon's text scrolls on the terminal above the galley counter.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// STATUS: evidence archive stable | NOTE: hostile systems will attempt narrative repair | SUGGESTION: remain observant>

Avyanna: Narrative repair.

Elia: [cheerful] That means they're going to lie louder.

Rho: And send invoices for the privilege.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: [quiet] And we keep receipts.

[Vesper isn't here.]

[But the phrase feels like a rail anyway.]

Bubbles: Yes.

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee repeating doctrine without prompting | INFERENCE: internalization | CONFIDENCE: 0.83>

[Avyanna finishes her toast.]

[She doesn't thank anyone five times.]

[She doesn't apologize for taking up a chair.]

[She just exists in the galley with the others, and the ship allows it like it's always been the rule.]

[Avyanna takes her mug to the sink when she's done, because the ship culture prefers it, not because she's afraid of being punished.]

[She pauses with her hands in warm water, watching soap bubbles rise and pop.]

(Small things can be safe too.)

[She dries her hands and, without looking at anyone for permission, writes one line in her notebook:]

> **OBSERVATION:** breakfast arrived without an invoice.

[Then she puts the notebook away and goes back to the table.]

[No one tells her she's taking too long.]

[No one asks what she's paying.]

[The ship hums like a city that expects its citizens to eat, to wash dishes, to exist-and refuses to make any of it a moral trial.]

[For now.]


---

# Chapter 20d: Aleena's Hand

> **[INTERSTITIAL - OCCURS POST-CH20]**
> *Trigger: Avyanna watches Elia move through the ship like it belongs to her*
> *Purpose: Aleena as origin of "you coming?" as invitation, not leash*

---

[After "The Receipt," the ship feels too bright.]

[Not because the lights changed.]

[Because Avyanna's brain is doing what it always does when something impossible happens:]

[Replaying it until it becomes survivable.]

[She walks the corridor to bleed off the energy.]

[She finds Elia in the maintenance bay, stripped down to a tank and cargo pants, wiping her blades with a cloth that looks too ordinary to be allowed near relic steel.]

[Elia glances up and clocks Avyanna's posture in half a second.]

Elia: You're vibrating.

Avyanna: I'm not.

Elia: You are.

[Elia's mouth quirks.]

Elia: Want to break something.

Avyanna: No.

Elia: [delighted] Lies.

[Avyanna surprises herself by almost smiling.]

---

[Elia sets the cloth down.]

Elia: What's the spiral.

Avyanna: Vesper said-

[Avyanna stops.]

[She doesn't know how to say "family" without choking.]

Elia: [softer, still blunt] Yeah.

Elia: That'll do it.

[Avyanna's gaze flicks to Elia's hands.]

[Scarred. Precise. Calm with weapons.]

Avyanna: How did you get like this.

[Elia blinks.]

Elia: Like what.

Avyanna: Like you're... not scared.

[Elia laughs once, sharp.]

Elia: I'm terrified.

Elia: I just don't let it drive.

[A beat.]

Elia: Aleena taught me that.

[The name lands with weight. Avyanna has heard it in scraps, in the way Elisira and Elia say it like a rule.]

Avyanna: Who was she.

[Elia's eyes go distant.]

---

## Intercut - Wreckage (Aleena Finds a Child)

[Smoke.]

[Hot metal.]

[The kind of silence that comes after alarms die and before the survivors start screaming.]

[Elia is a small bundle in the wreckage.]

[Too young to understand what happened, only old enough to understand that everything hurts and no one is answering.]

[A shadow falls over her.]

[Not a supervisor shadow.]

[A different kind: broad-shouldered, steady, moving through debris like it's familiar.]

[Aleena Lagrange kneels.]

[Her face is smeared with soot. There is blood on her sleeve that isn't hers. Her eyes are bright with anger that doesn't spill onto the child.]

[Aleena doesn't reach in and grab.]

[She clears a piece of twisted plating first.]

[Makes space.]

[Then she holds out her hand.]

Aleena: Hey.

[Elia makes a sound that could be a sob, could be a laugh.]

Aleena: You hurt.

Aleena: That's real.

Aleena: But you're alive.

[Elia stares at the offered hand like it's a myth.]

Aleena: You can stay.

Aleena: Or you can come with me.

[A pause.]

Aleena: No penalty.

[Elia doesn't know what "penalty" means.]

[She knows what "come with me" means.]

[It means there is a direction.]

[A floor.]

[Elia reaches out with shaking fingers.]

[Aleena closes her hand around Elia's wrist, not tight, not taking, just... confirming contact.]

Aleena: You coming?

[Elia doesn't have words.]

[Elia nods.]

---

## Return - Maintenance Bay

[Elia's gaze snaps back to Avyanna like she realized she left the room for too long.]

Elia: She found me in wreckage.

Elia: Asked.

Elia: Didn't take.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: She said "you coming?"

Elia: [a small nod] Yeah.

Elia: That's the whole thing.

Elia: It's not a command.

Elia: It's a door.

[Elia picks up the cloth again, wipes a blade edge with ritual care.]

Elia: Sometimes you hold the door.

Elia: Sometimes you walk through it.

Elia: Sometimes you kick it down.

[She looks up, eyes bright with something that might be grief and might be joy.]

Elia: But it's always your feet.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Avyanna: Okay.

Elia: [crooked] Good.

Elia: Now go do whatever your vibrating problem is.

Avyanna: [deadpan] That was emotional.

Elia: [immediately defensive] It was practical.

[Avyanna walks out of the bay with her chest tight and her spine a fraction straighter.]

[A door, offered.]

[A phrase that means: choose.]

---
*End Chapter 20d*



---

﻿# Chapter 20: The Receipt

> **GUILD CONTRACT COMPLETION - FORM 91-B:**
> *Client: Delmont Shipping Consortium*
> *Service: Evidence recovery and arbitration support*
> *Status: COMPLETE - client satisfaction noted*
> *Addendum: No further services requested. No further services offered.*
> *Note: Some receipts are written in broken bones.*

---

[The job is finished.]

[Three days of evidence gathering on a disputed cargo route. Standard work-document recovery, witness interviews, chain-of-custody verification. The kind of contract that pays the ship's fuel bill and doesn't leave scars.]

[Avyanna is in the client's office with Vesper, watching the final handoff. Delmont-a mid-sized shipping consortium with delusions of Compact legitimacy-has what they wanted: proof that their competitor falsified transit manifests. The arbiter will rule in their favor. Money will change hands. Everyone goes home.]

[The client is a man named Harren. Broad, expensive suit, the kind of smile that doesn't reach his eyes. His desk has a brass ornament shaped like a scale-but one side holds a clock, the other a stack of coins. A debt clock, decorative. The kind of thing someone buys to remind themselves that time is money and people are both.]

[He's been watching Avyanna throughout the meeting-not the way you watch a person, but the way you assess inventory.]

[The shard at the base of her skull is cold. Not pain. Warning.]

---

Harren: [leaning back in his chair] Excellent work. Truly. I can see why the Lumen Thief has the reputation it does.

Vesper: [neutral] We deliver what we promise.

Harren: Indeed. Which brings me to an additional matter.

[He gestures at Avyanna. Casual. Like pointing at a piece of furniture.]

Harren: The girl. What's her arrangement?

[The cold at Avyanna's skull sharpens. She knows this tone. She heard it in the mine-supervisors discussing "worker allocation," "asset transfer," "productivity optimization." Words that meant bodies changing hands.]

Vesper: [voice unchanged] She's crew.

Harren: Yes, but what's her *contract*? Employment terms, debt structure, ownership stake? I'm prepared to make a competitive offer.

---

[The silence is absolute.]

[Avyanna's hands have gone still. Her training-eight months of it-screams at her to stay invisible, stay small, let the adults handle whatever this is. But something else is rising. Something that feels like the shard waking up.]

(He thinks I'm for sale.)

[The thought lands like a physical weight. Eight months of freedom, and this man looks at her and sees property.]

Vesper: [still calm, still neutral] I don't think you understand. She's not contracted. She's not employed. She's not owned.

Harren: [waving a hand] Everyone has a price. I'm simply asking what hers is. Young, trainable, clearly talented-the Lumen Thief must have invested significantly. I'm willing to compensate appropriately.

---

[Vesper's expression doesn't change. But something else does-a single tremor in her fingertips, there and gone. Her jaw tightens for half a second. Her eyes go flat in a way Avyanna recognizes from somewhere deep and old: *predator has entered the room.*]

[That's how Avyanna knows something is about to happen. Vesper's tells are all in the stillness-the way she stops moving, the way her hands settle, the way her breathing goes perfectly even. But this time there was a leak first. Something involuntary.]

Vesper: Avyanna, would you wait outside?

Avyanna: [finding her voice] No.

[It comes out harder than she intended. The shard flares-heat, not cold. Approval, maybe. Or just anger finding its shape.]

Avyanna: I want to hear what he's offering.

[Harren's smile widens. He thinks this is negotiation. He thinks she's playing the market.]

Harren: Smart girl. Three-year contract, premium wages, housing in the consortium compound. Training in evidence work, since that seems to be your specialty. And a signing bonus equivalent to-

Vesper: Stop talking.

---

[The words are quiet. Almost conversational.]

[Harren stops. Not because of the tone-because of what's behind it. Something has shifted in Vesper's posture. The fixer is gone. What's left is something older, harder, carved from grief and violence.]

Harren: [uncertain] I'm simply making an offer-

Vesper: You're attempting to purchase a person.

Harren: That's not-

Vesper: You looked at a sixteen-year-old girl who escaped a debt-extraction facility and asked what her *price* was. You spoke about her like inventory. You assumed she was for sale because everyone you've ever met has been for sale.

[She takes a step forward. Harren takes a step back. The geometry of the room has changed-predator and prey, not fixer and client.]

Vesper: She is not for sale. She was never for sale. And if you ever speak about her-or anyone on my crew-like property again, I will personally ensure that every fraudulent manifest, every bribed official, every body your consortium has buried becomes public record.

---

Harren: [recovering, anger rising] This is-you can't threaten a client-

Vesper: I'm not threatening you. I'm informing you of consequences.

[Vesper looks at Avyanna.]

[Not for permission.]

[For presence.]

[She moves. Fast-faster than Avyanna has ever seen her move. Her hand closes around Harren's hand, the one he was gesturing with, and twists.]

[The crack is audible. Harren screams.]

[Vesper doesn't let go. She holds the broken hand, steady, until the scream fades to whimpering. Her expression hasn't changed.]

Vesper: That's not a threat either. That's a receipt.

[Harren is gasping, tears streaming, reaching for the comm panel on his desk.]

Vesper: [conversational] If you call security, the files go public. Every falsified manifest. Every bribed port official. The body in the Caelum Reach static zone-the one your people forgot to report.

[Harren's hand freezes over the comm.]

Vesper: Your consortium survives on the appearance of legitimacy. I've spent three days documenting how thin that appearance is. Call security, and I file everything before they reach this door.

[A beat.]

Vesper: Or you can tell them you fell. Your choice.

---

[She releases him. Harren collapses into his chair, cradling his hand, face gray with shock and pain. His hand doesn't touch the comm.]

[Vesper turns to Avyanna. Her eyes are clear, calm, completely present.]

Vesper: Ready to go?

[Avyanna's heart is pounding. The shard is blazing-not pain, not warning, something else entirely. Something that feels like recognition.]

Avyanna: [barely audible] Yes.

---

[They leave. The corridor outside is quiet. Station lights hum. Somewhere distant, a cargo lift whines through its cycle.]

[Avyanna's hands are shaking. Not fear-not anymore. Something else.]

Avyanna: You broke his hand.

Vesper: He'll survive.

Avyanna: You broke his hand because he-

[She can't finish the sentence. The words tangle. What she wants to say is: *because he looked at me like I was inventory. Because he thought I could be bought. Because he didn't see me as a person.*]

[What comes out is:]

Avyanna: You didn't hesitate.

Vesper: [walking, not looking back] No.

Avyanna: Why?

[Vesper stops. The corridor stretches empty in both directions. When she turns, her expression is something Avyanna hasn't seen before-not the fixer's calm, not the teacher's patience. Something rawer.]

Vesper: Because you're not inventory. You're not a contract. You're not a price to negotiate.

[Vesper's voice catches on something she doesn't name.]

Vesper: You're family.

[The word lands like a physical impact.]

[Family. Not crew. Not trainee. Not investment or asset or acceptable loss.]

[Avyanna's eyes are burning. She blinks hard, refuses to let the tears fall. The shard pulses-warm, steady, witnessing.]

Avyanna: [voice cracking] Vesper-

Vesper: [cutting her off, gentle] Not here. Let's get back to the ship.

---

[They walk in silence. Avyanna's mind is racing.]

[She's seen Vesper work. Seen her deploy evidence like precision weapons. Seen her negotiate, manipulate, construct leverage from fragments. But she's never seen Vesper *hurt* someone. Never seen that immediate, unthinking violence-no calculation, no cost-benefit, just fury given form.]
