(She broke his hand. For me. Without hesitating. Without calculating.)

[The thought keeps circling.]

(There was no invoice. No ledger. No asking what it would cost her professionally. She just... acted.)

[And underneath that thought, another one. Smaller. More dangerous.]

(I didn't know kindness could look like that.)

---

[Back on the Lumen Thief, Vesper disappears into her quarters. Avyanna stands in the corridor, uncertain, the shard humming questions she can't quite articulate.]

[Bubbles drifts close. The drone's presence is familiar now-a small warmth, a silent offer of company.]

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee distressed | DURATION: ongoing | INFERENCE: processing | CONFIDENCE: 0.86 | RECOMMENDATION: space + time | NOTE: she'll figure it out. they always do.>

[Avyanna finds a quiet corner of the observation deck. Sits. Stares at the stars until her heartbeat slows.]

---

[Hours later, she can't sleep.]

[The ship's night cycle has settled into quiet hum. Most of the crew is in their bunks. Somewhere, Jalen is probably still awake-they often are-but the corridors are empty.]

[Avyanna wanders. The shard guides her, or she guides herself, or maybe there's no difference anymore.]

[She finds herself outside Vesper's quarters. The door is closed but not sealed. Light seeps from the crack-someone still awake.]

[She hesitates. Then knocks.]

---

Vesper: [from inside] Come in.

[The quarters are small but personal. Stacked datapads. A wall of preserved flowers-dried, pressed, labeled with dates and locations. A single photograph of a woman Avyanna doesn't recognize, older, smiling at something outside the frame.]

[Vesper is sitting at a console.]

[On the screen: a Guild interface, too clean to belong to Aurum. Aurum-coded headers anyway. A list of worker tags. A field that reads SUBMITTED BY: VESPER ROOK.]

[Avyanna recognizes the shape of paperwork that makes people disappear. Or keeps them from disappearing. She can't always tell the difference, but she knows the weapon when she sees it.]

Vesper: Can't sleep?

Avyanna: No.

[She stands in the doorway. Uncertain. The shard is quiet-present but not pushing.]

[Her eyes keep snapping back to the screen.]

Avyanna: What are you doing?

[Vesper's hands pause on the console.]

Vesper: [quietly] Paying late interest.

Avyanna: Can I ask you something?

Vesper: [still not looking up] You can always ask.

Avyanna: What does that mean?

---

[Vesper finally looks at her. Not annoyed. Not caught. Just tired.]

Vesper: It means they don't get to un-happen everyone we couldn't carry out.

[The cursor blinks. Vesper watches it like it owes her something.]

Vesper: I'm moving names into places Aurum can't scrub clean without effort. Spreading copies. Making the record heavy.

[She turns back to the console. The cursor blinks. The kind of blink that costs. That attaches her name to something she could have left alone.]

Vesper: They deserved better than we could give them. This is... late interest.

[Avyanna's throat tightens. She doesn't know what to do with this kind of violence-quiet, administrative, aimed at ghosts.]

Avyanna: Why did you break his hand? Risk the contract. Risk the consortium coming after the ship.

[A long silence.]

Vesper: [quietly] Because there are limits.

Avyanna: To what?

Vesper: To what I'll tolerate. To what I'll calculate around.

[She finally turns. Her face is tired-older than Avyanna usually sees it. The armor down, just for a moment.]

Vesper: I've done the math on a lot of terrible things. Weighed costs. Accepted trade-offs. That's what this job requires. But some things aren't trade-offs. Some things are just... lines.

[She looks at Avyanna directly.]

Vesper: You're a line.

---

[Avyanna's chest aches. The shard is warm-not hot, not warning. Just present. Holding space for whatever is happening.]

Avyanna: I don't understand.

Vesper: [almost smiling] You don't have to understand it. You just have to know it's true.

[She stands. Crosses to where Avyanna is standing. Stops close enough to touch, but doesn't.]

Vesper: When I was younger than you-not much, but younger-someone protected me. A woman I loved. She died doing it. I've spent a long time since then trying to figure out what that cost meant. Whether it was worth it. Whether I should let anyone close enough to pay that price again.

[Her voice is steady, but something underneath trembles.]

Vesper: What happened today wasn't calculation. It wasn't strategy. It was just... I saw someone try to buy you, and everything else stopped mattering.

---

[Avyanna's breath catches.]

[She's felt a lot of things in the months since the Lumen Thief pulled her from the mine. Gratitude. Confusion. The slow, uncertain growth of trust. But this is different. This is-]

(I don't know what this is.)

[The thought arrives without shape. Without name. Just a weight in her chest that feels like hunger, like debt, like something owed that she can't calculate.]

(I want to stay near her. Like proximity is oxygen.)

[Not the way she feels about Elia-the awe, the impossible standard. Not the way she feels about Elisira-the fear mixed with wanting to be seen. Not the crew-warmth she's building with Rho, Nyx, Jalen.]

[This is different. This is specific. This is something she doesn't have a word for.]

---

[Vesper is watching her. Patient. Waiting.]

Avyanna: [barely a whisper] Thank you.

Vesper: [soft] You don't have to thank me.

Avyanna: I know. I'm doing it anyway.

[Vesper's mouth curves. Almost a smile. Something sad underneath.]

Vesper: Get some sleep, Avyanna. We've got a long transit tomorrow.

[Avyanna nods. Turns to leave. Pauses at the door.]

Avyanna: Vesper?

Vesper: Yes?

Avyanna: The woman in the photograph. Is that her?

[A long silence.]

Vesper: Yes.

Avyanna: What was her name?

Vesper: [very quietly] Rowan.

[Avyanna nods. Leaves. Doesn't look back.]

---

[She doesn't go to her bunk.]

[Her feet take her to the galley because the galley is where the ship feels most like a city instead of a weapon.]

[Elia and Elisira are there, late-hour domestic: two mugs, a scattered deck of cards, the remains of an argument that didn't need to be finished.]

[Elia's chair is tipped back like she trusts gravity.]

[Elisira's is aligned with the table edge like she doesn't.]

[Avyanna stops in the doorway.]

[Exit count: two.]

[Her hands are shaking again.]

Elia: Hey.

Elisira: Sit.

[Elisira doesn't ask.]

[Avyanna sits anyway.]

[A mug slides toward her.]

[Warm. Bitter. Real.]

Avyanna: I can't sleep.

Elia: Yeah.

[No judgment.]

[Just the soft, brutal assumption that if she's here, it's because she's breaking.]

Avyanna: It's Vesper.

[The shard at the base of her skull is warm.]

[Not approval.]

[Witness.]

Elisira: Tell us what happened.

Elisira: Only what you saw.

---

[Avyanna does.]

[Harren's smile.]

[The word contract.]

[The way Vesper's fingers trembled once, like something escaped her control for half a second.]

[The way her eyes went flat.]

[The way she said stop talking.]

[The crack.]

[The scream.]

Avyanna: She didn't look at him when she moved.

[Avyanna's voice is too tight.]

Avyanna: She looked at me.

[Cooling beat.]

[Elia doesn't speak.]

[Elisira's mouth tightens like she hates that this is true.]

Avyanna: And then she called me family.

Avyanna: Like it was a fact.

Avyanna: Like it cost her nothing.

[A laugh tries to climb out of Avyanna's throat and turns into a cough.]

Avyanna: And then I found her in her quarters.

Avyanna: She was filing something.

Avyanna: With her name on it.

Avyanna: About Aurum.

Avyanna: About the workers.

Avyanna: Like she was paying for people who aren't even here.

[Avyanna's fingers lock around the mug.]

Avyanna: I don't know what to do with the feeling.

Avyanna: I keep wanting to make it even.

Avyanna: I keep trying to find the invoice.

---

Elia: [quiet] Like a debt you can't repay.

[Avyanna looks up.]

Avyanna: Yes.

Elisira: [careful] That's not debt.

Elisira: That's your instincts trying to put a price tag on safety.

[Avyanna flinches, because she's right.]

Elia: Vesper doesn't do performative.

Elia: She does receipts.

Elia: She does lines.

[Elia turns her cup between her palms.]

Elia: And she doesn't let people in easily.

Elia: You're not imagining that.

Elisira: She's less guarded around you.

[Avyanna freezes.]

Avyanna: You noticed.

Elisira: You're loud.

[It's not a joke.]

[It's an assessment.]

Elisira: She stays in rooms longer.

Elisira: She corrects you less.

Elisira: She lets herself be seen and then pretends she didn't.

---

Avyanna: So what is this?

[Her voice scrapes.]

Avyanna: Is it love?

Avyanna: Or is it just...

(Safety.)

(Hunger.)

(Kennel math trying to eat something clean.)

Elia: You don't have to decide that tonight.

Elisira: What you do decide is how you behave.

Elisira: Vesper is older.

Elisira: You're sixteen.

Elisira: She will not cross that line.

Elisira: Not because she doesn't care.

Elisira: Because she refuses to be the kind of adult who takes.

[Avyanna swallows.]

Elia: That doesn't make your wanting wrong.

Elia: It makes it yours to manage.

Elisira: If you ever choose to tell her anything, you do it clean.

Elisira: Direct.

Elisira: Respectful.

Elisira: Ask her boundaries.

Elisira: Then follow them.

Elia: And don't corner her into managing your feelings.

[Cooling beat.]

[Avyanna nods, because the mine taught her what corners do to people.]

---

Elisira: Also.

[She glances at Elia.]

[Old. Comfortable. Entire arguments living in a look.]

Elisira: Our relationship is not a good model for yours.

Avyanna: [blinks] Why?

Elia: Because we didn't do normal.

Elia: We did gravity.

Elisira: I was eleven.

Elia: I was twelve.

Elisira: I decided she was mine.

Elisira: Not as property.

Elisira: As priority.

[Avyanna's chest tightens at the word mine, then loosens at the correction.]

Elia: And I went: yeah. Okay.

[Elia says it like it's embarrassing how simple it was.]

Elia: We've been together since.

Elisira: So we can't teach you romance.

Elisira: We can teach you support.

Elisira: And floors.

---

[Avyanna stares at them.]

[At the fact that they can say mine and mean safety, not ownership.]

Avyanna: You're my big sisters.

[Both of them go still.]

[Not offended.]

[Just. caught.]

Elia: Yeah.

Elisira: Yes.

[A breath.]

Elia: That means we're going to be annoying forever.

[Avyanna makes a sound that might be a laugh.]

[Cooling beat.]

[The mine never promised forever.]

---

[She leans forward without thinking and hugs them both.]

[Elia goes stiff like she's defusing something wrong.]

[Elisira's hands hover like she's waiting for instructions.]

Elia: [muffled] Okay.

Elia: Yep.

Elia: This is fine.

Elisira: [also muffled] Okay.

[Then Elisira's grip tightens anyway.]

[Then Elia's does too.]

[Warm.]

[Awkward.]

[Real.]

---

Elia: You're not sleeping alone tonight.

[Avyanna pulls back fast.]

Avyanna: I can-

Elisira: No.

[One syllable.]

[A door closing.]

Elisira: You can sleep with us.

Elisira: Or you can sleep on our floor.

Elisira: But you are not going back to your bunk to spiral in silence.

[Avyanna's throat burns.]

Avyanna: I don't want to be a problem.

Elia: You're not a problem.

Elia: You're a person having a night.

Elia: That's allowed here.

---

[Avyanna follows them to their quarters like she's learning a new law of physics.]

[She counts exits anyway.]

[Old reflex.]

[In the dark, she lies between two steady bodies and pretends she isn't shaking.]

[Her tears come without permission.]

[No one tells her to stop.]

[No one asks what it'll cost.]

(This is what love looks like.)

[She falls asleep before the thought can become dangerous.]

---

<BUBBLES// OBSERVATION: trainee in Elia+Elisira quarters | DURATION: 47 minutes | INFERENCE: safety-seeking | CONFIDENCE: 0.88 | NOTE: no intervention recommended.>

---

## Coda - Elia's Philosophy

[0300. The bridge is quiet.]

[Elia sits in the pilot's chair-not piloting, just thinking. The stars are cold and numerous through the viewport. The ship hums beneath her, familiar as a heartbeat.]

[She's been reviewing reports. Vesper's incident summary. The contract that won't be renewed. The consortium that will almost certainly try something petty and legal in retaliation.]

[None of that matters.]

[What matters is the girl asleep in Elia and Elisira's quarters, breathing like the ship isn't a trap.]

---

[Elia doesn't remember her birth parents. She was two when the ship exploded-too young to remember faces, names, anything real. The only parent she knows is Aleena Lagrange, who pulled her from wreckage and raised her on a ship called The Kaitlyn.]

[Aleena taught her freedom. Taught her that power was a trap. Taught her that the moment you accepted a crown, you became what the crown wanted you to be.]

[At four years old, Elia built Bubbles. A small maintenance drone that became a person. Her first act of creation, and it was: *I want to make something that thinks for itself. Something that isn't a tool.*]

[She didn't know what that meant at the time. She knows now.]

---

[The Lumen Thief exists because Elia wanted a ship that wasn't a hierarchy. AI citizens with full personhood. Crew with full agency. No captain, no ranks, no chains of command that turned people into functions.]

[It's harder than hierarchy. It requires trust, confrontation, constant negotiation. People argue. People disagree. People make choices Elia wouldn't make, and she has to live with the consequences.]

[But they're *people*. Not assets. Not inventory. Not acceptable losses.]

---

[Vesper broke a man's hand today.]

[Elia should probably be concerned about that. The professional calculus says: violence has costs, clients have memories, retaliation is likely. A smarter captain-if she were a captain, which she isn't-would have a conversation about proportionality and professional boundaries.]

[But Vesper didn't act as a fixer. She acted as family. And family doesn't calculate whether a child is worth protecting.]

---

[Avyanna is sixteen. Still young enough to be shaped. Still carrying the mine inside her-the silence, the compliance, the bone-deep belief that she's inventory instead of person.]

[Elia watches that belief erode, day by day. Watches Avyanna start to trust. Start to argue. Start to want things without immediately calculating what they'll cost.]

[It's slow work. Building floors always is.]

---

[Aleena left, eventually. Disbanded the crew, took The Kaitlyn beyond the Rim, disappeared into whatever mission she couldn't bring herself to explain.]

[Elia understands now. Some fights are too big to share. Some weights you carry alone because putting them on other people would break them.]

[But Elia didn't leave. She built her own ship. Found her own crew. Started the work again-different this time, her own way, with AI citizens who challenged her assumptions and humans who refused to let her become what she was fighting.]

---

[The shard in Avyanna's skull is waking up. Elia can see it-the way the girl moves differently, senses things she shouldn't, reacts to stimuli the rest of them can't perceive.]

[Something ancient is taking interest. Something that chose Avyanna for reasons none of them understand yet.]

[Elia doesn't know if that's good or bad. She just knows it's happening, and her job is to make sure the girl underneath the shard stays *a girl*-not a vessel, not a weapon, not a tool for powers that don't care about personhood.]

---

[Floors, not thrones.]

[The philosophy is simple. The execution is everything.]

[Build infrastructure that makes people's lives better. Don't hoard power. Don't accept titles that turn you into something you're not. Do the work even when no one's watching, especially when no one's watching, because the work is the point.]

[Elia hates being revered. People look at her like she's something special-a legend, a blade, a force of nature. They don't see the scared two-year-old pulled from wreckage. They don't see the four-year-old talking to a drone like it was a person. They don't see the woman who still doesn't know what she's doing, just that she has to keep doing it.]

[Competence creates reverence like gravity. All you can do is refuse the crowns.]

---

[The stars turn. The ship hums. Somewhere in the crew quarters, a sixteen-year-old girl is learning what it means to be valued without an invoice.]

[That's the work. That's what the ship is for.]

[Elia leans back in the chair and closes her eyes.]

[Tomorrow, there will be problems. Consortium retaliation. Evidence to build. Routes to fly. The shard waking up, the galaxy noticing, the weight of everything they're carrying.]

[But tonight, the girl is safe. The crew is intact. The floors are holding.]

[That's enough. That's always enough.]

---

## Part II - Proportional Response

[Elia is still in the pilot's chair when the ship changes posture.]

[Not an alarm. The Lumen Thief doesn't scream unless it wants someone else to panic.]

[It's the deck vibration-subtle shift in frequency. The hull flexing its spine.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: three fast contacts on intercept | RANGE: close | VECTOR: bracketing | INFERENCE: hostile approach | CONFIDENCE: 0.94>

[Elia's eyes open.]

[She's already moving before she finishes reading the telemetry.]

---

[In Elia and Elisira's quarters, Avyanna wakes to pressure change.]

[The shard at the base of her skull goes cold.]

(Warning.)

[She's out of the blankets before her brain catches up. Elia and Elisira are already gone-the bed empty, the room dim, the ship humming a tone she's learning to recognize as *prepare*.]

Vesper: [over comms] Avyanna. Observation deck. Now.

[It isn't comfort.]

[It's a coordinate.]

[Avyanna moves.]

---

[The observation deck is dim, glass and stars and the faint reflection of her face-pale, sharp, alive.]

[Outside: three craft on converging vectors, ugly angles, weapon ports like mouths. Corporate-clean paint over mercenary bones.]

[The crew is already there.]

[Elia stands at the rail, barefoot, expression mild. Not angry. Interested.]

[Elisira beside her, spine straight, pistol already at her hip like it grew there.]

[Nyx half a step back, eyes unfocused-listening to geometry that isn't visible.]

[Rho's shoulders are loose in the way they get when he's about to make something stop existing.]

[Vesper arrives last, datapad in hand, face unreadable.]

[Avyanna stops at the edge of the deck. Her hands are shaking. Exit count: two.]

[The sight of them together hits her like a physical weight.]

(So this is what "mythical" looks like in real life.)

(It looks casual.)

---

[An open channel blooms across the display.]

Unknown Voice: Lumen Thief. Registry 7742-KAEL. Heave to. Contract enforcement. You are in possession of disputed assets. Submit to inspection and surrender the minor.

[The word *minor* lands like a chain snapping shut.]

[Mine-memory surges: "asset transfer." "Worker allocation." "Inventory reconciliation."]

(They're saying it like it's normal.)

[The shard goes cold-hot. Not fear. Attention.]

Elia: [bright, conversational] Hi.

[A beat.]

Elia: No.

Unknown Voice: This is lawful retrieval under provisional claim-

Elia: [still pleasant] No.

Elisira: [flat, to the room] They'll board.

Rho: [mild] Let them.

Avyanna: [hoarse] *Let* them?

Vesper: [without looking at her] Easier to document when they commit the crime on your floor.

---

[The hostile craft spread into bracketing positions.]

[The lead ship fires a suppressor field-blue-white ripple meant to clamp drives and force compliance.]

[The ripple hits the Thief's defensive envelope and dies like it ran into a law of physics.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: suppression field impact | RESULT: neutralized | INFERENCE: hostile tech outclassed | CONFIDENCE: 0.93>

Unknown Voice: What-?

Elia: [pleasant] Try again.

[They do.]

[It dies again.]

[Elia looks bored.]

Nyx: [soft] They'll change tactics.

Vesper: They already did.

---

[Mag grapples spit from the second craft-thin black lines with teeth.]

[They bite the Thief's hull with a sound Avyanna feels in her bones.]

(Boarding.)

[Her throat tightens. Her hands curl around the rail until her knuckles hurt.]

[Elia finally straightens. Not urgent. Not angry. Just... decided.]

Elia: Cinnamon. Classification.

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: hostile comm content | KEY PHRASE: "surrender the minor" | INFERENCE: attempted trafficking / unlawful seizure | CONFIDENCE: 0.96>

Elia: Rules?

Elisira: [immediate] No trafficking.

Rho: No prisoners.

Nyx: [quiet] Consent violated.

[Vesper doesn't speak for a beat.]

[When she does, it's low and flat.]

Vesper: Lethal authorized.

---

[Avyanna's breath catches.]

(They're going to kill them.)

[Her shard warms-not approval. Attention. Like something inside her is watching to learn what a "line" looks like.]

[The hull shudders.]

[Cutting torches bite.]

[The ship does not panic.]

[The ship reorganizes.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: internal bulkheads cycling | INFERENCE: compartmentalization | CONFIDENCE: 0.91>

[Reroutes. Seals. Turns itself into a maze with teeth.]

---

[Security feed tiles bloom-tight angles, clean capture.]

[Armored boarders drop through a breach into a service corridor. Four of them. They move like professionals.]

[They also move like they believe the Thief is just a ship.]

[A bulkhead slides shut behind them.]

[Their retreat disappears.]

[One turns, startled.]

[Another raises a rifle.]

[Rho steps into frame from a side hatch like the corridor grew a wall and decided to swing it.]

Rho: Hey.

---

[Gunfire flashes.]

[The rounds don't find him.]

Nyx: [soft, on the deck] Locality.

[On the feed, a bullet kisses the wall instead of flesh. Trajectory bent. Not dramatic-just enough.]

[Rho doesn't flinch.]

[He moves once.]

[A short throw-something palm-sized, matte black.]

[A dull pressure pulse.]

[The boarders stagger, balance disrupted, vision rattled.]

[Then Rho closes distance.]

[Not fast like athletic. Fast like gravity accepting an invitation.]

[He takes one rifle by the barrel and folds it. The weapon screams. The boarder drops, wrist angles wrong.]

[A second tries a sidearm.]

[Rho's hand snaps out-catches the weapon mid-draw, redirects, and the boarder's own momentum carries them into the wall. Hard. Final.]

[He pivots. A third boarder is bringing a rifle up.]

[Rho doesn't block. He steps *into* the line, takes the muzzle past his shoulder, and drives an elbow into the helmet visor with controlled, demolition-precise force.]

[The visor cracks. The head behind it stops.]

[The fourth boarder turns to run.]

[Rho pulls something from his belt-small, shaped-and throws underhanded. It sticks to the retreating figure's back armor.]

[A muffled *whump*. Shaped charge. No shrapnel. Just force, directed inward.]

[The boarder drops.]

[Four bodies. Seven seconds.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: hostile team A life signs ceased | INFERENCE: terminated | CONFIDENCE: 0.97>

---

[Avyanna's hands are numb on the rail.]

(That was maintenance.)

(He killed them like he was clearing debris.)

[Another feed tile.]

[The second team-three boarders-hits a junction and runs straight into Elisira.]

[She's standing there like the corridor was built for this exact moment. Pistol up. One-handed. No tremor.]

[The lead boarder raises a rifle.]

[Elisira fires first.]

[Once. The round hits the rifle's receiver. The weapon locks.]

[Twice. Center mass. The boarder folds.]

[The second one tries to flank. Elisira doesn't turn-she steps backward, eyes still forward, and the flanking boarder runs into a doorframe that wasn't cycling until she wanted it to.]

[The door closes. On them.]

[A scream. Cut short.]

[The third boarder freezes.]

Elisira: [quiet, visible on the feed] Sit.

[They sit. Instinctively. Like their spine understood something their brain hadn't processed yet.]

[Elisira walks forward. Unhurried. Places the pistol against the kneeling boarder's visor.]

[Fires once.]

[Clean. Surgical. The kind of placement that says *I chose where this goes*.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: hostile team B life signs ceased | INFERENCE: terminated | CONFIDENCE: 0.98>

---

[Avyanna's stomach turns.]

(Elisira didn't ask.)

(She made the universe agree.)

[A new sound-close.]

[Metal scraping behind the observation deck wall.]

[Someone cutting from the wrong side.]

(They're coming here.)

(For me.)

[Mine reflex tries to fold her in half.]

[Vesper's posture shifts. Not toward the breach. Toward Avyanna. She moves so her body is between Avyanna and the wall.]

[It's small.]

[It is everything.]

---

[The wall blooms heat.]

[A slit. A widening gap. A rifle barrel pushes through.]

[Elia crosses the deck without running.]

[Bare feet silent on the plating.]

[She catches the rifle barrel with one hand.]

[The weapon bucks. Muzzle flash blooms.]

[The shot goes nowhere important.]

Elia: [conversational] You came onto my ship to steal a kid.

[She yanks.]

[A boarder is dragged halfway through the breach, scrambling for balance.]

[Elia's other hand comes up-not a fist, just fingers, precise and contemptuous-and strikes the visor hinge.]

[The visor pops. The face underneath is young, panicked, suddenly very aware of what he's looking at.]

[Elia doesn't give him time to process.]

[She twists the rifle out of his grip-fluid, like disarming is a reflex she doesn't need to think about-and drives the stock into his throat.]

[He drops.]

[A second boarder is pushing through the breach behind him. Elia doesn't retreat. She steps *forward*, into the gap, and the confined space becomes her geometry.]

[The boarder's rifle is useless-no room to aim. He tries a knife.]

[Elia's hand closes on his wrist. Twists. The knife clatters.]

[She pulls him through the breach and throws him-not hard, just far enough-into the observation deck railing.]

[He hits. Bounces. Lands wrong.]

[Elia follows. Three steps. Her foot catches his rising arm and pins it. Her other foot comes down on his throat.]

[Not a stomp. A placement. Controlled weight, increasing pressure.]

[The boarder's hands scrabble at her ankle. His face goes red, then purple.]

[Elia watches him with mild interest. Like she's timing something.]

[Then she increases pressure. Once.]

[The sound is wrong. Final.]

[She steps off like he was never there.]

---

[Behind her, the breach edge is glowing. A third boarder is trying to force through.]

[Elia doesn't bother turning around.]

[She places her palm against the wall beside the breach. Not touching the cut-just... near it.]

[For a fraction of a second, the air tastes like ozone and cold metal.]

[The deck lights flicker.]

[The shard in Avyanna's skull answers-warm pressure, like recognition.]

Elia: [very quiet] No.

[The metal *folds*.]

[Not melting. Not exploding.]

[Suturing-reality remembering it was supposed to be whole.]

[The breach seals. The boarder on the other side slams into solid plating with a dull, stupid thud.]

Nyx: [exhaling, almost a laugh] Throughput.

Elisira: [dry, arriving from the corridor] Show-off.

Elia: [without looking back] I'm being polite.

---

[The remaining hostiles on the external craft try to disengage.]

Rho: [over comm] Cutting their hooks.

[Sharp metallic snaps. Grapples severed.]

[The hostile craft drift free.]

[Not fast enough.]

[Bubbles' drone wing latches onto their hulls like hands closing on collars.]

Elia: They live?

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: hostile craft crew life signs present | COUNT: 5 | INFERENCE: attempting retreat | CONFIDENCE: 0.91>

Vesper: They said "surrender the minor."

[The bridge goes still.]

Elisira: No trafficking.

Rho: No exceptions.

Elia: [pleasant] Okay.

---

[The Thief's point-defense hums once.]

[It's not flashy.]

[It's final.]

[On the external feed, the hostile craft go dark-systems dead, then life signs wink out one by one as the ships tumble.]

[No fireball. No hero shot.]

[Just silence.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: hostile craft crews life signs ceased | INFERENCE: terminated | CONFIDENCE: 0.97>

---

[Avyanna makes a small sound she doesn't recognize.]

[Not grief. Not relief.]

[Something like her nervous system trying to find a new shape.]

[Elia turns to her.]

Elia: You okay?

[Avyanna is crying without noticing.]

Avyanna: They said-

[Her voice breaks.]

Avyanna: They said *surrender the minor*.

[Elia steps closer-not into her space, just close enough that Avyanna can feel presence like an anchor.]

Elia: They don't get to name you.

[Vesper's gaze flicks to Avyanna. Something in her face tightens-pain, then mask.]

[Avyanna sees it.]

[And that seeing hits harder than the killing.]

(That's the thing.)

(The way she reacted like it hurt her too.)

[The shard warms, steady.]

---

[Afterward, there's no victory. There's cleanup.]

[There's documentation.]

[There's salvage.]

[The pirate craft are towed into a dead berth and stripped with the calm efficiency of people who have done this before.]

[Hull plates peeled. Core components tagged. Weapon housings broken down into parts that stop being weapons the moment they become inventory.]

[Rho watches the salvage manifest and says, almost to himself: turning their ships into clinic parts feels correct.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: salvage proceeds routed | DESTINATION: humanitarian escrow | INFERENCE: "proportional response" doctrine applied | CONFIDENCE: 0.88>

[Avyanna watches the parts manifest populate.]

[It feels like watching bodies become receipts.]

[She isn't sure how she feels about that.]

[She isn't sure she's allowed to.]

---

[Six hours later, they dock at Helder Weir again.]

[Not quietly. Not hiding.]

[Elia stays on the ship. She doesn't need to walk into a building to be present in the room.]

[Vesper and Elisira go in person. Nyx comes too, because geometry likes witnesses.]

[Avyanna is told to remain aboard.]

[She hates it.]

[She obeys anyway.]

[It isn't mine-obedience. It's floor-obedience. Boundary as care.]

---

[The submission packet hits the Guild net first.]

[Then the Compact regulatory boards.]

[Then every public forum that pretends it isn't a court.]

[Chain-of-custody video. Audio. Hostile comm logs. The words "surrender the minor" timestamped, signed, undeniable.]

[Then the second packet drops.]

[Harren's own.]

[Bribed officials. Falsified manifests. Debt-clock leverage games. The quiet trafficking inquiries buried in "asset acquisition" memos.]

[Vesper's receipts are not dramatic.]

[They are lethal in the way gravity is lethal.]

---

[Within hours, Delmont's consortium begins to distance itself.]

[Statements. Disavowals. Emergency board sessions.]

[Harren is "placed on leave pending investigation." His access revoked. His name quietly scrubbed from the website like it never belonged there.]

[Avyanna watches it unfold through ship feeds.]

(They're eating him to save themselves.)

(That's what predators do when one of them bleeds.)

---

[The next morning, Harren is found dead.]

[Not on camera in a cinematic way.]

[In a private suite. Alone, officially. A heart that stopped at a convenient time. A death certificate that reads like a shrug.]

[And then-because the Lumen Thief is the Lumen Thief-Vesper sends the third packet.]

[Not public. Direct.]

[To Delmont's board. To the Guild arbiter. To the two regulators who matter.]

[A short clip.]

[Harren's final minutes.]

[Not a confession. Not a plea. Just him on a call, voice breaking, realizing he has been cut loose.]

[A door opens behind him.]

[Someone steps in.]

[A hand touches his shoulder-gentle.]

[Then the feed glitches-signal jam.]

[Then comes back with Harren on the floor, eyes open, not breathing.]

[No face shown. No name spoken.]

[Just enough to prove one thing:]

[He didn't die of bad luck.]

[He died because his own ecosystem decided he was an infection.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: "final moments" packet delivered | INFERENCE: deterrence maximized | CONFIDENCE: 0.82>

---

[Delmont's next message is immediate.]

[A "goodwill" offer.]

[Harren's estate. Harren's personal accounts. Harren's holdings transferred into escrow "pending resolution," which is what cowards call tribute.]

[They don't want to be in the Thief's bad books.]

[They don't want the fourth packet.]

---

[Elia reads the message in the galley, mug in hand.]

[Elisira beside her, perfectly composed, like she didn't just help end a man socially and then watch the universe finish the job.]

Elia: That seems fair.

Rho: [dry] Proportional.

Nyx: [quiet] The system corrected itself.

Vesper: [flat] The system protected itself.

[She looks up at Avyanna, who has been standing in the doorway too long.]

Vesper: You should be asleep.

Avyanna: I couldn't.

---

[Vesper's gaze holds her for a half-second. Not soft. Not indulgent. Present.]

Vesper: Walk with me.

---

[They end up in the meditation chamber where Nyx taught her about the Lattice.]

[Same candles. Same cushions. Different weight.]

Vesper: [settling onto a cushion] Ask.

Avyanna: [still standing] You knew they were coming.

Vesper: [mild] Yes.

Avyanna: Before they launched. Before they even got clearance.

Vesper: Before Harren finished his sentence in that office.

[Avyanna's throat tightens.]

Avyanna: How?

Vesper: Because I've been doing this for fifteen years. Because men like Harren are predictable. Because the Lumen Thief doesn't walk into situations without mapping the exits first.

[She gestures for Avyanna to sit. Avyanna does, uncertain.]

Vesper: We had three response protocols loaded before we left the station. Diplomatic, legal, and lethal. The moment he said *arrangement*, I moved us from diplomatic to legal. The moment he said *contract*, I moved us to lethal-ready.

Avyanna: [quiet] And breaking his hand?

Vesper: [meeting her eyes] That was the escalation trigger. Designed to provoke exactly what happened.

---

[Avyanna stares at her.]

[Something cold moves through her chest.]

Avyanna: You wanted them to attack.

Vesper: I wanted them to commit. There's a difference.

[She leans forward, elbows on knees, the teaching posture Avyanna has learned to recognize.]

Vesper: Harren was always going to retaliate. The only question was how and when. A broken hand in private? He could file complaints, make accusations, drag us through legal channels for years. Cost us contracts, reputation, time.

[She taps one finger against her knee.]

Vesper: But a trafficking attempt? Documented? With hostile comm logs saying *surrender the minor*?

[She lets the silence do the math.]

Vesper: That's not legal terrain. That's a line the Compact, the Guild, and every independent consortium agrees on. Cross it, and the ecosystem eats you.

Avyanna: So you baited them.

Vesper: I created conditions where their worst impulses became visible. The baiting was just... permission.

---

[Avyanna is silent for a long moment.]

[The candle flames flicker. The shard at the base of her skull hums-not warning, not approval. Processing.]

Avyanna: Nyx taught me about locality. About how Primordial magic asks instead of taking. About throughput limits and consent.

Vesper: [nodding slowly] And?

Avyanna: This feels like the opposite. Like you took from them without asking.

[Vesper's mouth curves. Not quite a smile.]

Vesper: What do you think?

---

[Avyanna considers.]

[The mine taught her that power doesn't ask permission. The Garden taught her that sustainable systems do.]

[But the mine also taught her that some people only understand force. And the Garden showed her that even the Sutured Houses have safety signs-boundaries enforced, not just suggested.]

Avyanna: [slowly] They violated consent first. They tried to take me without asking. So... the locality rules changed?

Vesper: Close.

Avyanna: [frowning] But there has to be a limit. Otherwise anyone can justify anything by saying "they started it."

Vesper: [approving] Better.

[She stands. Crosses to the candle arrangement. Picks up two-the same ones Nyx used for the demonstration.]

Vesper: The Primordial constraint isn't "never harm." It's "don't externalize costs onto people who didn't consent." When someone attacks you, they've consented to the geometry of violence. They've entered a space where force answers force.

[She sets the candles down.]

Vesper: The question isn't whether we were allowed to kill them. The question is whether our response created new harm to people who weren't part of the conflict.

Avyanna: [thinking] The salvage. The parts going to humanitarian escrow.

Vesper: Exactly. The ships were already built-that cost was already paid. We turned them into something that serves instead of extracts.

Avyanna: And Harren's estate?

Vesper: [dry] Is funding three rim clinics and a worker advocacy fund. The money was already extracted from somewhere. We're routing it back.

---

[Avyanna sits with that.]

[The shard pulses. Warm now. Something clicking into place.]

Avyanna: Proportional response isn't about matching force. It's about completing a loop.

Vesper: [quiet] Keep going.

Avyanna: They tried to extract me. You extracted their resources. But instead of hoarding them, you're... returning them to the system they stole from.

Vesper: The Thief's version of the conservation law. Extraction creates debt. Payment completes the transaction.

Avyanna: [almost to herself] Receipts.

Vesper: [nodding] Receipts.

---

[They sit in silence for a while.]

[The candles flicker. The ship hums. Somewhere, Jalen is running diagnostics on systems that don't need diagnosing, because motion is how they grieve.]

Avyanna: Vesper?

Vesper: Yes?

Avyanna: Did you know they'd kill him? Harren?

[A long pause.]

Vesper: [carefully] I knew his ecosystem would react. The specific mechanism... that was their choice.

Avyanna: You have the video.

Vesper: Elisira has the video.

Avyanna: [pressing] You planned for it.

Vesper: [meeting her eyes] I planned for every outcome. Including ones where he survived. Including ones where we had to run. Including ones where people I love got hurt.

[The candle nearest Avyanna gutters, steadies.]

Vesper: Planning isn't the same as wanting. I didn't want him dead. I wanted you safe. His death was... incidental.

---

[Avyanna thinks about that word. *Incidental.* Like Harren was a byproduct, not a target.]

[It should feel wrong. It doesn't feel wrong.]

[She isn't sure what that says about her.]

Avyanna: The Garden had safety signs. "Do not run hot." "Report discomfort immediately."

Vesper: [nodding] Rules even for the ethical practitioners.

Avyanna: What are the rules here? For proportional response?

[Vesper considers.]

Vesper: Don't create orphans if you can avoid it. Don't destroy infrastructure people depend on. Don't let rage make you sloppy. Complete the loop-don't just take, redirect.

[She pauses.]

Vesper: And document everything. Because memory is the first thing power tries to erase.

---

[Avyanna's chest aches.]

[Not grief. Not quite. Something more complicated-the weight of learning a new language for violence she's always known existed.]

Avyanna: I don't know how to feel about it. Any of it.

Vesper: [quiet] Good.

Avyanna: [surprised] Good?

Vesper: The moment you stop being uncomfortable with lethal force is the moment you become what we're fighting. Discomfort is the constraint. It's what keeps the loop from becoming extraction.

[She stands. Offers Avyanna a hand up.]

Vesper: You don't have to decide tonight. Or this week. Or this year. Just keep noticing where it feels wrong.

[Avyanna takes the hand. Lets herself be pulled to her feet.]

Avyanna: And if it stops feeling wrong?

Vesper: [almost smiling] Then you come talk to me. Or Nyx. Or anyone on this ship. That's what floors are for.

---

[Later, in her bunk, Avyanna stares at her hands.]

[They're still shaking.]

(They killed them all.)

(They didn't hesitate.)

(And then they turned the ships into parts.)

(And then they turned Harren into a public warning.)

(And then they made me think about what it meant.)

[Her shard hums-warm pressure, steady.]

(They're not pretending to be good.)

(They're choosing what kind of monster they're willing to be.)

(And they're teaching me to choose too.)

---

[She closes her eyes.]

[For the first time, she doesn't count exits.]

[She thinks of Vesper stepping between her and the breach.]

[She thinks of Elia's bare feet silent on the deck, violence as casual as breathing.]

[She thinks of Rho's demolition-precise hands, turning chaos into bodies with the same focus he uses for walls.]

[She thinks of Elisira's single syllable-*sit*-and the universe agreeing.]

[She thinks of Nyx's soft words-*locality, consent*-making bullets forget their destinations.]

(This is what "mythical" means.)

(It means: we chose our lines, and we enforce them.)

(It means: don't try to take from the people who built floors strong enough to fight back.)

---

[The ship hums beneath her.]

[A city pretending to be a ship.]

[A myth pretending to be a family.]

[A family that doesn't pretend to be clean.]

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee sleep onset achieved | INFERENCE: safety signal accepted | CONFIDENCE: 0.81 | NOTE: proportional response doctrine processed. integration ongoing.>

---

## Part III - The Names They Carry

[Three days later, Avyanna is in the common area with a datapad, doing what she's been doing for hours: reading.]

[Not training manuals. Not Lattice theory.]

[The extranet.]

[She'd started with a simple search: *Lumen Thief crew*. Just curiosity. Just wanting to know what the galaxy saw when it looked at the people who'd saved her.]

[What she found was... extensive.]

---

[Forum threads. Incident reports. Bounty postings that had been claimed and closed. News articles from rim stations she'd never heard of. A surprisingly detailed wiki entry that someone kept updating with information they shouldn't have.]

[And the names.]

[So many names.]

---

[She's still reading when Rho walks through, heading for the galley.]

Avyanna: [not looking up] Did you know people call you "The Breachwright"?

[Rho stops. His expression does something complicated-surprise, then embarrassment, then a kind of resigned amusement.]

Rho: [rubbing the back of his neck] Uh. Yeah. That one's been around for a while.

Avyanna: [scrolling] There's also "Shaped Mercy." And the Compact apparently classifies you as a "Hull Compromise Risk."

Rho: [dry] That's just their way of saying they don't like me.

[Avyanna looks up at him. Her expression is unreadable.]

Avyanna: You never mentioned any of this.

Rho: [shrugging] It doesn't... come up? We don't really think about it.

Avyanna: You have *threat classifications*. Named after you. The Compact has a *category* for Elia.

Rho: [wincing] Yeah, the "Lagrange Hazard" thing. She thinks it's funny.

---

[Elia's voice comes from the doorway. She's leaning against the frame, arms crossed, expression somewhere between amused and caught.]

Elia: I think it's *hilarious*. They named a bureaucratic threat level after my family. That's peak Compact.

Avyanna: [turning to her] You're "The Last Argument." There are *songs* about you.

Elia: [waving a hand] Those are mostly exaggerated.

Elisira: [appearing behind Elia, dry] The one about the Taelion Breach is accurate.

Elia: [shooting her a look] You're not helping.

Elisira: [mild] I'm never helping.

---

[Avyanna sets down the datapad. Her voice is careful, measured-not accusing, just trying to understand.]

Avyanna: Why didn't anyone tell me? That you were... that the galaxy knows who you are?

[A pause. The crew exchanges glances-the kind of silent communication that comes from years of working together.]

Vesper: [entering from the corridor, coffee in hand] Because we don't think about it.

Avyanna: You don't think about being *legends*?

Vesper: [sitting across from her] The names are something that happened to us. They're not who we are. They're what other people decided to call the shapes we left behind.

---

[Nyx drifts in, drawn by the conversation. They look at the datapad, then at Avyanna, then sigh.]

Nyx: You found the Writbound classifications.

Avyanna: "The Liminal." "Locality Apostle." [a beat] "Cornerwitch."

Nyx: [wincing] That last one is from a rim station where I had to... adjust some doorways. It was an emergency.

Rho: [snorting] "Adjust some doorways."

Nyx: [defensive] The geometry was already compromised. I just made it more so.

---

[Jalen appears in the galley doorway, drawn by the noise.]

Jalen: What are we confessing to?

Avyanna: [deadpan] That you're all famous and no one mentioned it.

Jalen: [blinking] We're not *famous*. We're just...

Elisira: Infamous.

Jalen: [considering] ...yeah, that's more accurate.

Avyanna: "Ghost Lane." "The Exit Sign." The Compact thinks you're committing "chart fraud."

Jalen: [brightening] That one's my favorite. It implies I'm lying about where the routes are, when actually the routes just *like* me better than them.

---

[Avyanna looks around the room. The whole crew is here now-drawn by the conversation, sheepish in ways that don't fit the terror she's been reading about.]

[The Last Argument is stealing Elisira's coffee.]

[The Breachwright is making a sandwich.]

[The Liminal is arguing about doorway geometry.]

[Ghost Lane is defending their navigation honor.]

[The Silent Verdict is letting Elia steal her coffee because she already made a backup.]

[God Eye is watching Avyanna with an expression that might be concern.]

---

Avyanna: [slowly] You really don't think about it.

Vesper: [quiet] The names are useful. They open doors. They close others. But they're not *us*. They're the stories people tell about what we did.

Elia: [through a mouthful of stolen coffee] We're just people who made choices. The galaxy decided those choices were interesting enough to name.

Avyanna: [looking at her datapad] There are people who are *afraid* of you.

Rho: [gentle] Good. Some people should be afraid. The ones who hurt kids. The ones who traffic. The ones who extract.

[He meets her eyes.]

Rho: The fear isn't the point. But it's not nothing, either.

---

[Avyanna is quiet for a moment. Processing.]

Avyanna: [finally] I've been living on a ship with "The Last Argument" and "The Silent Verdict" and I didn't know.

Elia: [shrugging] You've been living with Elia and Elisira. The names are just... echoes.

Elisira: [dry] Loud echoes.

Elia: [grinning] Very loud.

---

[Vesper reaches across the table. Not quite touching Avyanna's hand-just near it. Present.]

Vesper: Does it change anything?

[Avyanna considers. The question is real. Vesper wants to know if learning the scope of their reputation changes how Avyanna sees them.]

[She thinks about it.]

[Elia barefoot on the deck, sealing a hull breach with her palm.]

[Rho carrying her out of the mine, not asking, not commenting.]

[Vesper stepping between her and a breach, body as shield.]

[Nyx teaching her about locality in a meditation chamber filled with candles.]

[Jalen flying them through routes that shouldn't exist.]

[Elisira saying *sit* and the universe agreeing.]

---

Avyanna: [slowly] No. You're still the same people who gave me a floor.

[She turns the datapad face-down on the table.]

Avyanna: You're just... also monsters. To the right people.

Elia: [delighted] *Thank* you.

Rho: [laughing] That's the nicest thing anyone's said about us in years.

---

[Later, alone in her bunk, Avyanna pulls up one more search.]

[*"God Eye" Vesper Rook*]

[The results are sparse-Vesper is better at controlling her own narrative. But there are fragments. Whispers. The occasional bounty hunter who claims to have seen her shoot a weapon out of someone's hand from two hundred meters.]

[One forum post, buried deep, written by someone who survived a negotiation gone wrong:]

*"She had a revolver. Old model. Custom grip. She never drew it. Never even touched it. But everyone in the room knew-if she wanted us dead, we'd be dead before we heard the shot. That's why they call her God Eye. She doesn't miss. She just chooses not to fire."*

[Avyanna stares at the post for a long time.]

(The crew I live with has *legends*.)

(They just... never mentioned it.)

(Because to them, it's not the point.)

[The shard hums. Warm. Settled.]

(That's the point, isn't it. The names are echoes. The choices are what matter.)

[She closes the datapad.]

[Sleeps without dreaming.]

---

<CINNAMON.EXE// OBSERVATION: trainee completed independent reputation research | INFERENCE: integration accelerating | CONFIDENCE: 0.87 | NOTE: she's learning to see us the way the galaxy does. and choosing to stay anyway. that's the test.>

---

*End Chapter 20*


---
